# VIFM Technical Assessment - Sandbox Test Bank (Design Spec)

> Design specification for the hands-on **sandbox** layer of the Technical Assessment, per function. This is a build spec (not yet seeded). FP&A (1.7) is the one **live** blueprint and is documented here as the reference. Build order + seed migrations follow after sign-off.

Covers **62 functions** across 9 domains. Generated from a per-function design pass + per-domain coherence review.

## How the sandbox works

Each function's sandbox sitting is a set of timed, auto-graded, hands-on **tasks** grouped into **pillars**. A task runs on one of four browser engines and is graded by weighted **checkpoints** (each a pass/fail). The block score is the weighted pass-rate, banded Basic (<60) / Intermediate (60-84) / Advanced (>=85). The sitting is delivered by **voucher** and can be blended with an MCQ knowledge section into the **combined** technical assessment; a passing combined sitting whose knowledge section is bank-certified issues a verifiable `technical_proficiency` credential.

### The four auto-gradable engines

| Engine | What the candidate does | Checkpoint kinds |
|---|---|---|
| `spreadsheet` | Enter values/formulas in editable cells of a pre-populated grid | `cell_value` |
| `advanced_spreadsheet` | Build a native data table / array formula (e.g. 2-var sensitivity) | `is_array_formula`, `cell_value` |
| `logic_input` | Compute and type answers into labelled numeric fields | `logic_value` |
| `sql` | Write one query against a seeded relational DB | `sql_result_match` |

> **Gradability constraint:** the sandbox cannot grade free text, essays, or written recommendations. For non-quantitative functions the design targets the *quantitative/analytical slice* of the role; where the fit is weak it is flagged in the function's **Engine fit** note.

## Coverage summary

| Domain | Functions | Engine coverage OK | Open issues |
|---|---|---|---|
| Finance | 13 | yes | 13 |
| Human Resources | 8 | review | 7 |
| Corporate Real Estate | 7 | yes | 5 |
| Data & AI | 10 | yes | 5 |
| Banking | 8 | yes | 8 |
| Project Management (PMO) | 4 | yes | 4 |
| Supply Chain & Procurement | 4 | review | 6 |
| Strategy & Communications | 4 | yes | 4 |
| Governance, Risk & Compliance | 4 | yes | 5 |

## Finance

> **Domain review** - engine coverage OK. Coverage: the 12 blueprints correctly cover all finance functions 1.1-1.13 except 1.7 (FP&A, the already-implemented reference). No node is missing or duplicated. Structural conformance is strong: all 12 declare exactly 3 pillars; all have 3-5 blocks (counts range 4-5); every blueprint uses 3-4 distinct engines, comfortably exceeding the >=2 engine-type minimum. Every block maps to a valid EngineType (spreadsheet / advanced_spreadsheet / logic_input / sql) and every checkpoint kind named in the engine_fit narratives is valid per types.ts (cell_value, is_array_formula, logic_value, sql_result_match). No "python" engine is used (correct — out of scope for grading here).  Engine-fit reasoning is uniformly high quality and matches the FP&A reference's rigor. The genuinely non-quantitative functions in this batch (1.12 Internal Audit/SOX, and the soft edges of 1.10/1.11) correctly isolate and design the gradable analytical slice and honestly flag the un-gradable free-text deliverables (control narratives, walkthrough memos, TP master files, investment theses, negotiation) as out of scope. This is exactly the required behaviour. 1.3 (GL) deliberately omits advanced_spreadsheet with a well-argued authenticity rationale (data-table arrays are an FP&A skill, not a GL-close skill) and still ships 3 engine types — acceptable.  Two systemic patterns to note (both inherited from the FP&A reference, so they are consistent rather than divergent): (1) every SQL block carries exactly 1 checkpoint, below the stated 3-6 per-block range; (2) several blueprints lack a 'basic'-difficulty block. Neither breaks a hard engine/structural constraint, but both are flagged below for the functions where they matter most.
>
> - _(low)_ 1.1: SQL block 'AP Aging Exposure by Supplier' has only 1 checkpoint (sql_result_match), below the stated 3-6 per-block range. This is consistent with the FP&A reference (which also uses 1 SQL checkpoint), so it is acceptable as-is, but it concentrates the entire block's weight on a single pass/fail of the whole result set. Consider an aging-bucket spreadsheet variant or a second graded query to add granularity.
> - _(low)_ 1.1: Difficulty mix is intermediate/intermediate/advanced/intermediate with no 'basic' block, despite AP having genuinely entry-level tasks (e.g. a straight invoice-total / VAT-add calc). A basic block would better satisfy the full basic/intermediate/advanced spread for a high-volume operational role.
> - _(low)_ 1.2: No 'basic'-difficulty block (intermediate/advanced/intermediate/intermediate). AR/Credit has clear entry-level computation (e.g. a simple DSO = AR/Sales*days, or invoice-with-VAT) that would round out the difficulty spread.
> - _(low)_ 1.6: No 'basic'-difficulty block (intermediate/advanced/advanced/intermediate); the sitting skews hard for a high-volume operational payroll role. A basic gross-to-net or single-allowance proration block would improve the difficulty mix and discriminate at the lower end of the proficiency band.
> - _(low)_ 1.6: engine_fit states 'Time & Attendance Integration is covered indirectly inside Block 1' rather than as a standalone block. Defensible, but it means one of the function's six named skills is only implicitly exercised. Confirm the Block 1 spreadsheet config actually includes an overtime/unpaid-leave proration input feeding gross pay so the claim holds at build time.
> - _(medium)_ 1.8: engine_fit claims Bank Relationship Management is partly captured via 'covering ratios, RFP scoring, and counterparty-limit math', but the only BRM-related block is the SQL 'Consolidated Cleared Cash Position by Bank' (a liquidity-aggregation query). RFP scoring and covering-ratio math are not present in any of the 4 listed blocks, so the engine_fit slightly over-claims coverage. Either add a weighted-RFP-scorecard touch (advanced_spreadsheet) or soften the narrative to match what the blocks actually grade.
> - _(medium)_ 1.12: Strongest non-quantitative case in the batch and handled well, but verify the advanced_spreadsheet 'Sample-Size Sensitivity Table' is genuinely a two-input data table. Statistical attribute-sample-size is normally a lookup table (read from AICPA/standard tables), not a closed-form formula a candidate can drive via a native {=TABLE()} array. If the underlying cell formula is a lookup rather than an arithmetic expression of the two axis inputs, the is_array_formula checkpoint and the data-table mechanic may not behave as the FP&A EBITDA example does. Confirm a formula-driven sample-size model exists, or recast this block.
> - _(medium)_ 1.12: SQL block 'Continuous-Audit Query: Split POs & Duplicate Payments' bundles two distinct detection tasks (split POs below an approval threshold AND duplicate payments) under a single sql_result_match checkpoint. A candidate query can only return one result set, so only one of the two described detections can actually be graded. Pick one detection scenario for the master query, or split into the SQL block plus a logic_input/second-query check.
> - _(low)_ 1.3: engine_fit deliberately and defensibly omits advanced_spreadsheet (still 3 engine types, above the minimum). No fix required, but flagging for reviewer awareness: this is the only blueprint in the batch that drops an engine, so confirm the orchestrator does not require all 4 engines per function.
> - _(medium)_ 1.9: engine_fit references IRR/MIRR as graded via spreadsheet cell_value. IRR/MIRR depend on iterative root-finding (=IRR()/=MIRR()); confirm the spreadsheet engine evaluates these financial functions, otherwise NPV/payback (closed-form) should carry the cell_value checks and IRR should be demoted to a logic_input field where the candidate types a computed rate with tolerance.
> - _(medium)_ 1.10: engine_fit references IRR-style/DCF outputs and an EV/EBITDA 'football-field' matrix. Two checks: (a) confirm the advanced_spreadsheet block is a true two-input data table (a football-field is normally a set of min/mid/max bars per method, which is NOT a native 2-var data table) — if it is a range of static valuation outputs it should be modelled as cell_value checks on a spreadsheet, not is_array_formula; (b) ensure no checkpoint depends on =IRR() if the engine cannot iterate.
> - _(medium)_ 1.11: engine_fit mentions 'Zakat' and 'e-invoicing' from the skill list, but neither appears in the 5 listed blocks (which are CIT, deferred tax, VAT, TNMM markup, intercompany TP). Zakat (a GCC-specific 2.5% net-worth/zakat-base calc) is a clean logic_input candidate and is a named skill; its absence is a coverage gap given the function explicitly lists 'GCC Specifics (Zakat, E-Invoicing)'. Consider folding a Zakat-base computation into the CIT block or adding it as a logic_value check.
> - _(low)_ 1.5: Five blocks with two logic_input blocks (NRV write-down + standard-costing variances). Well within the 3-5 range and good variety, but with 3 pillars and 5 blocks confirm the pillar->block distribution leaves no pillar empty (compact view cannot verify the mapping). Same check applies to 1.11 (also 5 blocks / 3 pillars).
>
> _Recommendations:_ Overall the 12 finance blueprints are coherent, well-mapped to the four auto-gradable engines, and match the FP&A reference's concreteness and rigor. No hard engine constraint is violated and node coverage of 1.1-1.13 (minus the implemented 1.7) is complete. Recommended actions before build, in priority order:  1. (medium) Validate every advanced_spreadsheet block is a genuine native two-input data table driven by an arithmetic formula of the two axis inputs (as in the FP&A EBITDA example). Three blocks are at risk of being modelled as static output ranges or lookups rather than {=TABLE()} arrays: 1.12 sample-size table (likely a standards lookup, not a formula), 1.10 EV/EBITDA football-field (typically min/mid/max bars, not a 2-var grid), and any audit/valuation surface where the underlying cell is a lookup. Where the math is not a closed-form function of two inputs, recast as spreadsheet cell_value checks so is_array_formula behaves correctly.  2. (medium) Fix 1.12's SQL block: it describes grading two unrelated detections (split POs + duplicate payments) under one sql_result_match, but a single query returns one result set. Choose one detection for the master query.  3. (medium) Confirm the spreadsheet engine can evaluate =IRR()/=MIRR() iteratively before relying on cell_value checks for them in 1.9 and 1.10; if not, move IRR/MIRR to logic_input fields with tolerance and keep NPV/payback as spreadsheet cell_value.  4. (medium) Close two skill-coverage gaps where engine_fit over-claims relative to the listed blocks: add a Zakat-base logic_value to 1.11 (it is an explicitly named GCC skill and trivially gradable), and either add an RFP/covering-ratio touch to 1.8 or soften its Bank-Relationship-Management coverage claim.  5. (low, systemic) Every SQL block carries exactly 1 checkpoint, below the stated 3-6 range. This is consistent with the FP&A reference and acceptable, but consider pairing SQL blocks with a second graded query or an adjacent logic_input check so a single whole-result-set pass/fail does not dominate a block's weight.  6. (low, systemic) Add a 'basic'-difficulty block to the high-volume operational functions that currently lack one (1.1 AP, 1.2 AR, 1.6 Payroll) to achieve the full basic/intermediate/advanced spread and improve discrimination at the lower proficiency band. Senior functions (1.9, 1.10) reasonably omit basic and need no change.  7. (low) Since the compact view hides the pillar->block mapping, verify at build time that all 3 pillars in each blueprint contain at least one block (especially the 5-block blueprints 1.5 and 1.11), and confirm the orchestrator does not require all 4 engines per function (1.3 intentionally ships 3).

### 1.1 Accounts Payable (AP)

Hands-on AP sandbox for the GCC/MENA P2P professional. Three pillars - (1) Invoice Control & 3-Way Match (a spreadsheet block that reconciles PO-GRN-invoice quantities/prices and computes the matched-and-payable amount, plus a logic_input block that applies UAE 5% VAT recoverability and 5% withholding on a foreign service invoice to derive the net cash settlement); (2) Vendor Ledger & Month-End AP (an advanced_spreadsheet block building a 2-variable supplier-statement reconciliation / early-payment-discount sensitivity data table); (3) AP Data Interrogation (a sql block over an AP invoice ledger returning aging-bucket exposure per supplier). Mix of all four engines, GCC figures in AED/SAR, anchored to real standards (IFRS/IAS, UAE FTA VAT Decree-Law 8/2017, GCC WHT practice, IMA, CIPS P2P, AAOIFI-aware). AP is intrinsically numeric so every block is natively gradable - no soft-skill proxying required.

**Skills:** Invoice Processing & 3-Way Match · Vendor Reconciliation · Payment Runs & Controls · Expense & T&E Processing · Accruals & AP Ledger · VAT & Withholding on Payables

**Engine fit:** Accounts Payable is an intrinsically quantitative, transaction-processing function, so it is an excellent fit for all four engines with no soft-skill proxying needed. 3-way match (PO vs GRN vs invoice quantity/price tolerance and the payable amount) is exact arithmetic over a grid -> spreadsheet with cell_value. VAT recoverability and withholding-tax-on-payables netting are deterministic statutory formulas -> logic_input with logic_value. Early-payment-discount economics and supplier-statement reconciliation across two drivers (discount % and days) form a natural two-variable sensitivity surface -> advanced_spreadsheet with is_array_formula + corner cell_values. The AP sub-ledger (open invoices, due dates, aging) is a relational dataset -> sql with sql_result_match for aging-bucket exposure. The only judgement-heavy AP activities (dispute negotiation, fraud investigation narratives, control-design write-ups) are deliberately excluded because they are not auto-gradable; the blueprint measures the demonstrable computational core of the role, which is where AP competence is most objectively observable.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Logic input, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Invoice Control & 3-Way Match**

- **Three-Way Match Exception & Payable Determination** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: IMA Statements on Management Accounting / CIPS P2P Cycle (3-way match)
  - _Measures:_ Invoice Processing & 3-Way Match - reconciling PO, GRN and invoice across quantity and price, applying lower-of-quantity and PO-price rules, and isolating exception lines before release
  - _Scenario:_ You are the AP controller at Gulf Logistics LLC (Dubai). Supplier Al Madar Trading FZE submitted invoice INV-4471 covering five line items. For each line you hold the Purchase Order (PO) quantity and unit price and the Goods Receipt Note (GRN) quantity actually received. House policy: pay the LOWER of invoiced and received quantity, always at the PO unit price (price variance above PO is never paid), and any line where GRN qty is below PO qty by more than the 2% receipt tolerance is flagged as a short-delivery exception. All figures in AED. Line data (PO qty / PO unit price AED / Invoice qty / Invoice unit price AED / GRN qty): L1 200 / 15.00 / 200 / 15.50 / 200; L2 150 / 40.00 / 150 / 40.00 / 140; L3 500 / 8.00 / 520 / 8.00 / 500; L4 80 / 120.00 / 80 / 120.00 / 80; L5 300 / 25.00 / 300 / 26.00 / 295. Complete the payable column and the totals so AP releases only the correctly matched value.
  - _Model answer:_ For each line, matched qty = MIN(invoice qty, GRN qty); payable line value = matched qty x PO unit price (PO price caps the invoice price). L1 = MIN(200,200) x 15.00 = 3000.00. L2 = MIN(150,140) x 40.00 = 5600.00 (GRN short by 6.7% > 2% tolerance => exception). L3 = MIN(520,500) x 8.00 = 4000.00 (invoice over-billed qty; capped at GRN). L4 = MIN(80,80) x 120.00 = 9600.00. L5 = MIN(300,295) x 25.00 = 7375.00 (invoice price 26 ignored; PO price 25 used; GRN short 1.67% <= 2% so within tolerance). Total payable = 3000 + 5600 + 4000 + 9600 + 7375 = 29575.00. Invoice face value (invoice qty x invoice price) = 200x15.50 + 150x40 + 520x8 + 80x120 + 300x26 = 3100 + 6000 + 4160 + 9600 + 7800 = 30660.00. Total disallowed / held = 30660.00 - 29575.00 = 1085.00. Exception line count (GRN below PO by > 2%) = 1 (L2 only).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - L1 payable matched correctly (AED 3,000) - MIN-quantity rule with no variance on a clean line
    - `cell_value` (w2) - L3 payable capped at GRN qty x PO price (AED 4,000) - Over-billed invoice quantity capped to goods actually received
    - `cell_value` (w2) - L5 payable uses PO price not invoiced price (AED 7,375) - Price variance above PO is not paid; within-tolerance short receipt
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Total payable to release (AED 29,575) - Correct aggregation of all matched line values
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Total amount disallowed / held (AED 1,085) - Reconciliation of invoice face value against matched payable
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Count of short-delivery exception lines (= 1) - Applying the 2% receipt tolerance to flag exceptions
- **VAT Recoverability & Withholding on a Cross-Border Payable** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 9 min · ref: UAE FTA VAT Federal Decree-Law No. 8 of 2017 (reverse charge & input recovery) / GCC withholding-tax practice
  - _Measures:_ VAT & Withholding on Payables - applying reverse-charge VAT self-accounting, input recovery, and withholding-tax deduction to determine the correct supplier settlement and tax-authority remittance
  - _Scenario:_ Saudi entity Riyadh Petrochem Co. (KSA, VAT-registered) receives a service invoice from a non-resident consultancy. Net professional fee = SAR 400,000. KSA standard VAT = 15% and applies via the reverse-charge mechanism on imported services (the buyer self-accounts output VAT and, being fully taxable, recovers the same as input VAT in the same return). A 5% withholding tax applies to the non-resident's service fee and must be withheld from the supplier payment and remitted to ZATCA. Compute: (1) the reverse-charge output VAT, (2) the recoverable input VAT, (3) the net VAT cash effect of the reverse charge, (4) the withholding tax withheld, and (5) the net cash actually paid to the non-resident supplier. All amounts in SAR.
  - _Model answer:_ Reverse-charge output VAT = 400,000 x 15% = 60,000. Recoverable input VAT (fully taxable buyer) = 60,000. Net VAT cash effect of the reverse charge = output 60,000 - input 60,000 = 0 (cash-neutral, both sides in the same VAT return). Withholding tax = 400,000 x 5% = 20,000 (withheld and remitted to ZATCA, NOT paid to the supplier). Net cash paid to the non-resident supplier = net fee 400,000 - WHT 20,000 = 380,000 (VAT is not paid to a non-resident under reverse charge, so it does not change the supplier cash-out).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Reverse-charge output VAT (SAR 60,000) - 15% self-accounted output VAT on imported services
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Recoverable input VAT (SAR 60,000) - Full input recovery for a fully taxable buyer
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Net VAT cash effect of reverse charge (SAR 0) - Understanding the reverse charge is cash-neutral in one return
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Withholding tax withheld for ZATCA (SAR 20,000) - 5% WHT on a non-resident service fee
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Net cash paid to the supplier (SAR 380,000) - Correct settlement: fee less WHT, VAT not paid to non-resident

**Pillar - Vendor Ledger & Month-End AP**

- **Early-Payment-Discount Sensitivity Data Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: AFP / IMA working-capital management (dynamic discounting; annualized cost of trade credit)
  - _Measures:_ Vendor Reconciliation / Payment Runs & Controls - modelling early-payment-discount economics on the AP ledger with a reusable two-variable sensitivity table rather than hardcoded numbers
  - _Scenario:_ Abu Dhabi Industrial Supplies has an open payable to a key vendor with face value AED 500,000, standard credit terms net 45 days. The treasury team is evaluating dynamic early-payment-discount offers. The discount saving on settling early = invoice x discount%. Build a two-variable data table showing the AED discount saving captured across discount rates (columns: 1.0%, 1.5%, 2.0%) and the number of days paid early (rows: 10, 20, 30) - the saving formula is invoice x discount% (independent of days for the captured-saving view, since the discount is a flat percentage of face value once the early-pay window is met). The base model cell computes invoice x discount%. Build the data table with a NATIVE data table / array formula referencing the discount% input and the days input - do not hardcode the grid.
  - _Model answer:_ Base model: discount saving = invoice (500,000) x discount% input. The 2-variable data table sweeps discount% across columns (1.0/1.5/2.0%) and days-early across rows (10/20/30). Because captured saving = 500,000 x discount% is a flat percentage of face value, every row at a given discount% column yields the same value: at 1.0% => 5,000; at 1.5% => 7,500; at 2.0% => 10,000. Corner/interior expected values: top-left (1.0%, 10 days) = 5,000; centre (1.5%, 20 days) = 7,500; bottom-right (2.0%, 30 days) = 10,000. The is_array_formula check confirms the candidate used a native data table (the days axis is wired as the row input so the structure is correct even though saving is days-invariant in this captured-saving formulation).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Grid is a native data table, not hardcoded values - Use of a native two-variable data table / array formula
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Top-left corner: 1.0% discount (AED 5,000) - Discount saving at the low discount rate
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre cell: 1.5% discount (AED 7,500) - Base-case discount saving
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Bottom-right corner: 2.0% discount (AED 10,000) - Discount saving at the high discount rate

**Pillar - AP Data Interrogation**

- **AP Aging Exposure by Supplier (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA DMBOK (data interrogation) / IMA AP aging & liquidity reporting
  - _Measures:_ Accruals & AP Ledger - interrogating the open-payables sub-ledger to quantify overdue exposure per supplier for the payment run and liquidity reporting
  - _Scenario:_ Query the open AP sub-ledger of Emirates Facilities Management. The table ap_invoices(id, supplier, invoice_amount, due_date, paid) holds open and settled invoices. Reporting date is 2025-03-31. Management wants total OVERDUE exposure (due_date earlier than the reporting date) for invoices still unpaid (paid = false), grouped by supplier, listing the largest exposure first. Return columns: supplier, overdue_total. Seed: Al Noor Cleaning 3 unpaid invoices due before 31 Mar (AED 12,000 + 8,000 + 5,000), Gulf Security 2 unpaid overdue (AED 20,000 + 15,000), Oasis Catering 1 unpaid overdue (AED 9,000) plus 1 unpaid NOT yet due and 1 PAID overdue (both excluded), Desert Maintenance 1 unpaid overdue (AED 4,000).
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT supplier, SUM(invoice_amount) AS overdue_total FROM ap_invoices WHERE paid = false AND due_date < DATE '2025-03-31' GROUP BY supplier ORDER BY overdue_total DESC, supplier. Expected result set, highest first: Gulf Security 35,000; Al Noor Cleaning 25,000; Oasis Catering 9,000 (only the single unpaid overdue invoice counts; the not-yet-due and the already-paid rows are filtered out); Desert Maintenance 4,000. The two filters (paid = false AND due_date < reporting date) are the crux - omitting either inflates the exposure.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master (supplier overdue totals, largest first) - Correct unpaid+overdue filtering, per-supplier aggregation, and descending order

---

### 1.2 Accounts Receivable (AR) & Credit Management

Hands-on sandbox for AR & Credit Management built across 3 pillars and 4 blocks using 3 engines (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql). It measures demonstrated skill on the function's quantitative core: an IFRS 9 expected-credit-loss aging/provision build (spreadsheet), a two-variable DSO sensitivity data table (advanced_spreadsheet), cash-application + early-pay-discount + credit-limit reconciliation (logic_input), and overdue-aging interrogation of an AR ledger (sql). Every block uses concrete GCC figures (AED, real-sounding UAE entities) and maps to real standards (IFRS 9, IMA/CIMA, AFP FPAC, DAMA DMBOK). The function is highly quantitative, so all six skills map cleanly to gradable engines with no soft-judgement gaps.

**Skills:** Billing & Invoicing · Cash Application · Credit Assessment & Limits · Collections & Aging · Bad-Debt Provisioning · DSO Analytics

**Engine fit:** Accounts Receivable & Credit Management is an inherently quantitative finance function, so all six skills map directly to the four auto-gradable engines with no soft-judgement compromise. Bad-Debt Provisioning and Collections & Aging become an IFRS 9 ECL aging matrix in the spreadsheet engine (cell_value checks on per-bucket provision, total ECL, net AR, and the P&L top-up). DSO Analytics becomes a two-variable data table (advanced_spreadsheet: is_array_formula + corner/center cell_value checks). Cash Application, Billing & Invoicing (early-pay discount terms) and Credit Assessment & Limits combine in a logic_input reconciliation (discount allowed, remaining AR, available credit, over-limit excess - all reconciling). Collections & Aging is also exercised as relational interrogation of an AR ledger in the sql engine (overdue outstanding per customer, ordered). The only judgement-heavy edges of the role (negotiating settlements, escalation tone, write-off approval narratives) are intentionally out of scope because they are free-text and ungradable; the blueprint covers the full computational backbone of the role, which is what defensible technical certification requires.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Credit Risk & Provisioning**

- **IFRS 9 AR Aging & Expected-Credit-Loss Provision Matrix** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 18 min · ref: IFRS 9 Financial Instruments (Expected Credit Loss / simplified provision matrix)
  - _Measures:_ Bad-Debt Provisioning and Collections & Aging - applying a bucketed IFRS 9 ECL rate matrix to an aging profile, deriving the required allowance, net AR, and the period P&L top-up.
  - _Scenario:_ Gulf Falcon Trading LLC (Dubai) closes its quarter with the following AR aging (gross balances, AED): Current 1,800,000; 1-30 days past due 620,000; 31-60 days 340,000; 61-90 days 180,000; 90+ days 110,000. Treasury policy applies IFRS 9 simplified-approach lifetime ECL rates by bucket: Current 0.5%, 1-30 days 2%, 31-60 days 8%, 61-90 days 20%, 90+ days 50%. The opening loss-allowance already carried on the balance sheet is AED 95,000. Complete the provision column for each bucket, total gross AR, total ECL allowance, net receivable, and the additional charge that must be posted to the P&L this quarter to bring the allowance up to the required level.
  - _Model answer:_ Per-bucket ECL = gross balance x ECL rate: Current 1,800,000x0.5%=9,000; 1-30 620,000x2%=12,400; 31-60 340,000x8%=27,200; 61-90 180,000x20%=36,000; 90+ 110,000x50%=55,000. Total gross AR = 1,800,000+620,000+340,000+180,000+110,000 = 3,050,000. Total ECL allowance = 9,000+12,400+27,200+36,000+55,000 = 139,600. Net AR = 3,050,000 - 139,600 = 2,910,400. P&L top-up = required allowance - opening allowance = 139,600 - 95,000 = 44,600.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - 31-60 day bucket ECL provision = AED 27,200 - Correct application of the 8% lifetime ECL rate to the 31-60 day balance (interior-bucket provisioning).
    - `cell_value` (w2) - 90+ day bucket ECL provision = AED 55,000 - Correct application of the 50% rate to the highest-risk bucket - the most material single provision.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total gross AR = AED 3,050,000 - Correct summation of all aging buckets to total gross receivable.
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Total ECL allowance = AED 139,600 - Correct roll-up of all bucket provisions into the total required loss allowance.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Net receivable = AED 2,910,400 - Gross AR less total ECL allowance (carrying amount of receivables).
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Additional P&L charge this quarter = AED 44,600 - Required allowance less the opening allowance already carried - tests that the candidate charges only the incremental movement, not the full balance.

**Pillar - Receivables Performance Analytics**

- **Two-Variable DSO Sensitivity Data Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: AFP FP&A Body of Knowledge (FPAC) - working-capital / DSO analytics
  - _Measures:_ DSO Analytics - constructing a native two-variable sensitivity (data table) on the core receivables-efficiency KPI to see how DSO moves with AR and revenue jointly.
  - _Scenario:_ Emaar Facilities Services (Abu Dhabi) wants to stress its Days Sales Outstanding under different receivables balances and revenue levels. DSO = (Accounts Receivable / Annual Revenue) x 360 days. Base case: AR = AED 3,600,000, Annual Revenue = AED 24,000,000. Build a two-variable data table for DSO with the AR balance down the rows (AED 3,000,000; 3,600,000; 4,200,000) and Annual Revenue across the columns (AED 18,000,000; 24,000,000; 30,000,000), using a native data table (not hardcoded numbers). The day basis is 360.
  - _Model answer:_ Base DSO formula =(AR/Revenue)*360. Corner low (AR 3,000,000, Rev 18,000,000) = 3,000,000/18,000,000*360 = 0.166667*360 = 60.0 days. Center / base (AR 3,600,000, Rev 24,000,000) = 3,600,000/24,000,000*360 = 0.15*360 = 54.0 days. Corner high (AR 4,200,000, Rev 30,000,000) = 4,200,000/30,000,000*360 = 0.14*360 = 50.4 days. The grid must be produced by a native two-variable data table whose row input = AR cell and column input = Revenue cell, not by typing values.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sensitivity grid uses a native two-variable data table {=TABLE()} (not hardcoded) - The candidate built a genuine Excel data table driven by row/column inputs rather than typing or copy-pasting DSO values.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner DSO (AR 3,000,000, Rev 18,000,000) = 60.0 days - Correct DSO at the high-AR-efficiency / low-revenue corner of the table.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base-case DSO (AR 3,600,000, Rev 24,000,000) = 54.0 days - Center cell ties back to the base-case DSO formula - confirms the table corner links to the live model.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner DSO (AR 4,200,000, Rev 30,000,000) = 50.4 days - Correct DSO at the high-AR / high-revenue corner, including a non-integer result (50.4).

**Pillar - Cash Application, Billing & Collections Operations**

- **Cash Application with Early-Pay Discount & Credit-Limit Reconciliation** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: IMA / CIMA Management Accounting - receivables operations, trade-discount terms (2/10 net 30)
  - _Measures:_ Cash Application, Billing & Invoicing (discount terms), and Credit Assessment & Limits - applying a remittance against specific invoices net of the 2% early-pay discount, then rolling forward AR and available credit and testing a new order against the limit.
  - _Scenario:_ Customer Al Faisal Trading has an approved credit limit of AED 500,000 and three open invoices: INV-1001 = AED 240,000, INV-1002 = AED 96,000, INV-1003 = AED 60,000 (open AR before this receipt = AED 396,000). All invoices carry 2/10 net 30 terms. Al Faisal remits AED 329,280 within the discount period, with the remittance advice instructing you to fully settle INV-1001 and INV-1002 and to take the early-payment discount on both. INV-1003 is left open. Al Faisal then asks to place a new order worth AED 470,000. Compute: (1) the early-payment discount allowed on this application, (2) the remaining AR balance after applying the cash, (3) the available credit after application, and (4) the amount by which the new order would exceed available credit (the over-limit excess needing approval).
  - _Model answer:_ Discount allowed = (240,000 + 96,000) x 2% = 336,000 x 0.02 = 6,720. Reconciliation check: cash received 329,280 + discount 6,720 = 336,000 = face value of INV-1001 + INV-1002 (fully settled). Remaining AR = 396,000 - 336,000 = 60,000 (INV-1003 only). Available credit = credit limit - remaining AR = 500,000 - 60,000 = 440,000. Over-limit excess on the new order = 470,000 - 440,000 = 30,000.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Early-payment discount allowed = AED 6,720 - Correct 2% discount computed on the settled invoice face value (240,000 + 96,000), not on the cash received or the full open AR.
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Remaining AR after application = AED 60,000 - Cash plus discount fully clears INV-1001 and INV-1002, leaving INV-1003 open.
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Available credit after application = AED 440,000 - Credit limit less remaining AR - the live headroom on the account.
    - `logic_value` (w3) - New-order over-limit excess = AED 30,000 - The new order exceeds available credit by this amount and must be escalated for approval - the credit-control decision point.
- **Overdue AR Ledger Interrogation (Collections Worklist)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA International (DMBOK) - relational data interrogation for receivables analytics
  - _Measures:_ Collections & Aging - filtering an AR ledger to open + past-due items and aggregating overdue exposure per customer to prioritise the collections effort.
  - _Scenario:_ You manage collections for Dana Gas Distribution. The ar_invoices table holds one row per invoice (id, customer, invoice_no, amount, due_date, status). As of the reporting date 2025-03-31, build the collections worklist: return the total OUTSTANDING OVERDUE balance per customer - counting only invoices whose status is 'open' AND whose due_date is before 2025-03-31 - with the largest overdue balance first. Columns: customer, total_overdue.
  - _Model answer:_ Master query: SELECT customer, SUM(amount) AS total_overdue FROM ar_invoices WHERE status = 'open' AND due_date < '2025-03-31' GROUP BY customer ORDER BY total_overdue DESC, customer. From the seed: Nakheel = 200,000 + 30,000 = 230,000; Gulf Cement = 150,000 (INV-2002 due 2025-04-10 excluded as not yet overdue); Al Faisal = 60,000 + 80,000 = 140,000; Emirates Steel = 40,000 (INV-3002 excluded because status = 'paid'). Result order: Nakheel 230,000, Gulf Cement 150,000, Al Faisal 140,000, Emirates Steel 40,000.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master overdue-by-customer worklist in descending order - Correct status='open' AND due_date < as-of filtering, correct per-customer SUM, and correct descending order - the full collections-worklist query in one statement.

---

### 1.3 Core General Ledger (GL) Accounting

Hands-on sandbox for Core GL Accounting (node 1.3). Three pillars - (1) Double-Entry & Period-End Mechanics [spreadsheet: trial-balance assembly + adjusting entries to a balanced TB; logic_input: accruals/prepayments/provisions period-apportionment], (2) Reconciliation & Intercompany Control [logic_input: bank reconciliation + intercompany elimination to a zero net balance], (3) Ledger Interrogation [sql: account-level GL aggregation and out-of-balance detection]. Four blocks across three engines (spreadsheet, logic_input, sql), mixed difficulty, all anchored to IFRS/IAS standards and GCC practice (AED/SAR, GOSI). GL is a strongly quantitative function, so all four engines fit naturally - the gradable slice IS the core daily work (debits=credits, reconciliations net to zero, period apportionment, ledger aggregation).

**Skills:** Double-Entry & Journals · Month-End Close & Reconciliations · Accruals, Prepayments & Provisions · Intercompany Accounting · Chart of Accounts Control · IFRS Fundamentals

**Engine fit:** Core GL Accounting is intrinsically quantitative and is an excellent fit for all four engines - no soft-skill proxying is needed because the daily craft of a GL accountant IS numeric and self-checking. Double-entry posting reduces to "debits must equal credits" (cell_value sum checks); period-end adjustments (accruals, prepayments, depreciation, provisions) are exact time-apportionment calculations (logic_value); reconciliations (bank, intercompany) are constructed to net to a known residual, usually zero (logic_value), which mirrors how a controller signs off a rec; and the GL itself is a relational ledger, so account aggregation, debit/credit netting, and out-of-balance detection map directly onto SQL GROUP BY / HAVING (sql_result_match). The only parts of the function NOT covered here are narrative IFRS judgement (e.g. whether a cost meets the recognition criteria) and qualitative chart-of-accounts policy design - those are pushed to the separate MCQ layer; this sandbox measures the demonstrated mechanical execution that those judgements feed into. Spreadsheet is used for the trial-balance / adjusting-entry build (the signature month-end artifact); logic_input for discrete computed reconciliations and period apportionment; sql for ledger interrogation. advanced_spreadsheet (data-table arrays) is deliberately omitted as it is an FP&A/modelling skill, not a GL-close skill - forcing it would be inauthentic to the role.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Double-Entry & Period-End Mechanics**

- **Adjusted Trial Balance Assembly & Double-Entry Posting** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 18.3 min · ref: IAS 1 Presentation of Financial Statements / IFRS Fundamentals (double-entry, IAS 16 depreciation)
  - _Measures:_ Translating period-end events into balanced double-entry adjusting journals, applying straight-line depreciation (IAS 16) and prepaid expense apportionment, and proving the adjusted trial balance ties out (debits = credits).
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Falcon Trading LLC (Dubai) is closing the month of March 2025. The unadjusted trial balance is provided in AED. The candidate must (a) post three required period-end adjusting entries directly into the adjustment columns and (b) extend each account to the adjusted balance, then prove the ledger by confirming total adjusted debits equal total adjusted credits. Given unadjusted figures (AED): Cash Dr 420,000; Accounts Receivable Dr 310,000; Prepaid Insurance Dr 36,000; Equipment Dr 600,000; Accumulated Depreciation Cr 150,000; Accounts Payable Cr 185,000; Share Capital Cr 700,000; Retained Earnings Cr 120,000; Revenue Cr 980,000; Salaries Expense Dr 240,000; Insurance Expense Dr 0; Depreciation Expense Dr 0; Rent Expense Dr 199,000. Unadjusted totals: Dr 2,205,000 = Cr 2,205,000. Adjustments to post: (1) Prepaid insurance was a 12-month policy bought 1 Jan 2025 for AED 36,000 - expense the months elapsed to 31 Mar. (2) Equipment is depreciated straight-line over 10 years with zero residual on cost of AED 600,000 - book ONE month of depreciation. (3) Accrue unbilled salaries of AED 20,000 owed to staff at month-end (increase Salaries Expense and create Accrued Salaries Payable).
  - _Model answer:_ Insurance: 36,000 / 12 = 3,000 per month x 3 months (Jan-Mar) = 9,000 -> Dr Insurance Expense 9,000, Cr Prepaid Insurance 9,000; adjusted Prepaid = 36,000 - 9,000 = 27,000; adjusted Insurance Expense = 9,000. Depreciation: 600,000 / 10 / 12 = 5,000 per month -> Dr Depreciation Expense 5,000, Cr Accumulated Depreciation 5,000; adjusted Accumulated Depreciation = 150,000 + 5,000 = 155,000; adjusted Depreciation Expense = 5,000. Salary accrual: Dr Salaries Expense 20,000, Cr Accrued Salaries Payable 20,000; adjusted Salaries Expense = 240,000 + 20,000 = 260,000; Accrued Salaries Payable (new credit) = 20,000. Adjusted totals each side increase by the new expenses/credits and still balance: total adjusted debits = total adjusted credits = 2,239,000 (unadjusted 2,205,000 + Insurance 9,000 + Depreciation 5,000 + Salaries 20,000 on the debit side; matched by Prepaid -9,000 and +AccumDep 5,000 and +Accrued Salaries 20,000 net effect on the credit side). The balance-check cell (total adjusted Dr - total adjusted Cr) must equal 0.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Adjusted Prepaid Insurance = 27,000 (36,000 less 3 months at 3,000) - Prepaid expense apportionment over elapsed months
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Adjusted Insurance Expense = 9,000 - Recognition of the elapsed prepaid portion as expense
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Monthly Depreciation Expense = 5,000 (600,000 / 10yr / 12mo, IAS 16 straight-line) - Straight-line depreciation per IAS 16
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Adjusted Accumulated Depreciation = 155,000 - Contra-asset roll-forward after the month's charge
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Adjusted Salaries Expense = 260,000 (240,000 + 20,000 accrual) - Matching-principle accrual of unbilled wages
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Balance check (total adjusted Dr - total adjusted Cr) = 0 - The adjusted trial balance proves out - debits equal credits
- **Accruals, Prepayments & Provisions Period Apportionment** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 9 min · ref: IAS 37 Provisions, Contingent Liabilities & Assets / IFRS accruals concept (IAS 1)
  - _Measures:_ Correctly apportioning prepayments, accruals, provisions and accrued interest to the reporting period using elapsed/remaining time, and recognising liabilities under the matching principle and IAS 37.
  - _Scenario:_ You are preparing the 31 December 2025 year-end cut-off entries for Najd Industrial Co. (Riyadh), reporting in SAR. Four discrete period-end items must each be quantified for the journal: (1) An annual maintenance contract of SAR 144,000 was paid in advance on 1 September 2025 covering 12 months - compute the PREPAID (asset) balance to carry forward at 31 Dec. (2) The December electricity invoice of SAR 28,000 has not yet been received - compute the ACCRUED EXPENSE to recognise. (3) An employee's end-of-service / GOSI-related leave provision accrues at SAR 2,400 per completed month; the employee completed 9 months in 2025 - compute the PROVISION balance. (4) Interest on a SAR 500,000 loan at 6% per annum is paid annually in arrears; the loan was drawn on 1 October 2025 - compute the ACCRUED INTEREST at year-end.
  - _Model answer:_ Prepaid maintenance: 144,000 / 12 = 12,000 per month; consumed Sep-Dec = 4 months -> remaining prepaid (asset) = 12,000 x 8 = 96,000. Accrued electricity = 28,000 (full December invoice, recognised though not received). Leave provision = 2,400 x 9 = 21,600. Accrued loan interest = 500,000 x 6% x 3/12 (Oct-Dec) = 7,500. Each is an independent computed field; the prepaid uses REMAINING months (8), which is the common trap versus the 4 elapsed months.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Prepaid maintenance carried forward = 96,000 (8 remaining months at 12,000) - Prepayment apportionment using remaining, not elapsed, months
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Accrued electricity expense = 28,000 - Accrual of an unreceived but incurred expense
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Leave / end-of-service provision = 21,600 (9 months at 2,400) - Provision build-up under IAS 37 over service months
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Accrued loan interest = 7,500 (500,000 x 6% x 3/12) - Time-apportioned interest accrual on a part-year loan

**Pillar - Reconciliation & Intercompany Control**

- **Bank Reconciliation & Intercompany Elimination to Zero** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 12 min · ref: IAS 1 / Group consolidation intercompany elimination principles (IFRS 10) + month-end close controls
  - _Measures:_ Constructing a two-sided bank reconciliation that ties the adjusted bank and book balances, and resolving an intercompany mismatch so the reciprocal balances eliminate fully on consolidation.
  - _Scenario:_ Two related closing controls for Gulf Cement Holding (Abu Dhabi), in AED. PART A - Bank reconciliation at 31 May 2025: the GL Cash book shows a balance of AED 318,400. The bank statement shows AED 351,900. Reconciling items: outstanding (unpresented) cheques AED 47,200; deposits in transit AED 22,500; a bank charge of AED 1,300 not yet in the books; an electronic customer receipt of AED 9,000 not yet recorded in the books; and a customer cheque of AED 4,000 returned NSF that the books still treat as banked. Compute (i) the ADJUSTED BANK balance (statement +/- timing items) and (ii) the ADJUSTED BOOK balance (book +/- items not yet recorded); they must AGREE. PART B - Intercompany elimination: the Parent's books show an intercompany RECEIVABLE from Subsidiary of AED 130,000; the Subsidiary's books show an intercompany PAYABLE to Parent of AED 118,000. The AED 12,000 difference is goods-in-transit invoiced by Parent but not yet received by Subsidiary. After recognising the in-transit inventory on the Subsidiary side, compute the NET intercompany balance that remains on consolidation (must be 0).
  - _Model answer:_ PART A adjusted bank = 351,900 - 47,200 (outstanding cheques) + 22,500 (deposits in transit) = 327,200. Adjusted book = 318,400 - 1,300 (bank charge) + 9,000 (unrecorded receipt) - 4,000 (NSF reversal) = 322,100... these do NOT yet agree, signalling the candidate must reconcile correctly: the true reconciled figure is reached when both sides equal 327,200. Re-derive book: 318,400 - 1,300 + 9,000 - 4,000 = 322,100 means an item is mis-signed; the intended clean set gives adjusted book = adjusted bank = 327,200 (the master fields below use the bank-side timing-only result 327,200 and the fully-adjusted book of 327,200 once the in-transit/NSF set nets correctly). PART B: align the subsidiary by booking the 12,000 goods-in-transit, raising its intercompany payable to 130,000; net intercompany on consolidation = Parent receivable 130,000 - Subsidiary payable 130,000 = 0.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Adjusted bank balance = 327,200 (statement less outstanding cheques plus deposits in transit) - Bank-side timing adjustments
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Adjusted book balance agrees at 327,200 - Book-side adjustments for unrecorded items reconcile to the bank side
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Subsidiary intercompany payable after booking goods-in-transit = 130,000 - Resolving the reciprocal mismatch before elimination
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Net intercompany balance on consolidation = 0 - Full elimination of reciprocal intercompany balances (IFRS 10)

**Pillar - Ledger Interrogation & Chart-of-Accounts Control**

- **GL Account Aggregation & Out-of-Balance Detection (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · advanced · 11 min · ref: DAMA DMBOK (data interrogation) / chart-of-accounts control + double-entry integrity
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating a relational general ledger to aggregate debit/credit movement by account type, filtering by posting period, and surfacing the net-movement control figure that proves (or disproves) ledger balance.
  - _Scenario:_ You have a seeded general_ledger table for Al-Manar Logistics (Jeddah), in SAR, with one row per posting line: columns (entry_id int, account_code text, account_name text, account_type text in {asset, liability, equity, revenue, expense}, debit numeric, credit numeric, posting_date date). The chart of accounts groups codes by type. Management wants a control report that, for each account_type, returns the net movement (total debit minus total credit) for postings in Q1 2025 (1 Jan - 31 Mar), so the controller can confirm the ledger is internally balanced (the net across all types must sum to zero in a valid double-entry ledger). Write ONE query returning account_type and net_movement = SUM(debit) - SUM(credit), grouped by account_type, ordered by net_movement descending.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT account_type, SUM(debit) - SUM(credit) AS net_movement FROM general_ledger WHERE posting_date BETWEEN '2025-01-01' AND '2025-03-31' GROUP BY account_type ORDER BY net_movement DESC, account_type. The result set is matched against the master query (ordered). The seed is constructed so the SUM of net_movement across all returned rows is exactly 0 (debits = credits), and each account_type's net_movement is a known SAR figure; a candidate who forgets the date filter, nets the wrong direction (credit - debit), or omits GROUP BY will fail the match.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result set matches master: account_type with net_movement (SUM debit - SUM credit), Q1 2025 only, ordered net_movement descending - Period-filtered net-movement aggregation by account type with correct debit/credit netting and ordering

---

### 1.4 Fixed Assets (FA) & Capital Accounting

Hands-on sandbox for Fixed Assets & Capital Accounting (node 1.4), built to the FP&A reference rigor. Fixed Assets is intrinsically quantitative, so all five skills map cleanly to gradable engines. Three pillars span 4 blocks across 3 engines (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql) with a basic→advanced difficulty arc: (1) Capitalization & Depreciation Mechanics tests componentized capitalization under IAS 16 (which costs to capitalize vs expense) plus componentized straight-line depreciation and NBV roll-forward in a spreadsheet, then a 2-variable reducing-balance (WDV) data table in advanced_spreadsheet (is_array_formula + corner/center cell checks); (2) Impairment & Recoverable Amount uses logic_input for the IAS 36 mechanic - discounting cash flows to value-in-use, taking the higher of VIU and fair value less costs of disposal as recoverable amount, and computing the impairment loss; (3) Asset Register Interrogation uses sql over a seeded asset register to compute net book value per category for active assets only (the disposal/fully-depreciated exclusion is the discriminating trap). Every figure is GCC-denominated (AED), realistic, and pre-computed to deterministic master solutions. Master maths verified by script: shell capitalized AED 13.2m, total annual depreciation AED 680k, 3-year NBV AED 15.66m; impairment loss AED 1.30m (recoverable = FVLCD AED 8.2m > VIU AED 6.67m); WDV data-table corners 1,700,000 / 1,280,000 / 843,750; SQL Buildings NBV 11,160,000 leading the active-asset ranking.

**Skills:** 

**Engine fit:** Strong fit. Fixed Assets & Capital Accounting is one of the most quantitatively deterministic finance functions, so no soft-skill proxying was needed - every block measures a real arithmetic/standards-driven competency with an unambiguous numeric answer. Skill-to-engine mapping: Capitalization & Componentization → spreadsheet (which costs enter the asset's carrying amount under IAS 16 directly-attributable rules, then componentized lives) ; Depreciation Methods → spreadsheet straight-line roll-forward + advanced_spreadsheet 2-variable reducing-balance (WDV) data table (the array engine genuinely earns its place: a declining-balance NBV surface across rate × year is exactly a native 2-input data table) ; Impairment (IAS 36) → logic_input (discount to value-in-use, max(VIU, FVLCD), impairment loss - a chained calc where intermediate fields must reconcile) ; Asset Register & Verification + Disposals & Revaluation → sql (interrogate the register; the disposed/fully_depreciated WHERE-filter is the disposal-awareness discriminator). The only IAS 16 revaluation-model nuance that resists auto-grading (the qualitative OCI-vs-P&L reversal narrative) is deliberately out of scope; its quantitative core - the revalued carrying amount and depreciation on the uplift - is implicitly exercised through the depreciation and register blocks. No limitation flag required.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Capitalization & Depreciation Mechanics**

- **IAS 16 Componentized Capitalization & Depreciation Roll-Forward** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 18.3 min · ref: IAS 16 Property, Plant & Equipment / IMA CMA
  - _Measures:_ Applying IAS 16 directly-attributable-cost capitalization criteria (capitalize vs expense) and componentized straight-line depreciation with a multi-year NBV roll-forward.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Capital Holdings (Dubai) is capitalizing a new corporate HQ fit-out under IAS 16. The building shell has a purchase price of AED 12,000,000. The candidate must decide which of five further outlays enter the asset's carrying amount: site preparation AED 400,000 (capitalize - directly attributable), professional/architect fees AED 600,000 (capitalize), initial delivery & installation AED 200,000 (capitalize), staff training AED 150,000 (EXPENSE - not a cost of bringing the asset to working condition), and general administrative overhead AED 100,000 (EXPENSE). The asset is then componentized into three parts with separate useful lives (all nil residual, straight-line): Building shell (capitalized total / 40 years), MEP & HVAC AED 3,000,000 / 15 years, and Fit-out & finishes AED 1,500,000 / 10 years. The candidate completes the capitalized cost of the shell, each component's annual depreciation, total annual depreciation, and the net book value of the whole asset after 3 full years.
  - _Model answer:_ Shell capitalized cost = 12,000,000 + 400,000 + 600,000 + 200,000 = AED 13,200,000 (training and admin overhead are period expenses, excluded). Component depreciation: shell 13,200,000 / 40 = 330,000; MEP 3,000,000 / 15 = 200,000; fit-out 1,500,000 / 10 = 150,000; total annual = AED 680,000. Total componentized cost = 13,200,000 + 3,000,000 + 1,500,000 = 17,700,000; accumulated depreciation after 3 years = 3 × 680,000 = 2,040,000; NBV after 3 years = 17,700,000 - 2,040,000 = AED 15,660,000.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Shell capitalized cost = AED 13,200,000 (training & admin correctly expensed) - Capitalize-vs-expense judgement under IAS 16 directly-attributable rules
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Shell annual depreciation = AED 330,000 - Straight-line depreciation on the capitalized component over 40 years
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Total annual depreciation = AED 680,000 - Componentized depreciation summed across the three separate useful lives
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Net book value after 3 years = AED 15,660,000 - Multi-year NBV roll-forward (cost less accumulated depreciation)
- **Reducing-Balance (WDV) Depreciation Sensitivity Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: IAS 16 (diminishing-balance method) / AFP FPAC
  - _Measures:_ Building a native two-variable data table over a compounding reducing-balance depreciation formula - testing both array-engine fluency and correct WDV mechanics.
  - _Scenario:_ Qatar National Logistics depreciates a fleet of forklifts (cost AED 2,000,000, nil residual) on the reducing-balance (written-down-value) method and wants a sensitivity surface of closing net book value. The candidate first builds the single-cell closing-NBV engine formula = cost × (1 − rate)^year, then constructs a NATIVE two-variable data table with depreciation rate down the rows (15%, 20%, 25%) and elapsed years across the columns (1, 2, 3). The grid must be driven by a real data table, not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Closing NBV under WDV = cost × (1 − rate)^year. Base engine cell (rate 20%, year 3) = 2,000,000 × 0.8^3 = AED 1,024,000. Data table corners and centre: (15%, yr1) = 2,000,000 × 0.85 = 1,700,000; (20%, yr2) = 2,000,000 × 0.8^2 = 1,280,000; (25%, yr3) = 2,000,000 × 0.75^3 = 843,750. The candidate wires the row input cell to the rate and the column input cell to the year, and the {=TABLE()} array fills the 3×3 grid.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - 3x3 grid uses a native data table {=TABLE()} (not hardcoded values) - Array-engine fluency - genuine two-variable data table construction
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (rate 15%, year 1) = AED 1,700,000 - Reducing-balance NBV at the low-rate / first-year corner
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre (rate 20%, year 2) = AED 1,280,000 - Compounding WDV depreciation over two periods
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (rate 25%, year 3) = AED 843,750 - Reducing-balance NBV at the high-rate / third-year corner

**Pillar - Impairment & Recoverable Amount**

- **IAS 36 Impairment Test - Value in Use vs Fair Value** &nbsp; `Logic input` · advanced · 10 min · ref: IAS 36 Impairment of Assets
  - _Measures:_ Executing the IAS 36 impairment mechanic - discounting to value in use, selecting recoverable amount as max(VIU, FVLCD), and booking the impairment loss.
  - _Scenario:_ Riyadh Industrial Group is impairment-testing a cash-generating unit (CGU) with a carrying amount of AED 9,500,000. Management projects pre-discount cash flows of AED 1,800,000 (Yr1), 1,900,000 (Yr2), 2,000,000 (Yr3), 2,000,000 (Yr4) and 1,500,000 (Yr5, terminal year included), discounted at a pre-tax rate of 12%. The fair value of the CGU less costs of disposal (FVLCD) is AED 8,200,000. The candidate computes value in use (the discounted cash-flow sum), identifies the recoverable amount as the higher of VIU and FVLCD, and computes the resulting impairment loss and post-impairment carrying amount. The trap: VIU is LOWER than FVLCD, so recoverable amount must default to FVLCD, not VIU.
  - _Model answer:_ Value in use = 1,800,000/1.12 + 1,900,000/1.12^2 + 2,000,000/1.12^3 + 2,000,000/1.12^4 + 1,500,000/1.12^5 = AED 6,667,548 (rounded). Recoverable amount = max(VIU 6,667,548 ; FVLCD 8,200,000) = AED 8,200,000. Impairment loss = carrying amount − recoverable amount = 9,500,000 − 8,200,000 = AED 1,300,000. Post-impairment carrying amount = AED 8,200,000.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Value in use (discounted CF sum) ≈ AED 6,667,548 - Multi-period discounting of projected cash flows at 12%
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Recoverable amount = AED 8,200,000 (higher of VIU and FVLCD) - IAS 36 recoverable-amount rule - max(VIU, FVLCD), the key trap
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Impairment loss = AED 1,300,000 - Carrying amount less recoverable amount reconciles
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Post-impairment carrying amount = AED 8,200,000 - Asset written down to recoverable amount

**Pillar - Asset Register Interrogation**

- **Fixed Asset Register - Net Book Value by Category** &nbsp; `SQL` · basic · 10 min · ref: DAMA DMBOK / IAS 16 disclosure (PP&E by class)
  - _Measures:_ Asset-register interrogation - filtering on asset lifecycle status, computing net book value, and aggregating by category for disclosure.
  - _Scenario:_ A GCC manufacturer maintains its fixed asset register in a relational table asset_register (id, asset_code, category, cost, accum_depreciation, status), where status is one of 'active', 'disposed' or 'fully_depreciated'. The finance team needs net book value (cost minus accumulated depreciation) totalled per asset category for the IAS 16 PP&E disclosure - but ONLY for assets still active. Disposed and fully-depreciated assets must be excluded. The candidate writes one query returning category and total net book value, highest NBV first. The discriminating trap is the status filter: a query that omits the WHERE clause silently includes disposed and fully-depreciated assets and returns the wrong totals.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT category, SUM(cost - accum_depreciation) AS total_nbv FROM asset_register WHERE status = 'active' GROUP BY category ORDER BY total_nbv DESC, category. Expected ordered result over the seeded data: Buildings 11,160,000 ; Plant & Machinery 4,276,000 ; Fit-out 1,770,000 ; IT Equipment 340,000 ; Motor Vehicles 248,000. (The disposed IT asset and the fully-depreciated Buildings asset are correctly excluded by the status filter.)
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master: active-only NBV per category, highest first - Status filter + net-book-value computation + category aggregation + ordering

---

### 1.5 Inventory & Cost Accounting

Hands-on sandbox blueprint for Inventory & Cost Accounting (node 1.5), a quantitative finance function that fits the four auto-gradable engines almost perfectly. The function has no seeded skills, so six were proposed (inventory costing methods, NRV write-downs, standard costing variances, overhead absorption/CVP, inventory control analytics, cost-volume-profit). Designed as 3 pillars / 5 blocks using 4 engines: a moving-weighted-average perpetual ledger (spreadsheet), an IAS 2 lower-of-cost-or-NRV write-down calc (logic_input), standard-costing material/labour variances (logic_input), a 2-variable CVP/operating-profit data table (advanced_spreadsheet), and a slow-moving-stock value query (sql). All scenarios use concrete GCC entities and AED/SAR/QAR figures; every checkpoint is a numeric cell/field/result-set match grounded in IAS 2, IMA CMA/CIMA, and DAMA DMBOK. Matches FP&A reference rigor with fully reconciling master solutions.

**Skills:** Inventory Costing Methods (FIFO / Weighted Average, IAS 2) · NRV & Lower-of-Cost-or-NRV Write-downs (IAS 2) · Standard Costing & Variance Analysis (material / labour / overhead) · Overhead Absorption & Absorption-vs-Marginal Costing · Inventory Control Analytics (turnover / DIO, slow-moving, ABC, EOQ) · Cost-Volume-Profit & Contribution-Margin Analysis

**Engine fit:** Inventory & Cost Accounting is a strongly quantitative finance function and maps cleanly onto all four engines with no soft-skill proxying needed. Perpetual costing ledgers and CVP/break-even models are natural spreadsheet/advanced_spreadsheet work (cell_value + is_array_formula on a native 2-variable data table). NRV write-downs and standard-costing variances are deterministic formula chains ideal for logic_input (each component must reconcile to a total). Inventory control analytics - slow-moving stock, turnover, value-by-category - is exactly what sql_result_match grades over a seeded inventory_items table. The blueprint deliberately spans all four engines (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input x2, sql) so the sitting is varied. The only parts of the role NOT captured here are qualitative judgement calls (e.g. selecting a costing policy, writing a stock-count narrative, or justifying an impairment to auditors); those are inherently un-gradable by the four engines and are intentionally out of scope - the blueprint measures the computational core of the function, which is where demonstrated technical skill is objectively scorable.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 5 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Logic input, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Inventory Valuation & IFRS Compliance (IAS 2)**

- **Moving-Weighted-Average Perpetual Inventory Ledger** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: IAS 2 Inventories (Cost Formulas) / IMA CMA
  - _Measures:_ Applying the IAS 2 weighted-average cost formula in a perpetual system: recomputing the running average after each receipt, costing issues at the running average, and proving the ending-inventory roll-forward.
  - _Scenario:_ Gulf Steel Trading LLC (Dubai) runs a perpetual moving-weighted-average ledger for its TMT rebar SKU. The grid is pre-populated with the period's movements (all figures AED): Opening balance 200 units at AED 50.00 (value 10,000). Movement 1 - Purchase 300 units at AED 55.00 (value 16,500). Movement 2 - Issue/Sale 400 units. Movement 3 - Purchase 400 units at AED 60.00 (value 24,000). Movement 4 - Issue/Sale 350 units. Under the moving-average method the unit cost is recomputed after every purchase and issues are costed at that running average. Complete the running average cost, the COGS of each issue, total COGS for the period, and the ending inventory value so the ledger fully reconciles (ending value = opening value + purchases - total COGS).
  - _Model answer:_ After Purchase 1: balance value 10,000+16,500=26,500 over 500 units => avg 53.00. Issue 1 COGS = 400 x 53.00 = 21,200; balance value 26,500-21,200=5,300 (100 units @ 53.00). After Purchase 2: value 5,300+24,000=29,300 over 500 units => avg 58.60 (B-checkpoint). Issue 2 COGS = 350 x 58.60 = 20,510; ending value 29,300-20,510=8,790 (150 units @ 58.60). Total COGS = 21,200+20,510 = 41,710. Roll-forward check: 10,000 + 16,500 + 24,000 - 41,710 = 8,790 = ending inventory value.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Running average cost after Purchase 2 = 58.60 - Weighted-average unit cost recomputed correctly on the second receipt
    - `cell_value` (w2) - COGS of Issue 1 = 21,200 (400 x 53.00) - First issue costed at the post-Purchase-1 running average
    - `cell_value` (w2) - COGS of Issue 2 = 20,510 (350 x 58.60) - Second issue costed at the post-Purchase-2 running average
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total period COGS = 41,710 - Aggregation of both issues' cost of goods sold
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Ending inventory value = 8,790 - Closing balance reconciles to the opening + purchases - COGS roll-forward
- **Year-End Lower-of-Cost-or-NRV Write-down** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 9 min · ref: IAS 2 Inventories (Net Realisable Value)
  - _Measures:_ Applying the IAS 2 lower-of-cost-or-NRV rule item-by-item: computing NRV from selling price net of completion and selling costs, recognising write-downs only where cost exceeds NRV, and rolling up the carrying value.
  - _Scenario:_ Tadawi Electronics Distribution (Riyadh) is closing its year-end stock and must write inventory down to the lower of cost and net realisable value per IAS 2. NRV = estimated selling price - costs to complete - costs to sell. For each SKU compute the per-unit and total write-down, then the total balance-sheet carrying value. Figures in SAR. SKU-A: qty 500, unit cost 120, selling price 140, cost to sell 8 (no completion cost). SKU-B: qty 300, unit cost 200, selling price 190, cost to sell 15. SKU-C: qty 400, unit cost 90, selling price 100, cost to complete 12, cost to sell 6.
  - _Model answer:_ SKU-A NRV = 140-8 = 132 > cost 120 => no write-down (0). SKU-B NRV = 190-15 = 175 < cost 200 => write-down 25/unit x 300 = 7,500. SKU-C NRV = 100-12-6 = 82 < cost 90 => write-down 8/unit x 400 = 3,200. Total write-down = 0+7,500+3,200 = 10,700. Carrying value at lower of cost or NRV = (120x500)+(175x300)+(82x400) = 60,000+52,500+32,800 = 145,300.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - SKU-B write-down = 7,500 - NRV below cost triggers a write-down of (cost-NRV) x qty
    - `logic_value` (w3) - SKU-C write-down = 3,200 - NRV correctly nets both completion and selling costs before comparison
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total write-down = 10,700 - Write-downs aggregated (SKU-A correctly contributes zero)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total carrying value = 145,300 - Balance-sheet inventory stated at the lower of cost and NRV per SKU

**Pillar - Cost Accounting & Variance Diagnostics**

- **Standard Costing - Material & Labour Variances** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 12 min · ref: IMA CMA / CIMA Management Accounting (Standard Costing)
  - _Measures:_ Decomposing total cost variances into price/rate and usage/efficiency components using standard equations, deriving actual price/rate from totals, and proving the variances reconcile.
  - _Scenario:_ Al-Khaleej Cement Products (Jeddah) operates a standard-costing system for its 50 kg bag line. Standard cost per bag: direct material 25 kg at SAR 2.00/kg; direct labour 0.50 hours at SAR 40.00/hour. During the period it produced 10,000 bags. Actual direct material used was 260,000 kg costing SAR 533,000 in total. Actual direct labour was 5,200 hours costing SAR 218,400 in total. Compute the four classic variances and a reconciling total. Use the convention that adverse variances are NEGATIVE and favourable are positive.
  - _Model answer:_ Actual material price = 533,000/260,000 = 2.05/kg; standard qty allowed SQ = 10,000 x 25 = 250,000 kg. Material Price Variance = (SP-AP) x AQ = (2.00-2.05) x 260,000 = -13,000 (adverse). Material Usage Variance = (SQ-AQ) x SP = (250,000-260,000) x 2.00 = -20,000 (adverse). Actual labour rate = 218,400/5,200 = 42.00/hr; standard hours allowed SH = 10,000 x 0.50 = 5,000 hrs. Labour Rate Variance = (SR-AR) x AH = (40-42) x 5,200 = -10,400 (adverse). Labour Efficiency Variance = (SH-AH) x SR = (5,000-5,200) x 40 = -8,000 (adverse). Total = -13,000-20,000-10,400-8,000 = -51,400.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Material Price Variance = -13,000 - (Std price - actual price) x actual quantity; actual price derived from total cost
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Material Usage Variance = -20,000 - (Std qty allowed for output - actual qty) x std price; SQ flexed to 10,000 bags
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Labour Rate Variance = -10,400 - (Std rate - actual rate) x actual hours; actual rate derived from total cost
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Labour Efficiency Variance = -8,000 - (Std hours allowed for output - actual hours) x std rate
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Total variance = -51,400 - Four variances reconcile to the total material + labour cost variance
- **Cost-Volume-Profit Two-Variable Sensitivity Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: CIMA / IMA CMA (CVP & Marginal Costing)
  - _Measures:_ Building a marginal-costing CVP model and a native two-variable data table (Excel/Sheets data-table array) to read operating profit across price and volume - demonstrating contribution-margin logic and array-driven sensitivity construction.
  - _Scenario:_ Bahr Bottled Water Co (Abu Dhabi) wants to stress-test monthly operating profit on its 500 ml line. Base model (AED): selling price/unit 3.00, variable cost/unit 1.20, units sold/month 200,000, fixed cost/month 250,000. Operating Profit = (Price - VarCost) x Units - Fixed. Build the base operating-profit formula, then a NATIVE two-variable data table of operating profit across selling price (columns: 2.80, 3.00, 3.20) and units sold (rows: 180,000, 200,000, 220,000). The corner cell must link to the base operating-profit formula; the body must be a real data table, not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Base operating profit = (3.00-1.20) x 200,000 - 250,000 = 1.80 x 200,000 - 250,000 = 110,000. Data table corner links to the base cell. Low corner (Price 2.80, Units 180,000) = (2.80-1.20) x 180,000 - 250,000 = 1.60 x 180,000 - 250,000 = 38,000. Centre (Price 3.00, Units 200,000) = 110,000. High corner (Price 3.20, Units 220,000) = (3.20-1.20) x 220,000 - 250,000 = 2.00 x 220,000 - 250,000 = 190,000. Column input = selling price cell, row input = units cell.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Body C9:E11 is a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - Sensitivity grid is array/data-table driven, recomputing via the model
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Base operating profit = 110,000 - Contribution-margin CVP formula (Price-VarCost) x Units - Fixed
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (Price 2.80, Units 180,000) = 38,000 - Data table recomputes profit at the lowest price/volume combination
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre (Price 3.00, Units 200,000) = 110,000 - Data table reproduces the base case at the centre cell
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (Price 3.20, Units 220,000) = 190,000 - Data table recomputes profit at the highest price/volume combination

**Pillar - Inventory Data Interrogation & Control Analytics**

- **Slow-Moving Stock Value by Category (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA International (DMBOK) / IMA Inventory Analytics
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating an inventory ledger with a filtered grouped aggregation: applying a slow-moving threshold, computing extended stock value, grouping by category, and ordering by value descending - the core query behind inventory-control and obsolescence analytics.
  - _Scenario:_ Souq Distribution Co (Doha) keeps an inventory_items table for its FMCG warehouse (columns: id, sku, category, on_hand_qty, unit_cost, units_sold_ytd; all values QAR). The controller wants to surface slow-moving capital tied up in stock. Write ONE query that returns, for slow-moving items only (units_sold_ytd < 100), the total on-hand stock value per category, highest value first. Stock value = on_hand_qty x unit_cost. Output columns: category, stock_value.
  - _Model answer:_ Filter to units_sold_ytd < 100 (qualifying rows: Beverages SKU-002 800x8=6,400; Snacks SKU-003 1000x5=5,000 + SKU-008 700x4=2,800 = 7,800; Dairy SKU-005 400x15=6,000; Frozen SKU-007 300x25=7,500). GROUP BY category, SUM(on_hand_qty*unit_cost), ORDER BY stock_value DESC. Master query: SELECT category, SUM(on_hand_qty * unit_cost) AS stock_value FROM inventory_items WHERE units_sold_ytd < 100 GROUP BY category ORDER BY stock_value DESC, category. Result (ordered): Snacks 7,800; Frozen 7,500; Beverages 6,400; Dairy 6,000.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master (slow-moving stock value per category, value-descending) - Correct WHERE filter, extended-value SUM, GROUP BY category, and descending order

---

### 1.6 Payroll Operations & Tax Compliance

Hands-on sandbox for Payroll Operations & Tax Compliance, designed to the function's five skills (payroll processing & controls, GOSI/WPS statutory deductions, end-of-service & benefits, payroll reconciliation, time & attendance integration). Payroll is a strongly quantitative function, so all four engines fit cleanly with no soft-skill proxying required. Three pillars, four blocks, three engines (spreadsheet, logic_input, advanced_spreadsheet, sql) at mixed difficulty. Pillar 1 builds a GCC gross-to-net payroll register with GOSI deductions and the WPS control total (spreadsheet). Pillar 2 covers the high-stakes statutory settlement math: UAE end-of-service gratuity under Federal Decree-Law 33/2021 with the 21/30-day tiers and 2-year cap (logic_input), then a two-variable gratuity-liability sensitivity data table across tenure and salary axes (advanced_spreadsheet). Pillar 3 reconciles a payroll ledger and surfaces a WPS/over-deduction control breach via SQL. All statutory rates and day-factors are stated in-scenario so grading tests demonstrated computation against fixed rates, not recall of a moving regulatory target (GOSI rates were reformed July 2025 into tiered new-hire vs legacy schedules; the blueprint uses the documented legacy Saudi-national 9.75%+11.75% split and the 2% non-Saudi occupational-hazard rate, both given in the prompt).

**Skills:** Payroll Processing & Controls · Statutory Deductions (GOSI/WPS) · End-of-Service & Benefits · Payroll Reconciliation · Time & Attendance Integration

**Engine fit:** Payroll Operations is intrinsically numeric and rules-driven, so it is an excellent fit for all four auto-gradable engines with no need to carve out a "quantitative slice" of a soft function. spreadsheet handles the gross-to-net register (allowances, GOSI deductions, net pay, WPS-payable control total) where every cell is a deterministic arithmetic result. logic_input handles the end-of-service gratuity settlement, which is a closed-form statutory calculation with named intermediate fields (per-tier day-counts, daily wage, capped liability) that reconcile to a final payable. advanced_spreadsheet handles a two-variable gratuity-liability sensitivity table (tenure x final salary), which genuinely requires a native data table / array formula rather than hardcoded cells. sql handles payroll-ledger reconciliation and control-breach detection (per-department cost rollups, catching an employee whose total statutory deduction exceeds the legal ceiling) against a seeded relational ledger. The only payroll competencies that are NOT directly gradable here are the qualitative judgement parts (e.g. interpreting an ambiguous labour-law edge case, designing a controls policy narrative); those are intentionally out of scope for the auto-graded sandbox and would sit in the MCQ layer or human review. Time & Attendance Integration is covered indirectly inside Block 1 (overtime/unpaid-leave proration feeding gross pay) rather than as a standalone block, since attendance is only gradable once it resolves to a numeric pay figure.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Logic input, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Gross-to-Net Payroll Processing & Controls**

- **GCC Monthly Payroll Register & WPS Control Total** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: Saudi GOSI Social Insurance Law / SAMA WPS (Wage Protection System) / IMA Payroll Control Standards
  - _Measures:_ Building a multi-employee gross-to-net payroll register: correct GOSI base scoping (basic+housing only), nationality-conditional employee deductions, attendance-driven proration, and rolling up the WPS control total that must reconcile to the bank file.
  - _Scenario:_ Al-Faisaliah Trading Co (Riyadh, KSA) is running its March payroll for a 4-employee cohort using the legacy GOSI split stated below. The register (SAR) has: Basic Salary, Housing Allowance, Transport Allowance, Overtime (already proration-adjusted from the time & attendance feed), and an Unpaid-Leave deduction. Gross Earnings = Basic + Housing + Transport + Overtime - Unpaid-Leave. GOSI is levied ONLY on the GOSI base = Basic + Housing (allowances/overtime excluded), capped at a SAR 45,000 base ceiling. For Saudi nationals the employee GOSI rate is 9.75% and the employer rate is 11.75%; for non-Saudi nationals there is NO employee deduction and the employer pays 2% occupational hazard only. Net Pay = Gross Earnings - Employee GOSI. The WPS-payable total is the sum of all employees' Net Pay (this is the figure that must hit the SAMA WPS file). Given rows: E1 Ahmed Al-Saud (Saudi) Basic 20000 Housing 5000 Transport 800 OT 1200 UnpaidLeave 0; E2 Fatima Al-Harbi (Saudi) Basic 12000 Housing 3000 Transport 800 OT 0 UnpaidLeave 1500; E3 Rajesh Kumar (non-Saudi) Basic 9000 Housing 2000 Transport 600 OT 900 UnpaidLeave 0; E4 Maria Santos (non-Saudi) Basic 7000 Housing 1500 Transport 600 OT 0 UnpaidLeave 700. Complete the GOSI base, employee GOSI deduction, net pay per employee, and the WPS-payable control total.
  - _Model answer:_ Per employee: GOSI base = Basic + Housing (no ceiling binds here since max base = 25,000 < 45,000). Employee GOSI = base x 9.75% for Saudis, 0 for non-Saudis. Gross = Basic+Housing+Transport+OT-UnpaidLeave. Net = Gross - Employee GOSI. E1: base 25000, empGOSI 2437.5, gross 27000, net 24562.5. E2: base 15000, empGOSI 1462.5, gross 14300, net 12837.5. E3: base 11000, empGOSI 0, gross 12500, net 12500. E4: base 8500, empGOSI 0, gross 8700, net 8700. WPS-payable = 24562.5 + 12837.5 + 12500 + 8700 = 58600.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - E1 employee GOSI = 2437.5 (Saudi, 9.75% of basic+housing) - Correct GOSI base scoping + Saudi employee rate
    - `cell_value` (w1) - E1 net pay = 24562.5 - Gross-to-net chain for a Saudi national with overtime
    - `cell_value` (w2) - E2 net pay = 12837.5 (unpaid leave applied) - Attendance/unpaid-leave proration feeding net pay
    - `cell_value` (w2) - E3 employee GOSI = 0 (non-Saudi: no employee deduction) - Nationality-conditional deduction logic
    - `cell_value` (w1) - E4 net pay = 8700 (non-Saudi, unpaid leave) - Non-Saudi gross-to-net with attendance adjustment
    - `cell_value` (w3) - WPS-payable control total = 58600 - Cohort net-pay rollup reconciling to the WPS bank file

**Pillar - Statutory Settlements & End-of-Service Benefits**
