- **UAE End-of-Service Gratuity Settlement (Decree-Law 33/2021)** &nbsp; `Logic input` · advanced · 10 min · ref: UAE Federal Decree-Law No. 33 of 2021 (Labour Law), Art. 51 - End-of-Service Gratuity
  - _Measures:_ End-of-service gratuity computation under current UAE labour law: tiered day-factors (21 vs 30 days), pro-rata fractional years, daily-wage derivation, and the statutory 2-year-wage cap test - the single most error-prone, highest-liability payroll settlement calc in the GCC.
  - _Scenario:_ An employee at Emirates Gulf Logistics (Dubai) resigns after completing exactly 7.5 years of continuous unlimited-term service. Final basic salary (gratuity is computed on BASIC only, excluding allowances) is AED 18,000/month. Apply UAE Decree-Law 33/2021: for the FIRST 5 years of service the gratuity accrues at 21 days of basic wage per year; for EACH year BEYOND 5 years it accrues at 30 days of basic wage per year; fractional years are paid pro-rata. The total gratuity is capped at 2 years' total basic wage (i.e. 24 months of basic). Convert a daily wage as monthly basic / 30. Compute: (1) daily wage, (2) gratuity earned for the first 5 years, (3) gratuity earned for the years beyond 5 (the 2.5 remaining years), (4) total gratuity before the cap, and (5) the final payable after applying the 2-year cap.
  - _Model answer:_ Daily wage = 18000 / 30 = 600. First-5-years gratuity = 5 years x 21 days x 600 = 63000. Beyond-5 portion = 2.5 years x 30 days x 600 = 45000. Total before cap = 63000 + 45000 = 108000. Cap = 24 months x 18000 = 432000; total (108000) < cap, so final payable = 108000 (cap does not bind).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Daily wage = 600 - Daily-wage derivation (monthly basic / 30)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - First-5-years gratuity = 63000 - 21-day-per-year tier applied to first 5 years
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Beyond-5-years gratuity = 45000 (2.5 yrs x 30 days) - 30-day tier + pro-rata fractional-year handling
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total before cap = 108000 - Two-tier accrual reconciles to the gross gratuity
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Final payable after 2-year cap = 108000 - Correct cap test (recognising the cap does not bind here)
- **Gratuity Liability Sensitivity Matrix (Tenure x Final Salary)** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: IAS 19 Employee Benefits (end-of-service provisioning) / UAE Decree-Law 33/2021
  - _Measures:_ Scenario provisioning of end-of-service liability with a native two-variable data table - the spreadsheet-engineering skill that lets payroll/finance stress a gratuity accrual across tenure and pay assumptions without rebuilding the formula per cell.
  - _Scenario:_ The finance team at Emirates Gulf Logistics must provision the end-of-service liability for a senior hire across a range of scenarios for the IAS 19 accrual. Build a two-variable data table of total gratuity (AED, before the 2-year cap) where rows = years of service {3, 6, 9} and columns = final monthly basic salary {15000, 20000, 25000}. The driver cell computes gratuity using the same UAE rule as the settlement block: daily wage = monthly basic / 30; first 5 years at 21 days/year; each year beyond 5 at 30 days/year; pro-rata fractions. The table MUST be produced with a native two-variable data table (array formula) driven off the single gratuity formula cell - not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Driver gratuity formula g(yrs, basic): daily = basic/30; first = MIN(yrs,5)*21*daily; beyond = MAX(yrs-5,0)*30*daily; total = first + beyond. Corner/interior values: (3 yrs,15000): daily 500, first 3*21*500=31500, beyond 0 => 31500. (3,25000): daily 833.33, 3*21*833.33=52500 => 52500. (6,15000): daily 500, first 5*21*500=52500, beyond 1*30*500=15000 => 67500. (6,20000): daily 666.67, first 70000, beyond 20000 => 90000. (9,25000): daily 833.33, first 5*21*833.33=87500, beyond 4*30*833.33=100000 => 187500. The data table range must be array-formula driven.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sensitivity grid uses a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - Genuine array/data-table engineering, not manual cell entry
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Driver gratuity cell = 90000 (base case: 6 yrs, AED 20000) - The single gratuity formula the table is driven from
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (3 yrs, 15000) = 31500 - Sub-5-year, single-tier corner of the matrix
    - `cell_value` (w2) - High corner (9 yrs, 25000) = 187500 - Two-tier accrual at the top corner of the matrix
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Interior (6 yrs, 15000) = 67500 - Cross-tier interior cell (5 yrs at 21d + 1 yr at 30d)

**Pillar - Payroll Reconciliation & Cost Interrogation**

- **Payroll Ledger Reconciliation & Deduction-Ceiling Breach** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: Saudi GOSI Social Insurance Law / DAMA DMBOK (data interrogation) / payroll control reconciliation
  - _Measures:_ Payroll-ledger interrogation for control assurance: deriving total deductions, applying a percentage ceiling threshold in a WHERE clause, and ranking breaches - the SQL competency a payroll controller uses to catch over-deductions before the WPS release.
  - _Scenario:_ You are reconciling Al-Faisaliah Trading Co's payroll run against the statutory deduction ceiling. A table payroll_lines(id int, employee text, department text, nationality text, gross_pay numeric, gosi_employee numeric, other_deductions numeric, net_pay numeric) holds one row per employee. Policy control: an employee's TOTAL deductions (gosi_employee + other_deductions) must never exceed 35% of gross_pay - any row above that is a control breach to be escalated before the WPS file is released. Write ONE query that returns every breaching employee with the columns employee, department, gross_pay, and total_deductions (= gosi_employee + other_deductions), ordered by total_deductions highest first, then employee. Seed rows: (1,'Ahmed Al-Saud','Sales','Saudi',27000,2437.5,1500,23062.5),(2,'Fatima Al-Harbi','Sales','Saudi',14300,1462.5,800,12037.5),(3,'Rajesh Kumar','Ops','non-Saudi',12500,0,5000,7500),(4,'Maria Santos','Ops','non-Saudi',8700,0,3200,5500),(5,'Khalid Al-Otaibi','Finance','Saudi',16000,1560,4500,9940),(6,'Sara Mansour','Finance','Saudi',9000,877.5,2600,5522.5).
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT employee, department, gross_pay, gosi_employee + other_deductions AS total_deductions FROM payroll_lines WHERE (gosi_employee + other_deductions) > 0.35 * gross_pay ORDER BY total_deductions DESC, employee. Breach test per row: E3 Rajesh 5000/12500 = 40.0% (breach, total 5000); E4 Maria 3200/8700 = 36.8% (breach, total 3200); E5 Khalid 6060/16000 = 37.9% (breach, total 6060); E6 Sara 3477.5/9000 = 38.6% (breach, total 3477.5). E1 13.1% and E2 15.8% pass. Result ordered by total_deductions desc: Khalid 6060, Rajesh 5000, Sara 3477.5, Maria 3200.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Returns exactly the 4 breaching employees with correct total_deductions, ordered highest first - Threshold filter (>35% of gross), total-deduction derivation, and ranking all correct

---

### 1.8 Treasury & Cash Management

Treasury & Cash Management is a strongly quantitative finance function and an excellent fit for all four sandbox engines. The blueprint measures demonstrated treasury skill across three pillars: (1) Liquidity & Cash Forecasting — a direct rolling cash-flow forecast that derives closing balances and the peak funding shortfall against a minimum operating buffer (spreadsheet), plus a two-variable funding-cost data table flexing facility drawdown against interest rate (advanced_spreadsheet); (2) Market Risk Quantification — FX hedge valuation (spot vs forward) and interest-rate-shock interest impact on floating debt (logic_input); (3) Banking Data Interrogation — a cleared bank cash-position aggregation across a multi-bank account ledger (sql). Every block uses concrete GCC figures (AED, real GCC bank names, EIBOR) and maps to recognized treasury standards (AFP/CTP, ACT, Basel III LCR, ISO 20022, IFRS 9). No free text, drafting, or judgement is graded — only computed numeric values, native array formulas, and SQL result sets.

**Skills:** Cash & Liquidity Management · FX Risk Management · Interest-Rate Risk · Funding & Capital Markets · Bank Relationship Management · Cash Forecasting

**Engine fit:** Treasury & Cash Management is intrinsically quantitative, so all four engines map cleanly with no soft-skill proxy needed. Cash & Liquidity Management and Cash Forecasting are tested via a direct rolling cash-flow model in the spreadsheet engine (period-by-period net cash, closing-balance roll-forward, and peak funding shortfall vs a minimum buffer — all exact cell_value checks). Funding & Capital Markets is tested via an advanced_spreadsheet two-variable data table that flexes facility drawdown against interest rate to produce annual funding cost (is_array_formula plus corner/interior cell_values — defeats hardcoding). FX Risk Management and Interest-Rate Risk are tested via logic_input fields: unhedged vs forward-hedged AED value of a USD receivable, the resulting hedge cost, and the annual incremental interest from an EIBOR shock on floating debt (logic_value checks that reconcile). Bank Relationship Management / liquidity-position monitoring is tested via SQL aggregating cleared balances per bank across a multi-account ledger (sql_result_match, order-sensitive). The only treasury skills that are NOT directly gradable here are the qualitative relationship/negotiation aspects of Bank Relationship Management (covering ratios, RFP scoring, and counterparty-limit math ARE captured numerically, but soft negotiation is not) — these are out of scope for any auto-grader and would belong to a separate behavioural assessment.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Liquidity & Cash Forecasting**

- **Rolling Direct Cash-Flow Forecast & Funding Shortfall** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: AFP Certified Treasury Professional (CTP) / Association of Corporate Treasurers (ACT)
  - _Measures:_ Building a direct cash forecast: deriving net cash movement per period, rolling closing balances forward across periods, and sizing the peak liquidity shortfall against a minimum operating buffer.
  - _Scenario:_ VIFM Logistics LLC (Dubai) runs a 3-month direct (receipts-and-disbursements) cash forecast in AED 000s. Opening cash for Month 1 is 5,000. Monthly collections are 12,400 / 14,200 / 16,800; operating disbursements (AP & opex) are 9,800 / 10,500 / 11,200; payroll (WPS) is 3,200 / 3,200 / 3,400; capex is 1,500 / 800 / 2,000. The Board mandates a minimum operating cash buffer of 3,000. The candidate must compute each month's net cash movement, roll the closing balance into the next month's opening, and quantify the peak funding shortfall (the largest amount by which any month's closing cash falls below the 3,000 buffer) so Treasury can size the revolving credit facility (RCF) drawdown.
  - _Model answer:_ Net movement per month = collections − operating disbursements − payroll − capex. M1: 12,400 − 9,800 − 3,200 − 1,500 = −2,100; closing = 5,000 − 2,100 = 2,900. M2: 14,200 − 10,500 − 3,200 − 800 = −300; closing = 2,900 − 300 = 2,600. M3: 16,800 − 11,200 − 3,400 − 2,000 = +200; closing = 2,600 + 200 = 2,800. Shortfall per month = MAX(0, 3,000 − closing): M1 = 100, M2 = 400, M3 = 200. Peak funding shortfall (RCF sizing) = MAX of the three = 400.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Month 1 net cash movement = −2,100 - Correct period net cash movement from collections less all disbursements (collections − opex − payroll − capex).
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Month 1 closing cash = 2,900 - Closing balance derived from opening plus net movement.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Month 2 closing cash = 2,600 (opening rolled from M1) - Closing balance roll-forward: prior month's closing becomes current opening.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Month 3 closing cash = 2,800 - Full multi-period chain holds and the positive M3 movement is applied correctly.
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Peak funding shortfall vs 3,000 buffer = 400 - Largest amount by which any month's closing cash falls below the minimum operating buffer (RCF sizing).
- **Funding-Cost Sensitivity Data Table (Drawdown × Rate)** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: AFP FP&A / ACT Treasury Risk Management; Basel III liquidity framework
  - _Measures:_ Constructing a native two-variable sensitivity (data) table to stress annual funding cost across facility size and interest rate — funding/capital-markets cost analysis under uncertainty.
  - _Scenario:_ VIFM Logistics is negotiating a committed revolving credit facility with Emirates NBD. The base case draws AED 50,000 (000s) at an all-in rate of 5.5%, giving annual funding cost = drawn × rate. Treasury must stress the annual interest cost across a two-way grid: facility drawdown of 40,000 / 50,000 / 60,000 (row inputs) against all-in rates of 4.5% / 5.5% / 6.5% (column inputs). The candidate must build a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded figures) so the cost surface recalculates if the base model changes.
  - _Model answer:_ Base funding cost formula = drawn × rate = 50,000 × 0.055 = 2,750. The data table corner cell links to that base formula; Excel/engine substitutes each row value into the drawdown input and each column value into the rate input. Low corner (drawn 40,000, rate 4.5%) = 40,000 × 0.045 = 1,800. Base/centre (50,000, 5.5%) = 2,750. High corner (60,000, 6.5%) = 60,000 × 0.065 = 3,900. The grid must be produced by a native {=TABLE()} array, not typed numbers.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Cost grid uses a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - The 3×3 sensitivity grid is formula-driven via a native data-table array, not manually typed values.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Base annual funding cost = 2,750 - Base-case funding cost formula drawn × rate is correct (50,000 × 5.5%).
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (40,000 @ 4.5%) = 1,800 - Data table correctly substitutes the minimum drawdown and lowest rate.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre (50,000 @ 5.5%) = 2,750 - Interior cell of the data table equals the base case.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (60,000 @ 6.5%) = 3,900 - Data table correctly substitutes the maximum drawdown and highest rate.

**Pillar - Market Risk Quantification (FX & Interest Rate)**

- **FX Hedge Valuation & Interest-Rate Shock Impact** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: IFRS 9 Hedge Accounting / ACT FX & Interest-Rate Risk; CFA derivatives
  - _Measures:_ Quantifying FX transaction exposure (spot vs forward hedge valuation and hedge cost) and interest-rate risk (annual interest impact of a rate shock on floating-rate debt).
  - _Scenario:_ VIFM Trading FZE has a USD 8,000,000 receivable due in 90 days and floating-rate debt of AED 200,000,000 priced at 3-month EIBOR + 150 bps. The current spot is AED/USD 3.6725 and the 90-day outright forward is 3.6680. The candidate must value the receivable unhedged at spot, value it hedged via the forward, quantify the AED hedge cost (the give-up from locking the forward vs spot), and quantify the annual incremental interest if EIBOR rises by 75 bps. All four figures must reconcile to the underlying exposures.
  - _Model answer:_ Unhedged AED value = 8,000,000 × 3.6725 = 29,380,000. Forward-hedged AED value = 8,000,000 × 3.6680 = 29,344,000. Hedge cost (forward give-up vs spot) = 29,380,000 − 29,344,000 = 36,000 AED. Interest-rate shock: incremental annual interest = floating principal × rate change = 200,000,000 × 0.0075 = 1,500,000 AED. (Only the +75 bps moves the interest; the 150 bps spread is unchanged so it does not enter the delta.)
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Unhedged value at spot = 29,380,000 AED - USD receivable translated at spot AED/USD (8,000,000 × 3.6725).
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Forward-hedged value = 29,344,000 AED - USD receivable locked at the 90-day outright forward (8,000,000 × 3.6680).
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Hedge cost (forward vs spot) = 36,000 AED - The AED give-up from hedging = unhedged spot value − forward-locked value; reconciles the two valuations.
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Annual interest impact of +75 bps EIBOR = 1,500,000 AED - Interest-rate sensitivity on floating debt: principal × rate change (200,000,000 × 0.75%), spread excluded from the delta.

**Pillar - Banking Data Interrogation**

- **Consolidated Cleared Cash Position by Bank** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: ISO 20022 cash reporting (camt) / AFP CTP bank-relationship & liquidity reporting
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating a multi-bank account ledger to produce a consolidated cleared cash position per bank with correct filtering, aggregation, and ranking (bank-relationship / liquidity concentration monitoring).
  - _Scenario:_ VIFM Holding maintains accounts across four GCC banks. The bank_accounts ledger holds one row per balance line (bank, currency, balance_aed, status) where status is 'cleared' or 'pending'. To produce the daily group cash position, Treasury reports only CLEARED balances, totalled per bank, ranked from the largest cash holding to the smallest so concentration vs counterparty limits can be reviewed. Pending items must be excluded. Seed: ENBD cleared 4,200 + 1,800 (and a pending 900); FAB cleared 5,400; ADCB cleared 3,500 (and a pending 600); Mashreq cleared 2,100 + 700.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT bank, SUM(balance_aed) AS total FROM bank_accounts WHERE status = 'cleared' GROUP BY bank ORDER BY total DESC, bank. The WHERE clause drops the two pending rows (ENBD 900, ADCB 600); SUM aggregates per bank; ORDER BY total DESC ranks largest first. Expected result set: ENBD 6,000; FAB 5,400; ADCB 3,500; Mashreq 2,800.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Per-bank cleared totals, largest first, pending excluded - Result set matches the master: cleared-only filtering, correct per-bank SUM, and descending rank by total (ENBD 6000, FAB 5400, ADCB 3500, Mashreq 2800).

---

### 1.9 Investment Management & Capital Allocation

Blueprint for Investment Management & Capital Allocation (node 1.9, finance). The function's skills list was empty, so six skills were proposed grounded in GCC/MENA institutional-investor and corporate-treasury practice: Capital Budgeting & Project Appraisal (NPV/IRR/payback), Cost of Capital & Hurdle-Rate Setting (WACC/CAPM), Portfolio Construction & Asset Allocation, Risk-Adjusted Return Analytics (Sharpe/Sortino/alpha), Capital Rationing & Allocation Optimization, and Performance Attribution & Investment Reporting. The function is strongly quantitative, so all four engines fit cleanly. Design = 3 pillars / 4 blocks using 4 distinct engines: (1) Capital Budgeting & Project Appraisal — a spreadsheet DCF/NPV-IRR model for a Saudi real-estate development; (2) Cost of Capital & Risk-Return Analytics — a logic_input WACC+CAPM build and an advanced_spreadsheet two-variable NPV sensitivity data table over WACC x terminal growth; (3) Portfolio & Capital-Allocation Data Interrogation — a SQL block ranking a sovereign-wealth-style holdings ledger by unrealized gain. Difficulty mixes intermediate/advanced/intermediate across the sitting. Frameworks: CFA Institute curriculum (cost of capital, equity/portfolio), IMA CMA Part 2 (capital budgeting), AFP/FPAC, AAOIFI noted where Sharia-screened mandates are relevant, DAMA DMBOK for the data block.

**Skills:** Capital Budgeting & Project Appraisal (NPV / IRR / Payback) · Cost of Capital & Hurdle-Rate Setting (WACC / CAPM) · Portfolio Construction & Strategic Asset Allocation · Risk-Adjusted Return Analytics (Sharpe / Sortino / Alpha) · Capital Rationing & Allocation Optimization · Performance Attribution & Investment Reporting

**Engine fit:** Investment Management & Capital Allocation is a strongly quantitative function and maps cleanly to all four engines with no soft-skill compromise. Capital budgeting (discounted cash flows, NPV, IRR, MIRR, payback) is native spreadsheet work graded by exact cell values; cost-of-capital and risk-adjusted-return formulas (WACC, CAPM, Sharpe) are deterministic single-answer computations ideal for logic_input numeric fields; NPV sensitivity to WACC x terminal-growth is a textbook two-variable data table, the canonical advanced_spreadsheet array case; and an investment-holdings / capital-allocation ledger is a natural relational SQL target (unrealized gain per asset class, allocation drift vs policy bands). The only judgement-heavy slivers of the role — investment thesis narrative, manager-selection due diligence, IPS drafting — are deliberately excluded as ungradable free text; the blueprint measures the quantitative engine that underpins those decisions (the appraisal model, the hurdle rate, the risk-return screen, the allocation query) rather than the written recommendation. Full coverage across all 4 engines; no proxy/limitation flag required.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Logic input, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Capital Budgeting & Project Appraisal**

- **Discounted Cash Flow & NPV/IRR Investment Decision Model** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · advanced · 20 min · ref: IMA CMA Part 2 (Investment Decisions) / CFA Institute Corporate Finance
  - _Measures:_ Constructing a period-by-period DCF schedule and deriving the core appraisal metrics (NPV at a given WACC and IRR) that drive an accept/reject capital-allocation decision.
  - _Scenario:_ Emaar-style developer Al Rabwah Development (KSA) is appraising a 5-year mixed-use project in Riyadh. Initial capital outlay is SAR 50,000 (000s) at t0. Project free cash flows (SAR 000s) are: Year 1 = 12,000; Year 2 = 15,000; Year 3 = 18,000; Year 4 = 20,000; Year 5 = 22,000 (Year 5 includes a terminal/exit inflow). The investment committee hurdle rate (WACC) is 11%. The candidate must build the discounting schedule, then compute NPV, the cumulative discounted-cash-flow line, discounted payback inputs, and the project IRR, to support an accept/reject vs the 11% hurdle.
  - _Model answer:_ Discount factor each year DF_t = 1/(1.11^t): DF1=0.900901, DF2=0.811622, DF3=0.731191, DF4=0.658731, DF5=0.593451. Present value of each FCF = FCF_t x DF_t: PV1=10,810.81; PV2=12,174.34; PV3=13,161.44; PV4=13,174.62; PV5=13,055.92. Sum of PVs (Years 1-5) = 62,377.13. NPV = 62,377.13 - 50,000 = 12,377.13 (SAR 000s), rounded 12,377. IRR solves 0 = -50,000 + sum FCF_t/(1+r)^t; r approx 18.62% (=IRR on the {-50000,12000,15000,18000,20000,22000} stream). Cumulative discounted CF turns positive during Year 5: end of Y4 cumulative PV = 49,321.21, so cumulative net (less outlay) is -678.79 at end Y4 and +12,377.13 at end Y5. Decision: IRR 18.62% > 11% hurdle and NPV > 0, so ACCEPT (candidate need not type the word; metrics carry the decision). All cell values graded with tolerance.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Year 3 present value of FCF correct (=18,000/1.11^3) - Correct discount-factor application to a single-period cash flow
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Sum of PV of Years 1-5 cash flows (gross PV = 62,377) - Aggregation of the full discounted-cash-flow schedule
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Project NPV at 11% WACC (=12,377 SAR 000s) - Net present value net of the initial outlay - the primary accept/reject metric
    - `cell_value` (w1) - End-of-Year-4 cumulative discounted net position (-679) - Discounted-payback cumulative tracking across periods
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Project IRR (=18.62%, expressed as 0.1862) - Internal rate of return solved over the full cash-flow stream

**Pillar - Cost of Capital & Risk-Return Analytics**

- **WACC, CAPM Cost of Equity & Risk-Adjusted Return Build** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: CFA Institute (Cost of Capital, Portfolio Management) / AAOIFI where Sharia-screened
  - _Measures:_ Applying CAPM, after-tax cost of debt, the WACC weighting, and the Sharpe ratio - the deterministic hurdle-rate and risk-adjusted-return formulas underpinning capital allocation.
  - _Scenario:_ ADIA-style allocator Gulf Capital Partners (UAE) is setting the hurdle rate for a new mandate. Capital structure: equity market value AED 600m, debt market value AED 400m (so weights are 60% / 40%). Inputs: risk-free rate 4.0% (10-yr UAE sovereign), equity beta 1.20, equity risk premium 6.0%, pre-tax cost of debt 5.5%, marginal tax rate 9% (UAE corporate tax). Separately, the candidate evaluates the mandate's realized performance: portfolio annual return 14.0%, portfolio standard deviation 12.0%, against the same 4.0% risk-free rate. Compute cost of equity (CAPM), after-tax cost of debt, the blended WACC, and the portfolio Sharpe ratio.
  - _Model answer:_ Cost of equity (CAPM) = Rf + beta x ERP = 4.0% + 1.20 x 6.0% = 4.0% + 7.2% = 11.2%. After-tax cost of debt = 5.5% x (1 - 0.09) = 5.5% x 0.91 = 5.005% (approx 5.01%). WACC = w_e x Ke + w_d x Kd(after-tax) = 0.60 x 11.2% + 0.40 x 5.005% = 6.72% + 2.002% = 8.722% (approx 8.72%). Sharpe ratio = (Rp - Rf) / sigma_p = (14.0% - 4.0%) / 12.0% = 10 / 12 = 0.833 (approx 0.83). Each value typed into its named field; graded with tolerance (percentages entered as percent values, e.g. 11.2, with stated tolerance).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Cost of equity via CAPM (=11.2%) - CAPM cost-of-equity computation from beta, risk-free and equity risk premium
    - `logic_value` (w2) - After-tax cost of debt (=5.01%) - Tax-shield adjustment to the pre-tax cost of debt
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Weighted average cost of capital (=8.72%) - Capital-structure-weighted blend of equity and debt costs - the project hurdle rate
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Portfolio Sharpe ratio (=0.83) - Risk-adjusted excess return per unit of total risk
- **Two-Variable NPV Sensitivity Data Table (WACC x Terminal Growth)** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: AFP FP&A Body of Knowledge (FPAC) / CFA Institute Equity Valuation
  - _Measures:_ Building a native two-variable data table to stress a Gordon-growth valuation across discount-rate and growth assumptions - the array-formula sensitivity discipline behind investment-committee scenario packs.
  - _Scenario:_ Mubadala-style fund Sirius Investments (Abu Dhabi) values a terminal-value-driven infrastructure stake. Next-year free cash flow (FCF1) = AED 5,000 (000s). Equity value is modelled as a Gordon-growth terminal value: Value = FCF1 / (WACC - g). Base case WACC = 10.0%, terminal growth g = 3.0%, giving base value = 5,000 / (0.10 - 0.03) = 71,428.57. The candidate must build a two-variable data table showing the valuation across a WACC axis of {9%, 10%, 11%} (columns) and a terminal-growth axis of {2%, 3%, 4%} (rows), using a native data table - not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Driver cell = FCF1 / (WACC - g) = 5,000 / (B_wacc - B_g). The data table feeds column input = WACC cell, row input = growth cell. Values (rounded to whole AED 000s): at g=2%: WACC9%=71,428.57, WACC10%=62,500.00, WACC11%=55,555.56. At g=3% (base row): WACC9%=83,333.33, WACC10%=71,428.57, WACC11%=62,500.00. At g=4%: WACC9%=100,000.00, WACC10%=83,333.33, WACC11%=71,428.57. The corner cell must link to the driver (=value cell). Grade the table as a native array/data-table formula plus three corner/interior cells: low-WACC/high-growth corner (g=4%, WACC=9% -> 100,000), base interior (g=3%, WACC=10% -> 71,428.57), and high-WACC/low-growth corner (g=2%, WACC=11% -> 55,555.56).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sensitivity grid is a native data table {=TABLE()}, not hardcoded - Use of a genuine two-variable data table rather than typed constants
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Base-case interior cell (WACC 10%, g 3% = 71,429) - Gordon-growth value at the base assumptions reproduced inside the table
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Upside corner (WACC 9%, g 4% = 100,000) - Valuation sensitivity at the most favourable corner
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Downside corner (WACC 11%, g 2% = 55,556) - Valuation sensitivity at the most adverse corner

**Pillar - Portfolio & Capital-Allocation Data Interrogation**

- **Holdings Ledger Querying - Unrealized Gain by Asset Class (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA International (DMBOK) / CFA Institute Performance Reporting
  - _Measures:_ Aggregating a relational holdings ledger into a per-asset-class unrealized-gain ranking - the SQL interrogation behind investment performance and rebalancing reporting.
  - _Scenario:_ A PIF-style sovereign allocator holds a positions ledger. The holdings table records each position's asset_class, units, cost_price (book) and market_price (current). The investment-reporting desk needs total unrealized gain per asset class, highest gain first, to drive the rebalancing discussion. Unrealized gain for a position = units x (market_price - cost_price).
  - _Model answer:_ Seed a holdings table: (1,'Equities',1000,50,62),(2,'Equities',500,80,75),(3,'Fixed Income',2000,100,103),(4,'Real Estate',300,500,560),(5,'Real Estate',200,450,440),(6,'Private Equity',100,1000,1300),(7,'Fixed Income',1500,100,99). Per-position unrealized gain = units*(market_price-cost_price). Equities: 1000*12 + 500*(-5) = 12,000 - 2,500 = 9,500. Fixed Income: 2000*3 + 1500*(-1) = 6,000 - 1,500 = 4,500. Real Estate: 300*60 + 200*(-10) = 18,000 - 2,000 = 16,000. Private Equity: 100*300 = 30,000. Master query: SELECT asset_class, SUM(units*(market_price-cost_price)) AS unrealized_gain FROM holdings GROUP BY asset_class ORDER BY unrealized_gain DESC, asset_class. Expected ordered result: Private Equity 30,000; Real Estate 16,000; Equities 9,500; Fixed Income 4,500. Graded order-sensitive (DESC by gain).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master: unrealized gain per asset class, ranked highest first (ordered) - Correct GROUP BY aggregation of a computed gain expression with descending rank

---

### 1.10 Corporate Development, Valuations, & M&A

Hands-on sandbox for Corporate Development / Valuations / M&A. The function ships no skills list, so six skills were proposed grounded in GCC corporate-finance practice (DCF & intrinsic valuation; trading & transaction comparables; M&A deal structuring; accretion/dilution & synergy analysis; pipeline/target screening; transaction due-diligence analytics). All M&A work is inherently quantitative, so it maps cleanly to the four engines with no soft-skill proxy needed. Three pillars across four blocks using three engines: (1) Intrinsic & Relative Valuation - a spreadsheet 3-year DCF with Gordon-Growth terminal value (CFA/IPEV) and an advanced_spreadsheet two-variable EV/EBITDA football-field data table; (2) Deal Structuring & Returns - a logic_input stock-for-stock accretion/dilution model with after-tax synergies (IFRS 3 / ASC 805); (3) Pipeline & Target Screening - a SQL aggregation over an M&A target pipeline with a status filter and tie-break ordering. Difficulty spans intermediate to advanced; concrete AED figures and real-sounding GCC entities throughout.

**Skills:** DCF & Intrinsic Valuation (FCFF, WACC, Terminal Value) · Trading & Transaction Comparables (EV/EBITDA football field) · M&A Deal Structuring & Financing (cash vs. stock) · Accretion/Dilution & Synergy Analysis · Target Screening & Pipeline Analytics · Transaction Due-Diligence & Returns (IRR/MOIC)

**Engine fit:** Corporate Development / Valuations / M&A is a strongly quantitative function and a natural fit for all four engines - no soft-skill proxy was required. Intrinsic and relative valuation are the canonical spreadsheet/advanced_spreadsheet tasks (a fully linked DCF with discounting and a Gordon-Growth terminal value; a two-variable EV/EBITDA sensitivity matrix that demands a native data table, exactly mirroring the FP&A sensitivity block). Accretion/dilution math (after-tax synergies, new-share issuance, pro-forma EPS) decomposes into discrete named numeric outputs - an exact logic_input fit, reconciling like the PVM block. Target/pipeline screening is naturally relational, so the deal-pipeline aggregation is a clean SQL task with a status filter and a deterministic tie-break. The only genuinely un-gradable slice of this role - the qualitative investment thesis, negotiation narrative, and board memo - is deliberately excluded; the sandbox measures the analytical engine room (valuation, structuring, screening) that underpins those deliverables, which is where demonstrated technical skill is objectively checkable.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Intrinsic & Relative Valuation**

- **Discounted Cash Flow (FCFF) Enterprise & Equity Value** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18 min · ref: CFA Institute Equity Valuation / IPEV Guidelines
  - _Measures:_ Constructing a discounted-cash-flow valuation: period discounting, Gordon-Growth terminal value, EV build, the net-debt bridge to equity value, and per-share derivation.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Industrial Holding PJSC (Dubai) is a take-private target. You are handed a 3-year unlevered free-cash-flow (FCFF) forecast in AED millions: Year 1 = 200, Year 2 = 230, Year 3 = 260. The WACC is 10.0% and the perpetuity (Gordon) growth rate is 3.0%. Net debt at the valuation date is AED 450m and there are 500m shares outstanding. Build the DCF: discount each year's FCFF, compute a Gordon-Growth terminal value at the end of Year 3 (TV = FCFF3 x (1+g) / (WACC - g)), discount it back, sum to Enterprise Value, bridge to Equity Value, and derive the implied value per share.
  - _Model answer:_ Discount factors DF_t = 1/(1.10)^t -> 0.90909, 0.82645, 0.75131. PV of FCFF = 200x0.90909 = 181.82 (B6), 230x0.82645 = 190.08 (B7), 260x0.75131 = 195.34 (B8). Terminal value = 260 x 1.03 / (0.10-0.03) = 3,825.71 (B10); PV of TV = 3,825.71 x 0.75131 = 2,874.32 (B11). Enterprise Value = 181.82+190.08+195.34+2,874.32 = 3,441.56 (B12). Equity Value = EV - Net Debt = 3,441.56 - 450 = 2,991.56 (B13). Value per share = 2,991.56 / 500 = 5.98 (B14). Editable cells B6,B7,B8,B10,B11,B12,B13,B14; given inputs are FCFF (B2:B4), WACC, g, net debt, shares.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - PV of Year 1 FCFF (B6) - Single-period discounting at WACC is applied correctly (200/1.10).
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Terminal value at end of Year 3 (B10) - Gordon-Growth perpetuity is formed correctly: FCFF3 x (1+g)/(WACC-g) = 3,825.71.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - PV of terminal value (B11) - Terminal value is discounted back by the Year-3 factor, not an extra period (2,874.32).
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Enterprise Value (B12) - Sum of discounted explicit FCFFs plus PV of TV equals 3,441.56.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Equity Value after net-debt bridge (B13) - EV-to-equity bridge subtracts net debt of 450 to give 2,991.56.
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Implied value per share (B14) - Equity value divided by 500m shares gives AED 5.98.
- **EV/EBITDA Comparables Football-Field Matrix** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 15 min · ref: AICPA/IPEV Market-Approach Multiples Guidance
  - _Measures:_ Relative valuation via comparable-company multiples and Excel two-variable data-table mechanics to build a valuation football field.
  - _Scenario:_ For the same target you run a market-approach cross-check. Implied Enterprise Value = EV/EBITDA multiple x EBITDA. The base case uses an 8.0x multiple on AED 420m EBITDA. Build a two-variable data table that flexes the EBITDA estimate (rows: 380, 420, 460 in AED m) against the peer EV/EBITDA multiple (columns: 7.0x, 8.0x, 9.0x). The grid must be driven by a native two-variable data table linked to the base EV formula - not hardcoded products.
  - _Model answer:_ Base EV cell B5 = multiple x EBITDA = 8 x 420 = 3,360. The corner cell (top-left of the grid) links to B5. Row input cell = EBITDA driver (B2); column input cell = multiple driver (B1). Native data table over C9:E11 produces: low corner C9 (7.0x, EBITDA 380) = 2,660; centre D10 (8.0x, EBITDA 420) = 3,360; high corner E11 (9.0x, EBITDA 460) = 4,140. Grid is {=TABLE(B1,B2)}, evaluated by the engine - not typed numbers.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Grid uses a native two-variable data table (C9:E11) - The matrix is data-table driven {=TABLE()}, demonstrating real sensitivity mechanics rather than hardcoded multiplication.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner: 7.0x on EBITDA 380 (C9) - Bottom-end implied EV = 2,660.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base case: 8.0x on EBITDA 420 (D10) - Central implied EV ties to the base EV formula = 3,360.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner: 9.0x on EBITDA 460 (E11) - Top-end implied EV = 4,140.

**Pillar - Deal Structuring & Returns**

- **Stock-for-Stock Accretion / Dilution & Synergies** &nbsp; `Logic input` · advanced · 11 min · ref: IFRS 3 / ASC 805 Business Combinations
  - _Measures:_ M&A consideration mechanics and accretion/dilution analysis: share issuance for stock consideration, after-tax synergy treatment, pro-forma EPS, and the accretion/dilution verdict.
  - _Scenario:_ Gulf Capital Acquirer PJSC is buying Levant Target LLC in an all-stock deal. Acquirer standalone net income is AED 600m on 300m shares (share price AED 30). Target standalone net income is AED 180m. The deal is fully funded by issuing new acquirer shares at AED 30 to deliver a total consideration of AED 2,400m. Expected pre-tax annual cost synergies are AED 50m; the marginal tax rate is 20%. Ignore acquisition financing interest and transaction fees. Compute: (1) new shares issued, (2) after-tax synergies, (3) pro-forma combined EPS, and (4) the accretion/(dilution) in AED per share versus the acquirer's standalone EPS.
  - _Model answer:_ New shares = consideration / price = 2,400 / 30 = 80m. After-tax synergies = 50 x (1-0.20) = 40m. Combined net income = 600 + 180 + 40 = 820m. Combined shares = 300 + 80 = 380m. Pro-forma EPS = 820 / 380 = 2.1579. Standalone acquirer EPS = 600 / 300 = 2.0000. Accretion = 2.1579 - 2.0000 = +0.1579 per share (deal is accretive). Fields: new_shares_issued = 80, after_tax_synergies = 40, proforma_eps = 2.1579, accretion_dilution = 0.1579.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - New shares issued (m) - Stock consideration divided by issue price: 2,400 / 30 = 80m.
    - `logic_value` (w2) - After-tax annual synergies (AED m) - Pre-tax synergies are tax-effected: 50 x (1-0.20) = 40m.
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Pro-forma combined EPS (AED) - Combined net income (incl. after-tax synergies) over combined share count = 820 / 380 = 2.16.
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Accretion / (dilution) per share (AED) - Pro-forma EPS less standalone EPS = +0.16, correctly flagging the deal as accretive.

**Pillar - Pipeline & Target Screening**

- **M&A Target Pipeline Aggregation (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA International (DMBOK) Data Querying
  - _Measures:_ Relational interrogation of a deal pipeline: filtered aggregation, grouping, and deterministic ranked output with tie-breaking.
  - _Scenario:_ The corporate development team tracks its acquisition pipeline in a relational table targets(id, company, sector, deal_value_aed_m, status). Status is 'active' or 'dropped'. Leadership wants total committed deal value by sector for ACTIVE targets only, ranked from highest total to lowest. A large 'dropped' Banking target (5,000) must be excluded. Write one query returning columns sector, total - sectors with equal totals ordered alphabetically.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT sector, SUM(deal_value_aed_m) AS total FROM targets WHERE status = 'active' GROUP BY sector ORDER BY total DESC, sector. The WHERE clause drops the 5,000 'dropped' Banking row. Active rows: Banking 1200+800=2000, Healthcare 1500+400=1900, Logistics 650+300=950, Fintech 950. Ordered result: Banking 2000, Healthcare 1900, Fintech 950, Logistics 950 (Fintech before Logistics on the alphabetical tie-break at 950).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Sector totals for active targets, ranked DESC with alphabetical tie-break - Filters status='active' (excludes the 5,000 dropped Banking row), groups by sector, sums deal value, and orders by total DESC then sector - matching the master result set exactly and in order.

---

### 1.11 Corporate Tax (Direct & Indirect Compliance)

Hands-on tax-compliance sandbox for the GCC, built to match the FP&A reference in rigor and concreteness. Three pillars across four blocks using all four engines: (1) Direct Tax Computation & Provisioning - a spreadsheet UAE Corporate Tax computation (accounting profit to taxable income to 9% liability with the AED 375,000 0% band) and a logic_input IAS 12 deferred-tax + effective-tax-rate reconciliation; (2) Indirect Tax & Cross-Border Flows - a logic_input UAE VAT return net-payable build (output VAT vs recoverable input VAT with a partial-exemption restriction) plus withholding-tax-on-payments math; (3) Transfer Pricing & Compliance Interrogation - an advanced_spreadsheet OECD arm's-length comparables data table and a SQL interrogation of an intercompany-transaction ledger for TP documentation thresholds. Every block carries concrete AED/SAR figures, a real framework reference (UAE Federal Decree-Law No. 47 of 2022, UAE VAT Decree-Law No. 8 of 2017, OECD TP Guidelines / Transfer Pricing, IAS 12, ZATCA e-invoicing), an explicit master-solution computation, and 3-6 weighted pass/fail checkpoints. This is a high-fit function for the engines: corporate tax is intrinsically quantitative, so no soft-skill proxying was needed.

**Skills:** Corporate Income Tax · VAT & Indirect Tax · Withholding Tax · Transfer Pricing · Deferred Tax & Provisioning · GCC Specifics (Zakat, E-Invoicing)

**Engine fit:** Strong, native fit across all four engines - Corporate Tax is an intrinsically quantitative compliance discipline, so no soft-skill-to-quant proxying was required. Direct tax computation (accounting profit to taxable income to liability) and deferred-tax provisioning are deterministic arithmetic over statutory rules, ideal for spreadsheet cell_value and logic_input logic_value checks. The UAE VAT return (output minus recoverable input VAT, partial-exemption restriction) and withholding-tax math are clean logic_input scenarios that must reconcile to a net payable. Transfer pricing arm's-length benchmarking maps to an advanced_spreadsheet two-variable comparables/sensitivity table (is_array_formula + corner cell_values), and TP / e-invoicing documentation-threshold interrogation maps naturally to SQL over an intercompany-transaction ledger (sql_result_match). The only judgement-heavy slivers of the role - drafting TP master files, advance-pricing-agreement negotiation, voluntary-disclosure narratives - are deliberately out of scope here because they are free-text and non-gradable; this bank measures the computational/analytical spine of tax compliance that underpins those deliverables. Grading is fully objective with numeric tolerances.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 5 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Logic input, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Direct Tax Computation & Provisioning**

- **UAE Corporate Tax Computation - Accounting Profit to Liability** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: UAE Federal Decree-Law No. 47 of 2022 (Corporate Tax)
  - _Measures:_ Ability to reconcile accounting profit to taxable income via permanent/timing adjustments and apply the UAE 9% rate with the 0% small-business band correctly.
  - _Scenario:_ Gulf Crescent Trading LLC (Dubai mainland) reports accounting net profit before tax of AED 2,400,000 for the tax period ending 31 Dec 2024. You must build the tax computation that adjusts accounting profit for permanent and timing differences, applies the AED 375,000 0% threshold under Article 3, and computes the 9% Corporate Tax liability. Given add-backs and deductions: non-deductible fines AED 60,000 (add back), client-entertainment 50% disallowance on AED 200,000 spend = AED 100,000 add-back, accounting depreciation AED 300,000 (add back), tax depreciation AED 360,000 (deduct), and exempt dividend income from a UAE subsidiary AED 150,000 (deduct). The grid is pre-populated with labels and given figures in column B; the candidate completes the linked computation cells.
  - _Model answer:_ Taxable income = 2,400,000 + 60,000 (fines) + 100,000 (50% entertainment) + 300,000 (accounting depreciation add-back) - 360,000 (tax depreciation) - 150,000 (exempt dividend) = AED 2,350,000 (B12). Taxable income above the 0% band = 2,350,000 - 375,000 = AED 1,975,000 (B14). Corporate Tax @ 9% = 1,975,000 x 0.09 = AED 177,750 (B15). Effective tax rate on taxable income = 177,750 / 2,350,000 = 7.56% (B16). The 0% band makes ETR below the 9% headline rate - this is the conceptual checkpoint.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total add-backs computed correctly (B9 = 460,000) - Sums non-deductible fines + 50% entertainment disallowance + accounting depreciation add-back
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total deductions computed correctly (B11 = 510,000) - Sums tax depreciation + exempt dividend income
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Taxable income = AED 2,350,000 (B12) - Accounting profit adjusted for all permanent and timing differences
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Income above 0% band = AED 1,975,000 (B14) - Correct application of the AED 375,000 0% threshold (Article 3)
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Corporate Tax liability @ 9% = AED 177,750 (B15) - 9% rate applied only to income above the threshold
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Effective tax rate = 7.56% (B16) - Liability divided by taxable income shows the sub-headline ETR from the 0% band
- **Deferred Tax & Effective-Tax-Rate Reconciliation (IAS 12)** &nbsp; `Logic input` · advanced · 10 min · ref: IAS 12 Income Taxes
  - _Measures:_ Deferred tax recognition from temporary differences and tax losses under IAS 12, and assembling total tax expense from current plus deferred movement.
  - _Scenario:_ Sahara Logistics PJSC has a single asset with carrying amount AED 1,200,000 and tax base AED 900,000 at year-end (temporary taxable difference). It also has an unused tax loss carried forward of AED 200,000 it expects to utilise. The UAE Corporate Tax rate is 9%. Current tax payable for the year is AED 90,000. You must compute, in labelled numeric fields: the taxable temporary difference, the deferred tax liability, the deferred tax asset on the loss, the net deferred tax balance, and the total tax expense (current + movement in deferred). Assume opening deferred tax was nil, so the period movement equals the closing balance.
  - _Model answer:_ Taxable temporary difference = carrying amount - tax base = 1,200,000 - 900,000 = AED 300,000. Deferred tax liability = 300,000 x 9% = AED 27,000. Deferred tax asset on loss = 200,000 x 9% = AED 18,000. Net deferred tax = DTL - DTA = 27,000 - 18,000 = AED 9,000 (net liability). Total tax expense = current tax 90,000 + movement in net deferred tax 9,000 = AED 99,000 (opening deferred was nil, so movement equals closing net balance).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Taxable temporary difference = AED 300,000 - Carrying amount minus tax base
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Deferred tax liability = AED 27,000 - Temporary difference x 9% rate
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Deferred tax asset on loss = AED 18,000 - Tax loss x 9% rate, recognised as expected to be utilised
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Net deferred tax = AED 9,000 liability - DTL net of DTA
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Total tax expense = AED 99,000 - Current tax plus deferred-tax movement reconciles

**Pillar - Indirect Tax & Cross-Border Flows**

- **UAE VAT Return - Net Payable with Partial Exemption** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: UAE Federal Decree-Law No. 8 of 2017 (VAT)
  - _Measures:_ VAT output-tax computation and input-tax apportionment under partial exemption (turnover method), resolving to a correct net payable.
  - _Scenario:_ Marina Property Holdings (UAE, VAT-registered) files a quarterly VAT return at the 5% standard rate. Standard-rated sales (taxable supplies) were AED 4,000,000; exempt residential-lease supplies were AED 1,000,000. Total input VAT incurred was AED 90,000, of which AED 60,000 is directly attributable to taxable supplies (fully recoverable), AED 12,000 is directly attributable to exempt supplies (non-recoverable), and AED 18,000 is residual (overhead) input VAT that must be apportioned by the standard turnover-based method. Compute, in labelled numeric fields: output VAT, the recoverable share of residual input VAT, total recoverable input VAT, and net VAT payable to the FTA.
  - _Model answer:_ Output VAT = 4,000,000 x 5% = AED 200,000 (exempt supplies carry no output VAT). Recovery ratio = taxable turnover / total turnover = 4,000,000 / 5,000,000 = 80%. Recoverable residual input VAT = 18,000 x 80% = AED 14,400. Total recoverable input VAT = 60,000 (direct taxable) + 14,400 (residual share) = AED 74,400; the 12,000 directly attributable to exempt supplies is blocked. Net VAT payable = output VAT 200,000 - recoverable input VAT 74,400 = AED 125,600.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Output VAT = AED 200,000 - 5% applied to standard-rated supplies only; exempt supplies excluded
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Recoverable residual input VAT = AED 14,400 - Residual input VAT apportioned at the 80% turnover ratio
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total recoverable input VAT = AED 74,400 - Direct-taxable input plus recoverable residual; exempt-attributable input blocked
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Net VAT payable = AED 125,600 - Output VAT less total recoverable input VAT reconciles

**Pillar - Transfer Pricing & Compliance Interrogation**

- **Arm's-Length Markup Sensitivity Matrix (OECD TNMM)** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: OECD Transfer Pricing Guidelines (TNMM) / UAE TP Regulations
  - _Measures:_ Building an arm's-length cost-plus pricing model and a native two-variable sensitivity table to bracket the inter-quartile arm's-length range.
  - _Scenario:_ Falcon Distribution FZE provides intra-group distribution services and is tested under the Transactional Net Margin Method (TNMM) on a cost-plus basis. Its operating cost base is AED 5,000,000. You must build a two-variable data table showing the arm's-length transfer price (= cost base x (1 + cost-plus markup %)) across a range of operating-cost bases (rows: 4,000,000 / 5,000,000 / 6,000,000) and benchmarked markups (columns: 5% / 8% / 11% - the inter-quartile range of the comparable set). The corner cell links to the live transfer-price formula; the body must be a native data table, not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Base transfer price B5 = cost base x (1 + markup) = 5,000,000 x 1.08 = AED 5,400,000 (using base markup 8% in B2). The two-variable data table feeds the cost base (row input) and markup (column input) into B5. Corner low (cost 4,000,000, markup 5%) = 4,000,000 x 1.05 = AED 4,200,000. Base case (cost 5,000,000, markup 8%) = AED 5,400,000. Corner high (cost 6,000,000, markup 11%) = 6,000,000 x 1.11 = AED 6,660,000. The table must be a native {=TABLE()} array so the examiner sees a real what-if, not pasted values.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base transfer price = AED 5,400,000 (B5) - Cost base x (1 + 8% markup) computed live
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Body uses a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - Range is formula-driven {=TABLE()}, proving genuine sensitivity modelling
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner = AED 4,200,000 (cost 4m, markup 5%) - Bottom of the inter-quartile arm's-length range
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Base case = AED 5,400,000 (cost 5m, markup 8%) - Median benchmark interior cell of the table
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner = AED 6,660,000 (cost 6m, markup 11%) - Top of the inter-quartile arm's-length range
- **Intercompany Ledger Interrogation - TP Documentation Thresholds (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: UAE TP Regulations / OECD Master File-Local File Thresholds
  - _Measures:_ Relational interrogation of an intercompany ledger to aggregate, filter on a related-party flag, and apply a TP documentation materiality threshold via HAVING.
  - _Scenario:_ A seeded related_party_transactions ledger records intercompany dealings of a UAE group for the tax period: id, counterparty, country, category (goods/services/royalty/loan_interest), amount_aed, is_related_party (boolean). Tax wants the aggregate related-party exposure per category to assess which transaction categories breach the Local File documentation materiality threshold of AED 4,000,000. Write ONE query returning category and total related-party amount, for related-party transactions only, where the category total is at least AED 4,000,000, highest total first.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT category, SUM(amount_aed) AS total FROM related_party_transactions WHERE is_related_party = true GROUP BY category HAVING SUM(amount_aed) >= 4000000 ORDER BY total DESC, category. Seed data is arranged so that, after filtering to related-party rows, exactly the goods and royalty categories clear AED 4,000,000 while services and loan_interest fall below the threshold, and unrelated-party rows are correctly excluded by the WHERE clause. The result set is order-sensitive on total descending.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master (related-party category totals >= AED 4m, correct order) - Correct WHERE on is_related_party, GROUP BY category, HAVING threshold, and ORDER BY total descending

---

### 1.12 Internal Audit, Financial Risks, & SOX Governance

Internal Audit is governance-heavy and partly qualitative (control narratives, walkthroughs, audit reports), so this blueprint deliberately targets the QUANTITATIVE/ANALYTICAL slice of the role that the four auto-gradable engines can measure objectively: (1) risk-based audit planning as residual-risk and audit-universe prioritization math, (2) attribute-sampling and SOX deviation-rate testing as exact-formula logic, (3) audit analytics / CAATs as SQL over a transactions ledger for control-exception and fraud-indicator detection. Three pillars, four blocks, three engines (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql). Frameworks: IIA IPPF, COSO 2013 Internal Control & ERM, AICPA AU-C 530 (Audit Sampling), PCAOB AS 2315, ACFE fraud-risk, and ISACA for data-analytics. Each block uses concrete GCC figures (AED/SAR, real-sounding GCC entities) and reconciling checkpoints.

**Skills:** Risk-Based Audit Planning · Internal Controls (COSO) · Walkthroughs & Testing · Fraud Risk · Audit Reporting & Follow-up · Audit Analytics

**Engine fit:** Internal Audit / SOX is only partly quantitative - its core deliverables (control narratives, walkthrough memos, audit findings write-ups, management action plans) are free-text and NOT auto-gradable. This blueprint isolates the genuinely numeric, defensible-by-formula slice of the discipline and maps each task to one engine. (1) Risk-based audit planning is real arithmetic: inherent-risk scoring (likelihood x impact), control-effectiveness reduction to residual risk, and weighted audit-universe ranking -> spreadsheet with cell_value checks. (2) SOX/attribute sampling has exact standards-based formulas: sample-size lookup, deviation rate = deviations/sample, upper deviation limit vs tolerable rate, and a materiality/scoping band -> logic_input with logic_value checks that reconcile to a control conclusion. The same pillar adds a two-variable sample-size sensitivity table (sample size across tolerable-deviation-rate x expected-deviation-rate) -> advanced_spreadsheet with is_array_formula + corner cell_values, exercising audit-planning quantification at scale. (3) Audit analytics / CAATs is inherently set-based: detecting duplicate payments, split POs below an approval threshold, segregation-of-duties violations, and weekend/after-hours postings -> sql with sql_result_match. What is intentionally NOT covered (and cannot be by these engines): writing the audit observation, rating control design effectiveness qualitatively, drafting the COSO walkthrough narrative, and judgement on root cause. Those remain for a human/SME or MCQ layer. The blueprint therefore measures DEMONSTRATED audit-quantification and data-interrogation skill - the objectively scorable competencies that separate a strong auditor from a weak one - while honestly flagging the qualitative reporting craft as out of engine scope.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Logic input, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Risk-Based Audit Planning & Residual Risk Quantification**

- **Audit Universe Risk Scoring & Annual Plan Prioritization** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 18.3 min · ref: IIA IPPF Standard 2010 (Planning) / COSO ERM 2017
  - _Measures:_ Translating inherent risk, control-effectiveness reliance, and financial exposure into a defensible, ranked, hours-allocated annual audit plan (risk-based planning arithmetic).
  - _Scenario:_ You are on the Internal Audit team of Emirates Gulf Investment Bank (Dubai). The CAE is building the FY2026 risk-based audit plan over five auditable entities. For each entity you are given an Inherent Risk score (Likelihood 1-5 x Impact 1-5) and a Control Effectiveness factor (0.20 = strong controls reduce risk by 80%, up to 1.00 = no reliance). Residual Risk = Inherent Risk x Control Effectiveness. The audit-priority index weights Residual Risk by the entity's annual financial exposure (AED 000s) to rank where audit hours go first. Complete the inherent-risk, residual-risk, exposure-weighted index and ranking columns so the plan fully links.  Given per entity (Likelihood, Impact, Control Effectiveness factor, Exposure AED000s): - Treasury & FX Desk: L=4, I=5, CE=0.50, Exposure=180000 - Retail Lending Ops: L=3, I=4, CE=0.40, Exposure=95000 - Procurement & AP: L=5, I=3, CE=0.80, Exposure=42000 - IT General Controls: L=4, I=4, CE=0.60, Exposure=60000 - Trade Finance: L=3, I=5, CE=0.30, Exposure=120000  Audit-Priority Index = Residual Risk x (Exposure / 1000), rounded to the cell. The 'Total annual audit hours to allocate' (3,600) must be split pro-rata to each entity's share of the total priority index.
  - _Model answer:_ Inherent Risk = Likelihood x Impact. Treasury 4x5=20, Retail 3x4=12, Procurement 5x3=15, ITGC 4x4=16, Trade 3x5=15. Residual Risk = Inherent x CE: Treasury 20x0.50=10.0, Retail 12x0.40=4.8, Procurement 15x0.80=12.0, ITGC 16x0.60=9.6, Trade 15x0.30=4.5. Priority Index = Residual x (Exposure/1000): Treasury 10.0x180=1800, Retail 4.8x95=456, Procurement 12.0x42=504, ITGC 9.6x60=576, Trade 4.5x120=540. Sum of indices = 1800+456+504+576+540 = 3876. Highest priority (rank 1) = Treasury (1800). Hours to Treasury = 3600 x (1800/3876) = 1672.3 (round to 1672). Total residual-risk column sum = 10.0+4.8+12.0+9.6+4.5 = 40.9 used as a control check.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Inherent risk Treasury & FX (L x I = 20) - Likelihood x Impact inherent-risk calculation
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Residual risk Procurement & AP (15 x 0.80 = 12.0) - Control-effectiveness factor applied to inherent risk
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total residual-risk column = 40.9 - Residual risk computed correctly across all five entities
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Audit-priority index Treasury = 1800 - Exposure-weighted prioritization index
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Sum of priority indices = 3876 - Index total used as allocation base reconciles
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Pro-rata audit hours to Treasury = 1672 - Hours allocated proportional to risk-priority share

**Pillar - SOX Controls Testing & Attribute Sampling**

- **Attribute Sampling, Deviation Rate & Control Conclusion** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: AICPA AU-C 530 / PCAOB AS 2315 (Audit Sampling)
  - _Measures:_ Executing AU-C 530 attribute sampling: deviation-rate computation, projection to population, upper-deviation-limit vs tolerable-rate evaluation, and the resulting reliance conclusion.
  - _Scenario:_ Qatar National Holding's SOX team is testing the 'three-way match before payment' control over the AP population. The control operates ~5,000 times per year (daily, high-frequency manual control). Using the firm's attribute-sampling table the required sample size for a daily control at 90% confidence is 25 items. The team pulled and tested the sample and found deviations (control failures). Compute each field; your sample deviation rate and upper deviation limit must drive the control conclusion.  Inputs: - Population (annual control operations): 5,000 - Sample size tested: 25 - Deviations (failures) found in sample: 2 - Tolerable Deviation Rate (TDR) for a key control: 10% (0.10) - Sampling-risk allowance (precision add-on) for this plan: 6.0 percentage points  Compute: (1) Sample Deviation Rate = deviations / sample size, as a percentage. (2) Projected deviations to the population = sample deviation rate x population. (3) Upper Deviation Limit (UDL) = sample deviation rate + allowance, as a percentage. (4) Control conclusion code: enter 1 if UDL <= TDR (control RELIES / operating effectively), enter 0 if UDL > TDR (control does NOT rely - exception).
  - _Model answer:_ Sample Deviation Rate = 2/25 = 0.08 = 8.0%. Projected deviations to population = 0.08 x 5000 = 400. Upper Deviation Limit = 8.0% + 6.0pp = 14.0%. Conclusion: UDL 14.0% > TDR 10.0%, so the upper limit exceeds tolerable - the control does NOT support reliance -> conclusion code = 0. (The trap: sample rate 8% is below the 10% tolerable rate, but the sampling-risk allowance pushes the UDL above tolerable, so a candidate who compares only the point estimate gets the conclusion wrong.)
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Sample deviation rate = 8.0% - deviations / sample size as a percentage
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Projected deviations to population = 400 - Sample rate projected onto the control population
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Upper deviation limit = 14.0% - Point estimate plus sampling-risk allowance
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Control conclusion code = 0 (no reliance: UDL > TDR) - UDL-vs-tolerable evaluation drives the reliance decision (not the point estimate)
- **Sample-Size Sensitivity Table for Test Planning** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: AICPA AU-C 530 Appendix / IIA Practice Guide: Audit Sampling
  - _Measures:_ Building a reusable, array-driven audit-sampling planning model so test scope scales correctly as tolerable and expected deviation assumptions change.
  - _Scenario:_ Saudi Fransi Capital's audit manager is planning sample sizes for the next SOX cycle and wants a planning grid showing how required sample size moves with the Tolerable Deviation Rate (columns) against the Expected Population Deviation Rate (rows), holding confidence at 90%. Using the firm's simplified statistical sample-size model, Sample Size = ROUND( (confidence factor) / (Tolerable Rate - Expected Rate), 0 ), where the 90%-confidence factor = 2.31 and rates are entered as decimals. Build the base-case sample-size cell, then a two-variable data table over the price/volume-style axes: columns are Tolerable Deviation Rate {0.05, 0.08, 0.10}, rows are Expected Deviation Rate {0.01, 0.02, 0.03}. It must use a native data table, not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Base case (Tolerable=0.10, Expected=0.02): 2.31/(0.10-0.02) = 2.31/0.08 = 28.875 -> ROUND = 29. Two-variable data table cells = ROUND(2.31/(Tolerable - Expected),0). Low corner (Tolerable=0.05, Expected=0.01): 2.31/0.04 = 57.75 -> 58. High corner (Tolerable=0.10, Expected=0.03): 2.31/0.07 = 33.0 -> 33. Centre (Tolerable=0.08, Expected=0.02): 2.31/0.06 = 38.5 -> 39 (or 38 depending on round-half rule; tolerance covers +/-1). The grid must be produced by a native two-variable data table whose corner cell links to the base-case sample-size formula, with column input = Tolerable cell and row input = Expected cell.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base-case sample size = 29 (Tolerable 0.10, Expected 0.02) - Core sample-size formula 2.31/(TDR-EDR) rounded
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Grid uses a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - Sensitivity grid is formula/data-table driven, not typed numbers
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner sample size = 58 (Tolerable 0.05, Expected 0.01) - Smallest tolerable gap drives the largest sample
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner sample size = 33 (Tolerable 0.10, Expected 0.03) - Widest tolerable gap drives the smallest sample
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre sample size = 39 (Tolerable 0.08, Expected 0.02) - Interior data-table value computed by the array, not extrapolated

**Pillar - Audit Analytics, CAATs & Fraud-Indicator Detection**

- **Continuous-Audit Query: Split POs & Duplicate Payments** &nbsp; `SQL` · advanced · 10 min · ref: ISACA IS Audit / ACFE Fraud Examiners Manual (data analytics)
  - _Measures:_ Designing a CAATs detection query that operationalizes a delegation-of-authority control to catch threshold-circumvention (PO-splitting) fraud patterns via grouped having-clause logic.
  - _Scenario:_ You are running computer-assisted audit techniques (CAATs) over Abu Dhabi Civil Authority's procurement ledger. Management's delegation-of-authority policy requires any single purchase order at or above AED 50,000 to receive a second (manager) approval. A common control-circumvention fraud scheme is 'PO splitting': a buyer raises two or more POs to the same vendor on the same day, each individually under AED 50,000 but together at or above the AED 50,000 threshold, to avoid the second approval. Query the purchase_orders table to surface every such suspected split: for each (vendor, po_date) group where the COUNT of POs is at least 2, every individual PO amount is below 50,000, and the SUM of amounts is at least 50,000 - return the vendor, the po_date, the number of POs, and the total amount, ordered by total amount highest first then vendor.  Schema: purchase_orders (id int, vendor text, buyer text, po_date date, amount numeric, second_approval boolean). Expected columns: vendor, po_date, po_count, total_amount.
  - _Model answer:_ GROUP BY vendor, po_date with a HAVING clause enforcing all three conditions simultaneously: COUNT(*) >= 2 AND MAX(amount) < 50000 (every PO individually under threshold) AND SUM(amount) >= 50000 (aggregate at/over threshold). SELECT vendor, po_date, COUNT(*) AS po_count, SUM(amount) AS total_amount FROM purchase_orders GROUP BY vendor, po_date HAVING COUNT(*) >= 2 AND MAX(amount) < 50000 AND SUM(amount) >= 50000 ORDER BY total_amount DESC, vendor. The seed data must include at least one genuine split (e.g. two POs of 28000 + 27000 same vendor/date), one legitimate single large PO of 60000 (excluded - only one PO), and one same-day pair that sums under 50000 (excluded - SUM below threshold), so the HAVING logic is genuinely discriminating.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result set matches master split-PO detection (correct rows, ordered by total desc then vendor) - Grouped HAVING logic isolates exactly the threshold-circumvention pattern with correct ordering

---

### 1.13 Strategic Procurement & Tactical Sourcing

Hands-on sandbox for Strategic Procurement & Tactical Sourcing. The function had no defined skills, so I proposed six GCC-grounded skills and built the gradable quantitative slice of the role across 4 blocks and 4 engines. Pillar 1 (Sourcing Economics & Award Decisions) tests a two-supplier total-cost-of-ownership landed-cost model (spreadsheet) and a weighted vendor scorecard with a two-variable savings sensitivity data table (advanced_spreadsheet). Pillar 2 (Inventory & Replenishment Optimization) tests EOQ, safety stock and reorder point (logic_input). Pillar 3 (Spend Analytics & Supplier Intelligence) tests a spend-concentration SQL query over a PO ledger. Frameworks: CIPS, ISM/CPSM, APICS/ASCM CPIM, GCC customs/VAT context. All master solutions are arithmetic-verified; difficulty spans basic to advanced. Procurement is an excellent fit for all four engines, so no soft-function proxy was needed.

**Skills:** Strategic Sourcing & Category Management · Vendor Evaluation & Weighted Scorecards · Total Cost of Ownership (TCO) Analysis · Inventory Optimization (EOQ, Safety Stock & Reorder Point) · Negotiation & Savings Quantification · Spend Analytics & Tail-Spend Management

**Engine fit:** Strategic Procurement & Tactical Sourcing is a strongly quantitative function and an excellent fit for all four auto-gradable engines - no soft-function proxy was required. The award-decision work (total cost of ownership / landed cost, weighted vendor scoring, savings quantification) maps cleanly to the spreadsheet and advanced_spreadsheet engines via exact cell values plus a native two-variable data table for savings sensitivity. The replenishment work (EOQ, safety stock, reorder point) is closed-form arithmetic that maps to logic_input numeric fields. Spend analytics / tail-spend concentration maps to sql over a seeded purchase-order ledger. The only non-gradable parts of the role (negotiation behaviour, supplier-relationship judgement, contract drafting) are deliberately excluded; their gradable residue (quantified savings, weighted scorecards, spend concentration) is fully captured here.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Sourcing Economics & Award Decisions**

- **Total Cost of Ownership (TCO) Landed-Cost Comparison** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: CIPS Global Standard / ISM CPSM - Total Cost of Ownership
  - _Measures:_ Building a defensible landed-cost / TCO model that captures freight, duty and quality costs beyond unit price, and converting it into a per-unit comparison and an award decision.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Industrial Trading LLC (Abu Dhabi) is awarding a 5,000-unit annual contract for a control-valve assembly and must pick the lower total-cost-of-ownership supplier, NOT the lower unit price. Supplier A (local distributor): unit price AED 480, inbound freight AED 60,000, customs duty 5% of FOB merchandise value, pre-shipment inspection AED 15,000. Supplier B (overseas mill): unit price AED 455, inbound freight AED 145,000, customs duty 5% of FOB merchandise value, pre-shipment inspection AED 22,000. Complete the landed-cost build for both suppliers: merchandise FOB value, 5% duty, total landed cost, landed cost per unit, then the per-contract savings of the cheaper option and the award decision flag (1 = award Supplier B, 0 = award Supplier A).
  - _Model answer:_ Pre-populated grid, one column per supplier. FOB merchandise = unit price x 5,000. Supplier A: 480 x 5000 = 2,400,000; duty = 5% x 2,400,000 = 120,000; total landed = 2,400,000 + 60,000 + 120,000 + 15,000 = 2,595,000; per unit = 2,595,000 / 5000 = 519.00. Supplier B: 455 x 5000 = 2,275,000; duty = 5% x 2,275,000 = 113,750; total landed = 2,275,000 + 145,000 + 113,750 + 22,000 = 2,555,750; per unit = 2,555,750 / 5000 = 511.15. Savings of cheaper option = 2,595,000 - 2,555,750 = 39,250. Supplier B is cheaper on TCO despite higher freight, so award flag = 1. Checkpoints sit on the duty links, both total landed costs, the savings reconciliation and the award flag.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Supplier A customs duty (5% of FOB) - Applies the 5% duty to the correct FOB base (AED 120,000), not to total landed cost.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Supplier A total landed cost (AED 2,595,000) - Sums merchandise, freight, duty and inspection for Supplier A.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Supplier B total landed cost (AED 2,555,750) - Sums merchandise, freight, duty and inspection for Supplier B.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Supplier B landed cost per unit (AED 511.15) - Converts total landed cost to a per-unit basis for like-for-like comparison.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Per-contract TCO savings of cheaper option (AED 39,250) - Computes the savings differential between the two landed-cost totals.
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Award decision flag = 1 (award Supplier B) - Selects the lower-TCO supplier despite the higher unit-price-only supplier, proving TCO logic over headline price.
- **Weighted Vendor Scorecard & Savings Sensitivity Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18.3 min · ref: ISM CPSM - Supplier Evaluation / CIPS Category Management
  - _Measures:_ Constructing a defensible weighted multi-criteria vendor scorecard and a native two-variable sensitivity table that quantifies negotiated-savings risk across price and volume.
  - _Scenario:_ Saudi National Facilities Co. (Riyadh) is consolidating an MRO category and must (1) score three bidders on a weighted scorecard and (2) stress-test the annual savings of the preferred award across negotiated price and committed annual volume. Scorecard criteria and weights: Price 40%, Quality 25%, Delivery 20%, ESG/Localization 15%. Vendor raw scores (0-100): Vendor X = Price 80, Quality 90, Delivery 70, ESG 60. The savings model is Annual Savings = (Baseline Price - Negotiated Price) x Annual Volume, with baseline price SAR 200/unit. Build the weighted total score for Vendor X, then build a two-variable data table of annual savings with negotiated price {190, 185, 180} across the columns and annual volume {10000, 12000, 14000} down the rows. The table must use a native data table, not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Weighted score for Vendor X = 80x0.40 + 90x0.25 + 70x0.20 + 60x0.15 = 32 + 22.5 + 14 + 9 = 77.5. Savings driver cell = (Baseline 200 - Negotiated Price) x Annual Volume. Two-variable data table: column input = negotiated price cell, row input = annual volume cell, corner formula links to the savings driver. Corner values: low corner (price 190, vol 10000) = (200-190)x10000 = 100,000; center (price 185, vol 12000) = 15x12000 = 180,000; high corner (price 180, vol 14000) = 20x14000 = 280,000. is_array_formula confirms a real {=TABLE()} drives the matrix; cell_value checks pin the weighted score and three table cells.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Vendor X weighted total score (77.5) - Applies the 40/25/20/15 weights to the raw criterion scores correctly.
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Savings matrix uses a native two-variable data table - The savings grid is data-table driven, not hardcoded - proves the candidate built a real sensitivity table.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Savings low corner: price 190, vol 10000 (SAR 100,000) - Lower-left sensitivity corner computes correctly from the driver formula.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Savings base case: price 185, vol 12000 (SAR 180,000) - Interior/center sensitivity cell computes correctly.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Savings high corner: price 180, vol 14000 (SAR 280,000) - Upper-right sensitivity corner computes correctly from the driver formula.

**Pillar - Inventory & Replenishment Optimization**

- **EOQ, Safety Stock & Reorder Point** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: APICS / ASCM CPIM - Inventory Management (EOQ & Reorder Point)
  - _Measures:_ Applying closed-form inventory-optimization formulas (EOQ, total relevant cost, safety stock with a service-level Z, reorder point) to set a defensible replenishment policy.
  - _Scenario:_ Doha Logistics Park stocks a fast-moving packaging consumable. Annual demand D = 72,000 units, ordering cost S = QAR 250 per order, annual holding cost H = QAR 9 per unit per year. Lead time = 10 days on a 360-day planning year. The standard deviation of demand over the lead time is 300 units, and management targets a 95% service level (use Z = 1.65). Compute the Economic Order Quantity, the total annual relevant inventory cost at the EOQ (ordering + holding), the safety stock, and the reorder point.
  - _Model answer:_ EOQ = sqrt(2 x D x S / H) = sqrt(2 x 72000 x 250 / 9) = sqrt(4,000,000) = 2,000 units. At EOQ, annual ordering cost = (D/EOQ) x S = 36 x 250 = 9,000; annual holding cost = (EOQ/2) x H = 1,000 x 9 = 9,000; total annual relevant cost = 18,000 (they are equal at EOQ, a useful sanity check). Safety stock = Z x sigma_LT = 1.65 x 300 = 495 units. Average daily demand = 72,000/360 = 200; lead-time demand = 200 x 10 = 2,000; reorder point = lead-time demand + safety stock = 2,000 + 495 = 2,495 units. Checkpoints sit on EOQ, total relevant cost, safety stock and reorder point.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Economic Order Quantity (2,000 units) - Correctly applies the EOQ square-root formula to D, S and H.
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total annual relevant inventory cost at EOQ (QAR 18,000) - Sums ordering and holding cost at the EOQ, confirming the candidate understands the cost trade-off the EOQ minimizes.
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Safety stock at 95% service level (495 units) - Applies Z = 1.65 to the lead-time demand standard deviation.
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Reorder point (2,495 units) - Combines lead-time demand with safety stock for the trigger level.

**Pillar - Spend Analytics & Supplier Intelligence**

- **Category Spend Concentration Query (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · basic · 10 min · ref: CIPS Spend Analysis / DAMA DMBOK - Data Interrogation
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating a relational PO ledger to aggregate and rank category spend - the foundational analytic step for category strategy and tail-spend reduction.
  - _Scenario:_ A GCC group procurement team is running an annual spend-analysis cube to find category concentration and consolidation candidates. The purchase-order ledger po_lines holds one row per PO line with the category, vendor and line amount in AED. Write one query that returns total spend per category, highest spend first, so the team can see where the money concentrates. Return exactly two columns: category and total.
  - _Model answer:_ Seed po_lines with category/vendor/amount rows across IT, Facilities, Travel and Marketing. Master query: SELECT category, SUM(amount) AS total FROM po_lines GROUP BY category ORDER BY total DESC, category. Single sql_result_match checkpoint, order-sensitive, so the descending-by-spend ranking (the analytic point) must be correct, not just the totals.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Category totals returned, highest spend first - GROUP BY category with SUM(amount) and a correct descending order, matching the master result set exactly.
