## Human Resources

> **Domain review** - engine coverage needs attention. Engine validity: every block across all 8 blueprints maps to one of the 4 auto-gradable engines (spreadsheet / advanced_spreadsheet / logic_input / sql); no block uses the non-gradable 'python' enum member or any free-text/essay grading. Checkpoint kinds align with engines throughout (cell_value + is_array_formula on spreadsheets, logic_value on logic_input, single sql_result_match on every sql block, matching the FP&A reference convention). Engine-fit reasoning is strong and honest: each blueprint that covers a soft/non-quantitative role (2.4 Talent Acquisition, 2.5 Talent Management/OD, 2.6 L&D, 2.8 Employee Relations) explicitly identifies the gradable quantitative slice and flags the excluded qualitative core, which is exactly the required treatment.  Pillar count: all 8 report 3 pillars (compliant), BUT the compact view only states a pillar COUNT and does not show the pillar-to-block grouping. For the blocks to map cleanly onto exactly 3 pillars, blueprints with 4 blocks (2.1, 2.8) and especially the 6-block blueprints (2.3, 2.4) must distribute sensibly; this could not be fully verified from the compact view and should be confirmed in the full blueprint.  Block-count rule (3-5 blocks total): TWO violations. Node 2.3 (Payroll Administration) has 6 blocks and node 2.4 (Talent Acquisition) has 6 blocks - both exceed the hard 3-5 ceiling. 2.1 (4), 2.2 (5), 2.5 (5), 2.6 (5), 2.7 (5), 2.8 (4) are all within range.  Engine-type diversity (>=2, ideally 3): all 8 clear the >=2 bar; 2.1, 2.2, 2.3, 2.4 use all 4 engines; 2.5, 2.6, 2.7 use 3; 2.8 uses 3 (logic_input, sql, spreadsheet, with an explicit, defensible rationale for omitting advanced_spreadsheet). Good variety overall. engine_coverage_ok is set false ONLY because of the two block-count ceiling breaches, not because any engine is mis-mapped.  Difficulty mix: 2.1 (intermediate/advanced/intermediate/intermediate) and 2.4 (intermediate x3, advanced x2, intermediate) skew with NO 'basic' block - acceptable but thin on range. 2.8 has two 'advanced' spreadsheet blocks plus one intermediate logic_input and one intermediate sql - no 'basic', advanced-heavy. 2.2, 2.3, 2.5, 2.6, 2.7 each include at least one basic block and span the range well.  SQL checkpoint count: every sql block carries exactly 1 checkpoint (the single sql_result_match), consistent with the FP&A reference. Note this means each sql block contributes only one weighted check vs. the 4-6 on quantitative blocks - the design intends the result-set match to be all-or-nothing, which is the reference convention and is fine, but reviewers should ensure the SQL prompts are rich enough to justify their block weight.
>
> - _(high)_ 2.3: Block-count ceiling breach: 6 blocks (Gross-to-Net pay run, GOSI split, End-of-Service gratuity, Gratuity sensitivity table, WPS reconciliation SQL, Cost-centre allocation) exceeds the hard 3-5 block limit. Drop or merge one block to land at <=5. Candidate merge: fold 'Labour Cost Allocation Across Cost Centres' (spreadsheet) into the 'Gross-to-Net Monthly Pay Run' spreadsheet block, or drop the GOSI split given the End-of-Service block already exercises statutory deduction logic.
> - _(high)_ 2.4: Block-count ceiling breach: 6 blocks exceeds the hard 3-5 limit. Two spreadsheet blocks ('Recruitment Funnel Conversion & Yield-Ratio' and 'Source-of-Hire Quality Index & Cost-Adjusted Yield') and two logic_input blocks ('Time-to-Fill/Cost-per-Hire/Channel' and 'Headcount-Gap/Recruiter-Capacity/Selection-Ratio') overlap thematically; merge one spreadsheet pair and/or one logic_input pair to reach <=5 without losing the all-4-engine coverage.
> - _(medium)_ 2.4: Pillar-to-block mapping risk: 6 blocks must compress into the stated 3 pillars; the engine_fit narrative describes overlapping artifacts per skill area, raising the chance two pillars are uneven (e.g. one pillar holding 3-4 blocks). After cutting to 5 blocks, confirm a balanced ~2/2/1 distribution across the 3 pillars in the full blueprint.
> - _(low)_ 2.1: No 'basic' difficulty block (intermediate x3 + advanced x1). Total Rewards is a strong all-4-engine blueprint, but consider downgrading one intermediate block (e.g. the End-of-Service/social-insurance logic_input or the HRIS pay-data SQL) to 'basic' to match the required cross-block difficulty spread.
> - _(low)_ 2.8: Advanced-heavy, no 'basic' block: two 'advanced' spreadsheet blocks (eNPS/attrition dashboard and Disciplinary-Fairness/ER-Risk index) plus intermediate logic_input and sql. The omission of advanced_spreadsheet is well justified, but the difficulty mix would be healthier with one basic/intermediate spreadsheet rather than two advanced. Consider rebalancing one spreadsheet block down.
> - _(low)_ 2.2: Two logic_input blocks (Headcount Roll-Forward Reconciliation + GCC Statutory-Field Completeness Index) sit in a 5-block layout; engine coverage is fine (all 4 used) but verify these two are distributed across different pillars rather than stacked in one, so the 3-pillar grouping stays balanced.
> - _(low)_ 2.5: Two logic_input blocks (HiPo Flight-Risk & Retention Index + Forced-Distribution Calibration Reconciliation) in a 5-block design - acceptable and within limits; just confirm pillar balance across the 3 groupings since the SQL block carries only 1 checkpoint and one pillar could end up light.
>

For 2.3, merge the cost-centre allocation block into the gross-to-net pay run (both spreadsheet) so all four engines and the statutory-math core are preserved. For 2.4, collapse one of the two overlapping spreadsheet blocks and confirm a balanced ~2/2/1 block-to-pillar distribution. Both keep their full 4-engine variety after the cut.  Engine mapping and engine-fit are otherwise solid across the domain - the soft-role blueprints (2.4, 2.5, 2.6, 2.8) correctly carve out the gradable quantitative slice (recruiting numeracy + ATS SQL; 9-box/forced-distribution math + talent-review SQL; Phillips ROI + LMS analytics; statutory settlement math + case-ledger SQL + eNPS/ER-risk indices) and honestly flag the excluded qualitative core. No block needs an engine reassignment. When the full (non-compact) blueprints are produced, verify (a) the pillar-to-block grouping is balanced for every node (especially the trimmed 2.3/2.4 and the two-logic_input nodes 2.2/2.5), and (b) each sql block's single sql_result_match has a prompt rich enough to justify the block's weight, since SQL blocks contribute only one weighted check versus 4-6 on the quantitative blocks. The framework_refs cited (UAE Decree-Law 33/2021, GOSI/WPS, DAMA DMBOK, Phillips ROI, SHRM-style 4/5ths adverse impact) are appropriate and GCC-grounded.

### 2.1 Total Rewards (Compensation & Benefits Architecture)

Total Rewards is highly quantitative by nature, so all four sandbox engines fit cleanly with no soft-skill workarounds needed. The function's skills list was empty, so six GCC-grounded Total Rewards skills were proposed (salary-structure design, compa-ratio & range-penetration analytics, statutory entitlement costing, benefits & allowance modelling, pay-equity diagnostics, and rewards data interrogation). The blueprint has 3 pillars and 4 blocks across 3 engines: (1) Pay Structure & Market Pricing - a spreadsheet block building a salary grade table (midpoint progression, range spread, compa-ratio, range penetration) and an advanced_spreadsheet block building a two-variable merit-budget sensitivity data table; (2) Statutory & Benefits Costing - a logic_input block computing UAE end-of-service gratuity plus GCC GOSI/social-insurance employer cost on a fully-loaded CTC; (3) Rewards Data Interrogation - a SQL block querying an HRIS pay table for below-minimum (red-circle) outliers and gender pay gap by grade. Frameworks: WorldatWork Total Rewards model, UAE Federal Decree-Law No. 33 of 2021 (end-of-service), GOSI/GCC social insurance, and pay-equity practice aligned to GRI 405. Concrete AED/SAR figures and real-sounding GCC entities throughout. Difficulty is mixed across basic / intermediate / advanced.

**Skills:** Salary Structure & Grade Design (midpoints, spread, progression) · Compa-Ratio & Range Penetration Analytics · Statutory Entitlement Costing (End-of-Service, GOSI/social insurance) · Benefits, Allowances & Total Cost-to-Company Modelling · Pay-Equity & Gender Pay Gap Diagnostics · Merit / Increment Budget Sensitivity & Rewards Data Interrogation

**Engine fit:** Total Rewards is intrinsically quantitative, so all four engines fit with no soft-skill proxying required. spreadsheet handles salary-grade architecture (midpoint progression, range spread, compa-ratio, range penetration) - the core market-pricing calculations every C&B analyst performs. advanced_spreadsheet handles a two-variable merit-budget sensitivity table (total increment cost across merit % and promotion-uplift %), which mirrors real annual-review budget modelling and naturally requires a native data table. logic_input handles statutory entitlement costing (UAE end-of-service gratuity under Federal Decree-Law No. 33 of 2021 plus GOSI/GCC social-insurance employer contribution) where the candidate must apply tiered legal formulas and reconcile a fully-loaded cost-to-company - exact numeric fields, no judgement. sql handles rewards data interrogation over an HRIS pay table (red-circled employees paid below grade minimum, and average pay by gender within a grade for a pay-gap read). The only Total Rewards activities that are NOT gradable here are policy narrative, job-evaluation committee judgement, and benefits-vendor negotiation - those are deliberately excluded; the blueprint covers the analytical/quantitative slice that defines technical proficiency in the function.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Pay Structure & Market Pricing**

- **Salary Grade Architecture & Compa-Ratio Build** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: WorldatWork Total Rewards Model / Salary Structure Design
  - _Measures:_ Designing a salary range from a minimum and spread, then computing the two canonical placement metrics (compa-ratio and range penetration) for incumbents - the foundational market-pricing competency in Total Rewards.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Falcon Holding (Abu Dhabi) is rebuilding its Grade 7 professional band. The grade minimum is AED 18,000/month and the range spread is 50% (max = min x 1.50). The midpoint is the average of min and max. Three incumbents sit in the grade: Layla at AED 21,600, Omar at AED 27,000, and Sara at AED 30,600 (monthly base). Compute the grade max, midpoint, each incumbent's compa-ratio (salary / midpoint, as a decimal) and each incumbent's range penetration ((salary - min) / (max - min), as a decimal). The candidate completes the editable cells so the structure links and the analytics resolve.
  - _Model answer:_ Max = Min x (1 + spread) = 18000 x 1.50 = 27000 (B3). Midpoint = (Min + Max) / 2 = (18000 + 27000) / 2 = 22500 (B4). Compa-ratio = salary / midpoint: Layla 21600/22500 = 0.96 (C8), Omar 27000/22500 = 1.20 (C9), Sara 30600/22500 = 1.36 (C10). Range penetration = (salary - min)/(max - min), denominator = 27000-18000 = 9000: Layla (21600-18000)/9000 = 0.40 (D8), Omar (27000-18000)/9000 = 1.00 (D9), Sara (30600-18000)/9000 = 1.40 (D10). Sara penetrates above 100% (red-circled), a deliberate diagnostic the candidate's numbers should surface.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Grade maximum = Min x (1 + spread) = AED 27,000 - Correctly derives range maximum from minimum and range spread
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Midpoint = (Min + Max) / 2 = AED 22,500 - Computes the range midpoint, the compa-ratio reference point
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Omar compa-ratio = 1.20 - Compa-ratio = salary / midpoint computed correctly at midpoint+ position
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Layla range penetration = 0.40 - Range penetration = (salary - min) / (max - min) computed correctly
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Sara range penetration = 1.40 (above-max red-circle) - Penetration correctly exceeds 1.0 for a salary above range max, surfacing the outlier
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Sara compa-ratio = 1.36 - Compa-ratio computed correctly for the highest-paid incumbent
- **Merit & Promotion Budget Sensitivity Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: WorldatWork Merit Budgeting / AFP-style scenario modelling
  - _Measures:_ Building a two-variable sensitivity / data table to stress the annual rewards budget across merit and promotion-uplift assumptions - the array-modelling skill compensation analysts use for budget approval.
  - _Scenario:_ Saudi National Logistics Co. (Riyadh) is sizing its annual review budget for a 200-person population with a total annual base payroll of SAR 60,000,000. The annual increment cost = base payroll x (merit % + promotion-uplift %). Finance wants a two-variable sensitivity table showing total increment cost (SAR) across merit rates of 3%, 4%, 5% (columns) and promotion-uplift rates of 1%, 2%, 3% (rows). Build the base formula and a native two-variable data table over the axes. It must be a real data table, not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Base increment cost B5 = base payroll x (merit% + promo%) = 60,000,000 x (0.04 + 0.02) = 3,600,000 at the base case (merit 4%, promo 2%). Corner cell links to B5. Two-variable data table: column input = merit cell, row input = promo cell. Cell values = 60,000,000 x (merit% + promo%): low corner (merit 3%, promo 1%) = 60M x 0.04 = 2,400,000; base centre (merit 4%, promo 2%) = 60M x 0.06 = 3,600,000; high corner (merit 5%, promo 3%) = 60M x 0.08 = 4,800,000. The data-table range must be array-formula driven.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sensitivity grid uses a native data table {=TABLE()} (not hardcoded) - Candidate built a genuine two-variable data table rather than typing values
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base increment cost = SAR 3,600,000 (merit 4% + promo 2%) - Base scenario formula = payroll x (merit% + promo%) is correct
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (merit 3%, promo 1%) = SAR 2,400,000 - Data table interior resolves the lowest-cost scenario correctly
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (merit 5%, promo 3%) = SAR 4,800,000 - Data table interior resolves the highest-cost scenario correctly
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre cell (merit 4%, promo 2%) = SAR 3,600,000 - Data table base-case cell agrees with the standalone base formula

**Pillar - Statutory & Benefits Costing**

- **End-of-Service & Social-Insurance Cost-to-Company** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: UAE Federal Decree-Law No. 33 of 2021 (End-of-Service) + GOSI / GCC Social Insurance
  - _Measures:_ Applying tiered statutory entitlement formulas (UAE end-of-service gratuity day-rate tiers) and GCC social-insurance employer costing - the compliance-grade numeric skill that makes a Total Rewards specialist legally defensible.
  - _Scenario:_ Gulf Pioneer Industries must cost the full annual employer liability for a UAE-based employee. Monthly basic salary is AED 20,000 (gratuity is computed on basic only). The employee is a GCC national resigning after exactly 7 completed years of continuous service on an unlimited contract. UAE end-of-service gratuity rule: 21 days of basic pay per year for the first 5 years, then 30 days of basic pay per year thereafter; a day = monthly basic / 30. Separately, the employer's monthly social-insurance (GOSI-equivalent) contribution for a GCC national is 12.5% of a contributory wage of AED 24,000 (basic + fixed allowances). Compute: (a) gratuity for the first 5 years, (b) gratuity for the remaining 2 years, (c) total end-of-service gratuity, (d) the employer's ANNUAL social-insurance contribution.
  - _Model answer:_ Day rate = 20000 / 30 = 666.667. First 5 years: 21 days/yr x 5 = 105 days x 666.667 = AED 70,000 (field eos_first5). Years 6-7: 30 days/yr x 2 = 60 days x 666.667 = AED 40,000 (field eos_after5). Total gratuity = 70,000 + 40,000 = AED 110,000 (field eos_total). Employer monthly social insurance = 12.5% x 24,000 = AED 3,000; annual = 3,000 x 12 = AED 36,000 (field annual_social_insurance).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - First-5-years gratuity = AED 70,000 (21 days/yr tier) - Applies the 21-days-per-year tier on monthly-basic/30 day rate for the first five years
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Years 6-7 gratuity = AED 40,000 (30 days/yr tier) - Applies the higher 30-days-per-year tier for service beyond five years
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Total end-of-service gratuity = AED 110,000 - Sums the two statutory tiers to the correct total liability
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Annual employer social-insurance = AED 36,000 - Computes 12.5% of contributory wage and annualises the employer contribution

**Pillar - Rewards Data Interrogation**

- **HRIS Pay-Data Outlier & Pay-Gap Query** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: Pay-Equity Analysis aligned to GRI 405 / DAMA DMBOK data practice
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating an HRIS pay table with SQL to surface below-minimum (red-circled) compensation outliers - the data-fluency a Total Rewards analyst needs to audit pay integrity at scale.
  - _Scenario:_ An HRIS table employees(id, name, gender, grade, base_salary, grade_min) holds the Grade 7 population for Emirates Falcon Holding. Return every employee whose base_salary is below their grade_min (a red-circle compliance breach), showing name, grade, base_salary and grade_min, ordered by the shortfall (grade_min - base_salary) largest first.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT name, grade, base_salary, grade_min FROM employees WHERE base_salary < grade_min ORDER BY (grade_min - base_salary) DESC, name. The seed data is constructed so 2-3 employees fall below their grade minimum with distinct shortfalls, and the ORDER BY makes the result deterministic and order-sensitive.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Returns below-minimum employees, ordered by shortfall descending - Filters base_salary < grade_min and orders by the pay shortfall, matching the master result set exactly

---

### 2.2 HR Information Systems (HRIS) & Core Data Governance

HRIS & Core Data Governance is a strongly quantitative, gradable function: it lives on the integrity, completeness and reconciliation of the employee master record. The sandbox measures three demonstrated capabilities - (1) interrogating the HRIS/employee-master relational store with SQL (duplicate/orphan/integrity detection and headcount rollups), (2) auditing and scoring data quality against DAMA DMBOK / DCAM dimensions in a spreadsheet (completeness/validity scorecard plus a two-variable cleansing-impact data table), and (3) the core-data control math itself via logic_input (headcount roll-forward reconciliation joiners-leavers-movers, and a GCC compliance-completeness index over Emirates ID / GOSI / WPS / IBAN fields). All four engines are exercised. Skills proposed because the source node had none.

**Skills:** Employee Master Data Management & Record Lifecycle · Data Quality Auditing (Completeness, Validity, Uniqueness, Consistency) · Organizational Hierarchy & Position Management Integrity · Headcount & Movement Reconciliation (Joiners/Leavers/Movers) · HRIS Reporting, SQL Querying & Data Interrogation · Statutory & Compliance Field Governance (Emirates ID, GOSI, WPS, IBAN)

**Engine fit:** Strong fit across all four engines - HRIS & Data Governance is fundamentally quantitative despite sitting in HR. The discipline is built on countable, reconcilable, rule-checkable attributes of the employee master, so nothing here needs free-text grading. SQL is the natural home for data-interrogation skills: an employee/position relational store lets us grade duplicate-record detection, orphaned-position (broken manager FK) hierarchy checks, and headcount aggregations via exact result-set matching. logic_input grades the two signature control computations of the function with deterministic numeric fields: a headcount roll-forward reconciliation (opening + joiners - leavers +/- transfers = closing) and a weighted statutory-field completeness index over GCC-mandatory attributes (Emirates ID, GOSI number, WPS/IBAN, contract type) - each pure arithmetic over given counts. spreadsheet grades a DAMA-style data-quality scorecard (per-dimension scores rolled to a weighted DQ index), and advanced_spreadsheet grades a two-variable cleansing-impact data table (DQ index across error-volume x remediation-rate axes), requiring a native data table plus corner/interior cell checks. The ONLY non-gradable slice of this role - drafting a data-governance policy or stewardship RACI narrative - is deliberately excluded; everything in this blueprint is exact-number or result-set checkable.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 5 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Data Quality Governance & Cleansing Analytics**

- **DAMA Data-Quality Scorecard Build** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: DAMA International DMBOK2 / EDM Council DCAM (six data-quality dimensions)
  - _Measures:_ Operationalising DAMA/DCAM data-quality dimensions into a weighted, decision-ready DQ index and quantifying remediation effort to hit a governance threshold.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Capital Bank's HRIS team audits the employee master (4,000 active records) ahead of a Workday migration. For each of the six DAMA data-quality dimensions you are given the count of records that PASS the rule out of 4,000. Build the scorecard: compute each dimension's quality score as a percentage (pass / total), then a weighted overall Data Quality Index using the governance committee's published weights (Completeness 25%, Validity 20%, Uniqueness 20%, Consistency 15%, Timeliness 10%, Accuracy 10%). Finally compute how many records must be remediated to lift the lowest-scoring dimension to the 95% governance threshold. Given pass counts: Completeness 3,640; Validity 3,800; Uniqueness 3,960; Consistency 3,720; Timeliness 3,560; Accuracy 3,880. Total records 4,000.
  - _Model answer:_ Each dimension score = pass/4000 (Completeness 0.91, Validity 0.95, Uniqueness 0.99, Consistency 0.93, Timeliness 0.89, Accuracy 0.97). Weighted DQ Index = 0.91*0.25 + 0.95*0.20 + 0.99*0.20 + 0.93*0.15 + 0.89*0.10 + 0.97*0.10 = 0.2275+0.19+0.198+0.1395+0.089+0.097 = 0.941 (94.10%). Lowest dimension is Timeliness at 0.89 (3,560/4,000). Records needed at 95% = 0.95*4000 = 3,800; remediation gap = 3,800 - 3,560 = 240 records. Cells: completeness score B (0.91), timeliness score (0.89), DQ index (0.9410), records-to-remediate (240).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Completeness dimension score = 0.91 (3,640/4,000) - Per-dimension pass-rate computation
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Timeliness dimension score = 0.89 (lowest dimension identified) - Pass-rate computation and worst-dimension awareness
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Weighted Data Quality Index = 0.9410 (94.10%) - Correct weighted aggregation across six dimensions with published weights
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Records to remediate to lift Timeliness to 95% = 240 - Threshold-gap quantification (remediation sizing)
- **Cleansing-Impact Sensitivity Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: AFP / DAMA DMBOK data-remediation planning
  - _Measures:_ Constructing a native two-variable sensitivity model to plan a data-remediation programme under uncertainty about defect volume and vendor performance.
  - _Scenario:_ Continuing the Emirates Capital Bank cleansing programme, model the projected post-cleanse Completeness score as a function of two drivers: the number of defective records identified at audit (error volume) and the remediation success rate the cleansing vendor achieves. Base model: starting from 360 incomplete records out of 4,000, the post-cleanse Completeness score = (4000 - ErrorVolume*(1 - RemediationRate)) / 4000. Build a two-variable data table with error-volume rows (300, 360, 450) and remediation-rate columns (0.70, 0.85, 0.95). It must be a native data table, not hardcoded.
  - _Model answer:_ Base cell post-cleanse Completeness = (4000 - 360*(1-0.85))/4000 = (4000 - 54)/4000 = 3946/4000 = 0.98650. Data table: residual defects = ErrorVolume*(1-RemediationRate); score = (4000 - residual)/4000. Corner low (ErrorVol 450, Rate 0.70): residual=450*0.30=135, score=(4000-135)/4000=3865/4000=0.96625. Corner high (ErrorVol 300, Rate 0.95): residual=300*0.05=15, score=(4000-15)/4000=3985/4000=0.99625. Centre (ErrorVol 360, Rate 0.85): 0.98650. The data-table range must be array/data-table driven (colInput = remediation rate cell, rowInput = error-volume cell).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Range uses a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded values) - Native data-table construction over two inputs
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Base-case post-cleanse Completeness = 0.98650 (ErrVol 360, Rate 0.85) - Driver formula correctness at the base case
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Worst corner = 0.96625 (ErrVol 450, Rate 0.70) - Interior data-table value under high defects / low success
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Best corner = 0.99625 (ErrVol 300, Rate 0.95) - Interior data-table value under low defects / high success

**Pillar - Core-Data Control & Statutory Reconciliation**

- **Headcount Roll-Forward Reconciliation** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 9 min · ref: SHRM / CIPD workforce-data controls; HR data integrity reconciliation
  - _Measures:_ Headcount roll-forward integrity control - reconciling joiners/leavers/movers to detect an unexplained variance in the active-employee population.
  - _Scenario:_ As HRIS data steward at Riyadh-based Najd Holding, you must reconcile the Q2 active-headcount roll-forward before the board workforce report locks. Opening active headcount (1 Apr) = 2,140. During the quarter the system logged: 95 new hires (joiners), 18 inter-company transfers IN, 62 resignations and 11 terminations (leavers), 18 inter-company transfers OUT, and 9 records moved to 'unpaid leave' status (which are excluded from active headcount). The raw system extract reports closing active headcount = 2,160. Compute (a) total leavers, (b) net movement, (c) the reconciled closing headcount per the roll-forward, and (d) the unexplained variance between the system extract and your reconciled figure.
  - _Model answer:_ Total leavers = 62 + 11 = 73 (resignations + terminations; transfers and leave-status are tracked separately). Net movement = joiners 95 + transfers IN 18 - leavers 73 - transfers OUT 18 - unpaid-leave moves 9 = 95+18-73-18-9 = 13. Reconciled closing = 2,140 + 13 = 2,153. Unexplained variance = system extract 2,160 - reconciled 2,153 = 7. Fields: total_leavers=73, net_movement=13, reconciled_closing=2153, unexplained_variance=7.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total leavers = 73 (resignations + terminations only) - Correct classification of leaver vs transfer vs leave-status
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Net movement = 13 - Signed aggregation of all movement categories
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Reconciled closing headcount = 2,153 - Roll-forward from opening through net movement
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Unexplained variance vs system extract = 7 - Control reconciliation - detecting the data-integrity gap
- **GCC Statutory-Field Completeness Index** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: UAE WPS / GOSI (KSA) statutory payroll-data mandates; GCC HR data-compliance governance
  - _Measures:_ Governing GCC statutory data completeness - weighting fields by regulatory-blocking severity and isolating submission-ready records for WPS/GOSI filing.
  - _Scenario:_ Before the monthly WPS/GOSI submission, you govern the completeness of four statutory fields on Najd Holding's 2,000 active employees. Each record is checked for: Emirates ID / Iqama number, GOSI registration number, WPS/IBAN bank detail, and signed digital contract reference. Field-present counts are: Emirates ID/Iqama 1,980; GOSI number 1,940; WPS/IBAN 1,910; contract reference 1,860. The compliance committee weights the fields by submission-blocking severity: WPS/IBAN 40%, GOSI 30%, Emirates ID/Iqama 20%, contract reference 10%. A record is 'submission-ready' only if ALL FOUR statutory fields are present; the system reports 1,820 fully-complete records. Compute (a) the per-field completeness rate for WPS/IBAN, (b) the weighted statutory completeness index, (c) the count of records NOT submission-ready, and (d) the percentage of the active population that is submission-ready.
  - _Model answer:_ WPS/IBAN completeness rate = 1910/2000 = 0.9550 (95.50%). Weighted index = (1980/2000)*0.20 + (1940/2000)*0.30 + (1910/2000)*0.40 + (1860/2000)*0.10 = 0.99*0.20 + 0.97*0.30 + 0.955*0.40 + 0.93*0.10 = 0.198 + 0.291 + 0.382 + 0.093 = 0.964 (96.40%). Records NOT submission-ready = 2000 - 1820 = 180. Submission-ready % = 1820/2000 = 0.9100 (91.00%). Fields: wps_completeness_rate=0.955, weighted_index=0.964, not_ready_count=180, ready_pct=0.91.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - WPS/IBAN per-field completeness rate = 0.955 - Single-field completeness computation
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Weighted statutory completeness index = 0.964 - Severity-weighted multi-field aggregation
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Records not submission-ready = 180 - All-fields-present gating logic (complement of fully-complete)
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Submission-ready percentage = 0.91 - Population-level readiness rate

**Pillar - HRIS Data Interrogation & Integrity**

- **Employee-Master Integrity & Hierarchy Querying** &nbsp; `SQL` · advanced · 11.7 min · ref: DAMA DMBOK data-quality & master-data management; referential-integrity controls
  - _Measures:_ Detecting referential-integrity defects in a self-referencing org hierarchy via SQL - the core HRIS data-governance interrogation skill (orphaned manager FKs by department).
  - _Scenario:_ The Caliber HRIS holds an employees table (employee_id, full_name, department, manager_id, emirates_id, status, monthly_salary, hire_date). A pre-migration integrity audit needs ONE query that surfaces broken supervisory links: every ACTIVE employee whose manager_id is non-null but does NOT correspond to any active employee_id in the table (an orphaned manager reference - a hierarchy-integrity defect). Return the offending employee's department and a count of such orphaned-manager records per department, ordered by the count descending (then department ascending for ties). Seed data contains active employees pointing to manager_ids that are either missing entirely or belong to terminated employees, across the Finance, Operations and Technology departments.
  - _Model answer:_ Self-join / NOT IN anti-join on the manager FK: SELECT e.department, COUNT(*) AS orphan_count FROM employees e WHERE e.status = 'active' AND e.manager_id IS NOT NULL AND e.manager_id NOT IN (SELECT employee_id FROM employees WHERE status = 'active') GROUP BY e.department ORDER BY orphan_count DESC, e.department ASC. The result set is the department-level tally of active employees whose manager_id references a non-active or non-existent employee. Graded by ordered result-set match against the master query; the seed is constructed so the per-department orphan counts differ (no ties on count) to make ordering meaningful, with the ascending-department tiebreak as a robustness backstop.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result set matches master: orphaned-manager count per department, count-descending order - Anti-join referential-integrity detection on the self-referencing hierarchy plus correct grouping and ordering

---

### 2.3 Payroll Administration & Employee Allocations

Payroll Administration & Employee Allocations is a heavily quantitative HR operations function: it runs the gross-to-net payroll engine, computes GCC statutory deductions (GOSI/social insurance), accrues end-of-service / gratuity liabilities, reconciles the payroll register to WPS bank files, and allocates / distributes labour cost across cost centres and projects. The function's skills list was empty, so six GCC-grounded skills were proposed: (1) Gross-to-Net Pay Computation, (2) GCC Statutory Deductions (GOSI / Social Insurance), (3) End-of-Service Gratuity & Leave Accrual, (4) Payroll Register Reconciliation & WPS Compliance, (5) Labour Cost Allocation & Cost-Centre Distribution, (6) Payroll Analytics & Headcount Costing. Every skill resolves to a deterministic numeric output, so the function maps cleanly onto the four auto-graded engines with no soft-judgement gap. Three pillars (Payroll Computation Engine; Statutory Liabilities & Accruals; Allocation, Reconciliation & Compliance) carry 4 blocks across 3 engines (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql) at mixed difficulty, mirroring FP&A's concreteness with AED/SAR figures and real entities.

**Skills:** Gross-to-Net Pay Computation · GCC Statutory Deductions (GOSI / Social Insurance) · End-of-Service Gratuity & Leave Accrual · Payroll Register Reconciliation & WPS Compliance · Labour Cost Allocation & Cost-Centre Distribution · Payroll Analytics & Headcount Costing

**Engine fit:** Payroll Administration is one of the most quantitative functions in HR, so it is a strong fit for all four engines with no need for a softer proxy. The gross-to-net pay run, GOSI/social-insurance deductions, gratuity/end-of-service accruals, and cost-centre allocations are all closed-form arithmetic graded by exact cell/field values (spreadsheet + logic_input). The WPS/payroll-register reconciliation and headcount-cost analytics are naturally relational, graded by a result-set match against a master query (sql). A two-variable sensitivity on end-of-service cost (years-of-service x final basic salary) exercises the advanced_spreadsheet data-table requirement. The only honest limitation: real payroll software (SAP SuccessFactors, Oracle HCM, Bayzat) layers workflow, approvals, and statutory e-filing on top of the math; the sandbox grades the computational core (the part that is auto-verifiable and the part candidates most often get wrong), not the system-navigation or filing-submission steps.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 6 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Logic input, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Payroll Computation Engine**

- **Gross-to-Net Monthly Pay Run** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: UAE Federal Decree-Law No. 33 of 2021 (Labour Law) + WPS SIF specification
  - _Measures:_ Gross-to-net pay computation: assembling fixed + variable earnings, deriving overtime and pro-rata leave deductions from a daily/hourly rate, and reconciling to a correct net pay.
  - _Scenario:_ Emaar Facilities Management LLC (Dubai) runs its March payroll for employee Khalid Mansour. Basic salary AED 12,000; housing allowance AED 5,000; transport allowance AED 1,500; other fixed allowances AED 800. Variable this month: overtime is 14 hours paid at 1.25x the basic hourly rate (basic hourly rate = basic salary / 240 hours). Deductions: an unpaid-leave deduction of 2 days (daily rate = total fixed monthly pay / 30), a salary-advance repayment of AED 1,000, and a DEWA salary-deduction loan instalment of AED 450. Complete the payroll worksheet so gross pay, total deductions and net pay all link and compute.
  - _Model answer:_ Total fixed pay = 12000+5000+1500+800 = 19,300 (B8). Basic hourly = 12000/240 = 50; overtime = 14 x 50 x 1.25 = 875 (B10). Gross pay = 19,300 + 875 = 20,175 (B11). Daily rate = 19,300/30 = 643.333...; unpaid-leave deduction (2 days) = 1,286.67 (B14). Total deductions = 1,286.67 + 1,000 + 450 = 2,736.67 (B17). Net pay = 20,175 - 2,736.67 = 17,438.33 (B18).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total fixed earnings (B8 = 19,300) - Correctly sums basic + all fixed allowances
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Overtime pay (B10 = 875) - Derives basic hourly rate over 240 hrs and applies the 1.25x overtime multiplier
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Gross pay (B11 = 20,175) - Adds variable overtime to fixed earnings
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Unpaid-leave deduction (B14 = 1,286.67) - Computes a 30-day daily rate and pro-rates 2 unpaid days
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total deductions (B17 = 2,736.67) - Sums leave deduction + advance repayment + loan instalment
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Net pay (B18 = 17,438.33) - Gross minus total deductions reconciles end-to-end
- **GOSI Saudi Social-Insurance Contribution Split** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 9 min · ref: GOSI (General Organization for Social Insurance, KSA) contribution schedule
  - _Measures:_ GCC statutory deduction mechanics: applying split employee/employer social-insurance percentages to a defined contributory wage and distinguishing the national vs expatriate rate basis.
  - _Scenario:_ Al Rajhi Takaful (Riyadh) processes the GOSI contribution for a Saudi-national employee under the post-July-2024 schedule. Contributory wage = basic salary SAR 18,000 + housing allowance SAR 4,500 (total SAR 22,500). Apply the Saudi-national rates: employee deduction = 9.75% of the contributory wage (9% pension + 0.75% unemployment/SANED); employer contribution = 11.75% (9% pension + 2% occupational hazards + 0.75% SANED). Compute each side and the combined GOSI remittance. (Note: a non-Saudi expatriate would carry only the 2% employer occupational-hazards rate and no employee deduction - report that expat employer amount on the same contributory wage as a contrast field.)
  - _Model answer:_ Contributory wage = 18,000 + 4,500 = 22,500. Employee deduction = 22,500 x 9.75% = 2,193.75. Employer contribution = 22,500 x 11.75% = 2,643.75. Total GOSI remittance = 2,193.75 + 2,643.75 = 4,837.50. Expat employer-only (occupational hazards 2%) = 22,500 x 2% = 450.00.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Contributory wage (22,500) - Identifies basic + housing as the GOSI contributory base
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Employee GOSI deduction (2,193.75) - Applies the 9.75% Saudi-national employee rate
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Employer GOSI contribution (2,643.75) - Applies the 11.75% Saudi-national employer rate
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total GOSI remittance (4,837.50) - Sums employee + employer sides correctly
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Expat employer-only amount (450.00) - Knows expatriates carry only the 2% occupational-hazards rate

**Pillar - Statutory Liabilities & Accruals**

- **End-of-Service Gratuity & Leave Encashment** &nbsp; `Logic input` · advanced · 11 min · ref: UAE Labour Law (Decree-Law 33/2021) Arts. 51-54 - end-of-service gratuity
  - _Measures:_ End-of-service liability computation: tiered day-accrual rules, daily-rate derivation, statutory cap awareness, and leave encashment - the highest-error area in GCC payroll.
  - _Scenario:_ Majid Al Futtaim Retail (Dubai) calculates the end-of-service settlement for an employee resigning after exactly 7 years of unbroken service on an unlimited contract. Final basic salary = AED 21,000/month (gratuity is computed on BASIC pay only). UAE rule: 21 days of basic pay per year for the first 5 years, then 30 days of basic pay per year for each year beyond 5. The daily basic rate = monthly basic / 30. The total gratuity is capped at 2 years' total basic salary. Additionally the employee has 12 days of accrued untaken annual leave to encash at the daily basic rate. Compute the gratuity components, the total gratuity, the leave-encashment amount and the total final settlement.
  - _Model answer:_ Daily basic rate = 21,000/30 = 700. First-5-years gratuity = 5 x 21 x 700 = 73,500. Beyond-5-years gratuity = 2 x 30 x 700 = 42,000. Total gratuity (pre-cap) = 73,500 + 42,000 = 115,500. Cap = 2 years' basic = 24 x 21,000 = 504,000, so the cap does not bind; total gratuity = 115,500. Leave encashment = 12 x 700 = 8,400. Total final settlement = 115,500 + 8,400 = 123,900.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Daily basic rate (700) - Derives the 30-day daily basic rate used throughout the settlement
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Gratuity for first 5 years (73,500) - Applies 21 days/year on basic for the first 5 years
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Gratuity beyond 5 years (42,000) - Applies 30 days/year for service years 6 and 7
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total gratuity after cap test (115,500) - Sums tiers and correctly determines the 2-year cap is not breached
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Leave encashment (8,400) - Encashes 12 untaken days at the daily basic rate
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total final settlement (123,900) - Combines gratuity and leave encashment into the payable settlement
- **Gratuity Cost Sensitivity (Tenure x Final Salary)** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18.3 min · ref: IAS 19 Employee Benefits + UAE Decree-Law 33/2021 gratuity formula
  - _Measures:_ Liability modelling under IAS 19: expressing the tiered capped gratuity formula as a single driver cell and stress-testing it across tenure and salary with a native two-variable data table.
  - _Scenario:_ ADNOC Distribution (Abu Dhabi) is provisioning its end-of-service liability and wants a what-if matrix of gratuity cost across two drivers. Build a two-variable data table where the row axis is completed years of service {3, 8, 12} and the column axis is final monthly basic salary {AED 15,000, 25,000, 40,000}. The gratuity model (capped at 2 years' basic): daily basic = monthly basic / 30; gratuity = (21 days x min(years,5) + 30 days x max(years-5,0)) x daily basic, then capped at 24 x monthly basic. The corner cell of the table must link to the driver gratuity formula and the interior must be a native data table, not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Driver formula: daily = basic/30; raw = (21*MIN(yrs,5) + 30*MAX(yrs-5,0))*daily; gratuity = MIN(raw, 24*basic). Low corner (3 yrs, AED 15,000): daily=500; raw=21*3*500=31,500; cap=360,000 -> 31,500. Base interior (8 yrs, AED 25,000): daily=833.33; raw=(21*5+30*3)*833.33=(105+90)*833.33=195*833.33=162,500; cap=600,000 -> 162,500. High corner (12 yrs, AED 40,000): daily=1,333.33; raw=(105+30*7)*1,333.33=(105+210)*1,333.33=315*1,333.33=420,000; cap=960,000 -> 420,000.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Interior is a native data table (not hardcoded) - The 3x3 interior is driven by a native two-variable data table linked to the gratuity model
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Driver gratuity cell (8 yrs / 25,000 base = 162,500) - The standalone driver formula computes the capped tiered gratuity
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (3 yrs, AED 15,000 = 31,500) - Data-table corner evaluates the short-tenure / low-salary case
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Base interior (8 yrs, AED 25,000 = 162,500) - Interior cell crosses the 5-year tier boundary correctly
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (12 yrs, AED 40,000 = 420,000) - Data-table corner evaluates the long-tenure / high-salary case

**Pillar - Allocation, Reconciliation & Compliance**

- **Payroll Register Reconciliation & WPS Variance Query** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 11 min · ref: UAE Wage Protection System (WPS) SIF + MOHRE reconciliation controls
  - _Measures:_ Payroll-to-bank reconciliation: an outer join between the register and the disbursement file, detecting both missing and mismatched payments, and ranking exceptions by materiality.
  - _Scenario:_ Dubai Holding's shared-services team must reconcile the approved payroll register against the WPS bank-disbursed file before month-end sign-off. Two tables are seeded: payroll_register(emp_id, emp_name, cost_centre, net_pay) and wps_disbursed(emp_id, paid_amount). An employee is flagged when they exist in the register but the bank either did not pay them (no matching wps_disbursed row) OR paid a different amount than the register net pay. Write ONE query returning the exception list - employee id, name, register net pay, the paid amount (NULL if unpaid), and the variance (net_pay minus paid_amount) - ordered by the largest absolute variance first.
  - _Model answer:_ LEFT JOIN payroll_register r to wps_disbursed w on emp_id; keep rows where w.paid_amount IS NULL OR w.paid_amount <> r.net_pay; SELECT emp_id, emp_name, net_pay, paid_amount, (net_pay - COALESCE(paid_amount,0)) AS variance; ORDER BY ABS(net_pay - COALESCE(paid_amount,0)) DESC, emp_id. The result set surfaces every unpaid or mis-paid employee with the variance, largest first.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Exception rows match master (unpaid + mismatched, ranked by abs variance) - Outer join finds both missing and mismatched disbursements, computes the signed variance, and orders by absolute variance descending
- **Labour Cost Allocation Across Cost Centres** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 15 min · ref: IMA Cost Allocation Standards / activity-based labour distribution
  - _Measures:_ Cost-centre / project labour distribution: pro-rata allocation of direct labour and an overhead pool on a consistent driver, with a reconciling grand total - the core of employee cost allocations.
  - _Scenario:_ Saudi Aramco's project-services unit must distribute one employee's fully-loaded monthly cost across three projects by logged hours, then split a shared payroll overhead pool. Employee fully-loaded cost (salary + GOSI employer + gratuity accrual) = SAR 33,000 for the month, against 165 total logged hours: Project Jafurah 66 hrs, Project NEOM 49.5 hrs, Project Yanbu 49.5 hrs. Allocate the SAR 33,000 to each project pro-rata by hours. Then a department payroll-overhead pool of SAR 9,000 is allocated to the same three projects on the SAME hours basis. Complete the worksheet: per-project direct labour, per-project overhead share, per-project total, and the grand total (which must equal 33,000 + 9,000).
  - _Model answer:_ Allocation rates by hours: Jafurah 66/165 = 0.40; NEOM 49.5/165 = 0.30; Yanbu 49.5/165 = 0.30. Direct labour: Jafurah = 33,000 x 0.40 = 13,200; NEOM = 9,900; Yanbu = 9,900. Overhead (same basis): Jafurah = 9,000 x 0.40 = 3,600; NEOM = 2,700; Yanbu = 2,700. Per-project totals: Jafurah = 16,800; NEOM = 12,600; Yanbu = 12,600. Grand total = 16,800 + 12,600 + 12,600 = 42,000 = 33,000 + 9,000.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Jafurah direct labour (13,200) - Allocates direct labour at the 40% hours share
    - `cell_value` (w1) - NEOM direct labour (9,900) - Allocates direct labour at the 30% hours share
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Jafurah overhead share (3,600) - Allocates the overhead pool on the same hours driver
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Jafurah project total (16,800) - Sums direct labour + overhead for the project
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Grand total allocated (42,000) - Total distributed cost reconciles to direct labour + overhead pool with no leakage

---

### 2.4 Talent Acquisition (Sourcing, Recruitment, & Sourcing Yields)

Sandbox blueprint for Talent Acquisition built around the auto-gradable analytical core of the function: recruitment funnel yield mathematics, channel cost/quality efficiency, capacity-based workforce planning, and ATS data interrogation. Three pillars across four blocks using three engines (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql). The soft skills (interviewing technique, employer-brand storytelling, candidate experience) are reframed as their quantitative artifacts: funnel conversion rates, time-to-fill / cost-per-hire, source-of-hire yield and quality-of-hire indices, selection-ratio and adverse-impact (4/5ths) math, and SQL over an applicant-tracking schema. GCC/MENA context throughout (AED/SAR salaries, Emiratisation/Saudisation national-hire targets, GOSI-linked roles), with framework anchors in SHRM/CIPD recruitment-metrics standards, AFP-style ratio analysis, and EEOC Uniform Guidelines for the selection-ratio/adverse-impact slice.

**Skills:** Workforce Planning · Sourcing & Screening · Interviewing & Selection · Employer Branding · Onboarding · Recruitment Metrics

**Engine fit:** Talent Acquisition is a partly-soft function: interviewing, employer branding and onboarding involve judgement that the four engines cannot grade. The blueprint therefore measures the QUANTITATIVE / ANALYTICAL slice that practitioners are genuinely accountable for and that recruiters with real bench strength must master. Each soft skill maps to a gradable artifact: (1) Recruitment Metrics -> funnel conversion + yield-ratio spreadsheet and time-to-fill / cost-per-hire / cost-per-channel logic_input. (2) Sourcing & Screening / Employer Branding -> source-of-hire channel scorecard (advanced_spreadsheet sensitivity table on offer-accept rate x volume driving net hires, plus a weighted channel-efficiency index) - the brand/sourcing decision is reduced to its measurable channel economics. (3) Workforce Planning -> headcount-gap and recruiter-capacity / requisition-load math (logic_input). (4) Interviewing & Selection -> selection-ratio and 4/5ths adverse-impact arithmetic plus SQL over an ATS applicants table (stage funnel, pass-through, national-hire mix for Emiratisation/Saudisation) - the defensible, computable half of selection. Engines used: spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql (3+ engines, varied sitting). HONEST LIMITATION: the qualitative core of interviewing (probing quality, bias in live judgement beyond the 4/5ths check), employer-brand narrative, and onboarding experience design are NOT assessed here; this sandbox certifies recruiting NUMERACY and ATS data fluency, not interpersonal recruiting craft. A behavioural/CBI layer should complement it for a full picture.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 6 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Logic input, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Funnel Yield & Recruitment-Metrics Analytics**

- **Recruitment Funnel Conversion & Yield-Ratio Build** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: SHRM / CIPD Recruitment Metrics Standards
  - _Measures:_ Computing stage-to-stage funnel conversion rates, overall source yield (applications per hire), offer-acceptance and renege rates - the core numeracy behind every recruitment-metrics dashboard.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Gulf Bank (Abu Dhabi) ran a campaign to fill its 2025 Relationship Manager intake. The applicant funnel for the period: 4,000 applications received, 1,200 passed CV screen, 480 completed phone screen, 180 attended a panel interview, 60 received offers, 48 accepted offers, and 45 started (3 reneged). The recruiting team must report stage-to-stage conversion rates, the overall application-to-hire yield, the offer-acceptance rate, and the renege (offer-decline-after-accept) rate so leadership can see where the funnel leaks. Build the conversion column and the summary yield metrics in the pre-populated grid.
  - _Model answer:_ Stage counts (col B): Applications 4000, CV-screen pass 1200, Phone-screen pass 480, Panel interview 180, Offers 60, Offers accepted 48, Starts 45. Stage-to-stage conversion (col C) = current stage / prior stage x 100: CV pass-through = 1200/4000 = 30.00%; Phone = 480/1200 = 40.00%; Panel = 180/480 = 37.50%; Offer = 60/180 = 33.33%; Accept = 48/60 = 80.00%; Start = 45/48 = 93.75%. Summary block: Overall yield (applications per hire) = 4000/45 = 88.89; Application-to-hire % = 45/4000 x 100 = 1.125%; Offer-acceptance rate = 48/60 x 100 = 80.00%; Renege rate = (48-45)/48 x 100 = 6.25%. Cells expected: C4 (CV%) 30, C5 (phone%) 40, C6 (panel%) 37.5, C7 (offer%) 33.333, C8 (accept%) 80, C9 (start%) 93.75, B13 (apps-per-hire) 88.889, B14 (app-to-hire %) 1.125, B15 (offer-accept %) 80, B16 (renege %) 6.25.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - CV-screen pass-through % (1200/4000) - First-stage conversion (=30.00%) computed against the correct prior-stage denominator
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Offer-stage conversion % (60/180) - Mid-funnel conversion (=33.33%) - tests chaining ratios down the correct prior stage
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Offer-acceptance rate % (48/60) - Acceptance rate (=80.00%) - the headline sourcing-quality KPI
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Overall yield: applications per hire (4000/45) - Source-yield ratio (=88.89) used for channel planning
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Application-to-hire % (45/4000) - End-to-end funnel efficiency (=1.125%)
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Renege rate % ((48-45)/48) - Offer-decline-after-accept leakage (=6.25%) - tests the subtle accepted-vs-started distinction
- **Time-to-Fill, Cost-per-Hire & Channel Cost Efficiency** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: SHRM Talent Acquisition Metrics / ANSI Cost-per-Hire Standard
  - _Measures:_ ANSI/SHRM-standard cost-per-hire (internal + external over total hires), channel-level unit economics, and the time-to-fill vs time-to-start distinction - the efficiency half of recruitment metrics.
  - _Scenario:_ Saudi Telecom Services (Riyadh) closed 25 hires last quarter. Internal recruiting costs: SAR 180,000 (recruiter salaries, ATS licence, careers-page hosting). External costs: agency fees SAR 240,000, job-board spend SAR 60,000, referral bonuses SAR 70,000. Requisitions were opened (approved) on day 0; the first qualified candidate was sourced on average 18 days later; offers were accepted on average day 52; and new hires started on average day 71. Of the 25 hires, 12 came from agencies (SAR 240,000), 8 from job boards (SAR 60,000), and 5 from referrals (SAR 70,000). Compute the cost-per-hire, the cost-per-hire by each channel, the time-to-fill, and the time-to-start.
  - _Model answer:_ Cost-per-hire (ANSI) = (internal + external costs) / number of hires = (180000 + 240000 + 60000 + 70000) / 25 = 550000 / 25 = SAR 22,000. Agency cost-per-hire = 240000 / 12 = SAR 20,000. Job-board cost-per-hire = 60000 / 8 = SAR 7,500. Referral cost-per-hire = 70000 / 5 = SAR 14,000. Time-to-fill = days from requisition open to offer accepted = 52. Time-to-start = days from requisition open to first day = 71. (Time-to-source = 18 is given context, not asked.) Fields: cost_per_hire 22000, agency_cph 20000, jobboard_cph 7500, referral_cph 14000, time_to_fill 52, time_to_start 71.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Blended cost-per-hire (SAR) - ANSI cost-per-hire = total (internal+external) / hires = 22,000 - tests inclusion of ALL cost pools
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Agency channel cost-per-hire (SAR) - Channel unit economics = 240000/12 = 20,000
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Job-board channel cost-per-hire (SAR) - Channel unit economics = 60000/8 = 7,500 (cheapest channel)
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Referral channel cost-per-hire (SAR) - Channel unit economics = 70000/5 = 14,000
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Time-to-fill (days, req-open to offer-accepted) - Time-to-fill = 52 - tests using the offer-accepted milestone, not start date
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Time-to-start (days, req-open to first day) - Time-to-start = 71 - tests distinguishing fill from start (the onboarding-handover boundary)

**Pillar - Sourcing-Channel Economics & Quality of Hire**

- **Channel Net-Hires Sensitivity & Weighted Source Scorecard** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18.3 min · ref: CIPD Resourcing & Talent Planning / AFP Ratio Analysis
  - _Measures:_ Modelling sourcing-channel yield as a multiplicative funnel, then stress-testing net hires across volume and offer-accept rate with a native two-variable data table - the analytical backbone of channel-mix and employer-brand investment decisions.
  - _Scenario:_ Dubai Holding's talent team is deciding how hard to lean on a premium LinkedIn-sourcing campaign for 2025 senior hires. Each qualified candidate the campaign surfaces converts to a net hire only after passing interview and accepting an offer. Net hires = Qualified candidates x Pass-to-offer rate x Offer-accept rate. The base case: 200 qualified candidates, a 25% pass-to-offer rate, and an 80% offer-accept rate. Leadership wants a two-variable sensitivity table showing Net Hires across a range of qualified-candidate volumes (rows) and offer-accept rates (columns), holding pass-to-offer at 25%, so they can see how the hire count moves with both sourcing volume and offer competitiveness. Build the base-case net-hires formula and the native two-variable data table.
  - _Model answer:_ Base-case net-hires formula in B5 = Qualified x PassToOffer x OfferAccept = 200 x 0.25 x 0.80 = 40. Two-variable data table: row input cell = qualified candidates (B1), column input cell = offer-accept rate (B3); pass-to-offer fixed at B2 = 0.25. Row headers (qualified): 150, 200, 250. Column headers (offer-accept): 70%, 80%, 90%. Net hires = Qualified x 0.25 x AcceptRate. Corner/interior values: low corner (150, 70%) = 150 x 0.25 x 0.70 = 26.25; base/centre (200, 80%) = 200 x 0.25 x 0.80 = 40; high corner (250, 90%) = 250 x 0.25 x 0.90 = 56.25. The table range must be a native data table {=TABLE(...)}, not typed numbers.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base-case net hires (200 x 25% x 80%) - Multiplicative funnel formula in the corner driver cell = 40
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sensitivity grid is a native two-variable data table - Range is formula-driven {=TABLE(row,col)} not hardcoded - tests genuine data-table skill
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner: 150 qualified, 70% accept - Interior value 150 x 0.25 x 0.70 = 26.25
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre / base case: 200 qualified, 80% accept - Centre value = 40 reconciles to the base-case driver cell
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner: 250 qualified, 90% accept - Interior value 250 x 0.25 x 0.90 = 56.25
- **Source-of-Hire Quality Index & Cost-Adjusted Yield** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 15 min · ref: SHRM Quality-of-Hire / CIPD Source Effectiveness
  - _Measures:_ Constructing a composite quality-of-hire index from performance and retention, then normalising it against channel spend to produce a quality-per-cost ranking - moving sourcing decisions from gut feel to a defensible scorecard.
  - _Scenario:_ Qatar National Logistics evaluates four sourcing channels for its operations hires. For each channel you have: hires made, average 90-day performance rating of those hires (1-5 scale), 12-month retention rate of those hires (%), and total channel spend (QAR). The team wants a blended Quality-of-Hire index per channel = (performance rating / 5) x retention rate, expressed as a percentage, and a cost-adjusted yield = Quality-of-Hire index points delivered per QAR 1,000 of spend, so they can rank channels on quality-per-dirham, not just volume. Channels: Referrals (10 hires, rating 4.4, retention 92%, spend QAR 50,000); Agency (8 hires, rating 3.6, retention 70%, spend QAR 160,000); Job board (12 hires, rating 3.5, retention 65%, spend QAR 36,000); University (6 hires, rating 3.9, retention 88%, spend QAR 24,000). Build the Quality-of-Hire and cost-adjusted-yield columns.
  - _Model answer:_ Quality-of-Hire index (%) = (rating/5) x retention% x 100, i.e. (rating/5) x retention (retention entered as a fraction). Referrals = (4.4/5) x 0.92 = 0.88 x 0.92 = 0.8096 -> 80.96%. Agency = (3.6/5) x 0.70 = 0.72 x 0.70 = 0.504 -> 50.40%. Job board = (3.5/5) x 0.65 = 0.70 x 0.65 = 0.455 -> 45.50%. University = (3.9/5) x 0.88 = 0.78 x 0.88 = 0.6864 -> 68.64%. Cost-adjusted yield = (QoH index points x hires) / (spend / 1000), i.e. total quality points delivered per QAR 1,000. Referrals = (80.96 x 10) / (50000/1000) = 809.6 / 50 = 16.19. Agency = (50.40 x 8) / 160 = 403.2 / 160 = 2.52. Job board = (45.50 x 12) / 36 = 546 / 36 = 15.17. University = (68.64 x 6) / 24 = 411.84 / 24 = 17.16. Ranking on quality-per-dirham: University > Referrals > Job board > Agency.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Referrals Quality-of-Hire index % ((4.4/5)x92%) - Composite QoH = 80.96% - tests normalising a 1-5 rating and multiplying by retention
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Agency Quality-of-Hire index % ((3.6/5)x70%) - Composite QoH = 50.40% (the lowest-quality channel)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Job-board Quality-of-Hire index % ((3.5/5)x65%) - Composite QoH = 45.50%
    - `cell_value` (w3) - University cost-adjusted yield (points per QAR 1,000) - (68.64x6)/24 = 17.16 - the top channel once cost is netted, not the highest-volume one
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Agency cost-adjusted yield (points per QAR 1,000) - (50.40x8)/160 = 2.52 - exposes the expensive low-quality channel

**Pillar - Workforce Planning & Defensible Selection**

- **Headcount-Gap, Recruiter Capacity & Selection-Ratio / 4-5ths Math** &nbsp; `Logic input` · advanced · 10 min · ref: EEOC Uniform Guidelines (4/5ths Rule) / SHRM Workforce Planning
  - _Measures:_ Workforce-gap arithmetic that nets growth against attrition, capacity planning against recruiter throughput, and the EEOC selection-ratio / 4-5ths adverse-impact calculation that underpins defensible, Emiratisation-aware screening.
  - _Scenario:_ First Abu Dhabi region operations plans its 2025 ramp. Target end-of-year headcount is 520; current headcount is 430; expected attrition over the year is 8% of the current headcount. The TA team has 6 recruiters, each able to close 30 hires/year. Separately, for selection-defensibility the team reviews a screening test: of 250 UAE-national applicants, 120 passed the test; of 300 expatriate applicants, 180 passed. Compute the net hires required (gap + attrition replacement), the recruiter capacity vs requirement, the selection ratio for each group, and the adverse-impact ratio (4/5ths) of nationals relative to the higher-passing group.
  - _Model answer:_ Attrition replacement = 8% x 430 = 34.4 (keep as 34.4; tolerance covers rounding). Growth gap = target - current = 520 - 430 = 90. Net hires required = growth gap + attrition replacement = 90 + 34.4 = 124.4. Recruiter annual capacity = 6 x 30 = 180. Capacity surplus/(shortfall) vs requirement = 180 - 124.4 = 55.6 (positive = adequate). Selection ratios: nationals = 120/250 = 0.48 (48%); expats = 180/300 = 0.60 (60%). Higher-passing group = expats at 60%. Adverse-impact ratio (4/5ths) = national rate / expat rate = 0.48 / 0.60 = 0.80. A ratio of exactly 0.80 sits on the 4/5ths threshold (not below it), so it does NOT trip the adverse-impact flag. Fields: net_hires_required 124.4, recruiter_capacity 180, capacity_gap 55.6, national_selection_ratio 0.48, expat_selection_ratio 0.60, adverse_impact_ratio 0.80.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Net hires required (growth gap + attrition) - 124.4 = (520-430) + 8%x430 - tests netting growth AND replacement, the classic gap-plan error
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Annual recruiter capacity (6 x 30) - 180 hires of throughput
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Capacity surplus vs requirement - 180 - 124.4 = 55.6 - tests whether the plan is staffable
    - `logic_value` (w1) - National-applicant selection ratio (120/250) - 0.48 selection rate for the protected/national group
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Expat-applicant selection ratio (180/300) - 0.60 selection rate (the reference / higher-passing group)
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Adverse-impact (4/5ths) ratio of nationals vs reference - 0.48/0.60 = 0.80 - tests dividing by the HIGHEST-passing group and reading the 4/5ths threshold correctly
- **ATS Applicant-Tracking Funnel Interrogation (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA DMBOK / SHRM Recruiting Analytics
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating an ATS schema to aggregate hires by sourcing channel with correct filtering and ordering - the SQL fluency a modern TA analyst needs to drive channel-budget decisions from system-of-record data rather than spreadsheets.
  - _Scenario:_ A GCC bank's applicant-tracking system stores one row per applicant in an 'applicants' table with the requisition, sourcing channel, nationality flag (is_national), the furthest stage reached, and whether the applicant was ultimately hired. The TA lead wants to know which sourcing channels delivered the most actual hires so the 2026 channel budget can be reallocated. Write ONE query that returns, per source channel, the number of hired applicants - highest first.
  - _Model answer:_ Filter to hired applicants and aggregate by source: SELECT source, COUNT(*) AS hires FROM applicants WHERE hired = true GROUP BY source ORDER BY hires DESC, source. The seed data is constructed so the channel hire counts produce a clear, deterministic descending order with a tie broken by source name (hence the secondary ORDER BY source). Graded by result-set match against the master query, order-sensitive (ordered = true) because the prompt asks for highest-first ranking.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Hires per source channel, highest first (columns: source, hires) - Correct WHERE hired filter + GROUP BY source + COUNT + ORDER BY hires DESC; result set and ranking order match the master query exactly

---

### 2.5 Talent Management & Organizational Development (OD)

Talent Management & OD is a predominantly qualitative HR function (talent reviews, calibration discussions, culture and change work), so the sandbox targets the quantitative/analytical slice that drives those decisions: 9-box talent-review math, forced performance-calibration distributions, attrition/retention and flight-risk indices, span-of-control and bench-strength org-design ratios, and HRIS interrogation. Six skills were proposed (the source skills list was empty): Succession Planning & 9-Box Calibration; Performance Management & Calibration; Competency Frameworks & Skills-Gap Analysis; Workforce/Org Design & Span-of-Control; Engagement, Attrition & Retention Analytics; High-Potential (HiPo) Identification & Talent Review. The sitting has 3 pillars and 4 blocks across 3 engines (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql) with concrete AED/SAR GCC scenarios and real standards (SHRM/CIPD, SuccessionFactors/9-box practice, ISO 30414 human-capital reporting, GOSI-context turnover math). All checkpoints are objective numeric/array/SQL matches; no free-text talent narratives or development plans are graded - that limitation is flagged per block in engine_fit.

**Skills:** Succession Planning & 9-Box Calibration · Performance Management & Calibration · Competency Frameworks & Skills-Gap Analysis · Workforce / Org Design & Span-of-Control · Engagement, Attrition & Retention Analytics · High-Potential (HiPo) Identification & Talent Review

**Engine fit:** Talent Management & OD is largely non-quantitative (talent-review facilitation, culture/change work, IDPs, written succession narratives) - none of which is auto-gradable. The blueprint therefore measures the ANALYTICAL spine that underpins those decisions, which maps cleanly onto the four engines: (1) spreadsheet for the 9-box talent grid and bench-strength/span-of-control org-design ratios (deterministic cell math from performance/potential scores and headcount); (2) advanced_spreadsheet for a two-variable salary-increase-budget / merit-matrix sensitivity table (native data table across performance rating x compa-ratio band); (3) logic_input for HiPo flight-risk and retention-index scoring plus annualised attrition math (exact weighted-index and rate formulas that reconcile); (4) sql over a seeded HRIS talent table for talent-review aggregates (ready-now successors per critical role, regretted-attrition by grade). HONEST LIMITS: the engines cannot assess the QUALITATIVE core of the role - calibration-meeting facilitation, the soundness of a succession narrative, change-readiness diagnosis, or development-plan quality. What is graded is the candidate's command of the numbers a Talent/OD professional must get right BEFORE those conversations (correct 9-box placement, a valid forced distribution, a defensible flight-risk index, accurate turnover/bench metrics). This is a strong proxy for analytical rigour but is not a complete measure of OD competence.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 5 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Logic input, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Talent Review & Succession Analytics**

- **9-Box Grid Placement & Bench-Strength Roll-Up** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: SHRM Talent Management BoCK / 9-Box Talent Review practice
  - _Measures:_ Correctly operationalising a 9-box talent grid into a numeric index, applying the ready-successor rule, and rolling up bench-strength metrics that feed succession decisions.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Falcon Holding (Abu Dhabi) is running its annual talent review for 6 division heads. Each leader carries a Performance score (1-3: 1=Low, 2=Solid, 3=High) and a Potential score (1-3: 1=Limited, 2=Growth, 3=High). The 9-box cell index is computed as box = (Potential - 1) * 3 + Performance, giving 1-9 where box 9 = top-right 'Star'. HR policy: a leader is a 'Ready Successor' (flag = 1) only if box >= 8 (i.e. High Potential with Solid-or-better Performance: box 8 or 9). The CHRO needs the grid populated and three roll-ups: count of Ready Successors, the average box index across the 6 leaders, and the Bench-Strength Ratio = Ready Successors / number of critical roles (critical roles = 4, given). Pre-populated grid has each leader's Performance and Potential in columns B and C; the candidate must compute box index (D), the Ready flag (E), and the three summary cells.
  - _Model answer:_ Leaders rows 4-9. D = (C-1)*3 + B per row: L1 (P=3,Pot=3) box 9; L2 (P=2,Pot=3) box 8; L3 (P=3,Pot=2) box 6; L4 (P=1,Pot=2) box 4; L5 (P=2,Pot=2) box 5; L6 (P=3,Pot=1) box 3. E = IF(D>=8,1,0): L1=1, L2=1, rest 0. D12 Ready count = SUM(E4:E9) = 2. D13 Average box = AVERAGE(D4:D9) = (9+8+6+4+5+3)/6 = 35/6 = 5.833333. D14 Bench-Strength Ratio = D12 / 4 (critical roles) = 2/4 = 0.5.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Box index L1 = 9 (High/High Star) - 9-box index formula (Potential-1)*3+Performance on the top-right case
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Box index L4 = 4 (Limited potential, low perf) - Index applied correctly to a low-quadrant leader
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Ready flag L2 = 1 (box 8 qualifies) - Ready-successor threshold rule box>=8 catches the boundary case
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Ready Successor count = 2 - Roll-up SUM of ready flags across the cohort
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Average box index = 5.833 - AVERAGE across the 6 box indices (tolerance for rounding)
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Bench-Strength Ratio = 0.50 - Ready successors divided by critical roles - the headline succession KPI
- **HiPo Flight-Risk & Retention Index** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: CIPD Talent Management & Retention / ISO 30414 human-capital metrics
  - _Measures:_ Building a defensible weighted flight-risk index (including correctly inverting a satisfaction driver into a risk driver), applying a decision threshold, and quantifying retention-offer cost.
  - _Scenario:_ Riyadh-based Najd Capital flags a High-Potential analyst for a targeted retention review. The Flight-Risk Index is a weighted 0-100 score from four normalised drivers, each rated 0-10 then weighted: Compensation gap below market (weight 0.35), Time since last promotion (weight 0.25), Manager-relationship score INVERTED i.e. risk = 10 - score (weight 0.20), and External-market demand (weight 0.20). Index = SUM(driver_0to10 * weight) * 10 to put it on a 0-100 scale. Drivers given: Comp gap = 8, Time-in-role = 6, Manager relationship score (satisfaction) = 7 so its risk contribution uses (10-7)=3, External demand = 9. Policy: Retention-Priority flag = 1 if Index >= 65, else 0. Also compute the candidate's Retention-Offer Cost as a one-off: market-adjustment of SAR 4,500/month uplift x 12 months = annualised retention cost. Fields: flight_risk_index, manager_risk_contribution, retention_priority_flag, annual_retention_cost.
  - _Model answer:_ manager_risk_contribution = 10 - 7 = 3. Weighted sum = 8*0.35 + 6*0.25 + 3*0.20 + 9*0.20 = 2.80 + 1.50 + 0.60 + 1.80 = 6.70. flight_risk_index = 6.70 * 10 = 67.0. retention_priority_flag = 1 (67 >= 65). annual_retention_cost = 4500 * 12 = 54000 (SAR).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Manager risk contribution = 3 (10 - satisfaction 7) - Correctly inverts a satisfaction score into a risk driver
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Flight-Risk Index = 67.0 - Weighted multi-driver index on a 0-100 scale
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Retention-Priority flag = 1 - Threshold decision rule applied to the index (boundary above 65)
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Annual retention cost = 54,000 SAR - Annualisation of the monthly comp uplift

**Pillar - Performance Calibration & Reward Modelling**

- **Merit-Matrix Salary-Budget Sensitivity Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18.3 min · ref: WorldatWork Total Rewards / SHRM Compensation - merit matrix design
  - _Measures:_ Constructing a native two-variable sensitivity table for a merit-budget model so Comp can see total cost across the performance x multiplier grid - core to calibration-driven reward planning.
  - _Scenario:_ Doha-based Al-Wakra Logistics is modelling next year's merit-increase budget. The annual merit % an employee receives is a function of TWO inputs: their performance rating and a Merit Multiplier set by Comp. The base formula for one representative employee on a base salary of QAR 240,000 is: Annual Merit Cost = Base x (PerfRating x Multiplier) / 100, where PerfRating runs 3-5 and Multiplier runs 1.0-1.4. The candidate must (a) build the live merit-cost cell B5 = (B1 * (B2 * B3)) / 100 where B1=base 240000, B2=PerfRating, B3=Multiplier, then (b) build a two-variable data table over PerfRating (column headers C8:E8 = 3, 4, 5) and Multiplier (row headers A9:A11 = 1.0, 1.2, 1.4) showing annual merit cost. It MUST be a native data table, not hardcoded. Corner C9 = rating 3 / mult 1.0; centre D10 = rating 4 / mult 1.2; high corner E11 = rating 5 / mult 1.4.
  - _Model answer:_ B5 = (240000 * (B2 * B3)) / 100 at base inputs. Data table cell formula per (rating r, multiplier m) = 240000 * r * m / 100. C9 (r=3,m=1.0) = 240000*3*1.0/100 = 7200. D10 (r=4,m=1.2) = 240000*4*1.2/100 = 11520. E11 (r=5,m=1.4) = 240000*5*1.4/100 = 16800. The candidate sets the data-table corner = B5, column input = PerfRating cell (B2), row input = Multiplier cell (B3), and fills C9:E11 with a native {=TABLE()}.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - C9:E11 is a native data table (not hardcoded) - Use of a genuine two-variable data table / array formula rather than typed numbers
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Live merit cost B5 = 11,520 (base case rating 4 x mult 1.2) - The driver formula links base, rating and multiplier correctly
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner C9 = 7,200 (rating 3, mult 1.0) - Data-table low corner value
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre D10 = 11,520 (rating 4, mult 1.2) - Data-table interior base-case value
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner E11 = 16,800 (rating 5, mult 1.4) - Data-table high corner value
- **Forced-Distribution Calibration Reconciliation** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 8.3 min · ref: CIPD Performance Management / forced-ranking calibration guidance
  - _Measures:_ Translating a guided/forced distribution policy into exact target headcounts and identifying calibration over-allocation that must be challenged in the talent review.
  - _Scenario:_ Kuwait's Burgan Manufacturing applies a guided performance distribution to a calibration population of 400 employees across 5 rating bands. Target distribution: Band 5 (Exceptional) 10%, Band 4 (Exceeds) 20%, Band 3 (Meets) 45%, Band 2 (Partially Meets) 20%, Band 1 (Below) 5%. The candidate must compute the TARGET headcount per band, then reconcile against managers' first-pass submission of Band 5 = 60 people. HR rule: a band is 'over-allocated' (flag 1) if submitted count exceeds target by more than 10 headcount. Fields: target_band5, target_band3, band5_overage, band5_over_flag, total_target_check.
  - _Model answer:_ target_band5 = 400 * 0.10 = 40. target_band3 = 400 * 0.45 = 180. band5_overage = submitted 60 - target 40 = 20. band5_over_flag = 1 (20 > 10). total_target_check = sum of all five target bands = 40 + 80 + 180 + 80 + 20 = 400 (must reconcile to population).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Target Band 5 headcount = 40 - Applying a distribution percentage to the calibration population
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Target Band 3 headcount = 180 - Largest-band target computed correctly
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Band 5 overage = 20 - Variance of submitted vs target headcount
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Band 5 over-allocation flag = 1 - Calibration over-allocation threshold rule (>10 over)
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Total target check = 400 (reconciles to population) - All band targets sum back to the calibration population

**Pillar - Workforce Analytics & HRIS Interrogation**

- **Talent-Review HRIS Query (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: ISO 30414 Human Capital Reporting / DAMA DMBOK data interrogation
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating an HRIS talent table to aggregate ready-now successor depth by critical grade - the data backbone of a succession review.
  - _Scenario:_ Manama-based Gulf Pearl Bank stores its talent-review outcomes in an HRIS table. The Head of OD wants, for succession planning, the count of employees flagged ready_now = true for each critical grade, but ONLY for grades that are designated critical (is_critical_role = true), ranked by ready-successor count highest first. Seeded table employees(id, name, grade, division, is_critical_role boolean, ready_now boolean, regretted_leaver boolean). Return columns: grade, ready_count.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT grade, COUNT(*) AS ready_count FROM employees WHERE is_critical_role = true AND ready_now = true GROUP BY grade ORDER BY ready_count DESC, grade. The seed contains several grades; only critical-role rows with ready_now true are counted, grouped by grade, and ordered by count descending (grade as the tiebreaker for deterministic ordering).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master: ready-now successors per critical grade, highest first - Correct filtering (critical roles + ready_now), grouping by grade, aggregate count, and descending order

---

### 2.6 Learning & Development (L&D) Operations & Instructional Design

L&D Operations & Instructional Design is largely a qualitative discipline (program design, facilitation, career pathing), so this blueprint isolates the quantitative/analytical slice that is auto-gradable: training ROI and benefit-cost economics (Phillips Level-5), per-head cost and capacity/utilization modelling with a two-variable sensitivity table, competency-gap and bench-strength scoring (weighted gap index), and LMS/HRIS data interrogation for completion, compliance, and overdue-training analytics. Three pillars across four blocks using four engines (logic_input, spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, sql) so the sitting is varied. All scenarios use concrete GCC figures (AED/SAR) and real professional standards (Kirkpatrick, Phillips ROI Methodology, ATD, SHRM/CIPD, Saudi HRDF, 9-box succession, ISO 30414 human-capital reporting). Free-text deliverables (storyboards, facilitator guides, course narratives) are deliberately excluded as ungradable.

**Skills:** Training Needs Analysis · Program Design · Delivery & Facilitation · Competency Frameworks · L&D Evaluation (ROI) · Succession & Career Pathing

**Engine fit:** L&D is a predominantly qualitative function — instructional design, facilitation quality, course storyboarding and career conversations are subjective and NOT auto-gradable, so they are excluded by design. The gradable core is the L&D operations analytics layer that any modern L&D / HR-analytics professional must own: (1) Evaluation/ROI math — benefit-cost ratio and Phillips Level-5 ROI%, fully deterministic, mapped to logic_input.
