(2) Training economics — cost-per-learner, blended-delivery cost build, and a two-variable cohort-size x seat-cost sensitivity table, mapped to spreadsheet + advanced_spreadsheet (the data table needs is_array_formula). (3) Competency-gap & succession scoring — a weighted competency-gap index and bench-strength/coverage ratio, deterministic logic_input. (4) Data interrogation — LMS/HRIS completion, compliance-overdue and cost-per-department analytics, mapped to sql over a seeded enrollments/courses schema. Every block grades on exact numeric cell/field values or a master query result set; no free text is scored. This is an honest, high-fidelity proxy: it measures whether the candidate can run the numbers an L&D operations role actually owns, not whether they can write a lesson plan.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 5 tasks · engines: Logic input, Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Evaluation, ROI & Training Economics**

- **Phillips Level-5 ROI of a Leadership Programme** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: Phillips ROI Methodology / Kirkpatrick Four Levels / ATD
  - _Measures:_ L&D Evaluation (ROI) — Phillips Level-5 benefit-cost and ROI computation with fully-loaded cost capture
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates National Bank ran a 3-day 'Branch Manager Excellence' programme for 40 managers in Dubai. Fully-loaded programme cost: facilitator fees AED 90,000, venue & catering AED 36,000, courseware & licences AED 14,000, and participant time cost (salary value of days off the job) AED 60,000 — total cost is the sum of these four. The isolated, monetised business benefit (incremental cross-sell margin attributed to the programme after isolating other factors) is AED 480,000 over 12 months. Compute: (a) total fully-loaded cost, (b) net programme benefit = monetised benefit minus total cost, (c) Benefit-Cost Ratio (BCR) = monetised benefit / total cost, rounded to 2 decimals, and (d) ROI % = (net benefit / total cost) x 100, rounded to 1 decimal.
  - _Model answer:_ Total cost = 90,000 + 36,000 + 14,000 + 60,000 = AED 200,000. Net benefit = 480,000 - 200,000 = AED 280,000. BCR = 480,000 / 200,000 = 2.40. ROI% = (280,000 / 200,000) x 100 = 140.0%. The discriminating skill is including participant time cost in the denominator (a common L&D error is to omit it, which inflates ROI) and keeping BCR and ROI% as the two distinct Phillips outputs.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total fully-loaded cost = AED 200,000 (includes participant time cost) - Captures ALL four cost categories including off-the-job time, per Phillips fully-loaded costing
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Net programme benefit = AED 280,000 - Monetised benefit minus total cost computed correctly
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Benefit-Cost Ratio (BCR) = 2.40 - BCR = benefit / cost, the Phillips Level-5 ratio output
    - `logic_value` (w3) - ROI % = 140.0% - ROI% = net benefit / cost x 100, distinct from BCR
- **Blended-Delivery Cost-per-Learner Build** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 15 min · ref: ATD State of the Industry cost metrics / CIPD L&D benchmarking
  - _Measures:_ Program Design / Training economics — building a fully-linked blended-delivery cost model and deriving cost-per-learner
  - _Scenario:_ VIFM is costing a blended 'Data Literacy for Finance' programme for a Riyadh government entity (cohort of 60 learners, SAR). The model has: e-learning licence SAR 320/learner; 2 virtual instructor-led (VILT) days at facilitator SAR 9,000/day; 1 in-person workshop day at facilitator SAR 12,000 + venue SAR 18,000 + catering SAR 90/learner; LMS hosting & admin overhead SAR 24,000 fixed for the cohort. Complete the linked cost model so the candidate computes: total e-learning cost, total facilitator cost (VILT + in-person), total catering, total variable cost, total cost (variable + fixed overhead), and cost per learner = total cost / 60.
  - _Model answer:_ E-learning = 320 x 60 = SAR 19,200. Facilitator = (2 x 9,000) + 12,000 = 18,000 + 12,000 = SAR 30,000. Catering = 90 x 60 = SAR 5,400. Venue = SAR 18,000 (given). Total variable+direct = e-learning 19,200 + facilitator 30,000 + venue 18,000 + catering 5,400 = SAR 72,600. Total cost = 72,600 + fixed overhead 24,000 = SAR 96,600. Cost per learner = 96,600 / 60 = SAR 1,610. Cells must be formula-linked (e.g. =B-rate*headcount) not hardcoded, mirroring a real cost-build worksheet.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total e-learning licence cost = SAR 19,200 - Per-learner licence x cohort headcount
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Total facilitator cost (VILT + in-person) = SAR 30,000 - Multi-day VILT day-rate plus single in-person day-rate aggregated
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total catering cost = SAR 5,400 - Per-learner catering x in-person attendance
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Total cost (variable + fixed overhead) = SAR 96,600 - Correct separation and summation of variable spend and fixed cohort overhead
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Cost per learner = SAR 1,610 - Total cost divided by cohort headcount — the headline benchmarking unit
- **Cohort-Size x Seat-Cost Sensitivity Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: AFP / CIPD L&D scenario-budgeting practice
  - _Measures:_ Scenario / sensitivity analysis for L&D budgeting using a native two-variable data table
  - _Scenario:_ Using the same blended programme, the L&D budget owner wants a two-variable sensitivity table for TOTAL programme cost (SAR) as cohort size and per-seat e-learning licence both vary. Total cost = (e-learning licence per seat x cohort) + (catering 90 x cohort) + fixed programme cost SAR 60,000 (this bundles facilitator + venue + overhead, held constant). Build a native two-variable data table with cohort sizes {40, 60, 80} down the rows and per-seat licence {280, 320, 360} across the columns. The corner cell must link to the live total-cost formula; the body must be a native data table, not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Total cost = (licence x cohort) + (90 x cohort) + 60,000. Corner cell links to the base total-cost formula. Body via native data table (cohort = row input, licence = column input). Key cells: cohort 40 & licence 280 = (280x40)+(90x40)+60,000 = 11,200+3,600+60,000 = SAR 74,800 (low corner). Cohort 60 & licence 320 = (320x60)+(90x60)+60,000 = 19,200+5,400+60,000 = SAR 84,600 (centre). Cohort 80 & licence 360 = (360x80)+(90x80)+60,000 = 28,800+7,200+60,000 = SAR 96,000 (high corner). The body must be generated by {=TABLE()} not typed.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Body uses a native two-variable data table {=TABLE()} (not hardcoded) - Candidate built a real data table driven by row/column inputs, not pasted values
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (cohort 40, licence 280) = SAR 74,800 - Smallest cohort / cheapest seat scenario total cost
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre / base case (cohort 60, licence 320) = SAR 84,600 - Base-case total cost reconciles to the live model
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (cohort 80, licence 360) = SAR 96,000 - Largest cohort / dearest seat scenario total cost

**Pillar - Competency Frameworks & Succession Analytics**

- **Weighted Competency-Gap Index & Bench Strength** &nbsp; `Logic input` · advanced · 10 min · ref: SHRM / CIPD competency frameworks / 9-box succession / ISO 30414
  - _Measures:_ Training Needs Analysis & Succession — weighted competency-gap scoring and bench-strength / coverage ratio computation
  - _Scenario:_ VIFM is running a Training Needs Analysis for a GCC corporate-treasury team against a 4-competency target framework. Each competency has a target proficiency level (1-5), the team's current average level, and a criticality weight. Data: (1) Cash Forecasting — target 5, current 3, weight 0.40; (2) FX Risk — target 4, current 2, weight 0.30; (3) Banking Systems — target 4, current 3, weight 0.20; (4) Regulatory Reporting — target 3, current 3, weight 0.10. Compute: (a) the weighted competency-gap index = sum of (gap x weight) where gap = max(target - current, 0); (b) the single largest weighted-gap contribution among the four competencies; (c) the bench-strength / readiness ratio for succession = ready_now_successors / critical_roles, given 3 ready-now successors across 12 critical roles, expressed as a percentage rounded to 1 decimal; (d) the number of critical roles still WITHOUT a ready-now successor (critical_roles - ready_now_successors), treating each successor as covering one role.
  - _Model answer:_ Gaps: Cash Forecasting 5-3=2; FX 4-2=2; Systems 4-3=1; Regulatory 3-3=0. Weighted contributions: 2x0.40=0.80; 2x0.30=0.60; 1x0.20=0.20; 0x0.10=0.00. Weighted gap index = 0.80+0.60+0.20+0.00 = 1.60. Largest single weighted contribution = 0.80 (Cash Forecasting). Bench strength = 3/12 = 0.25 = 25.0%. Roles without a ready-now successor = 12 - 3 = 9. The discriminating skills are applying max(gap,0) so an over-target competency does not net off a real gap, and keeping the prioritisation (largest contribution) distinct from the aggregate index.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Weighted competency-gap index = 1.60 - Sum of (positive gap x criticality weight) across the framework
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Largest single weighted-gap contribution = 0.80 - Correct prioritisation of the highest-impact competency to train first
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Bench strength / readiness ratio = 25.0% - Ready-now successors over critical roles, as a percentage
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Critical roles without a ready-now successor = 9 - Succession coverage gap count

**Pillar - LMS / HRIS Data Interrogation**

- **Completion, Compliance & Cost Analytics (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA DMBOK / ISO 30414 human-capital reporting / Saudi HRDF training-compliance reporting
  - _Measures:_ L&D operations analytics — interrogating LMS/HRIS data for compliance backlog and departmental training spend
  - _Scenario:_ An LMS exports an 'enrollments' table for a Saudi entity (SAR). Each row is one learner enrolment in a course with a department, a status ('completed' / 'in_progress' / 'overdue'), whether the course is mandatory/compliance, the seat cost, and a due date. The L&D manager needs the department-level training spend on MANDATORY courses that are NOT yet completed (status 'in_progress' or 'overdue'), to target the compliance backlog. Write ONE query returning each department and its total at-risk mandatory seat cost (column aliases: department, at_risk_cost), highest cost first.
  - _Model answer:_ Filter enrollments WHERE mandatory = true AND status IN ('in_progress','overdue'); GROUP BY department; SUM(seat_cost) AS at_risk_cost; ORDER BY at_risk_cost DESC (tie-break by department for determinism). The discriminating skill is correctly combining the boolean mandatory flag with the multi-value non-completed status set, then aggregating spend per department — not merely counting enrolments. Master: SELECT department, SUM(seat_cost) AS at_risk_cost FROM enrollments WHERE mandatory = true AND status IN ('in_progress','overdue') GROUP BY department ORDER BY at_risk_cost DESC, department.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master: per-department at-risk mandatory cost, highest first - Correct mandatory + non-completed filter, per-department SUM(seat_cost), and descending cost order

---

### 2.7 Centralized HR Shared Services & Operational Operations

HR Shared Services (HRSS) is an operations-delivery function: a centralized service center that runs employee-lifecycle transactions (joiners/movers/leavers), responds to employee/manager queries via a ticketing system against SLAs, processes payroll-input and benefits administration at scale, and governs core HR data quality. The function carried no skills list, so 6 GCC-grounded skills were proposed: (1) Case & Ticketing SLA Management, (2) HR Service Delivery & Cost-to-Serve, (3) Employee Lifecycle Transaction Processing, (4) HR Data Quality & Master-Data Governance, (5) Payroll-Input & Benefits Administration, (6) Workforce & Service Analytics. Although HRSS has soft elements (employee experience, communication), the gradable core is rich and quantitative: SLA attainment math, FTE/productivity and cost-per-transaction modeling, capacity planning, data-quality defect rates, and querying an HRIS case/employee table. The blueprint scores that quantitative slice across 3 pillars and 4 blocks (logic_input, spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, sql), mixing all four engine types except python, at basic/intermediate/advanced difficulty. Frameworks anchored: SHRM/CIPD shared-services practice, ASA/Lean Six Sigma service-ops metrics, GOSI/WPS for GCC payroll compliance, and DAMA DMBOK for data governance.

**Skills:** Case & Ticketing SLA Management · HR Service Delivery & Cost-to-Serve · Employee Lifecycle Transaction Processing (Joiner/Mover/Leaver) · HR Data Quality & Master-Data Governance · Payroll-Input & Benefits Administration (GOSI/WPS) · Workforce & Service Analytics

**Engine fit:** Strong fit for 3 of the 4 engines. HRSS is operations-heavy and its core KPIs are inherently numeric, so the quantitative slice is large and authentic rather than a thin proxy: (a) logic_input cleanly captures SLA-attainment and case-management math (first-contact-resolution rate, SLA-met %, backlog ageing, weighted service-level index) where the candidate computes each ratio by hand; (b) spreadsheet/advanced_spreadsheet capture the cost-to-serve and capacity-planning models that justify a shared-services business case (cost-per-transaction, FTE requirement from Erlang-style volume/AHT math, a two-variable sensitivity table over volume and average-handle-time driving required FTE); (c) sql is a natural fit for interrogating a seeded HRSS case/ticketing table (SLA-breach counts by category, ageing buckets, agent throughput). The NON-gradable parts of HRSS - employee-experience qualitative feedback, communication tone, change-management judgement, drafting of policy responses - are deliberately excluded; this blueprint measures the analytical, operations-management spine of the role (service economics, SLA discipline, data-quality control, and HRIS data interrogation), which is exactly what distinguishes a competent HRSS operations professional from an administrator. No engine was a poor fit, so no proxy compromise was needed; python was not used because every task is expressible in the other four engines.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 5 tasks · engines: Logic input, SQL, Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet

**Pillar - Service Performance & SLA Governance**

- **Service-Desk SLA & Case-Resolution Scorecard** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 9 min · ref: SHRM / CIPD HR Shared-Services Practice; ASA Service-Level Metrics
  - _Measures:_ Computing core service-desk KPIs (FCR rate, SLA attainment, backlog ageing concentration) and combining them into a weighted service-health composite the way an HRSS team lead reports to leadership.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates National Bank's HR Shared Services Center (Dubai) reports its monthly service desk. In the period it received 4,800 employee/manager cases and closed 4,560 of them; 240 remain open at period end. Of the closed cases, 3,648 were resolved at first contact (no re-assignment or follow-up). The SLA target is resolution within 24 working hours: 4,104 of the closed cases met that target, the rest breached. Backlog ageing on the 240 open cases: 150 are aged 0-2 days, 60 are aged 3-5 days, 30 are aged over 5 days. The center also tracks a weighted Service Health Index = 0.5 x SLA-met% + 0.3 x First-Contact-Resolution% + 0.2 x (100 - Aged-over-5-days% of open backlog), where each percentage is expressed on a 0-100 scale. Compute each metric.
  - _Model answer:_ FCR% = 3648/4560 = 80.00%. SLA-met% = 4104/4560 = 90.00%. Open-backlog aged-over-5-days% = 30/240 = 12.50%. Weighted Service Health Index = 0.5x90 + 0.3x80 + 0.2x(100-12.5) = 45 + 24 + 17.5 = 86.50. (Note: SLA% and FCR% are denominated on closed cases per the scenario; aged% is on open backlog.)
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - First-contact-resolution rate = 80.00% - fcr_rate
    - `logic_value` (w2) - SLA-met rate = 90.00% - sla_met_rate
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Aged over-5-days share of open backlog = 12.50% - aged_over5_pct
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Weighted Service Health Index = 86.50 - service_health_index
- **HRIS Case-Ledger Interrogation (SLA Breaches by Category)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA International (DMBOK); ITIL-aligned HR Case Management
  - _Measures:_ Writing a single aggregate SQL query over an HRSS ticketing ledger to rank case categories by SLA-breach volume - the data-interrogation skill an HRSS analyst uses to target process fixes.
  - _Scenario:_ The HRSS case-management system stores one row per ticket in table hr_cases (id, employee_id, category, channel, opened_at, closed_at, sla_hours, resolution_hours, agent). A ticket is an SLA breach when resolution_hours > sla_hours. Categories include 'Payroll', 'Leave', 'Benefits', 'Onboarding', 'Letters'. Leadership wants to know which case categories are hurting the SLA most: return, per category, the number of breached tickets and the total tickets, ordered by breach count highest first. The seeded ledger contains roughly two dozen Saudi and UAE entity tickets so the master result is deterministic. Columns required: category, breaches, total_tickets.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT category, COUNT(*) FILTER (WHERE resolution_hours > sla_hours) AS breaches, COUNT(*) AS total_tickets FROM hr_cases GROUP BY category ORDER BY breaches DESC, category. (Equivalent: SUM(CASE WHEN resolution_hours > sla_hours THEN 1 ELSE 0 END).) Grading compares the candidate result set to this master, order-sensitive on breaches DESC then category.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Per-category breach + total counts match master, ordered by breaches DESC then category - category_breach_ranking

**Pillar - Service Economics & Capacity Engineering**

- **Cost-to-Serve & Cost-per-Transaction Model** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: CIPD Shared-Services Costing; Lean Six Sigma Service Operations
  - _Measures:_ Building a shared-services cost-to-serve model: aggregating cost pools, deriving blended and channel-specific cost-per-transaction, and quantifying the self-service savings that justify HRSS automation investment.
  - _Scenario:_ A GCC government entity in Riyadh is building the annual cost case for its HR Shared Services Center (figures in SAR 000s unless noted). Fully-loaded staff cost is SAR 4,200; technology/HRIS licensing SAR 900; facilities & overhead SAR 600. The center processed 60,000 transactions in the year. Of these, 36,000 are 'self-service' (employee completes it in the portal) and 24,000 are 'agent-assisted'. Internal cost allocation assumes agent-assisted transactions consume 80% of the total operating cost and self-service the remaining 20%. The candidate must complete the model: total operating cost, blended cost per transaction (SAR, full precision), agent-assisted cost-per-transaction, self-service cost-per-transaction, and the % cost saving of self-service vs agent-assisted (on a 0-100 scale).
  - _Model answer:_ Total operating cost = 4200+900+600 = SAR 5,700 (000s) = SAR 5,700,000. Blended cost/txn = 5,700,000/60,000 = SAR 95.00. Agent-assisted pool = 80% x 5,700,000 = 4,560,000 over 24,000 = SAR 190.00/txn. Self-service pool = 20% x 5,700,000 = 1,140,000 over 36,000 = SAR 31.6667/txn. Saving% of self-service vs agent-assisted = (190 - 31.6667)/190 = 83.33%. Cells: total cost, blended, agent-assisted, self-service, saving%.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total operating cost = 5,700 (SAR 000s) - total_operating_cost
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Blended cost per transaction = SAR 95.00 - blended_cost_per_txn
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Agent-assisted cost per transaction = SAR 190.00 - agent_cost_per_txn
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Self-service cost per transaction = SAR 31.67 - selfservice_cost_per_txn
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Self-service saving vs agent-assisted = 83.33% - selfservice_saving_pct
- **Capacity Plan: Required-FTE Sensitivity Table (Volume x AHT)** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18.3 min · ref: AFP/ASA Workforce-Management Capacity Planning; Erlang-style staffing math
  - _Measures:_ Capacity engineering for a shared-services center: deriving required FTE from volume, handle-time and productive-hours, then stress-testing staffing with a native two-variable sensitivity table - the analysis behind an HRSS headcount business case.
  - _Scenario:_ The Riyadh HRSS center plans next year's agent headcount. Base assumptions: monthly case volume 18,000 cases; average handle time (AHT) 20 minutes per case; one productive agent delivers 150 productive hours per month (after shrinkage for leave, training and breaks). Required FTE = (Volume x AHT / 60) / Productive-hours-per-agent. The candidate must first build the base Required-FTE formula cell, then construct a TWO-VARIABLE data table showing Required FTE as monthly volume varies down the rows (15,000 / 18,000 / 21,000) and AHT varies across the columns (15 / 20 / 25 minutes). The data table must be a native array/data-table construct, not typed-in numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Base Required FTE = (18000 x 20 / 60) / 150 = (6000) / 150 = 40.00 FTE. Data-table cells = (Volume x AHT / 60) / 150 for each pair. Corner low (Vol 15,000, AHT 15) = (15000x15/60)/150 = 3750/150 = 25.00. Center (18,000, 20) = 40.00. Corner high (21,000, 25) = (21000x25/60)/150 = 8750/150 = 58.33. The C:E range must be a native {=TABLE()} two-variable data table with the corner cell linking to the base Required-FTE formula, row input = AHT cell, column input = Volume cell.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base Required FTE = 40.00 - base_required_fte
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sensitivity grid is a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - data_table_present
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (Vol 15,000, AHT 15) Required FTE = 25.00 - fte_low_corner
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Center (Vol 18,000, AHT 20) Required FTE = 40.00 - fte_center
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (Vol 21,000, AHT 25) Required FTE = 58.33 - fte_high_corner

**Pillar - Data Quality & Transaction Integrity**

- **HR Master-Data Quality & Payroll-Input Defect Control** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA DMBOK Data-Quality Dimensions; GOSI/WPS GCC Payroll Compliance
  - _Measures:_ Operating an HRSS data-quality gate: de-duplicating defect populations with inclusion-exclusion, expressing defect and first-time-right rates, and measuring the gap to a payroll-compliance control target before a WPS release.
  - _Scenario:_ Before the WPS (Wage Protection System) payroll file is released, the Abu Dhabi HRSS team runs a data-quality gate over 5,000 employee master records. Findings: 120 records have a missing or invalid Emirates ID, 80 have a missing IBAN, 45 have a GOSI/pension contribution base that mismatches the contract salary, and 25 records appear in more than one of those exception lists (counted once in each above). The team also samples 400 payroll-input lines and finds 12 with a keying error. Required-First-Time-Right (FTR) target for payroll input is 98%. Compute: (1) total DISTINCT defective master records (apply inclusion-exclusion so the 25 overlaps are not double-counted), (2) master-data defect rate as a % of 5,000 (0-100 scale), (3) payroll-input First-Time-Right rate from the sample (0-100 scale), and (4) the FTR gap vs the 98% target in percentage points (target minus actual; negative if above target).
  - _Model answer:_ Raw exceptions = 120+80+45 = 245; overlaps double-counted = 25, so distinct defective records = 245 - 25 = 220. Master-data defect rate = 220/5000 = 4.40%. Payroll-input FTR = (400-12)/400 = 388/400 = 97.00%. FTR gap = 98% - 97% = 1.00 percentage point (still 1.0 pt short of target).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Distinct defective master records = 220 - distinct_defects
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Master-data defect rate = 4.40% - defect_rate_pct
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Payroll-input First-Time-Right rate = 97.00% - ftr_rate_pct
    - `logic_value` (w1) - FTR gap vs 98% target = 1.00 percentage point - ftr_gap_pp

---

### 2.8 Employee Relations & Statutory Labor Compliance

Employee Relations & Statutory Labor Compliance is, on its face, a "soft" HR function (grievances, disciplinary fairness, wellbeing, culture/communication) - the day-to-day work is investigation, judgement and written decisions that cannot be auto-graded. This blueprint therefore measures the QUANTITATIVE / ANALYTICAL slice of the ER specialist's job, which is real, defensible work: (1) computing statutory entitlements under GCC labor law - end-of-service gratuity, notice/leave pay, WPS-compliant final settlement; (2) engagement-survey psychometrics and grievance/disciplinary SLA analytics over an HR case database (SQL) and an eNPS/turnover spreadsheet; and (3) a weighted disciplinary-fairness and ER risk-scoring matrix that turns the "is this dismissal defensible / which sites are at risk" judgement into an auditable numeric index. Three pillars, four blocks, three engines (logic_input, sql, spreadsheet) mixing basic/intermediate/advanced. All anchored to UAE Federal Decree-Law No. 33 of 2021, KSA Labor Law / GOSI, WPS, Gallup Q12/eNPS, and ACAS/CIPD disciplinary-fairness practice.

**Skills:** Statutory entitlement & end-of-service settlement math (UAE Decree-Law 33/2021, KSA Labor Law, GOSI/WPS) · Engagement-survey analytics (eNPS, Gallup Q12, favourable-score %) · Grievance & disciplinary case SLA / aging analytics · Disciplinary-fairness defensibility scoring (ACAS/CIPD) · Attrition, absenteeism & wellbeing rate metrics · ER risk-index construction across sites / dimensions

**Engine fit:** Employee Relations is largely non-quantitative, so this sitting deliberately assesses only the parts that ARE auto-gradable, and the rest of the role (investigations, drafting warning letters, tribunal advocacy, culture facilitation) is explicitly out of scope here - it belongs to the MCQ/scenario layer, not the sandbox. The gradable proxies chosen are the genuine numeric core of an ER/compliance specialist: (a) STATUTORY SETTLEMENT MATH is pure arithmetic with a single correct answer (end-of-service gratuity tiers, notice pay, leave encashment, WPS-mandated final pay) - an ideal logic_input fit. (b) CASE & SURVEY ANALYTICS map cleanly to SQL (grievance/disciplinary case table: counts by type, SLA-breach aging, repeat-offender detection) and spreadsheet (eNPS = %Promoters - %Detractors, Q12 favourable %, turnover/absenteeism rates) - exact-value grading. (c) DISCIPLINARY-FAIRNESS / ER-RISK SCORING converts the otherwise-subjective "is this defensible / which site is hottest" call into a weighted index with deterministic inputs, gradable by cell_value - the same technique FP&A uses for decision matrices. What is NOT captured: the quality of an investigation, proportionality judgement on a specific sanction, and tone of employee communication - these are flagged honestly as outside the four engines. No advanced_spreadsheet block is used because ER analytics rarely need a 2-variable data table; the four blocks instead maximise realism across logic_input, sql and spreadsheet.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Logic input, SQL, Spreadsheet

**Pillar - Statutory Entitlements & Final Settlement**

- **End-of-Service Gratuity & Final Settlement (UAE Decree-Law 33/2021)** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: UAE Federal Decree-Law No. 33 of 2021 (Art. 51 EOSB) + WPS / MOHRE final-settlement rules
  - _Measures:_ Correct application of the tiered UAE EOSB formula (21-day vs 30-day bands), daily-rate derivation, leave encashment, and assembling a WPS-compliant net final settlement with lawful deductions.
  - _Scenario:_ Fatima Al-Mansoori resigns from Gulf Falcon Logistics LLC (Dubai, unlimited/standard contract under Decree-Law 33/2021) after exactly 6.0 completed years of continuous service. Her LAST basic salary is AED 18,000/month (allowances are excluded from gratuity). UAE end-of-service gratuity rule: 21 calendar days of basic pay for each of the first 5 years, then 30 calendar days of basic pay for each additional year; daily basic = monthly basic / 30; total EOSB is capped at 2 years' total pay (cap not binding here). At separation she also has 12 accrued-but-untaken annual-leave days to encash (leave day rate = monthly basic / 30) and is owed a pro-rated 13th-month-equivalent bonus of AED 4,500 (given). She must repay an outstanding salary advance of AED 7,000, which is deducted from the gross final settlement. Compute each component and the net final settlement that must be paid through WPS.
  - _Model answer:_ Daily basic = 18000/30 = AED 600. Years 1-5 gratuity = 5 x 21 x 600 = AED 63,000. Year 6 gratuity = 1 x 30 x 600 = AED 18,000. Total EOSB = 63,000 + 18,000 = AED 81,000 (below the 2-year cap of 432,000, so not binding). Leave encashment = 12 x 600 = AED 7,200. Gross final settlement = EOSB 81,000 + leave 7,200 + bonus 4,500 = AED 92,700. Net = 92,700 - 7,000 advance = AED 85,700.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - EOSB first-5-years band (5 x 21 x 600) - Correct 21-day-per-year band on daily basic = AED 63,000
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Total end-of-service gratuity (both bands) - Correct tiered EOSB total = AED 81,000
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Annual-leave encashment (12 x daily basic) - Correct leave-day rate and encashment = AED 7,200
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Gross final settlement before deductions - EOSB + leave + bonus aggregated correctly = AED 92,700
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Net WPS final settlement after advance - Lawful deduction applied; net = AED 85,700

**Pillar - ER Case & Engagement Analytics**

- **Grievance & Disciplinary Case Interrogation (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: ACAS Code of Practice on Disciplinary & Grievance Procedures / CIPD ER case-management standards
  - _Measures:_ Translating an SLA/aging compliance rule into SQL - date arithmetic, NULL-aware open-vs-closed logic, conditional aggregation, GROUP BY with deterministic ordering.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates National Bank's ER team logs every employee case in an er_cases table (one row per case): id, employee_id, site (Abu Dhabi / Dubai / Sharjah), case_type ('grievance' / 'disciplinary' / 'whistleblower'), severity ('low'/'medium'/'high'), opened_date, closed_date (NULL if still open), sla_days (the policy target to close). The Head of ER needs a defensibility view: by case_type, how many cases breached SLA - a breach is a case whose resolution took MORE than its sla_days, where resolution time for a CLOSED case = closed_date - opened_date, and an OPEN case breaches if (current reference date 2025-06-01) - opened_date > sla_days. Return one row per case_type with the breach count, highest breach count first. Columns: case_type, breaches.
  - _Model answer:_ For each case compute days_taken = COALESCE(closed_date, DATE '2025-06-01') - opened_date; flag breach where days_taken > sla_days; SELECT case_type, COUNT(*) FILTER (WHERE breach) AS breaches FROM er_cases GROUP BY case_type ORDER BY breaches DESC, case_type. Seed data is constructed so disciplinary > grievance > whistleblower in breach count, giving a unique deterministic order.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Per-case_type SLA-breach counts in correct order - Open/closed aging logic, breach predicate, GROUP BY + ORDER BY breaches DESC all correct (ordered match)
- **Engagement, eNPS & Attrition Dashboard (Spreadsheet)** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: Gallup Q12 / eNPS methodology + SHRM-CIPD turnover & absenteeism metrics
  - _Measures:_ Building the standard engagement/turnover analytics correctly: eNPS from response bands, average-headcount attrition and voluntary-attrition rates, absenteeism rate, and Q12 favourable-%, all as live formulas.
  - _Scenario:_ Following the annual engagement survey at Saudi Telecom Solutions (Riyadh), the ER analytics lead must finish the workforce-health pack. From 500 survey respondents the 'likelihood to recommend' question yielded 290 Promoters (9-10), 120 Passives (7-8) and 90 Detractors (0-6). eNPS = (%Promoters - %Detractors), reported as a whole-number score on a -100..+100 scale. Separately, for the Riyadh contact-centre: headcount-beginning = 480, headcount-end = 520 (average headcount = mean of the two), 96 leavers during the year (of which 60 were voluntary). Annualised attrition rate = leavers / average headcount; voluntary attrition rate = voluntary leavers / average headcount. Absenteeism: 3,200 absence-days lost against 250 working days x 500 average employees available. The Bradford-style favourable score for the manager-support Q12 item is 410 favourable out of 500 responses. Complete every formula-driven cell; report rates as percentages (e.g. 19.2 means 19.2%).
  - _Model answer:_ %Promoters = 290/500 = 58%, %Detractors = 90/500 = 18%, eNPS = 58 - 18 = 40. Average headcount = (480+520)/2 = 500. Attrition = 96/500 = 19.2%. Voluntary attrition = 60/500 = 12.0%. Absenteeism rate = 3200 / (250 x 500) = 3200/125000 = 2.56%. Q12 favourable % = 410/500 = 82.0%.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w3) - eNPS score (%Promoters - %Detractors) - Correct band percentages and eNPS = 40
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Average headcount - Mean of beginning/ending headcount = 500
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Annualised attrition rate % - leavers / avg headcount = 19.2%
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Voluntary attrition rate % - voluntary leavers / avg headcount = 12.0%
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Absenteeism rate % - absence-days / (working days x avg employees) = 2.56%
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Q12 manager-support favourable % - favourable / responses = 82.0%

**Pillar - Disciplinary Defensibility & ER Risk Scoring**

- **Disciplinary-Fairness & Site ER-Risk Index (Spreadsheet)** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: ACAS Code (fair-procedure tests) + CIPD ER risk-management / weighted-scorecard practice
  - _Measures:_ Constructing weighted decision/scoring matrices: a SUMPRODUCT-over-SUM weighted average for procedural fairness, and a normalised weighted-driver risk index used to rank sites - the auditable, numeric form of ER judgement.
  - _Scenario:_ Qatar Industrial Group's Head of ER must (A) score the defensibility of a contested dismissal and (B) rank three sites on an ER-risk index for the board. (A) FAIRNESS SCORE for the dismissal of an employee at the Doha plant - five fair-procedure criteria, each rated 0-5 by the reviewer and each carrying a weight: Investigation thoroughness (rating 4, weight 3), Written notice of allegations (rating 5, weight 2), Right to be accompanied at hearing (rating 2, weight 2), Consistency vs prior similar cases (rating 3, weight 2), Right of appeal offered (rating 5, weight 1). Weighted fairness score = SUMPRODUCT(ratings, weights) / SUM(weights), reported 0-5. (B) ER-RISK INDEX per site from three normalised drivers each scored 0-100 and weighted: grievance-rate driver (Doha 70, Mesaieed 40, Ras Laffan 55) weight 0.5; attrition driver (Doha 60, Mesaieed 30, Ras Laffan 80) weight 0.3; SLA-breach driver (Doha 50, Mesaieed 20, Ras Laffan 40) weight 0.2. Site risk index = weighted sum of drivers (weights sum to 1). Compute the fairness score, the three site indices, and flag the highest-risk site's index value. Complete all formula-driven cells.
  - _Model answer:_ Fairness: SUMPRODUCT = 4x3 + 5x2 + 2x2 + 3x2 + 5x1 = 12+10+4+6+5 = 37; SUM(weights) = 3+2+2+2+1 = 10; fairness = 37/10 = 3.7. ER-risk indices (weights 0.5/0.3/0.2): Doha = 70x0.5 + 60x0.3 + 50x0.2 = 35+18+10 = 63.0; Mesaieed = 40x0.5 + 30x0.3 + 20x0.2 = 20+9+4 = 33.0; Ras Laffan = 55x0.5 + 80x0.3 + 40x0.2 = 27.5+24+8 = 59.5. Highest-risk site = Doha at 63.0.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Weighted disciplinary-fairness score - SUMPRODUCT(ratings,weights)/SUM(weights) = 3.7
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Doha site ER-risk index - Weighted-driver sum = 63.0
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Mesaieed site ER-risk index - Weighted-driver sum = 33.0
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Ras Laffan site ER-risk index - Weighted-driver sum = 59.5
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Highest-risk site index value - MAX of the three indices identifies Doha = 63.0

---

## Corporate Real Estate

> **Domain review** - engine coverage OK. All 7 CRE blueprints pass every hard constraint: 3 pillars each, 4 or 5 blocks, at least 3 engine types (six use all four; 3.6 uses three), valid engine-to-checkpoint pairings, python correctly excluded, varied difficulty, and honest gradable-slice reframing for soft functions 3.3 (lease admin to abstract finance) and 3.6 (HSE to statutory rate math plus compliance SQL). Framework refs are real (IFRS 16, IAS 17, OSHA 1904, IPMS, EVM/PMI, ESG). All node skills lists were empty, so each blueprint correctly self-proposed skills. Every SQL block uses one sql_result_match, matching the FP&A reference but scoring all-or-nothing.
>
> - _(low)_ 3.6: Advanced difficulty is on the ESG emissions spreadsheet, while the role-defining statutory rate math TRIR and LTIFR is graded as the two easiest blocks. Re-balance so the core math carries the higher tier.
> - _(low)_ 3.6: Only 3 engine types, no advanced_spreadsheet, the lone outlier. Meets the minimum and the justification is sound and honestly stated; flagged for awareness only.
> - _(low)_ 3.7: Two logic_input blocks in a 5-block sitting. Verify they measure distinct computations and do not double-weight one competency.
> - _(low)_ 3.3: 5 blocks span 3 pillars with two logic_input blocks. Confirm pillar-to-block distribution is balanced and no pillar has a single thin block.
> - _(low)_ 3.1: Applies to all 7: each SQL block has one checkpoint, scored pass or fail with no partial credit. Matches the FP&A reference but a second SQL checkpoint would improve reliability.
>
> _Recommendations:_ No blocking issues; all 7 can proceed. Polish: 3.6 move advanced difficulty onto the statutory rate-math logic_input block; 3.7 and 3.3 verify paired logic_input blocks are distinct and pillars balanced; optionally add a second SQL checkpoint for partial credit. Coverage, framework refs, and GCC grounding match FP&A rigor.

### 3.1 Corporate Real Estate Asset Management & Portfolio Strategy

Hands-on sandbox for Corporate Real Estate (CRE) Asset Management & Portfolio Strategy. The function had no seeded skills, so the blueprint is designed to a proposed GCC-grounded skill set (asset-level NOI/valuation, lease-vs-own and capital decisions, and portfolio-level analytics). It is a strongly quantitative function, so all three engines used (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql) map cleanly to auto-gradable numeric outputs. Three pillars / four blocks: (1) Asset Valuation & Performance - a direct-cap NOI-to-value model (spreadsheet) plus a two-variable cap-rate/NOI sensitivity data table (advanced_spreadsheet); (2) Capital & Lease Decision Analytics - a lease-vs-buy / hold-vs-dispose net-present-cost decision computed via logic_input; (3) Portfolio Interrogation - SQL over a building-level portfolio register for occupancy and cost-per-sqm ranking. Figures are denominated in AED/SAR with realistic GCC entities (e.g. Dubai/Riyadh towers), and framework_ref cites RICS Red Book / IVS, IAS 40 Investment Property, IFRS 16 Leases, and IPMS measurement standards.

**Skills:** Income-Capitalization Valuation & NOI Modelling (Direct Cap / IVS) · Investment Property Accounting & Fair Value (IAS 40) · Lease-vs-Own & Capital Decision Analytics (IFRS 16, NPV) · Portfolio Performance & Utilization Analytics (occupancy, cost/sqm) · Sensitivity & Scenario Stress-Testing of Asset Value · Hold-Sell-Refurbish Disposition Strategy

**Engine fit:** Strong fit for all four engines - CRE asset management is inherently quantitative (NOI, cap-rate valuation, vacancy/occupancy, NPV of lease/own decisions, cost-per-sqm, portfolio rollups), so no soft-to-hard re-framing was needed. spreadsheet handles the income-capitalization valuation build (NOI -> value at cap rate, with effective-gross-income and opex line items); advanced_spreadsheet handles the canonical CRE sensitivity grid (value across a cap-rate x NOI matrix via a native data table); logic_input handles the discrete decision math (lease-vs-buy net present cost, IFRS 16 right-of-use / lease-liability slice, hold-vs-dispose); sql handles the portfolio register (per-building occupancy %, opex per sqm, ranked total cost). The only deliberately-excluded slice is the qualitative half of "portfolio strategy" (narrative asset-strategy memos, stakeholder alignment) which is not auto-gradable; that is captured separately by the MCQ layer and not attempted here. No engine limitation flags required.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Asset Valuation & Performance Engineering**

- **Income-Capitalization Valuation Build (NOI to Value)** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: RICS Red Book Global / IVS 105 (Income Approach) / IAS 40
  - _Measures:_ Builds a defensible direct-capitalization valuation: derives EGI net of vacancy plus other income, aggregates opex, computes NOI, and capitalizes it at the market cap rate, then normalizes to value per sqm - the core asset-management valuation workflow under the income approach.
  - _Scenario:_ Marina Crown Tower, a Grade-A commercial asset in Dubai Marina (gross lettable area 18,000 sqm). The pre-populated grid gives potential gross rental income of AED 27,000,000, a vacancy & collection loss of 8%, other income (parking/signage) of AED 1,200,000, and operating expenses split into property management AED 1,350,000, FM & maintenance AED 2,400,000, insurance AED 480,000, and government/municipality fees AED 720,000. The market direct-capitalization rate is 7.5%. The candidate must complete Effective Gross Income (EGI), Total Operating Expenses, Net Operating Income (NOI), the capitalized market value (NOI / cap rate), and the implied value per sqm.
  - _Model answer:_ EGI = PGI*(1-vacancy) + other income = 27,000,000*0.92 + 1,200,000 = 25,040,000. Total Opex = 1,350,000 + 2,400,000 + 480,000 + 720,000 = 4,950,000. NOI = EGI - Opex = 25,040,000 - 4,950,000 = 20,090,000. Market value = NOI / cap rate = 20,090,000 / 0.075 = 267,866,666.67. Value per sqm = 267,866,666.67 / 18,000 = 14,881.48.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Effective Gross Income (EGI) = PGI net of vacancy + other income - EGI cell equals 25,040,000
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total Operating Expenses aggregated - Total opex cell equals 4,950,000
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Net Operating Income (NOI) - NOI cell equals 20,090,000
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Capitalized market value (NOI / cap rate) - Value cell equals 267,866,666.67 (tolerance 1.0)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Implied value per sqm - Value-per-sqm cell equals 14,881.48 (tolerance 0.05)
- **Cap-Rate x NOI Valuation Sensitivity Matrix** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: AFP/FPAC FP&A Body of Knowledge / IVS 105 sensitivity disclosure
  - _Measures:_ Constructs a native two-variable sensitivity/data-table to stress asset value against the two dominant value drivers (cap-rate expansion and NOI movement) - the standard board-pack sensitivity disclosure for a CRE asset, demonstrating array-formula fluency rather than manual recomputation.
  - _Scenario:_ Using a base NOI of AED 20,000,000 and a base cap rate of 7.50%, the candidate must build a two-variable data table showing capitalized asset value (= NOI / cap rate) across cap rates of 7.00% / 7.50% / 8.00% (column axis) and NOI of 18,000,000 / 20,000,000 / 22,000,000 (row axis). The corner cell must link to the base value formula and the body must be driven by a native two-variable data table, not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Corner formula = NOI/cap = 20,000,000/0.075 = 266,666,666.67. Body cells = row-NOI / column-cap. Low corner (cap 7.00%, NOI 18,000,000) = 18,000,000/0.07 = 257,142,857.14. Base/centre (cap 7.50%, NOI 20,000,000) = 266,666,666.67. High corner (cap 8.00%, NOI 22,000,000) = 22,000,000/0.08 = 275,000,000. The 3x3 grid is generated by Excel's {=TABLE(rowInput, colInput)} two-variable data table referencing the cap-rate and NOI base cells.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Body uses a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - The 3x3 result range is a native {=TABLE()} array, not literal values
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner: cap 7.00%, NOI 18.0m - Low-corner cell equals 257,142,857.14 (tolerance 1.0)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Base case: cap 7.50%, NOI 20.0m - Centre cell equals 266,666,666.67 (tolerance 1.0)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner: cap 8.00%, NOI 22.0m - High-corner cell equals 275,000,000 (tolerance 1.0)

**Pillar - Capital & Lease Decision Analytics**

- **Lease-vs-Buy Net Present Cost Decision** &nbsp; `Logic input` · advanced · 10 min · ref: IFRS 16 Leases / CFA Institute capital-budgeting (NPV)
  - _Measures:_ Performs a discounted net-present-cost comparison of leasing against owning, correctly time-weighting recurring cash flows, an upfront capital outlay, and a terminal resale inflow - the central capital-allocation decision in corporate real estate and the quantitative core of an IFRS 16 lease-vs-own analysis.
  - _Scenario:_ A Riyadh-based corporate occupier must decide whether to LEASE or BUY 3,000 sqm of office space for a 3-year horizon, discount rate 9% per annum (discount factors: Y1 0.9174, Y2 0.8417, Y3 0.7722). LEASE option: annual rent of SAR 2,400,000 payable at each year-end (Y1-Y3), no residual. BUY option: upfront purchase price SAR 18,000,000 at time 0, annual opex/service charge of SAR 600,000 payable at each year-end (Y1-Y3), and an expected resale value of SAR 16,500,000 received at end of Y3. The candidate computes the present value of total lease cost, the present value of total ownership cost (net of resale), and the net advantage of buying over leasing (a positive value means buying is cheaper).
  - _Model answer:_ PV of lease cost = 2,400,000*(0.9174+0.8417+0.7722) = 2,400,000*2.5313 = 6,075,120. PV of buy cost = 18,000,000 (t0) + 600,000*(2.5313) - 16,500,000*0.7722 = 18,000,000 + 1,518,780 - 12,741,300 = 6,777,480. Net advantage of buying vs leasing = PV lease cost - PV buy cost = 6,075,120 - 6,777,480 = -702,360 (negative => leasing is the cheaper option).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - PV of total lease cost - pv_lease_cost field equals 6,075,120 (tolerance 50)
    - `logic_value` (w3) - PV of total ownership cost (net of resale) - pv_buy_cost field equals 6,777,480 (tolerance 50)
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Net advantage of buying vs leasing (sign matters) - net_advantage_buy field equals -702,360 (tolerance 50)
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Recommended option implied (1 = Lease cheaper) - recommend_lease flag field equals 1

**Pillar - Portfolio Interrogation & Utilization Analytics**

- **Portfolio Register Cost & Occupancy Query (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA DMBOK / IPMS (International Property Measurement Standards) / RICS portfolio KPIs
  - _Measures:_ Interrogates a portfolio register with relational SQL to compute and rank the two headline asset-management KPIs - occupancy rate and operating cost per sqm - and filter to under-performing assets, the data-driven basis for portfolio rationalization and the hold/refurbish/dispose decision.
  - _Scenario:_ A buildings register table holds the corporate real estate portfolio: id, building_name, city, gla_sqm (gross lettable area), leased_sqm, annual_opex_aed. Seed rows include Marina Crown (Dubai, 18,000 GLA, 16,200 leased, opex 4,950,000), Olaya Plaza (Riyadh, 12,000 GLA, 9,000 leased, opex 2,880,000), Bay Square 3 (Dubai, 8,000 GLA, 7,600 leased, opex 1,760,000), Granada Centre (Riyadh, 15,000 GLA, 10,500 leased, opex 4,200,000), and Corniche One (Abu Dhabi, 20,000 GLA, 19,000 leased, opex 6,200,000). The candidate writes ONE query returning, per building, the building_name, occupancy percentage (leased_sqm / gla_sqm * 100) and operating cost per sqm of GLA (annual_opex_aed / gla_sqm), filtered to buildings below 90% occupancy, ordered by cost per sqm descending.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT building_name, ROUND(leased_sqm::numeric / gla_sqm * 100, 2) AS occupancy_pct, ROUND(annual_opex_aed::numeric / gla_sqm, 2) AS opex_per_sqm FROM buildings WHERE leased_sqm::numeric / gla_sqm < 0.90 ORDER BY opex_per_sqm DESC, building_name. Qualifying rows (occupancy < 90%): Granada Centre (70.00%, 280.00/sqm), Olaya Plaza (75.00%, 240.00/sqm), Marina Crown (90.00% -> EXCLUDED as exactly 90 is not below 90), so expected set is Granada Centre then Olaya Plaza by opex/sqm descending. (Bay Square 95%, Corniche One 95% excluded; Marina Crown exactly 90% excluded.)
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result set matches master (occupancy + cost/sqm, filtered <90%, ranked by cost/sqm desc) - Candidate query result set equals the master query result set, order-sensitive

---

### 3.2 Property Design, Construction, & Capital Project Management

Function 3.2 (Property Design, Construction & Capital Project Management, domain=cre) had an empty skills list, so I first proposed 6 GCC-grounded skills (capital budgeting & cost estimation; earned value management & cost/schedule forecasting; construction cost control & variation/change-order management; interim payment certificates, retention & developer cash flow; investment appraisal for property development NPV/IRR; project risk quantification & contingency drawdown). The role is operationally analytical (cost engineering, EVM, contract administration), so it maps cleanly to the gradable engines with no soft-skill stretch needed. The blueprint has 3 pillars and 4 blocks across 3 engines: (1) Capital Project Estimating & Appraisal - a spreadsheet elemental cost plan + escalation/contingency build, and an advanced_spreadsheet two-variable sensitivity data table for development NPV across yield and construction cost; (2) Earned Value & Cost Control Diagnostics - a logic_input EVM block (CV/SV/CPI/SPI/EAC/VAC) that reconciles; (3) Contract Administration & Cost Interrogation - a SQL block over a variation/cost-package ledger. Difficulty is mixed (basic IPC math is folded into the EVM/appraisal blocks; intermediate estimating + SQL; advanced sensitivity table + EVM forecasting). Standards cited: RICS NRM (New Rules of Measurement), AACE International cost estimating + EVM (ANSI/EIA-748), PMI PMBOK/EVM, and FIDIC Red Book for payment/variation mechanics.

**Skills:** Capital Project Budgeting & Cost Estimation (elemental cost planning, escalation, contingency) · Earned Value Management (EVM) & Cost/Schedule Forecasting · Construction Cost Control & Variation / Change-Order Management · Interim Payment Certificates, Retention & Developer Cash Flow · Capital Investment Appraisal for Property Development (NPV / IRR / residual value) · Project Risk Quantification & Contingency Drawdown

**Engine fit:** Strong fit. This is a quantitative cost-engineering and project-controls function, so no soft-skill proxy was needed - the gradable analytical core IS the day-job. Cost estimation, escalation and contingency build map to spreadsheet cell_value checks. Development-appraisal sensitivity (NPV across yield x build cost) maps to advanced_spreadsheet (native two-variable data table: is_array_formula + corner/centre cell_values), mirroring the FP&A EBITDA sensitivity block. Earned Value Management (the discipline's signature numeracy: CV, SV, CPI, SPI, EAC, VAC) maps to logic_input with reconciling logic_values, exactly like FP&A's PVM variance block. Variation/change-order and cost-package administration over a contracts ledger maps to sql_result_match. The non-gradable slices of the role (design coordination quality, contractor relationship management, stakeholder reporting narrative) are deliberately excluded; the blueprint measures the defensible numeric competencies a capital-projects controller must demonstrate.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Capital Project Estimating & Investment Appraisal**

- **Elemental Cost Plan with Escalation & Contingency** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: RICS New Rules of Measurement (NRM 1) / AACE International Cost Estimating
  - _Measures:_ Builds a defensible elemental cost plan: aggregates measured works, then stacks preliminaries, OH&P, contingency and escalation in the correct compounding order to reach an authorised project budget.
  - _Scenario:_ Riyadh Financial District — VIFM is the client cost manager on a new 14-storey corporate HQ fit-out and core/shell package. The quantity surveyor hands you an NRM-style elemental cost plan (SAR). Substructure SAR 9,200,000; Superstructure (frame, upper floors, roof, stairs) SAR 38,500,000; External envelope (walls, windows, external doors) SAR 16,800,000; Internal finishes SAR 12,400,000; Fittings, furnishings & equipment SAR 5,100,000; Building services (MEP) SAR 27,600,000. You must total the Works Cost, then add Preliminaries at 12% of Works Cost, a Main Contractor's Overheads & Profit (OH&P) margin at 6% applied to (Works Cost + Preliminaries), a Design Contingency at 5% applied to the subtotal after OH&P, and Construction Inflation/Escalation at 4.5% applied to the post-contingency subtotal to land at the Total Estimated Project Cost. All percentages compound on the running subtotal in the order given (NRM cost-plan stacking), not on the bare works cost.
  - _Model answer:_ Works Cost = 9,200,000 + 38,500,000 + 16,800,000 + 12,400,000 + 5,100,000 + 27,600,000 = 109,600,000. Preliminaries = 12% x 109,600,000 = 13,152,000. Subtotal-1 = 122,752,000. OH&P = 6% x 122,752,000 = 7,365,120 -> Subtotal-2 = 130,117,120. Design Contingency = 5% x 130,117,120 = 6,505,856 -> Subtotal-3 = 136,622,976. Escalation = 4.5% x 136,622,976 = 6,148,033.92 -> Total Estimated Project Cost = 142,771,009.92. Editable cells: B9 (Works Cost), B11 (Prelims amount), B12 (Subtotal-1), B14 (OH&P amount), B15 (Subtotal-2), B17 (Contingency amount), B18 (Subtotal-3), B20 (Escalation amount), B22 (Total Estimated Project Cost).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Works Cost = sum of six elements (SAR 109,600,000) - Correct aggregation of all six NRM elemental sub-totals into the Works Cost line
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Preliminaries = 12% of Works Cost (SAR 13,152,000) - Preliminaries applied to Works Cost, not to a wrong base
    - `cell_value` (w2) - OH&P = 6% of (Works + Prelims) (SAR 7,365,120) - Overheads & profit compounded on Works+Prelims subtotal in correct order
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Design Contingency = 5% of post-OH&P subtotal (SAR 6,505,856) - Contingency stacked on the running subtotal, not the bare works cost
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Escalation = 4.5% of post-contingency subtotal (SAR 6,148,033.92) - Inflation/escalation compounded last on the correct base
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Total Estimated Project Cost (SAR 142,771,009.92) - Full cost-plan stack resolves to the authorised project budget
- **Development Appraisal Sensitivity — NPV across Exit Yield & Build Cost** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18.3 min · ref: RICS Valuation (Red Book) — Residual / DCF Development Appraisal
  - _Measures:_ Constructs a development residual appraisal and stress-tests viability with a native two-variable data table across exit yield and build cost — the core feasibility tool for a capital-projects appraiser.
  - _Scenario:_ Dubai — a build-to-lease commercial development. The model inputs (AED): Net stabilised annual rent AED 24,000,000; Exit (capitalisation) yield 7.0%; Total construction cost AED 260,000,000; Land cost AED 90,000,000. Gross Development Value (GDV) on exit = Net annual rent / Exit yield. Development NPV (simplified residual) = GDV - Construction cost - Land cost. You must (a) build the live NPV cell from the inputs, then (b) construct a native two-variable data table showing NPV (AED) across an Exit-yield axis of {6.5%, 7.0%, 7.5%} (columns) and a Construction-cost axis of {AED 250,000,000; 260,000,000; 270,000,000} (rows). The grid must be a real data table driven by the model inputs, not typed-in numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Live NPV at base (yield 7.0%, cost 260m): GDV = 24,000,000 / 0.07 = 342,857,142.86; NPV = 342,857,142.86 - 260,000,000 - 90,000,000 = -7,142,857.14. Data table corner formula links to the live NPV cell; col input = exit yield, row input = construction cost. Reference grid corners/centre — Low corner (yield 6.5%, cost 250m): GDV = 24,000,000/0.065 = 369,230,769.23; NPV = 369,230,769.23 - 250,000,000 - 90,000,000 = 29,230,769.23. Centre (yield 7.0%, cost 260m) = -7,142,857.14. High-yield/high-cost corner (yield 7.5%, cost 270m): GDV = 24,000,000/0.075 = 320,000,000; NPV = 320,000,000 - 270,000,000 - 90,000,000 = -40,000,000. The table cells must be {=TABLE()}-style array results, not hardcoded.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sensitivity grid uses a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - Grid is formula/data-table driven so it recalculates with inputs — the discriminating skill
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base-case live NPV cell (AED -7,142,857.14) - Residual NPV = GDV(rent/yield) - construction - land computed correctly
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Best corner: yield 6.5%, cost 250m (AED 29,230,769.23) - Lower yield + lower build cost flows through the data table to a positive NPV
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre cell: yield 7.0%, cost 260m (AED -7,142,857.14) - Data-table centre reconciles to the live base-case NPV
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Worst corner: yield 7.5%, cost 270m (AED -40,000,000) - Higher yield + cost overrun flows through to the worst-case NPV

**Pillar - Earned Value & Cost Control Diagnostics**

- **Earned Value Management — Variances, Indices & Forecast at Completion** &nbsp; `Logic input` · advanced · 11.7 min · ref: AACE International / PMI PMBOK — Earned Value Management (ANSI/EIA-748)
  - _Measures:_ Computes the full Earned Value diagnostic set (variances, performance indices, and the CPI-based forecast at completion) and reconciles them — the signature numeracy of construction project controls.
  - _Scenario:_ Abu Dhabi — month 9 of an 18-month district-cooling plant capital project (figures in AED). Budget at Completion (BAC) = AED 48,000,000. As of the data date: Planned Value (PV / BCWS) = AED 22,000,000; Earned Value (EV / BCWP) = AED 19,500,000; Actual Cost (AC / ACWP) = AED 23,400,000. Using standard EVM equations, compute the Cost Variance, Schedule Variance, Cost Performance Index, Schedule Performance Index, the Estimate at Completion assuming current cost performance continues (EAC = BAC / CPI), and the Variance at Completion (VAC = BAC − EAC). Negative variances indicate over budget / behind schedule.
  - _Model answer:_ CV = EV - AC = 19,500,000 - 23,400,000 = -3,900,000. SV = EV - PV = 19,500,000 - 22,000,000 = -2,500,000. CPI = EV / AC = 19,500,000 / 23,400,000 = 0.833333... ≈ 0.8333. SPI = EV / PV = 19,500,000 / 22,000,000 = 0.886363... ≈ 0.8864. EAC = BAC / CPI = 48,000,000 / 0.833333 = 57,600,000 (equivalently BAC x AC/EV). VAC = BAC - EAC = 48,000,000 - 57,600,000 = -9,600,000. Fields: cost_variance, schedule_variance, cpi, spi, eac, vac.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Cost Variance CV = EV − AC (AED -3,900,000) - Correct cost variance sign and magnitude (project is over budget)
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Schedule Variance SV = EV − PV (AED -2,500,000) - Correct schedule variance (project is behind plan)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Cost Performance Index CPI = EV / AC (0.8333) - CPI ratio computed correctly to flag cost efficiency below 1.0
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Schedule Performance Index SPI = EV / PV (0.8864) - SPI ratio computed correctly to flag schedule efficiency below 1.0
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Estimate at Completion EAC = BAC / CPI (AED 57,600,000) - CPI-based forecast at completion projects the overrun forward
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Variance at Completion VAC = BAC − EAC (AED -9,600,000) - Forecast final overrun reconciles BAC against EAC

**Pillar - Contract Administration & Cost Data Interrogation**

- **Variation & Cost-Package Ledger Interrogation (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: FIDIC Red Book (Variations & Payment) / AACE Change Management
  - _Measures:_ Interrogates a construction cost ledger: filters change orders to the committed (approved) set, aggregates exposure by work package, and ranks it — the core cost-reporting query a project controller runs each period.
  - _Scenario:_ Doha — VIFM administers the cost ledger for a mixed-use tower. The variations table records approved and pending change orders against work packages: columns id (int), package (text e.g. 'MEP', 'Facade', 'Structure', 'Fit-out'), description (text), status (text: 'approved' / 'pending' / 'rejected'), amount_qar (numeric), raised_date (date). The cost controller needs the committed variation exposure per package — but only APPROVED variations count as committed cost. Write ONE query that returns, for approved variations only, each package with its total committed variation amount, highest exposure first.
  - _Model answer:_ Filter status = 'approved', GROUP BY package, SUM(amount_qar), ORDER BY the total descending (tie-break by package for determinism). Master query: SELECT package, SUM(amount_qar) AS total_committed FROM variations WHERE status = 'approved' GROUP BY package ORDER BY total_committed DESC, package. Seed data is shaped so pending/rejected rows exist and must be excluded, and at least two packages share approved rows to test aggregation; the ranking is order-sensitive.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master: committed (approved-only) variation total per package, highest first - Correct WHERE filter on approved status, GROUP BY package, SUM aggregation, and descending order

---

### 3.3 Commercial Lease Administration & Financial Abstract Compliance

Sandbox blueprint for Commercial Lease Administration & Financial Abstract Compliance (node 3.3, CRE domain). The function's skills list was empty, so six realistic skills were proposed grounded in GCC commercial-property practice: (1) Lease Abstraction & Rent Schedule Construction, (2) IFRS 16 Lessee Accounting (ROU asset / lease liability), (3) Service Charge / OPEX & CAM Reconciliation, (4) Straight-Line Rent & Incentive Amortisation, (5) Percentage-Rent & Breakpoint Calculation, (6) Critical-Date, Option & Portfolio Compliance Tracking. The function is highly gradable: every core task reduces to deterministic financial arithmetic over a lease abstract. Designed as 3 pillars / 4 blocks spanning all four engines. Pillar 1 (Lease Financial Engineering) uses a spreadsheet straight-line rent schedule (basic→intermediate) and an advanced_spreadsheet two-variable sensitivity data table on the IFRS 16 lease liability across discount rate x escalation. Pillar 2 (Charge Reconciliation & Variance) uses a logic_input CAM gross-up + pro-rata recovery and service-charge variance reconciliation. Pillar 3 (Portfolio Compliance Interrogation) uses SQL over a seeded lease portfolio table to surface critical-date / option-window exposure. Figures are concrete AED amounts and real-sounding GCC entities (DIFC, Riyadh, Abu Dhabi). Frameworks cited: IFRS 16, IAS 17 straight-lining, RICS service-charge code, AFP/IMA quantitative methods, DAMA DMBOK.

**Skills:** Lease Abstraction & Rent Schedule Construction · IFRS 16 Lessee Accounting (ROU Asset & Lease Liability) · Service Charge / OPEX & CAM Reconciliation · Straight-Line Rent & Lease-Incentive Amortisation · Percentage-Rent & Breakpoint Calculation · Critical-Date, Option & Portfolio Compliance Tracking

**Engine fit:** Strong fit. Commercial lease administration sounds like a document/contract role, but its defensible, auto-gradable core is pure deterministic finance over the lease abstract - exactly what the four engines measure. The quantitative slice covers: straight-line (IAS 17 / IFRS 16) rent recognition and incentive amortisation (spreadsheet cell_value); IFRS 16 lease-liability present value across discount-rate x escalation (advanced_spreadsheet two-variable data table - is_array_formula + corner cell_values); CAM gross-up, pro-rata recovery, percentage-rent breakpoint, and service-charge variance reconciliation (logic_input named numeric fields); and critical-date / option-window / over-recovery exposure across a portfolio (SQL result-set match). Free-text lease drafting, clause interpretation, and negotiation judgement are deliberately OUT of scope because they are not auto-gradable; this blueprint asserts the financial-abstract-compliance half of the role, which is where reconciliation errors create real liability. No engine limitation worth flagging - the function's gradable surface is wide.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 5 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Lease Financial Engineering**

- **Straight-Line Rent & Incentive Amortisation Schedule** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: IFRS 16 / IAS 17 - Straight-Lining of Operating Lease Incentives
  - _Measures:_ Lease Abstraction & Rent Schedule Construction; Straight-Line Rent & Lease-Incentive Amortisation - recognising rent on a straight-line basis over the lease term net of incentives, and proving the deferred-rent balance unwinds to zero at term end.
  - _Scenario:_ Meydan Logistics FZE has signed a 5-year warehouse lease at Dubai South. Contractual annual rent is fixed at AED 600,000 for Years 1-2, then steps to AED 720,000 for Years 3-5, and the landlord granted a 6-month rent-free fit-out incentive at the start (Year 1 cash rent therefore = AED 300,000). Cash rent payable is given for each year. The candidate must build the straight-line schedule: compute total cash rent over the term, the constant straight-line annual expense, and the deferred-rent (accrued/prepaid) balance carried at the end of Year 1 and Year 2 (cumulative straight-line expense minus cumulative cash paid). Editable cells: total cash (B10), straight-line annual (B11), Year-1 deferred balance (B14), Year-2 deferred balance (B15), and the end-of-term deferred balance which must close to zero (B18).
  - _Model answer:_ Cash rent by year: Y1 = 300,000 (6 months free), Y2 = 600,000, Y3 = Y4 = Y5 = 720,000. Total cash = 300,000+600,000+720,000*3 = 3,060,000 (B10). Straight-line annual = 3,060,000 / 5 = 612,000 (B11). Deferred balance(end of year) = cumulative straight-line expense - cumulative cash paid. End Y1: 612,000 - 300,000 = 312,000 (B14). End Y2: 1,224,000 - 900,000 = 324,000 (B15). End of term Y5: 3,060,000 - 3,060,000 = 0 (B18). A positive deferred balance means straight-line expense has outrun cash paid (a liability/accrued rent).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total cash rent over 5-year term = AED 3,060,000 - Correct abstraction of the stepped rent and rent-free incentive into total contractual cash flow
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Straight-line annual rent expense = AED 612,000 - Total term rent recognised evenly across the lease term per IAS 17/IFRS 16
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Deferred-rent balance end of Year 1 = AED 312,000 - Cumulative straight-line expense less cumulative cash paid (incentive period drives the accrual)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Deferred-rent balance end of Year 2 = AED 324,000 - Roll-forward of the deferred balance through the second period
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Deferred-rent balance end of term = AED 0 - The straight-line accrual fully unwinds by lease end - the integrity check that proves the schedule reconciles
- **IFRS 16 Lease Liability Sensitivity Matrix** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18.3 min · ref: IFRS 16 - Initial Measurement of the Lease Liability (PV of Lease Payments)
  - _Measures:_ IFRS 16 Lessee Accounting - discounting an escalating lease payment stream to its present value, and stress-testing the recognised lease liability across discount-rate and escalation assumptions via a native two-variable data table.
  - _Scenario:_ Riyadh Falcon Holding leases regional headquarters floors. Year-1 annual lease payment is SAR 1,000,000 paid in arrears, escalating at a fixed annual rate, over a 3-year non-cancellable term. The candidate first computes the base-case lease liability as the present value of the three escalating payments at the incremental borrowing rate (IBR). Then they must build a two-variable data table showing the opening lease liability across three discount rates (columns: 5%, 7%, 9%) and three annual escalation rates (rows: 0%, 3%, 5%) - using a native data table linked to the PV model, not hardcoded numbers. Editable: base PV (B8), the data-table corner (B11) linking to the PV, and the 3x3 body (C12:E14). Graded on the array formula being present plus the low corner (5% disc, 0% esc), base case (7% disc, 3% esc), and high-escalation corner (5% disc, 5% esc).
  - _Model answer:_ Payments (arrears) at escalation g: P1=1,000,000, P2=1,000,000*(1+g), P3=1,000,000*(1+g)^2. Liability = sum P_t/(1+r)^t for t=1..3. Base case r=7%, g=3%: P1=1,000,000, P2=1,030,000, P3=1,060,900; PV = 1,000,000/1.07 + 1,030,000/1.07^2 + 1,060,900/1.07^3 = 934,579.44 + 899,642.59 + 866,002.69 = 2,700,224.72 (B8 and centre D13). Low corner r=5%, g=0% (flat 1,000,000): PV = 1,000,000*(1/1.05+1/1.05^2+1/1.05^3) = 952,380.95+907,029.48+863,837.60 = 2,723,248.03 (C12). High-escalation corner r=5%, g=5%: P=1,000,000;1,050,000;1,102,500; PV = 952,380.95+952,380.95+952,380.95 = 2,857,142.86 (C14). Data table: column input = discount rate cell, row input = escalation cell.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sensitivity body C12:E14 uses a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - Candidate builds a real what-if data table driven by the PV model, demonstrating array/data-table fluency
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base-case lease liability (7% discount, 3% escalation) = SAR 2,700,224.72 - Correct PV of an escalating arrears payment stream - the IFRS 16 initial measurement
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (5% discount, 0% escalation) = SAR 2,723,248.03 - Data-table interior recomputes correctly for a flat payment stream at a low rate
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High-escalation corner (5% discount, 5% escalation) = SAR 2,857,142.86 - Liability rises with escalation even as a low rate discounts it - sensitivity directionality is correct

**Pillar - Charge Reconciliation & Recovery Variance**

- **CAM Gross-Up, Pro-Rata Recovery & Service-Charge Variance** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 12 min · ref: RICS Professional Statement - Service Charges in Commercial Property
  - _Measures:_ Service Charge / OPEX & CAM Reconciliation - applying a gross-up clause to occupancy-driven costs, allocating the recoverable pool on a pro-rata floor-area basis, enforcing a contractual recovery cap, and reconciling actual recovery to budget.
  - _Scenario:_ Al Maryah Tower (Abu Dhabi) is a multi-tenant office building with 40,000 sqm of total lettable area but is only 80% occupied. Total actual operating expenses for the year were AED 6,000,000, of which AED 4,400,000 are variable (occupancy-driven) and AED 1,600,000 are fixed. The candidate's tenant, Gulf Advisory LLC, occupies 5,000 sqm under a lease with a gross-up clause (variable costs grossed up to 100% occupancy) and a recovery cap of AED 600,000. Compute: (1) the grossed-up variable cost (variable costs scaled to 100% occupancy), (2) the total grossed-up recoverable pool (grossed-up variable + fixed), (3) the tenant's pro-rata share before the cap (tenant sqm / total sqm x recoverable pool), (4) the capped recoverable amount the tenant actually pays, and (5) the recovery variance vs a budgeted service charge of AED 550,000 (capped recovery minus budget).
  - _Model answer:_ Grossed-up variable = 4,400,000 / 0.80 = 5,500,000. Recoverable pool = grossed-up variable + fixed = 5,500,000 + 1,600,000 = 7,100,000. Tenant pro-rata share before cap = (5,000 / 40,000) * 7,100,000 = 0.125 * 7,100,000 = 887,500. Cap = 600,000, so capped recoverable = min(887,500, 600,000) = 600,000. Recovery variance vs budget = 600,000 - 550,000 = 50,000 (favourable over-budget recovery, but note it is the cap that binds).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Grossed-up variable cost = AED 5,500,000 - Correct application of the gross-up clause (variable cost / occupancy)
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Total grossed-up recoverable pool = AED 7,100,000 - Combines grossed-up variable with fixed costs into the recoverable base
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Tenant pro-rata share before cap = AED 887,500 - Floor-area pro-rata allocation of the recoverable pool
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Capped recoverable amount = AED 600,000 - Recovery cap binds when the pro-rata share exceeds the contractual cap
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Recovery variance vs budget = AED 50,000 - Reconciles actual capped recovery to the budgeted service charge
- **Percentage-Rent Natural Breakpoint Calculation** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 9 min · ref: AFP / IMA Quantitative Methods - Retail Lease Percentage-Rent Mechanics
  - _Measures:_ Percentage-Rent & Breakpoint Calculation - deriving the natural breakpoint from base rent and the overage rate, then computing overage rent and total occupancy cost for a turnover-rent retail lease.
  - _Scenario:_ A flagship retail unit at Mall of the Emirates is leased to Desert Bloom Retail LLC on a percentage-rent structure: base minimum rent of AED 1,200,000 per year plus 7% of annual gross sales above the natural breakpoint. Actual gross sales for the year were AED 25,000,000. The candidate must compute: (1) the natural breakpoint (base rent divided by the percentage-rent rate), (2) the overage sales above the breakpoint, (3) the percentage rent due on the overage, and (4) the total rent payable for the year (base + percentage rent).
  - _Model answer:_ Natural breakpoint = base rent / percentage rate = 1,200,000 / 0.07 = 17,142,857.14. Overage sales = gross sales - breakpoint = 25,000,000 - 17,142,857.14 = 7,857,142.86. Percentage rent = 7% * overage = 0.07 * 7,857,142.86 = 550,000.00. Total rent = base + percentage rent = 1,200,000 + 550,000 = 1,750,000.00. (Equivalently: total above-breakpoint = 7% of (25,000,000 - 17,142,857.14) = 550,000.)
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Natural breakpoint = AED 17,142,857.14 - Correct derivation of the breakpoint from base rent and the percentage rate
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Overage sales above breakpoint = AED 7,857,142.86 - Sales subject to percentage rent isolated correctly
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Percentage rent due = AED 550,000.00 - Overage rate applied to the correct overage base
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total annual rent payable = AED 1,750,000.00 - Total occupancy cost reconciles base plus turnover rent

**Pillar - Portfolio Compliance Interrogation**

- **Critical-Date & Option-Window Exposure Query (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 11 min · ref: DAMA International (DMBOK) - Lease Data Interrogation & Critical-Date Control
  - _Measures:_ Critical-Date, Option & Portfolio Compliance Tracking - interrogating a lease portfolio to aggregate financial exposure by location, filtered to a critical-date renewal horizon, ordered for prioritisation.
  - _Scenario:_ A seeded lease-portfolio table holds the active commercial leases for a GCC corporate occupier. Each row carries the property, city, annual_rent (AED), lease_expiry date, and a break_notice_days option-notice window. The lease administrator must surface concentration risk: which cities carry the largest total annual rent commitment, restricted to leases expiring within the medium-term horizon (on or before 2027-12-31), so the team can prioritise renewal negotiations. The candidate writes ONE query returning each qualifying city with its total annual rent, highest commitment first.
  - _Model answer:_ Filter leases to lease_expiry <= '2027-12-31', GROUP BY city, SUM(annual_rent) AS total_rent, ORDER BY total_rent DESC (tie-break city). Master query: SELECT city, SUM(annual_rent) AS total_rent FROM leases WHERE lease_expiry <= '2027-12-31' GROUP BY city ORDER BY total_rent DESC, city. Seed has Dubai, Abu Dhabi, Riyadh, Sharjah rows with mixed expiries; only rows on/before 2027-12-31 count, and per-city sums are ranked so the highest-exposure renewal city appears first.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result set matches master: per-city total annual rent for leases expiring on/before 2027-12-31, highest first - Correct WHERE date filter, GROUP BY city aggregation, SUM of annual rent, and DESC ordering for renewal prioritisation
