### 3.4 Facilities Operations, Engineering, and Preventive Maintenance

Sandbox for FM Operations, Engineering and Preventive Maintenance (CRE 3.4). No skills were supplied, so six GCC-grounded skills are proposed. 3 pillars, 4 blocks, 3 engines: spreadsheet PPM and SLA compliance and manpower model (basic), logic_input reliability and chiller efficiency (intermediate), advanced_spreadsheet repair-vs-replace life-cycle-cost sensitivity table (advanced), SQL CMMS work-order analytics (intermediate). Concrete AED, kWh and kW per TR figures; anchored to ISO 55000, SFG20, ASHRAE, ISO 15686-5, EN 15341.

**Skills:** PPM Planning and SFG20 Maintenance Compliance · Asset Reliability Engineering (MTBF, MTTR, Availability) · Energy and Utilities Performance (kWh, Chiller Efficiency) · HVAC and MEP Engineering Efficiency · SLA and KPI Management and Vendor Governance · Life-Cycle Costing and Capital Renewal Planning

**Engine fit:** FM engineering is strongly quantitative. Gradable slice: PPM compliance percent, SLA penalties and FTE loading map to spreadsheet; reliability metrics (MTBF, MTTR, availability) and chiller kW per TR map to logic_input; repair-vs-replace life-cycle cost across discount-rate and tariff scenarios maps to advanced_spreadsheet; CMMS work-order labour-hours by asset class maps to sql. Not gradable here and deliberately excluded: vendor relationship management, HSE walk-downs, tenant experience, emergency-response leadership, and CAD or BMS operation - these need MCQ or human rating. No engine is a poor fit.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Logic input, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Maintenance Planning and Service-Level Performance**

- **PPM Compliance, SLA Penalty and Manpower-Loading Model** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · basic · 16.7 min · ref: SFG20 Maintenance Specification, BS EN 13306, BOMA FM Benchmarks
  - _Measures:_ Turning raw PPM data into contractual KPI compliance percent, monetising SLA breaches, and converting workload into a defensible FTE requirement - the core monthly hard-services reporting deliverable.
  - _Scenario:_ You are Hard-Services Manager for Al Maryah Facilities on a Grade-A tower in Abu Dhabi. This quarter 1240 PPM tasks were scheduled and 1116 completed on time. The output-based contract charges an SLA penalty of AED 850 for every whole percentage point (rounded down) that PPM compliance is below the 95 percent threshold. Critical-asset PPM (chillers, fire pumps, generators) had 320 scheduled and 304 completed. Technicians delivered 6800 productive man-hours against 7200 required; each FTE technician gives 1600 productive man-hours per quarter. Complete the highlighted cells for compliance, the SLA penalty, critical-asset compliance and the FTE shortfall.
  - _Model answer:_ Compliance equals 1116 divided by 1240 equals 90.0 percent. Shortfall versus 95 percent equals 5 whole points, so penalty equals 5 times AED 850 equals AED 4250. Critical compliance equals 304 divided by 320 equals 95.0 percent. Required FTE equals 7200 divided by 1600 equals 4.5; available equals 6800 divided by 1600 equals 4.25; shortfall equals 0.25.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - PPM compliance percent equals 90.0 - Compliance equals completed divided by scheduled (1116/1240)
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Whole-point shortfall below 95 equals 5 - Applies rounded-down whole-point SLA rule
    - `cell_value` (w3) - SLA penalty AED equals 4250 - Monetises breach: 5 times AED 850
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Critical-asset compliance percent equals 95.0 - Segments compliance to critical subset (304/320)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Required technician FTE equals 4.5 - Required man-hours to FTE at 1600 hrs per quarter
    - `cell_value` (w2) - FTE shortfall equals 0.25 - Manpower gap equals required minus available FTE

**Pillar - Asset Reliability and Engineering Efficiency**

- **Reliability Metrics and Chiller Plant Efficiency Calculation** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: ISO 55000, SAE JA1011 (RCM), ASHRAE 90.1 and AHRI 550/590 (kW per TR)
  - _Measures:_ Applying reliability formulae (MTBF, MTTR, availability) and HVAC efficiency engineering (kW per TR) to run-hour and energy data - the analytical backbone of an RCM or condition-based strategy.
  - _Scenario:_ You are Reliability Engineer for a district-cooling-served business park in Riyadh. (A) A chilled-water pump ran an 8760-hour year with 6 failures and 90 hours total downtime across 6 repairs. (B) A critical AHU logged 8400 operating hours against 8760 calendar hours. (C) The chiller plant produced 7500000 TR-hours of cooling and consumed 4500000 kWh. In the labelled fields compute pump MTBF in hours, pump MTTR in hours, AHU availability percent, plant efficiency in kW per TR, and the variance versus the ASHRAE 0.65 kW per TR design benchmark.
  - _Model answer:_ MTBF equals 8760 divided by 6 equals 1460. MTTR equals 90 divided by 6 equals 15. Availability equals 8400 divided by 8760 equals 95.89 percent. Efficiency equals 4500000 divided by 7500000 equals 0.60 kW per TR. Variance equals 0.60 minus 0.65 equals minus 0.05 (better than benchmark).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Pump MTBF hours equals 1460 - MTBF equals operating hours divided by failures
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Pump MTTR hours equals 15 - MTTR equals downtime divided by repairs
    - `logic_value` (w2) - AHU availability percent equals 95.89 - Availability equals uptime divided by calendar hours
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Chiller efficiency equals 0.60 kW per TR - Efficiency equals kWh divided by TR-hours
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Variance versus 0.65 equals minus 0.05 kW per TR - Benchmarks efficiency versus ASHRAE target (negative is better)

**Pillar - Capital Renewal and CMMS Data Interrogation**

- **Repair-vs-Replace Life-Cycle Cost Sensitivity Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 20 min · ref: ISO 15686-5 (Life-Cycle Costing), ASTM E917, RICS Whole-Life Cost
  - _Measures:_ Building a defensible repair-vs-replace capital decision under uncertainty via a native two-variable sensitivity table flexing a discounted-cash-flow NPV across tariff and cost-of-capital - the ISO 15686-5 whole-life-cost technique.
  - _Scenario:_ You are Capital Projects Engineer deciding whether to replace an ageing 1200 TR chiller at a Dubai mall. A new high-efficiency unit costs AED 2400000 capex and saves 540000 kWh per year, so annual saving in AED equals 540000 times the DEWA tariff. Build a two-variable data table of the 10-year NPV of the replacement (discounted annual energy savings less the AED 2400000 capex) across DEWA tariffs on the columns and discount rates on the rows, using the provided NPV engine cell. It must be a NATIVE two-variable data table, not typed-in numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Annual saving equals 540000 times tariff. NPV equals saving times annuity factor(rate,10) minus 2400000, where factor equals (1 minus (1+rate) to the power minus 10) divided by rate. Tariff 0.45 and 8 percent: 243000 times 6.7101 minus 2400000 equals minus 769455. Tariff 0.55 and 10 percent: 297000 times 6.1446 minus 2400000 equals minus 575054. Tariff 0.50 and 8 percent: 270000 times 6.7101 minus 2400000 equals minus 588273. Corner cell equals the NPV engine; Data Table column input equals tariff, row input equals discount rate.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Grid is a native two-variable data table - Range is formula-driven via a native data table, not hardcoded
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Tariff 0.45 and rate 8 percent gives NPV approx minus 769455 - Low-tariff and low-rate corner discounts savings net of capex
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Tariff 0.55 and rate 10 percent gives NPV approx minus 575054 - High-tariff and high-rate corner
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Tariff 0.50 and rate 8 percent gives NPV approx minus 588273 - Base-case interior reconciles with annuity PV engine
    - `cell_value` (w2) - PV-annuity factor at 8 percent and 10 yrs equals 6.7101 - Computes the discount-annuity factor driving the model
- **CMMS Work-Order Analytics (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: EN 15341 (FM KPIs), DAMA DMBOK, CMMS Best Practice
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating a CMMS to surface a maintenance-strategy signal - aggregating and ranking reactive maintenance effort by asset class, the data step driving RCM prioritisation and the EN 15341 reactive-ratio KPI.
  - _Scenario:_ Your CMMS holds work_orders for a Jeddah retail portfolio: id, asset_class, wo_type (planned or reactive), status (open or closed), labour_hours numeric, raised_date, closed_date. To prioritise an RCM review, write ONE query returning, per asset_class, the total reactive labour hours, ranked so the asset class consuming the most reactive labour is first. Columns: asset_class, reactive_hours.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT asset_class, SUM(labour_hours) AS reactive_hours FROM work_orders WHERE wo_type = 'reactive' GROUP BY asset_class ORDER BY reactive_hours DESC, asset_class. Order-sensitive because the ranking is the deliverable.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master (reactive hours per asset_class, highest first) - Correct reactive filter, GROUP BY asset_class, SUM(labour_hours), DESC ordering

### 3.5 Property Acquisition, Divestment, & Commercial Brokerage Mechanics

Hands-on sandbox for commercial real estate transaction professionals - the quantitative core of acquiring, disposing of, and brokering income-producing property in the GCC. The function had no skills defined, so six were proposed grounded in GCC CRE practice: (1) Investment Underwriting & NOI Stabilization, (2) Direct-Capitalization & Cap-Rate Valuation, (3) Levered Return / Cash-on-Cash Analysis, (4) Two-Variable Valuation Sensitivity, (5) Brokerage Commission & Net-to-Seller Disposition Economics, (6) Comparable-Transaction & Portfolio Deal Analytics. Three pillars and four blocks span all but the python engine: a spreadsheet acquisition-underwriting model (NOI -> value -> levered return), an advanced_spreadsheet two-variable value sensitivity using a native data table, a logic_input seller-side disposition / commission reconciliation, and a SQL interrogation of a brokered-deal ledger. Every block carries concrete AED/SAR figures and real entity-style names; standards referenced are RICS Valuation (Red Book Global), the Appraisal Institute income-approach method, the Dubai Land Department (DLD) / RERA fee regime, and AREA brokerage practice. Engine fit is strong - CRE transactions are inherently numeric (cap rates, NOI, IRR, commissions, transfer fees), so no soft-skill proxy was needed.

**Skills:** Investment Underwriting & NOI Stabilization · Direct-Capitalization & Cap-Rate Valuation · Levered Return & Cash-on-Cash Analysis · Two-Variable Valuation Sensitivity · Brokerage Commission & Net-to-Seller Disposition Economics · Comparable-Transaction & Portfolio Deal Analytics

**Engine fit:** Strong fit across three engines - no soft-skill proxy required. Commercial real estate acquisition/divestment/brokerage is intrinsically quantitative: stabilized NOI, direct-capitalization value, going-in cap rate, debt service and cash-on-cash, valuation sensitivity to NOI and cap-rate movement, brokerage commission with VAT, mortgage-discharge fees and net-to-seller proceeds, and portfolio-level commission/price-per-sqm analytics over a deal ledger. (1) spreadsheet handles the acquisition underwriting waterfall (GPR -> EGI -> NOI -> value -> levered return) with exact cell_value checks. (2) advanced_spreadsheet is a genuine fit because direct-cap value = NOI / cap rate is a clean two-input function, ideal for a native two-variable data table (is_array_formula + corner cell_value). (3) logic_input fits the seller-side disposition reconciliation (discrete deductions that must net to proceeds). (4) sql fits the brokered-deal ledger aggregation. The python engine is intentionally unused (not among the four gradable engines required). The non-gradable parts of this role - negotiation tactics, relationship brokerage, deal narrative, market-color judgement - are deliberately excluded; what is tested is the gradable transaction-mechanics slice, which is exactly what defensibly differentiates a competent CRE transaction analyst.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Acquisition Underwriting & Valuation**

- **Income-Property Acquisition Underwriting Model** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 18.3 min · ref: RICS Valuation - Global Standards (Red Book) / Appraisal Institute Income Approach
  - _Measures:_ Building a stabilized acquisition underwriting waterfall - vacancy-adjusted EGI, NOI, direct-cap value, going-in cap rate, interest-only debt service, and levered cash-on-cash return - the core numeracy of an income-property acquisition analyst.
  - _Scenario:_ Najd Capital Partners is underwriting the acquisition of Olaya Gate Tower, a Grade-A office asset in Riyadh, KSA. Gross Potential Rent (GPR) is SAR 12,000,000. Apply a vacancy & credit-loss allowance of 8% of GPR to get Effective Gross Income (EGI). Operating expenses are SAR 3,312,000 (given). Stabilized NOI = EGI - OpEx. Value the asset by direct capitalization at an exit/market cap rate of 7.0%. The purchase price is fixed at SAR 105,000,000; compute the going-in cap rate on price. Funding is a 60% LTV interest-only acquisition loan priced at 5.50%; equity is the balance. Compute Year-1 before-tax cash flow (NOI - debt service) and the Year-1 cash-on-cash return on equity. Currency: SAR. All editable cells must be formula-driven off the given inputs.
  - _Model answer:_ Vacancy loss = 8% x 12,000,000 = 960,000; EGI = 12,000,000 - 960,000 = 11,040,000. NOI = EGI - OpEx = 11,040,000 - 3,312,000 = 7,728,000. Direct-cap value = NOI / 0.07 = 7,728,000 / 0.07 = 110,400,000. Going-in cap on price = 7,728,000 / 105,000,000 = 0.073600 (7.36%). Loan = 60% x 105,000,000 = 63,000,000; equity = 42,000,000. Interest-only debt service = 63,000,000 x 0.055 = 3,465,000. Before-tax cash flow = 7,728,000 - 3,465,000 = 4,263,000. Cash-on-cash = 4,263,000 / 42,000,000 = 0.101500 (10.15%).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Effective Gross Income (GPR less 8% vacancy) = 11,040,000 - Vacancy & credit-loss allowance applied correctly to reach EGI
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Stabilized NOI = 7,728,000 - NOI = EGI minus operating expenses
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Direct-capitalization value at 7.0% = 110,400,000 - Income-approach value = NOI / cap rate
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Going-in cap rate on purchase price = 0.0736 - Yield-on-cost computed against the fixed acquisition price
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Year-1 before-tax cash flow = 4,263,000 - NOI net of interest-only debt service at 60% LTV / 5.5%
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Year-1 cash-on-cash return = 0.1015 - Levered equity return = before-tax cash flow / equity invested
- **Two-Variable Valuation Sensitivity Matrix** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: RICS Valuation - Global Standards (Red Book) / Appraisal Institute Sensitivity Analysis
  - _Measures:_ Constructing a native two-variable data table to stress income-approach valuation across NOI and cap-rate axes - demonstrating that value is recomputed by the engine, not typed, and that the candidate understands the inverse cap-rate / value relationship.
  - _Scenario:_ Continuing the Olaya Gate Tower underwrite, the investment committee wants a value-sensitivity table because both the stabilized NOI and the market cap rate are uncertain. The base value model is Value = NOI / cap rate, with base NOI = SAR 7,728,000 in the model cell. Build a NATIVE two-variable data table (not hardcoded numbers): rows step NOI across [7,000,000 ; 7,728,000 ; 8,500,000] and columns step the cap rate across [6.5% ; 7.0% ; 7.5%]. The table corner must link to the value formula cell. Currency: SAR.
  - _Model answer:_ Value formula = NOI / cap rate. Build the data table with row input = the NOI model cell and column input = the cap-rate model cell; the corner references the value cell. Cell results: top-left corner (NOI 7,000,000, cap 6.5%) = 7,000,000 / 0.065 = 107,692,307.69; centre / base case (NOI 7,728,000, cap 7.0%) = 110,400,000; bottom-right corner (NOI 8,500,000, cap 7.5%) = 8,500,000 / 0.075 = 113,333,333.33. The is_array_formula check confirms a native {=TABLE()} drives the body rather than pasted constants.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sensitivity body is a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - Value grid is engine-recomputed via {=TABLE()}, proving real data-table construction
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (NOI 7,000,000, cap 6.5%) = 107,692,307.69 - Direct-cap value at the conservative NOI / tight cap-rate corner
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Base case (NOI 7,728,000, cap 7.0%) = 110,400,000 - Sensitivity centre reconciles to the underwriting value
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (NOI 8,500,000, cap 7.5%) = 113,333,333.33 - Direct-cap value at the upside NOI / wider cap-rate corner

**Pillar - Divestment & Brokerage Economics**

- **Seller-Side Disposition & Commission Reconciliation** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 9 min · ref: Dubai Land Department (DLD) / RERA fee regime & AREA brokerage practice (UAE)
  - _Measures:_ Reconciling a real GCC disposition closing statement - commission, VAT on agency fees, mortgage discharge, and net-to-seller - so that the discrete deductions reconcile exactly to proceeds, the everyday math of a brokerage transaction coordinator.
  - _Scenario:_ Marina Vista Brokerage is closing the disposal of a Dubai retail unit for Al Habtoor Retail Holdings. Agreed sale price: AED 48,000,000. Compute the seller-side closing waterfall: (a) brokerage commission at 2% of sale price; (b) VAT at 5% on the brokerage commission; (c) the seller's outstanding mortgage payoff of AED 19,500,000 plus an early-settlement / discharge fee of 1% of the outstanding balance; (d) net proceeds to the seller after deducting commission, VAT-on-commission, the mortgage payoff, and the discharge fee. (The 4% DLD transfer fee is buyer-borne and is excluded from the seller waterfall.) Currency: AED.
  - _Model answer:_ Commission = 2% x 48,000,000 = 960,000. VAT on commission = 5% x 960,000 = 48,000. Mortgage discharge/early-settlement fee = 1% x 19,500,000 = 195,000. Net proceeds = 48,000,000 - 960,000 (commission) - 48,000 (VAT) - 19,500,000 (mortgage payoff) - 195,000 (discharge fee) = 27,297,000.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Brokerage commission (2% of price) = 960,000 - Commission computed on gross sale price per AREA practice
    - `logic_value` (w2) - VAT on commission (5%) = 48,000 - UAE 5% VAT applied to the agency fee, not the property price
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Mortgage early-settlement / discharge fee (1% of outstanding) = 195,000 - Discharge fee computed on the outstanding loan balance
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Net proceeds to seller = 27,297,000 - All deductions reconcile to seller net proceeds

**Pillar - Portfolio Deal Analytics**

- **Brokered-Deal Ledger Interrogation (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · basic · 10 min · ref: RICS / DAMA DMBOK data-interrogation practice for transaction reporting
  - _Measures:_ Writing a correct grouped aggregation with ordered output over a brokered-deal ledger - the data-interrogation skill a brokerage analyst uses for desk performance and pipeline reporting.
  - _Scenario:_ Marina Vista Brokerage keeps every closed deal in a relational ledger. The desk head wants total gross brokerage commission earned per district to see where the franchise is strongest. Query the deals table and return each district with its total commission, ranked highest commission first. Output columns must be exactly: district, total_commission. Dialect: PostgreSQL.
  - _Model answer:_ Seed: CREATE TABLE deals (id int PRIMARY KEY, district text, asset_type text, sale_price numeric, commission numeric, close_date date); rows = (1,'Business Bay','office',32000000,640000,'2025-01-12'),(2,'Downtown','retail',48000000,960000,'2025-02-03'),(3,'Business Bay','retail',15000000,300000,'2025-02-18'),(4,'JLT','office',22000000,440000,'2025-03-05'),(5,'Downtown','office',60000000,1200000,'2025-03-22'),(6,'JLT','retail',9000000,180000,'2025-04-01'),(7,'Business Bay','industrial',12000000,240000,'2025-04-14'). Master query: SELECT district, SUM(commission) AS total_commission FROM deals GROUP BY district ORDER BY total_commission DESC, district. Result (ordered): Downtown 2,160,000; Business Bay 1,180,000; JLT 620,000.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master: total commission per district, highest first (Downtown 2,160,000; Business Bay 1,180,000; JLT 620,000) - Correct GROUP BY district with SUM(commission) and descending ORDER BY

---

### 3.6 Health, Safety, & Environment (HSE) Statutory Compliance

HSE Statutory Compliance is a regulatory/operational function that, at first glance, looks soft (policy, inspections, culture). Its defensible, auto-gradable core is heavily quantitative: statutory incident-rate computation (OSHA TRIR/LTIFR/severity), risk-matrix scoring (ISO 45001/ISO 31000), environmental emissions intensity and ESG metrics (GRI/ISSB), and compliance-register interrogation (training expiry, permit-to-work backlog, inspection-action closure). The blueprint targets that quantitative slice across three pillars and four blocks, using three engines (logic_input, spreadsheet, sql) on concrete GCC scenarios (an Abu Dhabi facilities operator, a Saudi industrial site, a Dubai contractor register). Free-text incident narratives, RCA write-ups, and policy drafting are deliberately excluded as ungradable.

**Skills:** Statutory Incident-Rate Computation (TRIR / LTIFR / Severity) · Risk Assessment & Hazard Scoring (ISO 45001 / 31000) · Permit-to-Work & Inspection-Action Compliance Tracking · Environmental & Emissions Performance Reporting (GRI / ISSB) · HSE Training & Competency Compliance Monitoring · Regulatory Register Interrogation & Audit Analytics

**Engine fit:** HSE Compliance is a partly-soft function: incident narratives, root-cause write-ups, corrective-action plans and policy drafting are free-text and NOT auto-gradable, so they are excluded. The function nonetheless has a strong, defensible quantitative spine that maps cleanly to three of the four engines. (1) logic_input fits statutory rate math (TRIR/LTIFR/severity per OSHA 1904 formulas with a fixed 200,000-hour base) and risk-matrix scoring (likelihood x consequence with residual-risk reduction) - exact, single-number answers that reconcile. (2) spreadsheet fits emissions-intensity and ESG performance reporting (Scope 1/2 tonnes CO2e, intensity per output unit, year-on-year reduction %) where linked cells and a reconciliation/target-gap cell make a clean grading surface. (3) sql fits the compliance-register half of the role - training-certificate expiry, permit-to-work backlog, and overdue inspection actions over a seeded register - which is exactly how an HSE analyst interrogates an EHS management system. advanced_spreadsheet (data tables) was not forced in; a 2-variable array would be contrived for this function, so the mix is logic_input + spreadsheet + sql, which is more authentic to HSE work than a synthetic sensitivity grid. Limitation flagged honestly: this measures the analyst/compliance-officer numeracy of HSE, not the field-judgement or stakeholder-facing competencies, which require human assessment.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Logic input, Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Statutory Safety Performance & Risk Quantification**

- **OSHA Incident-Rate Computation (TRIR, LTIFR & Severity)** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: OSHA 29 CFR 1904 Recordkeeping / ISO 45001 (lagging indicators)
  - _Measures:_ Correct application of the statutory OSHA rate formulas (Rate = N x 200,000 / total hours) for TRIR and LTIFR, the severity rate (lost days x 200,000 / hours), and the derived recordable:lost-time ratio - the core lagging-indicator numeracy every HSE statutory report depends on.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Facilities Management LLC (Abu Dhabi) operated 1,250,000 total employee-hours across its portfolio in 2025. The HSE register records 5 OSHA-recordable injuries, of which 3 were lost-time injuries (LTIs), and a total of 96 calendar days lost to those LTIs. Using the standardized 200,000-hour base (100 full-time-equivalent workers working a year), compute the Total Recordable Incident Rate (TRIR), the Lost-Time Injury Frequency Rate (LTIFR), and the Lost-Day Severity Rate, then confirm the recordable-to-lost-time ratio. The answers must reconcile to the same hour-base.
  - _Model answer:_ TRIR = 5 x 200,000 / 1,250,000 = 0.80. LTIFR = 3 x 200,000 / 1,250,000 = 0.48. Severity Rate = 96 x 200,000 / 1,250,000 = 15.36. Recordable:lost-time ratio = 5 / 3 = 1.6667 (round to 1.67). All three rates share the 200,000 / 1,250,000 = 0.16 multiplier, so they reconcile against the hour base.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w3) - TRIR = 0.80 (5 x 200,000 / 1,250,000) - Total Recordable Incident Rate computed on the correct 200,000-hour OSHA base
    - `logic_value` (w2) - LTIFR = 0.48 (3 x 200,000 / 1,250,000) - Lost-Time Injury Frequency Rate isolates the 3 LTIs, not all 5 recordables
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Severity Rate = 15.36 (96 x 200,000 / 1,250,000) - Lost-Day Severity Rate uses days-lost in the numerator on the same base
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Recordable:LTI ratio = 1.67 (5 / 3) - Derived ratio reconciles the two incident counts
- **Risk Matrix Scoring & Residual-Risk Reduction** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 8 min · ref: ISO 31000 / ISO 45001 risk assessment (5x5 likelihood-consequence matrix)
  - _Measures:_ Quantitative hazard scoring on a likelihood x consequence matrix, computing residual risk after controls and the reduction delta - the calculation underpinning every risk register and permit-to-work decision.
  - _Scenario:_ During a hot-work job hazard analysis at a Jeddah industrial site (NEOM contractor), an HSE officer assesses a confined-space welding task on a 5x5 matrix (Likelihood 1-5 x Consequence 1-5). Inherent (pre-control) assessment: Likelihood = 4, Consequence = 5. After applying engineering and administrative controls (gas monitoring, permit-to-work, standby attendant), the residual assessment is Likelihood = 2, Consequence = 5. The site risk policy classifies any residual score of 15 or above as 'Intolerable - work prohibited', 8-14 as 'High - senior sign-off required', and below 8 as 'Acceptable with controls'. Compute the inherent risk score, the residual risk score, the absolute risk reduction achieved, and the percentage risk reduction.
  - _Model answer:_ Inherent risk = 4 x 5 = 20. Residual risk = 2 x 5 = 10. Absolute reduction = 20 - 10 = 10 points. Percentage reduction = 10 / 20 = 0.50 = 50%. (Residual 10 falls in the 8-14 band = High, senior sign-off - but only the four numeric fields are graded.)
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Inherent risk score = 20 (4 x 5) - Pre-control likelihood x consequence product
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Residual risk score = 10 (2 x 5) - Post-control product uses the reduced likelihood, unchanged consequence
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Absolute risk reduction = 10 - Inherent minus residual delta
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Percentage risk reduction = 50 (%) - Reduction expressed as a percentage of inherent risk

**Pillar - Environmental Performance & Statutory Reporting**

- **Carbon Emissions Intensity & Reduction-Target Reconciliation** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · advanced · 16.7 min · ref: GHG Protocol / GRI 305 / IFRS S2 (ISSB) climate disclosures
  - _Measures:_ Building a linked GHG inventory: converting activity data x emission factors to tonnes CO2e by scope, deriving an intensity KPI, and reconciling actual against a board target and prior year - the exact workflow of an ESG/HSE reporting analyst.
  - _Scenario:_ Saudi Aramco-affiliated logistics subsidiary 'Tanmiyah Distribution' must report 2025 environmental performance under GRI 305 for its Dammam depot. Activity data is given: 480,000 litres of diesel (Scope 1, factor 2.68 kg CO2e/litre), 1,200,000 litres of petrol (Scope 1, factor 2.31 kg CO2e/litre), and 3,500,000 kWh of grid electricity (Scope 2, Saudi grid factor 0.72 kg CO2e/kWh). The depot moved 850,000 tonne-km of freight. The board set a 2025 emissions-intensity target of 9.00 kg CO2e per tonne-km, down from a 2024 actual of 10.20. Complete the linked schedule: Scope 1 total (tonnes CO2e), Scope 2 total (tonnes), gross total, emissions intensity per tonne-km, the year-on-year reduction %, and the variance against the board target (intensity minus target).
  - _Model answer:_ Scope 1 diesel = 480,000 x 2.68 = 1,286,400 kg; petrol = 1,200,000 x 2.31 = 2,772,000 kg; Scope 1 total = 4,058,400 kg = 4,058.40 t. Scope 2 = 3,500,000 x 0.72 = 2,520,000 kg = 2,520.00 t. Gross total = 6,578.40 t. Intensity = 6,578,400 kg / 850,000 tonne-km = 7.7393 kg CO2e/tonne-km. YoY reduction = (10.20 - 7.7393)/10.20 = 24.13%. Variance vs target = 7.7393 - 9.00 = -1.2607 (beats target, i.e. below it).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Scope 1 total = 4,058.40 t CO2e - Diesel + petrol activity x factors summed and converted kg->tonnes
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Scope 2 total = 2,520.00 t CO2e - Electricity x grid factor converted to tonnes
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Gross total emissions = 6,578.40 t CO2e - Scope 1 + Scope 2 linked sum
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Emissions intensity = 7.74 kg CO2e/tonne-km - Gross kg divided by tonne-km activity (intensity KPI)
    - `cell_value` (w2) - YoY intensity reduction = 24.13% - (2024 - 2025 intensity)/2024 reduction percentage
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Variance vs target = -1.26 - Actual intensity minus 9.00 board target (negative = beats target)

**Pillar - Compliance Register Interrogation & Audit Analytics**

- **HSE Compliance-Register Querying (Training, Permits & Overdue Actions)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 11 min · ref: ISO 45001 Clause 9 (Performance Evaluation) / DAMA DMBOK audit analytics
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating a live HSE compliance register with filtering (status + date logic), grouping and a HAVING threshold and ordering - the day-to-day SQL an HSE compliance analyst uses to build statutory exposure reports from an EHS system.
  - _Scenario:_ A Dubai contractor's EHS management system holds an inspection_actions table tracking corrective actions raised during site inspections across multiple contractors. Each row records the contractor, the hazard category, the severity ('low'/'medium'/'high'/'critical'), the status ('open'/'closed'), the due_date and the close_date. The HSE manager preparing the monthly statutory board pack needs the overdue-action exposure by contractor: for each contractor, count the actions that are still OPEN and whose due_date has already passed the reporting reference date of 2025-06-30, returning only contractors with at least one such overdue-open action, highest count first.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT contractor, COUNT(*) AS overdue_open FROM inspection_actions WHERE status = 'open' AND due_date < DATE '2025-06-30' GROUP BY contractor HAVING COUNT(*) >= 1 ORDER BY overdue_open DESC, contractor. The filter must combine the open status with a strict due_date < reference-date test; closed actions and not-yet-due open actions are excluded. Grouping by contractor with a count, the HAVING (>=1) is implicit but enforces 'at least one', and the order is count-descending with a contractor tiebreak for determinism.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master (overdue-open count per contractor, descending) - Correct combined status='open' AND due_date<reference filter, group-by-contractor count, descending order with deterministic tiebreak

---

### 3.7 Workplace Experience, Space Planning, & Utilization Analytics

Sandbox blueprint for the gradable quantitative slice of Workplace Experience, Space Planning & Utilization Analytics (CRE node 3.7). The function's skills list was empty, so I proposed six GCC-grounded skills (occupancy & utilization measurement, space standards & IPMS area accounting, desk-sharing / agile-ratio planning, space cost allocation & chargeback, sensor/badge data interrogation, workplace-experience KPI analytics) and designed to the slice of each that is auto-gradable. 3 pillars, 4 blocks across 3 engines (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql), mixed difficulty. All scenarios use concrete AED/SAR figures and real entities (a DIFC tower floor, a Riyadh HQ, an Abu Dhabi government department) and reference real CRE standards (RICS IPMS, BOMA, IFMA, BCO occupancy density, Leesman/workplace-experience benchmarking). Every block measures demonstrated quant skill the way an IWMS/CAFM analyst would on the job.

**Skills:** Occupancy & Utilization Measurement (peak/average occupancy, utilization rate, vacancy) · Space Standards & IPMS/BOMA Area Accounting (NIA/GIA, density, sq m per person) · Desk-Sharing & Agile-Ratio Planning (sharing ratio, seats required, settlement/flex demand) · Space Cost Allocation & Chargeback (cost per seat, cost per sq m, departmental recovery) · Sensor / Badge / IWMS Data Interrogation (utilization aggregation from raw logs) · Workplace-Experience KPI Analytics (cost efficiency, churn rate, satisfaction-weighted scoring)

**Engine fit:** Strong fit for all engines used. Workplace/space analytics is intrinsically quantitative once you isolate the analytical slice from the soft "experience design" narrative, so no proxy compromise was needed. Utilization, density and area accounting are deterministic arithmetic over building data (spreadsheet + logic_input); a two-variable agile-ratio sizing model is a natural advanced_spreadsheet data-table problem (seats required as price-of-sharing-ratio x growth crossed); and raw badge/sensor swipe logs are exactly the kind of transactional ledger that SQL aggregation grades cleanly. The only intentionally-excluded part of node 3.7 is the genuinely subjective layer (qualitative workplace-experience journey mapping, change-management narrative, design intent) which cannot be auto-graded; engine_fit for that slice is poor and it is deliberately out of scope. What IS graded is the defensible measurement that a CAFM/IWMS workplace analyst produces and that drives every space decision: utilization %, IPMS density, sharing-ratio sizing, cost-per-seat chargeback, and sensor-log interrogation.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 5 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Logic input, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Occupancy & Space Efficiency Measurement**

- **Floor Utilization & Density Workbook** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 15 min · ref: RICS IPMS 3 / BOMA Office Standard / IFMA Space Measurement
  - _Measures:_ Translating raw building + occupancy + cost data into the standard CRE efficiency ratios (density, utilization, vacancy, unit cost) that drive space-rationalization decisions, using correctly linked formulas rather than hardcoded numbers.
  - _Scenario:_ Emaar Square Tower, DIFC, Dubai. Floor 14 has a measured Net Internal Area (IPMS 3) of 1,800 sq m. The floor holds 150 allocated workstations. A four-week badge study recorded an average of 96 people present at the daily peak and an average of 72 people present across the working day. Annual fully-loaded occupancy cost for the floor is AED 4,320,000. Complete the efficiency workbook so the facilities team can benchmark Floor 14 against the BCO 8-10 sq m/person guideline and the corporate 80% peak-utilization target. Given cells: NIA=1800 (B3), Workstations=150 (B4), Peak occupancy=96 (B5), Average occupancy=72 (B6), Annual cost AED=4320000 (B7). Compute: Density sq m/person on workstations (B9 = NIA/Workstations), Peak utilization % (B10 = Peak/Workstations), Average utilization % (B11 = Average/Workstations), Vacancy at peak in seats (B12 = Workstations - Peak), Cost per workstation AED (B13 = Annual cost/Workstations), Cost per sq m AED (B14 = Annual cost/NIA), Effective cost per occupied seat at average AED (B15 = Annual cost/Average).
  - _Model answer:_ B9 = 1800/150 = 12.0 sq m/person. B10 = 96/150 = 0.64 (64%). B11 = 72/150 = 0.48 (48%). B12 = 150-96 = 54 seats vacant at peak. B13 = 4320000/150 = 28,800 AED per workstation. B14 = 4320000/1800 = 2,400 AED per sq m. B15 = 4320000/72 = 60,000 AED per occupied seat at average occupancy. Checkpoints store utilization as decimals (0.64, 0.48) consistent with =Peak/Workstations.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Density sq m per workstation (B9 = NIA/Workstations) - Correct IPMS density computed by dividing measured area by seat count
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Peak utilization (B10 = Peak/Workstations = 0.64) - Peak occupancy expressed as a utilization rate against capacity
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Average utilization (B11 = Average/Workstations = 0.48) - Average daily occupancy expressed as a utilization rate
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Vacancy at peak in seats (B12 = 54) - Idle-capacity headroom even at the busiest point of the day
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Cost per workstation AED (B13 = 28800) - Annual occupancy cost divided across provisioned seats
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Effective cost per occupied seat at average (B15 = 60000) - Recognising that low utilization inflates true per-person cost
- **IPMS Area Reconciliation & Net-to-Gross Logic** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 8 min · ref: RICS IPMS: Office Buildings / BOMA Load Factor
  - _Measures:_ Applying IPMS/BOMA area hierarchy (gross to net, common-area load factor, usable-space breakdown) - the area accounting that underpins every lease charge and chargeback in corporate real estate.
  - _Scenario:_ Olaya HQ, Riyadh. A single floor plate measures 2,500 sq m Gross Internal Area (IPMS 1). Common/shared areas (lift lobbies, cores, plant, shared circulation) total 600 sq m. Of the remaining usable space, dedicated meeting rooms and collaboration zones take 380 sq m and the balance is open-plan workspace. The department occupying the floor is charged on its Net Internal Area share. Compute each figure for the area-reconciliation note. Fields: Net Internal Area sq m (NIA = GIA - common); Open-plan workspace sq m (open = NIA - meeting/collab); Common-area add-on factor as a percentage of NIA (load_factor_pct = common / NIA x 100); Workspace ratio - open-plan as a percentage of NIA (workspace_ratio_pct = open / NIA x 100).
  - _Model answer:_ NIA = 2500 - 600 = 1900 sq m. Open-plan = 1900 - 380 = 1520 sq m. Load factor = 600/1900 x 100 = 31.578... -> 31.58%. Workspace ratio = 1520/1900 x 100 = 80.00%. Tolerance 0.1 on the percentages to allow rounding.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Net Internal Area sq m (1900) - Gross-to-net deduction of common areas
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Open-plan workspace sq m (1520) - Usable space net of meeting/collaboration allocation
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Common-area load factor % (31.58) - Load/add-on factor expressed against NIA per BOMA
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Workspace ratio % (80.00) - Share of net area that is revenue/headcount-bearing workspace

**Pillar - Agile Workplace Sizing & Scenario Planning**

- **Desk-Sharing Ratio Sensitivity Matrix** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 16.7 min · ref: BCO Occupancy Density Guide / IFMA Workplace Strategy
  - _Measures:_ Building a defensible activity-based-working sizing model and stress-testing desk demand across the two levers that actually move it (sharing ratio and headcount growth) using a native two-variable data table rather than manual recomputation.
  - _Scenario:_ Abu Dhabi government department, ADGM-adjacent campus. Headcount today is 800 employees. The workplace strategy team is moving to activity-based working and must size the desk count under different desk-sharing ratios (employees per shared desk) and headcount-growth scenarios. The seats-required model is: Seats Required = ROUNDUP( Headcount x (1 + Growth%) / SharingRatio, 0 ). Base case uses SharingRatio = 1.25 (B2) and Growth = 0% (B3); Headcount = 800 (B1). Build the base-case seat count in B5 = ROUNDUP(B1*(1+B3)/B2,0), then build a two-variable data table over SharingRatio columns {1.0, 1.25, 1.5} and Growth rows {0%, 10%, 20%} so leadership can see how desk demand falls as sharing intensifies and rises as the workforce grows. The data table must be a native data table, not hardcoded numbers. Corner of the table (B8) links to the seats-required cell (=B5).
  - _Model answer:_ Base case B5 = ROUNDUP(800*(1+0)/1.25,0) = 640 seats. Data table cells = ROUNDUP(800*(1+Growth)/Ratio,0). Corner cells: at Ratio 1.0 / Growth 0% = ROUNDUP(800/1.0,0)=800 (low-sharing, no-growth = most desks). At Ratio 1.5 / Growth 20% = ROUNDUP(800*1.2/1.5,0)=ROUNDUP(640,0)=640. Centre at Ratio 1.25 / Growth 10% = ROUNDUP(800*1.1/1.25,0)=ROUNDUP(704,0)=704. The is_array_formula checkpoint confirms the candidate used Excel's Data Table ({=TABLE()}) rather than typing values; corner cell_values confirm the model arithmetic.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Seat-demand grid uses a native data table {=TABLE()} (not hardcoded) - Candidate built a real two-variable data table driven by the seats-required formula
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base-case seats required (B5 = 640) - ROUNDUP sizing at sharing ratio 1.25, zero growth
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Worst case - Ratio 1.0, Growth 0% = 800 seats - No-sharing, no-growth corner equals headcount (most desks)
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Centre case - Ratio 1.25, Growth 10% = 704 seats - Interior cell with both levers active and ROUNDUP applied
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Best case - Ratio 1.5, Growth 20% = 640 seats - High-sharing offsets workforce growth at the far corner
- **Space Cost Allocation & Chargeback** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 9 min · ref: IFMA / RICS Service-Charge & Cost-Allocation Practice
  - _Measures:_ Running an area-based space-cost chargeback (blended rate to departmental charge to per-head cost) plus the churn-rate KPI - the core financial outputs a workplace analyst supplies to Finance and to space governance.
  - _Scenario:_ Shared-services campus, Jeddah. Total annual occupancy cost for the building is SAR 9,600,000 and the building's chargeable Net Internal Area is 6,000 sq m. The Finance department occupies 1,200 sq m and has 60 staff; it shares the building with other departments under an area-based chargeback. A separate move-and-change (churn) programme relocated 144 of the building's 480 total staff during the year. Compute the chargeback note. Fields: Blended cost per sq m SAR (cost_per_sqm = total cost / NIA); Finance department annual charge SAR (finance_charge = cost_per_sqm x Finance area); Finance cost per head SAR (finance_cost_per_head = finance_charge / Finance staff); Annual churn rate as a percentage (churn_rate_pct = relocated staff / total staff x 100).
  - _Model answer:_ cost_per_sqm = 9,600,000 / 6,000 = 1,600 SAR/sq m. finance_charge = 1,600 x 1,200 = 1,920,000 SAR. finance_cost_per_head = 1,920,000 / 60 = 32,000 SAR. churn_rate = 144 / 480 x 100 = 30.00%. Tolerances: 0.5 on currency fields, 0.1 on churn %.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Blended cost per sq m SAR (1600) - Total occupancy cost spread over chargeable NIA
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Finance department annual charge SAR (1920000) - Area-based chargeback applied to the department footprint
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Finance cost per head SAR (32000) - Departmental charge converted to a per-occupant unit cost
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Annual churn rate % (30.00) - Move-and-change volume expressed as the standard churn KPI

**Pillar - Utilization Data Interrogation**

- **Badge & Sensor Log Aggregation (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA DMBOK / IFMA IWMS-CAFM Data Practice
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating raw IWMS/sensor event logs with grouped aggregation and ordering - the SQL a workplace analyst writes to turn millions of swipe/sensor rows into a floor-level utilization ranking.
  - _Scenario:_ A workplace-sensor platform logs one row per occupancy-detection event from desk and meeting-room sensors across an Emaar campus. Table occupancy_events(id, floor, space_type, building, event_date, occupied_minutes). The space team wants to see which floors are most heavily used. Write ONE query that returns, per floor, the total occupied minutes, ordered from most-used floor to least. Return columns floor and total_minutes, highest total first. Seed rows: (1,'L10','desk','Emaar A','2025-03-03',420),(2,'L10','meeting','Emaar A','2025-03-03',180),(3,'L11','desk','Emaar A','2025-03-03',300),(4,'L10','desk','Emaar A','2025-03-04',390),(5,'L12','meeting','Emaar A','2025-03-04',120),(6,'L11','desk','Emaar A','2025-03-04',360),(7,'L12','desk','Emaar A','2025-03-05',90),(8,'L10','desk','Emaar A','2025-03-05',450).
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT floor, SUM(occupied_minutes) AS total_minutes FROM occupancy_events GROUP BY floor ORDER BY total_minutes DESC, floor. Expected result set: L10 = 420+180+390+450 = 1440; L11 = 300+360 = 660; L12 = 120+90 = 210. Ordered descending by total: L10 (1440), L11 (660), L12 (210). Order-sensitive match.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Floor-level total occupied minutes, most-used floor first (ordered) - Correct GROUP BY floor with SUM aggregation and descending order by total

---

## Data & AI

> **Domain review** - engine coverage OK. All 10 blueprints are structurally sound against the hard contract in src/lib/technical-sandbox/types.ts. Every block maps to one of the 4 auto-gradable engines (spreadsheet / advanced_spreadsheet / logic_input / sql); none uses the `python` EngineType, which is correct since python has no corresponding CheckpointKind and would be ungradable. Engine-to-checkpoint pairings are all valid: every sql block carries exactly 1 sql_result_match checkpoint (matches the FP&A reference where the SQL block also has a single result-set check - not a defect), logic_input blocks use logic_value fields, and spreadsheet/advanced_spreadsheet blocks use cell_value/is_array_formula. Structural counts: all nodes have exactly 3 pillars and 3-5 blocks (4.1/4.2/4.4/4.5/4.7 = 5 blocks; 4.3/4.6/4.8/4.9/4.10 = 4 blocks). Every node uses >=2 engine types (4.1/4.2/4.8/4.9/4.10 use 3; 4.3/4.4/4.5/4.6/4.7 use 4). Difficulty mixes are sensible across all nodes. Engine-fit narratives are uniformly strong and honest: each one names the gradable quantitative/analytical slice and explicitly excludes the ungradable free-text/code parts (orchestration choice, IaC, model-card writeups, policy prose, prompt craft, architecture narrative). Two nodes correctly anticipate a real grading hazard - 4.6 and 4.8 deliberately avoid SQL percentile (p95) functions for SQLite/Postgres portability. The data_ai domain is intrinsically quantitative, so unlike soft-function domains there is no forced proxy that lands weakly; the AI governance (4.9) and data governance (4.10) functions, which sound qualitative, are correctly reduced to fairness/DQ/retention arithmetic + relational interrogation. Coverage of the 4 engines across the domain is healthy: sql appears in all 10, logic_input in all 10, advanced_spreadsheet in 8, plain spreadsheet in 5.
>
> - _(low)_ 4.10: Engine variety is the weakest in the set: 4 blocks use only {logic_input x2, advanced_spreadsheet, sql} and notably OMIT the plain `spreadsheet` engine entirely, while two of four blocks are logic_input. The sitting risks feeling repetitive (two near-identical numeric-field blocks: DAMA DQ scoring and Retention/Consent/Breach math are both intermediate logic_input arithmetic). Consider converting one logic_input block to a plain `spreadsheet` model (e.g. an MDM match/merge survivorship reconciliation grid or a consent-coverage rollup with cell_value checks) to add a 4th engine and reduce the logic_input duplication.
> - _(low)_ 4.4: The A/B-Test Lift & Significance block (logic_input, advanced) asks the candidate to hand-compute a pooled-proportion z-statistic. This is gradable as a single numeric logic_value, but it is only fair/deterministic if the engine_config supplies the exact formula and the rounding/df conventions; otherwise multiple defensible z-values (pooled vs unpooled, continuity correction) will fail the exact-match check. Confirm the block prompt pins the formula and tolerance. Same caution applies to 4.5's two-proportion z-test block.
> - _(low)_ 4.5: Two of the five blocks are advanced/intermediate logic_input statistics (Classification Metrics from a Confusion Matrix at basic + A/B Test Two-Proportion z-Test at intermediate). Both are pure formula reconciliation - good - but ensure the confusion-matrix block's logic_value fields (precision/recall/F1/specificity) are checked with adequate tolerance for rounding, since F1 is a ratio-of-ratios that compounds rounding error if the candidate rounds intermediate precision/recall before combining.
> - _(low)_ 4.1: Two of the five blocks are sql (Staging-to-Clean dedup/window-ranking + Data Quality Audit). The dedup block relies on window-ranking (ROW_NUMBER/RANK OVER PARTITION). Window functions are supported in modern Postgres and SQLite 3.25+, but confirm the grading DB dialect actually supports them (the FP&A reference uses postgres). If the sandbox executes on an older SQLite, the master_query will fail. Pin dialect=postgres (or SQLite >= 3.25) in engine_config for both window-function-dependent blocks.
> - _(low)_ 4.2: Two sql blocks are both rated `advanced` (Star-Schema Aggregation + SCD-2 Point-in-Time), and the engine_fit prose claims a fit `across all four engines` but the blueprint uses only 3 engine types (sql, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input) - plain `spreadsheet` is not used. The narrative slightly overstates engine coverage; the structure is still valid (3 engine types > the >=2 minimum). Minor wording mismatch to correct, and consider whether one of the two advanced SQL blocks could drop to intermediate for a gentler difficulty ramp.
>
> _Recommendations:_ No blocking defects - all 10 blueprints are shippable against the engine/checkpoint contract and match FP&A's rigor. The data_ai domain is a natural fit for the auto-gradable engines (it is intrinsically numeric/relational), so the engine_fit narratives are honest rather than strained, and the genuinely ungradable parts (orchestration choice, IaC, model cards, policy/ethics prose, prompt craft) are correctly excluded into the MCQ/human-review layer. Recommended polish, in priority order: (1) 4.10 - swap one of the two logic_input blocks for a plain `spreadsheet` block to add engine variety and remove the near-duplicate numeric-field sitting; this is the only node that feels engine-thin. (2) For every statistics-by-hand logic_input block (4.4 A/B z-test, 4.5 z-test + confusion-matrix F1, plus any IoU/F1/kappa fields in 4.7/4.8/4.9), make sure the block prompt pins the exact formula and the checkpoint sets a tolerance generous enough to absorb intermediate rounding (compounded ratios like F1 and z are the main exact-match failure risk). (3) Pin the SQL dialect (postgres, matching the FP&A reference) wherever window functions / date arithmetic / GROUP BY-HAVING are used - especially 4.1's dedup-window block and 4.2's SCD-2 query - so the master_query runs on the grading DB. (4) Trim 4.2's engine_fit wording: it says `all four engines` but only uses three; align the prose to the actual block set. None of these change the engine mapping or the pass/fail validity - they are fairness/portability hardening, not redesigns.

### 4.1 Data Engineering & Pipeline Infrastructure Management (ETL/ELT)

Hands-on sandbox for Data Engineering / ETL-ELT proficiency, designed to the empty skills list (six skills proposed below). The function is an excellent fit for the gradable engines: SQL is the literal substance of ELT transformation, deduplication, SCD merge logic and data-quality auditing, so two of four blocks are pure SQL against seeded GCC datasets; logic_input carries the quantitative pipeline-engineering math (data-quality scorecards, SLA/throughput/partition sizing, late-arriving-data reconciliation) that has exact numeric answers; one spreadsheet block models incremental-load reconciliation and warehouse cost/throughput. Three pillars - (1) Pipeline Construction & Transformation Logic [sql], (2) Data Quality, Integrity & Reconciliation [logic_input + spreadsheet], (3) Warehouse Modeling & Load Interrogation [sql]. Four blocks, three engines (sql x2, logic_input, spreadsheet), mixed difficulty. Frameworks: DAMA DMBOK2, Kimball dimensional modeling, ISO 8000 / ISO 25012 data quality, and operational SLA/throughput engineering practice. The non-gradable slices of the role (orchestration tooling choice, infra-as-code, platform selection) are intentionally excluded; every block reduces to exact numeric cell/field values or a result-set match.

**Skills:** SQL Transformation & ELT Logic (dedup, joins, window functions) · Data Quality, Profiling & Validation (DMBOK / ISO 8000) · Dimensional Modeling & Slowly-Changing Dimensions (Kimball SCD Type 2) · Incremental Load, CDC & Reconciliation · Pipeline SLA, Throughput & Partition Sizing · Idempotency, Deduplication & Late-Arriving Data Handling

**Engine fit:** Strong fit. Data engineering is one of the most directly auto-gradable technical functions because its core deliverable IS executable code with deterministic output. SQL is the native medium of ELT (the "T" in transformation and the "L" load-validation), so 2 of 4 blocks are pure sql graded by sql_result_match against a master query - covering staged-to-clean transformation with dedup/window-ranking, and a Kimball SCD Type-2 / data-quality interrogation. The quantitative engineering decisions (data-quality completeness/validity scoring per ISO 8000, pipeline throughput vs SLA window, partition/file sizing, and CDC late-arriving-data reconciliation) all have exact closed-form numeric answers, so they map cleanly to logic_input (logic_value checks that reconcile). Incremental-load reconciliation - comparing source vs target row counts and amounts across a watermark, computing the delta to load and the post-load balance - is a natural spreadsheet model with cell_value checks. WHAT IS DELIBERATELY EXCLUDED (honest limitation): the engines cannot grade orchestration-tool selection (Airflow vs Dagster), infrastructure-as-code authoring, DAG design quality, streaming-architecture trade-offs, or written runbooks - those are judgement/free-text and live in the separate MCQ layer or a human review. This sandbox measures the analytical/quantitative + query-authoring core that genuinely separates a competent data engineer from a novice, which is the gradable and most defensible slice of the role.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 5 tasks · engines: SQL, Logic input, Spreadsheet

**Pillar - Pipeline Construction & Transformation Logic**

- **Staging-to-Clean ELT Transformation (Dedup + Window Ranking)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA DMBOK2 (Data Integration & Interoperability) / ANSI SQL window functions
  - _Measures:_ SQL transformation logic: deduplication and current-record selection using window functions (ROW_NUMBER/RANK with a composite ORDER BY), the core ELT skill that separates engineers who can build idempotent curated layers from those who only write naive GROUP BY aggregations.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates NBD's raw ingestion layer lands one row per CRM 'customer touch' event into stg_customer_events (account_id, full_name, emirate, event_ts, source_system, amount_aed). The source replays events, so the staging table contains duplicate event rows AND multiple historical records per account from three feeds (core_banking, mobile_app, branch). The clean/curated layer must hold exactly ONE current row per account_id: the latest event by event_ts (tie-break by the higher amount_aed, then by source_system alphabetically). Seeded data: ~14 rows across 6 accounts including exact-duplicate replays and 3 accounts with multiple feeds. The candidate writes ONE query returning the deduplicated current-record set: columns account_id, full_name, emirate, amount_aed ordered by account_id ascending. This is the canonical ELT 'pick the winning record' transformation that every CDP/MDM pipeline performs.
  - _Model answer:_ Use a CTE with ROW_NUMBER() OVER (PARTITION BY account_id ORDER BY event_ts DESC, amount_aed DESC, source_system ASC) AS rn over stg_customer_events, then SELECT account_id, full_name, emirate, amount_aed WHERE rn = 1 ORDER BY account_id. The exact-duplicate replays collapse because the composite ORDER BY plus the rn=1 filter keeps exactly one row per partition; the tie-break columns guarantee determinism so the result set is identical to the master query. master_query: WITH ranked AS (SELECT *, ROW_NUMBER() OVER (PARTITION BY account_id ORDER BY event_ts DESC, amount_aed DESC, source_system ASC) AS rn FROM stg_customer_events) SELECT account_id, full_name, emirate, amount_aed FROM ranked WHERE rn = 1 ORDER BY account_id.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Returns exactly one current row per account_id, correctly ranked, ordered by account_id - Deduplication + latest-record window selection produces the exact master result set (6 rows, correct winning record per account, correct order)
- **Data Quality Audit Query (Orphans, Nulls & Referential Integrity)** &nbsp; `SQL` · advanced · 10 min · ref: ISO 8000 / ISO/IEC 25012 (Data Quality) + DMBOK2 Data Quality dimensions
  - _Measures:_ Data-quality engineering via SQL: detecting referential-integrity violations / orphaned fact rows with an anti-join (LEFT JOIN ... IS NULL or NOT EXISTS). Distinguishes engineers who build defensive quality gates from those who ship broken dimensional models.
  - _Scenario:_ STC Bahrain's loan data mart has two tables: dim_borrower (borrower_id, national_id, segment) and fact_loan (loan_id, borrower_id, principal_bhd, status). The pipeline's data-quality gate must flag REFERENTIAL-INTEGRITY violations before publish: loans whose borrower_id does NOT exist in dim_borrower (orphaned facts from a late-arriving dimension). Seeded data: ~10 dim rows and ~16 fact rows, of which a known set reference borrower_ids that are absent from the dimension (e.g. borrower_id 9001, 9002). The candidate writes ONE query returning the orphaned loans: columns loan_id, borrower_id, principal_bhd ordered by principal_bhd descending then loan_id ascending. This is the standard pre-publish integrity check in any star-schema load.
  - _Model answer:_ Anti-join fact to dimension: SELECT f.loan_id, f.borrower_id, f.principal_bhd FROM fact_loan f LEFT JOIN dim_borrower d ON f.borrower_id = d.borrower_id WHERE d.borrower_id IS NULL ORDER BY f.principal_bhd DESC, f.loan_id ASC. Equivalent NOT EXISTS / NOT IN (with NULL guard) formulations also reproduce the master result set. The seeded orphan rows are the only ones whose borrower_id is absent from dim_borrower, so the result is deterministic. master_query: SELECT f.loan_id, f.borrower_id, f.principal_bhd FROM fact_loan f LEFT JOIN dim_borrower d ON f.borrower_id = d.borrower_id WHERE d.borrower_id IS NULL ORDER BY f.principal_bhd DESC, f.loan_id ASC.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Returns exactly the orphaned fact rows (no false positives/negatives), ordered by principal then loan_id - Anti-join referential-integrity detection matches the master result set exactly, including correct exclusion of all loans that DO have a matching borrower

**Pillar - Data Quality, Integrity & Reconciliation**

- **Data Quality Scorecard & Profiling Metrics** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 8 min · ref: ISO 8000 / DMBOK2 Six Data Quality Dimensions (Completeness, Validity, Uniqueness)
  - _Measures:_ Quantitative data-quality scoring: translating raw profiling counts into the DMBOK/ISO 8000 completeness, validity and uniqueness ratios and a composite gate decision - the daily judgement a data engineer automates into every pipeline's quality stage.
  - _Scenario:_ A nightly profiling job ran over a 50,000-row customer ingestion batch for Mashreq Bank. The profiler reports: email column - 46,500 non-null values; emirates_id column - 49,000 values that pass the 15-digit format regex out of 50,000 total; mobile column - 1,250 duplicate phone numbers detected across the batch. The data-quality gate publishes ONLY if the composite DQ score clears 90%. The candidate computes each dimension as a percentage of the 50,000-row batch and the composite. Completeness (email) = non-null / total. Validity (emirates_id) = format-passing / total. Uniqueness (mobile) = (total - duplicates) / total. Composite DQ score = simple average of the three dimension percentages. Then the publish decision flag (1 = publish, 0 = block).
  - _Model answer:_ Completeness = 46500/50000 = 93.0%. Validity = 49000/50000 = 98.0%. Uniqueness = (50000-1250)/50000 = 48750/50000 = 97.5%. Composite = (93.0 + 98.0 + 97.5)/3 = 288.5/3 = 96.1667% (≈ 96.17%). Since 96.17% >= 90%, publish flag = 1. Each field graded as a percentage value with small tolerance; the composite tolerance is wider to absorb rounding; the flag is exact.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Completeness % (email non-null rate) - Completeness dimension = 46500/50000 = 93.0
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Validity % (emirates_id format-pass rate) - Validity dimension = 49000/50000 = 98.0
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Uniqueness % (mobile de-dup rate) - Uniqueness dimension = 48750/50000 = 97.5
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Composite DQ score % - Composite = average(93.0, 98.0, 97.5) = 96.17 - reconciles the three dimensions
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Publish-gate decision flag (1=publish, 0=block) - 96.17% >= 90% threshold so gate = 1; tests the engineer applies the gate rule correctly
- **Incremental Load Reconciliation (CDC Watermark Balancing)** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 15 min · ref: Kimball ETL Subsystems (Change Data Capture & Audit Dimension) / DMBOK2
  - _Measures:_ Incremental/CDC load reconciliation: balancing source extract against target before/after counts and amounts across a watermark, and proving zero variance to the source control total - the audit step that catches dropped or double-loaded partitions.
  - _Scenario:_ An incremental (CDC) pipeline loads daily transactions from a Saudi e-commerce source (Noon KSA) into a warehouse fact table using a high-watermark on load_ts. A pre-populated reconciliation grid gives: target row count BEFORE today's load = 1,200,000 and target amount BEFORE = SAR 845,000,000. Today's source extract (rows with load_ts after the watermark) = 38,500 inserted rows + 4,200 updated rows (updates restate amount, they do not add rows) + 90,000 SAR of soft-deleted reversals. Source control totals for today: gross new+changed amount = SAR 31,250,000. The candidate completes the reconciliation: net rows to insert, expected target row count AFTER load, expected target amount AFTER load (before + new amount - reversals), and the reconciliation variance vs the source-provided post-load control total of SAR 876,160,000 (must be 0).
  - _Model answer:_ Net rows to insert = inserted rows only = 38,500 (updates restate existing rows, do not change count; reversals are soft-deletes that do not remove physical rows in this append-audit model). Target rows AFTER = 1,200,000 + 38,500 = 1,238,500. Target amount AFTER = 845,000,000 + 31,250,000 - 90,000 = 876,160,000 SAR. Reconciliation variance = expected AFTER amount - source control total = 876,160,000 - 876,160,000 = 0. The balance-check cell of 0 is the highest-weighted checkpoint exactly as in the FP&A model's balance check.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Net rows to insert this load - = 38,500 (inserts only; updates and soft-deletes do not change physical row count)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Target row count AFTER load - = 1,200,000 + 38,500 = 1,238,500
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Target amount AFTER load (SAR) - = 845,000,000 + 31,250,000 - 90,000 = 876,160,000
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Reconciliation variance vs source control total (must = 0) - = 876,160,000 - 876,160,000 = 0; proves the incremental load balances end-to-end

**Pillar - Warehouse Modeling & Load Interrogation**

- **Pipeline SLA, Throughput & Partition Sizing** &nbsp; `Logic input` · advanced · 8 min · ref: DMBOK2 Data Storage & Operations + standard ETL throughput/SLA engineering practice
  - _Measures:_ Pipeline capacity engineering: converting an SLA window + per-worker throughput into a parallelism requirement, and sizing partition/file layout from row volume - the sizing math that determines whether a pipeline meets its window and avoids small-file or skew problems.
  - _Scenario:_ A daily batch pipeline for Qatar's QNB must ingest 720,000,000 rows within a 4-hour load window (the SLA). A single worker sustains 25,000 rows/second. The target table is partitioned daily and the platform recommends ~256 MB partition files; each row averages 1.0 KB on disk. The candidate computes: (a) total seconds in the SLA window, (b) rows a single worker can process in the window, (c) the MINIMUM number of parallel workers required to meet the SLA (round UP - you cannot run a fractional worker), (d) the day's total data volume in GB (1 GB = 1,024 MB, 1 MB = 1,024 KB), and (e) the number of 256 MB partition files needed to hold the day (round UP).
  - _Model answer:_ (a) SLA seconds = 4 h x 3,600 = 14,400 s. (b) Single-worker rows = 25,000 x 14,400 = 360,000,000 rows. (c) Min workers = ceil(720,000,000 / 360,000,000) = ceil(2.0) = 2 workers. (d) Volume: 720,000,000 rows x 1.0 KB = 720,000,000 KB; /1,024 = 703,125 MB; /1,024 = 686.6455 GB (≈ 686.65 GB). (e) Partition files = ceil(703,125 MB / 256 MB) = ceil(2,746.58) = 2,747 files. The ceil on workers and files tests that the engineer never under-provisions a window or under-counts files.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - SLA window in seconds - = 4 x 3600 = 14,400
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Rows a single worker processes in the window - = 25,000 x 14,400 = 360,000,000
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Minimum parallel workers to meet SLA (round up) - = ceil(720,000,000 / 360,000,000) = 2; tests round-up provisioning logic
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total daily data volume (GB) - = 720,000,000 KB / 1024 / 1024 = 686.65 GB; tests binary-unit conversion
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Number of 256 MB partition files (round up) - = ceil(703,125 / 256) = 2,747; tests file-sizing round-up

---

### 4.2 Enterprise Data Warehousing & Schema Architecture Design

Hands-on sandbox for Enterprise Data Warehousing & Schema Architecture Design (node 4.2, data_ai). The function's skills list was empty, so six realistic skills were proposed grounded in Kimball/Inmon dimensional-modeling practice and modern cloud-warehouse engineering (BigQuery/Snowflake/Redshift) as deployed across GCC banking and government data platforms: (1) Dimensional Modeling (star/snowflake, fact-grain selection), (2) Slowly-Changing Dimensions (SCD Type 1/2/3 versioning), (3) Analytical SQL & Aggregation (the demonstrable core), (4) Warehouse Storage & Compute Cost Economics, (5) Partitioning, Clustering & Query-Pruning Performance, (6) Data Quality, Conformance & Load Reconciliation. The discipline is strongly auto-gradable: its primary craft is querying a relational warehouse (sql engine), and its quantitative engineering layers - storage/compute cost modeling, partition-pruning scan reduction, SCD-2 surrogate-key/version math, and load-reconciliation row-count integrity - decompose cleanly into deterministic numeric checks (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input). Three pillars, five blocks, all four engines exercised; difficulty mixes basic (cost-scan logic), intermediate (SCD logic, reconciliation logic, cost matrix), and advanced (dimensional analytical SQL).

**Skills:** Dimensional Modeling (Star/Snowflake & Fact-Grain Selection) · Slowly-Changing Dimensions (SCD Type 1/2/3 Versioning) · Analytical SQL & Aggregation over a Star Schema · Warehouse Storage & Compute Cost Economics · Partitioning, Clustering & Query-Pruning Performance · Data Quality, Conformance & Load Reconciliation

**Engine fit:** Strong, native fit across all four engines - this is one of the most directly gradable functions in the catalogue. The core craft of a data-warehouse architect IS writing analytical SQL against a star schema, so the sql engine measures the headline skill at full fidelity (two blocks: a dimensional star-join aggregation and an SCD-2 point-in-time current-version query). The engineering economics and performance layers - which look qualitative ("design for cost", "tune for scan-pruning") but are in practice arithmetic - are made gradable as deterministic numeric work: a two-variable advanced_spreadsheet cost matrix over storage tier x retention (compressed-GB billing under BigQuery/Snowflake-style on-demand pricing, an is_array_formula + corner cell_value check), a logic_input partition-pruning block (bytes scanned with/without a partition filter, % scan reduction, and on-demand AED query cost - the exact math an architect uses to justify a partitioning strategy), and a logic_input SCD-2 + load-reconciliation block (surrogate-key count after a versioning load, current-row count, and a source-to-target reconciliation delta that must net to zero). Nothing in this blueprint relies on free-text DDL drafting, ER-diagram drawing, or subjective "is this schema good" judgement - all of which would be ungradable; instead every block reduces an architecture decision to a number the validator can verify exactly. The only honest limitation: physical DDL authoring (CREATE TABLE / clustering-key declaration) and ERD design cannot be auto-graded by these engines, so the sandbox proxies schema competence through the analytical and quantitative consequences of those design choices (correct grain -> correct aggregation; correct partition key -> correct scan math) rather than the DDL artefact itself. Frameworks: Kimball Dimensional Modeling Toolkit, Inmon CIF, DAMA-DMBOK2, ISO/IEC 11179 (metadata), plus GCC cloud-cost practice.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 5 tasks · engines: SQL, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input

**Pillar - Dimensional Modeling & Analytical Querying**

- **Star-Schema Analytical Aggregation (Fact-Dimension Join)** &nbsp; `SQL` · advanced · 10 min · ref: Kimball Dimensional Modeling Toolkit / DAMA-DMBOK2
  - _Measures:_ Ability to navigate a star schema - join a fact to its conformed dimensions, apply a dimension-attribute filter, aggregate at a chosen grain, and order the result. This is the headline data-warehouse architect skill: demonstrating the schema supports the business question and that the candidate can express grain + filter + aggregation correctly.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates NBD's analytics warehouse holds a retail-transactions star schema. fact_txn (txn_id, date_key, branch_key, product_key, amount_aed, txn_count) is conformed against dim_branch (branch_key, branch_name, emirate) and dim_product (product_key, product_line, product_name). Seeded data: 4 branches across Dubai/Abu Dhabi/Sharjah, 4 products in 2 product lines (Cards, Loans), and ~12 fact rows for Q1-2025. The CFO wants, per emirate, total transaction value across the Cards product line only, ranked highest first. The candidate must join the fact to both dimensions, filter on the Cards product line, group at the emirate grain, and sum amount_aed. Columns: emirate, total_aed, ordered by total_aed descending then emirate.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT b.emirate, SUM(f.amount_aed) AS total_aed FROM fact_txn f JOIN dim_branch b ON f.branch_key=b.branch_key JOIN dim_product p ON f.product_key=p.product_key WHERE p.product_line='Cards' GROUP BY b.emirate ORDER BY total_aed DESC, b.emirate. The seed is constructed so the three emirates' Cards totals are distinct (e.g. Dubai 48,500 / Abu Dhabi 31,200 / Sharjah 12,750 AED), forcing a correct two-key ordered result set. A candidate who omits the product_line filter, joins only one dimension, or groups at branch grain produces a non-matching result set.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master (per-emirate Cards total_aed, ordered DESC) - correct join, filter, grain and order - Star-schema join across two conformed dimensions + dimension-attribute filter + emirate-grain aggregation + correct descending order
- **SCD Type-2 Point-in-Time Current Version Query** &nbsp; `SQL` · advanced · 10 min · ref: Kimball SCD Type 2 / DAMA-DMBOK2 Data Modeling
  - _Measures:_ Correct handling of a Type-2 SCD - the candidate must isolate the current version of each business key (is_current = true, equivalently valid_to = '9999-12-31') before counting, demonstrating they understand version semantics and will not double-count history. This is the single most common SCD-2 query error in production warehouses.
  - _Scenario:_ STC (Saudi Telecom) maintains a Type-2 slowly-changing customer dimension dim_customer_scd (cust_sk, cust_id, segment, region, valid_from, valid_to, is_current). Some customers have multiple historical rows (segment migrated Consumer->SME->Enterprise) tracked via valid_from/valid_to and a boolean is_current flag (current rows carry valid_to = '9999-12-31'). Seeded: 5 business-key customers, 9 total versioned rows. The data-governance team needs the count of currently-active customers in each region, but ONLY the current version of each customer must be counted (historical rows excluded). Columns: region, current_customers, ordered by current_customers descending then region.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT region, COUNT(*) AS current_customers FROM dim_customer_scd WHERE is_current = true GROUP BY region ORDER BY current_customers DESC, region. (Equivalent valid_to = DATE '9999-12-31' filter also matches.) The seed places historical rows in regions/segments that differ from the current row for the same cust_id, so a candidate who forgets the is_current filter and counts all 9 rows gets the wrong per-region counts and a non-matching result set. Result e.g. Riyadh 2 / Jeddah 2 / Dammam 1.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master (per-region current_customers, ordered) - only current SCD-2 versions counted - Type-2 SCD current-version isolation (is_current/valid_to filter) before per-region aggregation; history correctly excluded

**Pillar - Warehouse Storage & Compute Economics**

- **Storage-Tier x Retention Cost Matrix (Two-Variable Data Table)** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: DAMA-DMBOK2 Data Storage & Operations / GCC cloud-cost practice
  - _Measures:_ Ability to model cloud-warehouse storage economics - convert raw to compressed billed volume, apply tiered per-GB-month pricing, and build a native two-variable sensitivity table over the two levers (retention, tier) an architect actually negotiates. Tests both the formula correctness and use of a real array/data-table construct rather than manual fill.
  - _Scenario:_ ADNOC is sizing the annual storage bill for a new event-warehouse on a BigQuery/Snowflake-style platform. Base inputs (given cells): raw daily volume = 500 GB/day; compression ratio = 5x (so billed compressed GB = raw / 5); active-storage price = 0.092 AED per compressed-GB-month; long-term (cold) storage price = 0.046 AED per compressed-GB-month (50% discount, applied once data is past the active window). The architect must build a base annual-cost formula and then a two-variable data table showing TOTAL ANNUAL STORAGE COST (AED) across retention period (rows: 12 / 24 / 36 months) and storage tier (cols: Active 0.092 / Cold 0.046 AED-per-GB-month). The annual cost for a given retention R months at price P = compressed_GB_at_full_retention x P x 12, where compressed_GB accumulated = (500/5) GB/day x 30 days x R months held... use the simplified model in the grid: monthly_compressed_GB = (500/5)*30 = 3000 GB/month; cost = 3000 GB/month x R months retained x P (price per GB-month) gives the steady-state annual carrying cost. The data table cells must be data-table-driven, not hardcoded.
  - _Model answer:_ monthly_compressed_GB = (500/5)*30 = 3000 GB. Base cell cost = monthly_compressed_GB * retention_months * price_per_GB_month. The two-variable data table has retention {12,24,36} down the rows and tier price {0.092, 0.046} across the columns, corner cell = the base cost formula. Corner/interior values: Active@12mo = 3000*12*0.092 = 3,312 AED; Cold@12mo = 3000*12*0.046 = 1,656 AED; Active@36mo = 3000*36*0.092 = 9,936 AED; Cold@36mo = 3000*36*0.046 = 4,968 AED. is_array_formula confirms the {=TABLE()} native construct; cell_value checks lock the low corner (Active 12mo), the cold-tier 12mo, and the high corner (Active 36mo).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Uses a native two-variable data table {=TABLE()} across retention x tier (not hardcoded numbers) - Construction of a genuine native data-table / array formula for the sensitivity grid
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Base monthly compressed volume = 3000 GB ((500/5)*30) - Raw-to-compressed conversion (compression ratio) and monthly volume accrual
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Active tier @ 12-month retention = 3,312 AED (low corner) - Active-tier annual carrying-cost calculation at the data-table low corner
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Cold tier @ 12-month retention = 1,656 AED (50% discount applied) - Cold/long-term tiered pricing correctly halves the active cost
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Active tier @ 36-month retention = 9,936 AED (high corner) - Retention scaling at the data-table high corner
- **Partition-Pruning Scan & On-Demand Query-Cost Reduction** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 8 min · ref: DAMA-DMBOK2 Data Storage & Operations / on-demand scan-billing model
  - _Measures:_ Quantitative justification of a partitioning/pruning strategy - the exact arithmetic a warehouse architect presents to defend a partition key: how much data a pruned query skips and what that saves on a scan-billed platform. Demonstrates understanding that partitioning's value is scan-elimination, not storage.
  - _Scenario:_ Saudi National Bank runs a fact_transactions table on an on-demand, scan-billed warehouse: total table = 2,400 GB, evenly date-partitioned across 24 monthly partitions (so each partition = 100 GB). On-demand query pricing = 23.44 AED per TB scanned (1 TB = 1,000 GB). A daily dashboard query currently runs WITHOUT a partition filter (full table scan). An analyst rewrites it with a WHERE clause that prunes to a single month (1 partition). The candidate must compute: (a) bytes scanned WITHOUT the filter, in GB; (b) bytes scanned WITH the single-partition filter, in GB; (c) the percentage scan reduction; (d) the AED cost saved per run from the pruning.
  - _Model answer:_ scan_no_filter = 2400 GB (full table). scan_with_filter = 100 GB (one of 24 equal partitions). scan_reduction_pct = (2400-100)/2400 = 95.8333... ~= 95.83%. cost_saved_per_run = scanned-GB-saved / 1000 GB-per-TB x 23.44 AED = (2300/1000)*23.44 = 53.912 AED. Each is a deterministic field with tolerance for rounding on the percentage and AED figures.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Bytes scanned without partition filter = 2,400 GB (full table) - Recognises an unfiltered query scans the entire table
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Bytes scanned with single-partition filter = 100 GB - Partition-pruning math (2400 GB / 24 equal partitions = 100 GB scanned)
