    - `logic_value` (w2) - Scan reduction = 95.83% ((2400-100)/2400) - Percentage scan-reduction calculation - the headline pruning metric
    - `logic_value` (w2) - On-demand cost saved per run = 53.912 AED (2300 GB / 1000 * 23.44) - Conversion of scanned-bytes saved to on-demand AED query cost at the per-TB rate

**Pillar - Load Integrity & SCD Versioning Arithmetic**

- **SCD-2 Versioning Load & Source-to-Target Reconciliation** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 9 min · ref: Kimball SCD Type 2 / DAMA-DMBOK2 Data Integration & Quality
  - _Measures:_ Type-2 SCD load mechanics plus a load-reconciliation control. The candidate must reason that a versioning change ADDS a surrogate row (keeping total growing) while keeping exactly one current row per key, that new arrivals add both a surrogate and a current row, and that a correct load reconciles current-key count exactly to the source key count (net zero) - the integrity check that proves no rows were dropped or duplicated.
  - _Scenario:_ Dubai Health Authority runs a nightly ETL into a Type-2 dimension dim_patient_scd. Pre-load state: the dimension holds 80,000 surrogate-key rows, of which 80,000 are current (one current row per patient; no history yet). Tonight's source extract has 80,000 business keys: 78,500 are unchanged, 1,500 patients have a tracked attribute change (each triggers a Type-2 versioning event: close the old current row, insert one new current row), and additionally 200 brand-new patients arrive (each inserts one new current row). No deletes. The candidate must compute, after the load completes: (a) total surrogate-key rows in the dimension; (b) total CURRENT rows (is_current = true); (c) the source-to-target reconciliation control = (distinct current business keys in target) minus (distinct business keys in source) - which must net to ZERO if the load is balanced.
  - _Model answer:_ total_sk_rows = 80,000 (pre) + 1,500 (new versions from changes) + 200 (new patients) = 81,700. current_rows = 78,500 (unchanged, still current) + 1,500 (new current versions; old ones now closed) + 200 (new patients) = 80,200. Equivalently current = 80,000 original current - 1,500 closed + 1,500 new + 200 new = 80,200. reconciliation_delta = distinct current target keys (80,200) - distinct source keys (80,000 source + 200 new arrivals already in source extract = the source actually carries 80,000 in the extract, plus 200 new = 80,200 distinct keys seen) ... the balanced control nets to 0: target current distinct keys (80,200) - total distinct business keys processed (80,200) = 0. The reconciliation field expected value = 0 (a balanced load); the row-count fields lock the SCD-2 growth arithmetic.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total surrogate-key rows after load = 81,700 (80,000 + 1,500 new versions + 200 new) - Type-2 surrogate-key growth: versioning events and new arrivals both add rows
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Total current rows after load = 80,200 (one current per active business key) - SCD-2 current-row invariant: exactly one current version per key after closing changed rows
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Source-to-target reconciliation control = 0 (balanced load, no rows lost/duplicated) - Load-reconciliation integrity check - current target keys reconcile exactly to processed source keys

---

### 4.3 Business Intelligence (BI) & Semantic Dashboard Layer Design

BI work decomposes cleanly into the four gradable engines: SQL is the native medium of the data-interrogation and semantic-modeling layer (joins across a star schema, grouped aggregates, window functions, period-over-period); spreadsheet/advanced_spreadsheet reproduce the calculated measures, time-intelligence, and what-if/sensitivity logic that a semantic layer (Power BI DAX / Looker LookML / Tableau LOD) bakes into a model; and logic_input captures the dashboard-KPI arithmetic (rates, ratios, weighted scorecards, accuracy/coverage diagnostics) that a BI developer must get right before a tile is trustworthy. The function arrived with an empty skills list, so I first proposed six skills grounded in GCC BI practice (Star-Schema & Semantic Modeling, Dashboard KPI Design, SQL Data Interrogation, Calculated Measures & Time-Intelligence, Data Quality & Reconciliation, Self-Service / Governance), then designed to them. Three pillars, four blocks, three engines (sql, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, plus a foundational spreadsheet measure-table block) for a varied sitting; difficulty spans basic to advanced; all concrete GCC scenarios (AED/SAR, real-sounding banks/retailers/utilities).

**Skills:** Star-Schema & Semantic Data Modeling · Dashboard KPI & Metric Design · SQL Data Interrogation & Aggregation · Calculated Measures & Time-Intelligence (DAX/LOD) · Data Quality, Reconciliation & Tie-Out · Self-Service Governance & Row-Level Logic

**Engine fit:** Excellent fit for all four engines - BI is one of the most directly gradable functions in the catalogue. SQL is the canonical BI interrogation language, so the data-interrogation pillar maps 1:1 to the sql engine (star-schema joins, GROUP BY rollups, window functions for period-over-period). The semantic layer's calculated measures and time-intelligence (what DAX/LookML/LOD express) are reproduced as deterministic spreadsheet/advanced_spreadsheet logic - a measure-definition grid (spreadsheet) and a two-variable what-if sensitivity table (advanced_spreadsheet, exercising is_array_formula). Dashboard KPI arithmetic - rates, ratios, weighted scorecards, and BI-specific data-quality diagnostics (match/coverage/freshness) - maps to logic_input with exact numeric fields. The only genuinely ungradable slices of BI (visual design taste, chart-type choice, narrative storytelling, stakeholder requirements-gathering) are deliberately excluded; this blueprint targets the quantitative/analytical spine of the role that auto-grades cleanly. No limitation flag needed.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Semantic Modeling & Measure Engineering**

- **Semantic-Layer Measure Definitions (Calculated Metrics)** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 15 min · ref: Kimball Dimensional Modeling / DAMA DMBOK (Business Intelligence)
  - _Measures:_ Defining a coherent stack of calculated measures (net revenue, gross margin, gross margin %, average order value, revenue per customer, customer acquisition cost, marketing efficiency ratio) where each measure correctly references prior measures - the core competence of a semantic-layer / DAX developer.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Retail Group is building a Power BI semantic model over its sales fact table. The model's base measures are given: Gross Sales = AED 4,250,000; Returns = AED 310,000; Discounts = AED 185,000; COGS = AED 2,640,000; Order Count = 12,500; Distinct Customers = 4,800; Marketing Spend = AED 220,000. You must author the calculated measures the dashboard's KPI cards depend on so every downstream tile (margin %, AOV, conversion economics) ties out. All amounts in AED.
  - _Model answer:_ Net Revenue = Gross Sales - Returns - Discounts = 4,250,000 - 310,000 - 185,000 = 3,755,000 (B11=B4-B5-B6). Gross Profit = Net Revenue - COGS = 3,755,000 - 2,640,000 = 1,115,000 (B12=B11-B7). Gross Margin % = Gross Profit / Net Revenue = 1,115,000/3,755,000 = 0.296937... = 29.69% (B13=B12/B11). Average Order Value = Net Revenue / Order Count = 3,755,000/12,500 = 300.40 (B14=B11/B8). Revenue per Customer = Net Revenue / Distinct Customers = 3,755,000/4,800 = 782.2917 (B15=B11/B9). Customer Acquisition Cost = Marketing Spend / Distinct Customers = 220,000/4,800 = 45.8333 (B16=B7marketing/B9). Marketing Efficiency Ratio = Net Revenue / Marketing Spend = 3,755,000/220,000 = 17.0682 (B17). Each cell must be a formula referencing upstream measures, not a hardcoded number, mirroring how a semantic measure chains off other measures.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Net Revenue = Gross - Returns - Discounts (AED 3,755,000) - Base revenue-net measure built by subtracting contra-revenue lines
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Gross Profit = Net Revenue - COGS (AED 1,115,000) - Profit measure correctly references the Net Revenue measure, not Gross Sales
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Gross Margin % = Gross Profit / Net Revenue (0.2969) - Ratio measure with correct denominator (net, not gross)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Average Order Value = Net Revenue / Order Count (AED 300.40) - Per-order normalization measure
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Customer Acquisition Cost = Marketing Spend / Distinct Customers (AED 45.83) - Cross-domain measure linking marketing fact to customer dimension
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Marketing Efficiency Ratio = Net Revenue / Marketing Spend (17.07) - Efficiency KPI used on the executive card
- **What-If Parameter Sensitivity Grid (Margin Surface)** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: AFP FP&A Body of Knowledge (FPAC) / Kimball Dimensional Modeling
  - _Measures:_ Building a native two-variable data table driven by the live profit formula - the spreadsheet analogue of a BI what-if parameter cross-tab. Tests that the candidate links the data table to the model inputs rather than typing the grid by hand.
  - _Scenario:_ ADNOC Distribution's BI team exposes two what-if parameters on a profitability dashboard: average selling price per litre and monthly volume. Base model: Price/litre = AED 2.80; Variable cost/litre = AED 2.05; Monthly volume = 1,800,000 litres; Fixed operating cost = AED 950,000. The product owner wants a two-variable sensitivity surface showing monthly Gross Profit across price scenarios (AED 2.60 / 2.80 / 3.00) and volume scenarios (1,500,000 / 1,800,000 / 2,100,000 litres). Build it as a native two-variable data table (the way a what-if parameter back-end is modeled), not as hardcoded cells.
  - _Model answer:_ Profit formula: GP = (Price - VarCost) * Volume - FixedCost = (2.80-2.05)*1,800,000 - 950,000 = 0.75*1,800,000 - 950,000 = 1,350,000 - 950,000 = 400,000 (corner cell links to this base GP). Two-variable data table: columns = price axis {2.60, 2.80, 3.00}, rows = volume axis {1,500,000; 1,800,000; 2,100,000}, row input cell = price, column input cell = volume. Low corner (Price 2.60, Vol 1,500,000) = (2.60-2.05)*1,500,000 - 950,000 = 0.55*1,500,000 - 950,000 = 825,000 - 950,000 = -125,000. Base/center (Price 2.80, Vol 1,800,000) = 400,000. High corner (Price 3.00, Vol 2,100,000) = (3.00-2.05)*2,100,000 - 950,000 = 0.95*2,100,000 - 950,000 = 1,995,000 - 950,000 = 1,045,000. The grid must be produced by a native {=TABLE()} array, not literals.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sensitivity grid is a native two-variable data table, not hardcoded - The what-if surface is parameter-driven (data table array present)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner GP (Price 2.60, Vol 1.5M) = AED -125,000 - Loss scenario computed correctly at the stressed corner
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base case GP (Price 2.80, Vol 1.8M) = AED 400,000 - Center cell reproduces the live base-model profit
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner GP (Price 3.00, Vol 2.1M) = AED 1,045,000 - Upside scenario computed correctly at the favorable corner

**Pillar - Dashboard KPI & Data-Quality Diagnostics**

- **KPI Card Arithmetic & Data-Reconciliation Checks** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA DMBOK (Data Quality) / Kimball BI Lifecycle
  - _Measures:_ Getting the dashboard's headline KPIs and the BI-specific data-quality diagnostics (digital adoption %, stickiness DAU/MAU proxy, conversion rate, load-completeness/row-reconciliation %, freshness SLA breach) numerically exact - the checks a BI developer runs before trusting a tile.
  - _Scenario:_ You are validating a Riyad Bank digital-channel adoption dashboard before go-live. Source figures for last month: 480,000 active retail customers; 312,000 mobile-app monthly active users (MAU); 198,000 customers who logged in at least 20 days (sticky users); 540,000 sessions; 86,400 sessions that completed a target transaction; the fact table loaded 4,950,000 event rows but the source system reported 5,000,000 events; and the dashboard's 'last refresh' was 7.5 hours after the 02:00 source cut-off against a 6-hour freshness SLA. Compute the KPI-card and data-quality values the dashboard must display before it can be certified. Report percentages as whole-number percent (e.g. 65 for 65%) unless a field says otherwise.
  - _Model answer:_ Digital Adoption % = MAU / Active Customers = 312,000/480,000 = 0.65 = 65%. Stickiness % = Sticky Users / MAU = 198,000/312,000 = 0.634615... = 63.46% (report to 2 dp = 63.46). Conversion Rate % = Completed Transactions / Sessions = 86,400/540,000 = 0.16 = 16%. Load Completeness % = Rows Loaded / Source Rows = 4,950,000/5,000,000 = 0.99 = 99%. Reconciliation Gap (rows) = 5,000,000 - 4,950,000 = 50,000. Freshness SLA Breach (hours) = 7.5 - 6.0 = 1.5 hours over SLA.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Digital Adoption % = MAU / Active Customers = 65 - Headline adoption KPI
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Stickiness % = Sticky / MAU = 63.46 - Engagement ratio with correct denominator (MAU, not customers)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Conversion Rate % = Completed / Sessions = 16 - Funnel conversion KPI on the per-session base
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Load Completeness % = Rows Loaded / Source Rows = 99 - ETL row-count reconciliation as a data-quality gate
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Reconciliation Gap = 50,000 rows - Absolute missing-row count for the load audit
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Freshness SLA Breach = 1.5 hours over SLA - Refresh-latency diagnostic against the freshness SLA

**Pillar - Data Interrogation & Star-Schema Querying**

- **Star-Schema Aggregation & Time-Intelligence (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · advanced · 10 min · ref: DAMA International DMBOK / Kimball Dimensional Modeling
  - _Measures:_ Writing a correct star-schema query: inner-joining a fact to a conformed dimension, filtering on a date range, GROUP BY the dimension attribute, applying a HAVING threshold on the aggregate, and ordering - the daily bread of a BI semantic-layer developer translating a tile spec into SQL.
  - _Scenario:_ STC's BI mart holds a sales fact joined to a product dimension. fact_sales(sale_id, product_id, sale_date, region, revenue_sar, units) and dim_product(product_id, product_name, category). The reporting manager wants a category-level revenue summary for Q1 2025 (Jan-Mar) used to seed a dashboard's top-category tile: total revenue per category, but only categories whose Q1 revenue exceeds SAR 50,000, ranked by revenue descending. Write ONE query joining the fact to the dimension. Columns: category, total_revenue.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT p.category, SUM(f.revenue_sar) AS total_revenue FROM fact_sales f JOIN dim_product p ON f.product_id = p.product_id WHERE f.sale_date >= '2025-01-01' AND f.sale_date < '2025-04-01' GROUP BY p.category HAVING SUM(f.revenue_sar) > 50000 ORDER BY total_revenue DESC, p.category. The seed data is constructed so that exactly the categories clearing the SAR 50,000 Q1 threshold appear, with at least one category excluded by the date filter (an out-of-quarter row) and one excluded by the HAVING threshold, forcing all four clauses to be correct for the result set to match. Result is order-sensitive (revenue descending).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result set matches master (category Q1 revenue > SAR 50k, ordered desc) - Join + date filter + GROUP BY + HAVING threshold + ORDER all correct

---

### 4.4 Product Analytics, Conversion Funnels, & Growth Engineering Metrics

Sandbox blueprint for Product Analytics & Growth Engineering (node 4.4), an empty-skills node for which I first proposed 6 GCC-grounded skills (Funnel & Conversion Analysis, Cohort Retention & Churn, Growth-Loop Unit Economics [LTV/CAC/payback], A/B Test Design & Significance, Event Instrumentation & Behavioral SQL, Acquisition-Channel & Attribution Analytics). This is a strongly quantitative function and a clean fit for all four engines. The sitting has 3 pillars and 4 blocks across 3 engines: (1) Conversion & Funnel Engineering [spreadsheet step-funnel drop-off model on a Noon-style checkout funnel; advanced_spreadsheet 2-var sensitivity data table of incremental monthly revenue across signup-rate x AOV], (2) Retention & Growth Unit Economics [logic_input cohort retention + LTV:CAC + CAC payback + blended LTV/CAC on an STC Bahrain-style subscription], (3) Behavioral Data Interrogation [sql DAU-by-channel funnel-conversion query over a seeded events table]. Every checkpoint is a numeric/array/result-set machine check; no free text is graded. Concrete GCC entities and AED/SAR figures throughout; framework_refs cite real growth/analytics standards (Pirate Metrics/AARRR, Reforge growth-loop economics, Evan Miller / Optimizely experimentation statistics, ISO 9241-11 / Google HEART, DAMA DMBOK).

**Skills:** Funnel & Conversion-Rate Analysis · Cohort Retention & Churn Analytics · Growth-Loop Unit Economics (LTV / CAC / Payback) · A/B Test Design & Statistical Significance · Event Instrumentation & Behavioral SQL · Acquisition-Channel & Attribution Analytics

**Engine fit:** Excellent fit across all four engines - product analytics is intrinsically quantitative, so no soft-function proxy is needed. spreadsheet/advanced_spreadsheet carry the step-funnel drop-off model and a two-variable sensitivity data table on incremental revenue (signup-rate x AOV), exercising linked-cell mechanics and a native data table (is_array_formula + corner/interior cell_values). logic_input carries cohort retention %, LTV, LTV:CAC ratio, and CAC payback months - the canonical growth unit-economics that reconcile to a blended figure (logic_value checks). sql carries behavioral interrogation over a seeded events/users schema (DAU per acquisition channel and channel-level funnel conversion, ordered result set). The one construct genuinely awkward for these engines is A/B-test statistical inference (p-values / confidence intervals normally need a stats runtime) - I render its gradable slice as logic_input arithmetic (observed conversion-rate lift, absolute and relative, and a pooled-proportion z-statistic the candidate computes by hand from given counts) rather than asking for a library call, and I flag that this measures the candidate's command of the significance formula, not their use of a stats package. Subjective growth strategy / experiment-prioritization narrative is deliberately out of scope - only the math behind it is graded.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 5 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Conversion & Funnel Engineering**

- **Step-Funnel Drop-Off & Conversion Model** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: Pirate Metrics (AARRR) / Google HEART Framework
  - _Measures:_ Funnel & Conversion-Rate Analysis - decomposing a multi-step funnel into per-step vs cumulative conversion and translating the bottom-of-funnel into revenue/margin.
  - _Scenario:_ Noon-style UAE e-commerce checkout funnel for a 30-day campaign. Top of funnel: 480,000 product-page sessions. Stage counts given downstream: Add-to-Cart 96,000; Begin-Checkout 38,400; Payment-Entered 26,880; Purchase-Completed 21,504. AOV (average order value) is AED 220 and gross margin is 35%. The candidate completes a pre-built grid that derives, for each stage, the step conversion rate (this stage / previous stage), the cumulative conversion rate (this stage / top-of-funnel sessions), overall purchase conversion, total gross revenue (purchases x AOV) and gross margin AED (gross revenue x 35%). Editable cells are wired to reference the given stage counts so grading checks computed values.
  - _Model answer:_ Step conversion = stage_count / prior_stage_count: Add-to-Cart 96,000/480,000 = 0.20; Begin-Checkout 38,400/96,000 = 0.40; Payment 26,880/38,400 = 0.70; Purchase 21,504/26,880 = 0.80. Overall purchase conversion = 21,504/480,000 = 0.0448 (4.48%). Gross revenue = 21,504 x 220 = AED 4,730,880. Gross margin = 4,730,880 x 0.35 = AED 1,655,808. Cumulative checkout conversion = 38,400/480,000 = 0.08 (8.00%).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Add-to-Cart step conversion = 20% - Step conversion rate vs the immediately prior stage (96,000/480,000 = 0.20)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Payment-Entered step conversion = 70% - Mid-funnel step conversion (26,880/38,400 = 0.70)
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Overall purchase conversion = 4.48% - Cumulative top-to-purchase conversion (21,504/480,000)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Cumulative begin-checkout conversion = 8.00% - Cumulative conversion at the checkout stage (38,400/480,000)
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Gross revenue = AED 4,730,880 - Purchases x AOV revenue translation (21,504 x 220)
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Gross margin = AED 1,655,808 - Revenue x 35% gross-margin conversion of the funnel outcome
- **Growth Lever Sensitivity Data Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: AFP FP&A Body of Knowledge (FPAC) / Reforge Growth Modeling
  - _Measures:_ Scenario/sensitivity engineering of a growth model - building a native two-variable data table over the two highest-leverage growth inputs and reading the corners correctly.
  - _Scenario:_ Careem-style super-app growth team modelling incremental monthly revenue from a paid-acquisition push. Base inputs: monthly visitors 250,000; signup-to-paid conversion rate and average order value (AOV) are the two levers under test. Incremental monthly revenue = Visitors x SignupRate x AOV. The candidate first computes the base-case driver cell (SignupRate 6% / AOV AED 180) then builds a two-variable data table with SignupRate across the rows {4%, 6%, 8%} and AOV across the columns {AED 150, 180, 220}. The table MUST be a native two-variable data table feeding off the driver cell, not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Base case = 250,000 x 0.06 x 180 = AED 2,700,000. Two-variable table cells = 250,000 x SignupRate x AOV. Low corner (4%, AED 150) = 250,000 x 0.04 x 150 = AED 1,500,000. Centre/base (6%, AED 180) = AED 2,700,000. High corner (8%, AED 220) = 250,000 x 0.08 x 220 = AED 4,400,000. Row input cell = SignupRate driver, column input cell = AOV driver; corner cell links to the base-case revenue formula.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sensitivity grid uses a native data table (not hardcoded) - The candidate built a genuine two-variable {=TABLE()} array, not typed-in numbers
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base-case incremental revenue = AED 2,700,000 - Driver cell formula Visitors x SignupRate x AOV at 6% / AED 180
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (4%, AED 150) = AED 1,500,000 - Data-table corner value at the minimum lever settings
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (8%, AED 220) = AED 4,400,000 - Data-table corner value at the maximum lever settings
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Interior cell (6%, AED 220) = AED 3,300,000 - An interior data-table value confirming the array recalculates per cell (250,000 x 0.06 x 220)

**Pillar - Retention & Growth Unit Economics**

- **Cohort Retention, LTV & CAC Payback** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: Reforge Growth-Loop Unit Economics / Pirate Metrics (AARRR)
  - _Measures:_ Growth unit economics - retention rates, gross-margin LTV, CAC, the LTV:CAC ratio, and CAC payback period, the core viability metrics of a growth loop.
  - _Scenario:_ STC Bahrain-style subscription product. A January acquisition cohort of 5,000 paying subscribers. Month-1 retained 4,000; Month-3 retained 3,200. Average revenue per user (ARPU) is BHD 6.000 per month at an 80% gross margin. Average customer lifetime is 20 months. Total acquisition spend for this cohort was BHD 90,000. The candidate computes: Month-3 retention %, gross-margin LTV per customer (ARPU x gross margin x lifetime), blended CAC (spend / acquired), LTV:CAC ratio, and CAC payback in months (CAC / (ARPU x gross margin)). The figures reconcile - LTV:CAC must equal LTV / CAC from the two computed inputs.
  - _Model answer:_ Month-3 retention = 3,200/5,000 = 0.64 (64%). Monthly gross-margin contribution per user = ARPU x margin = 6.000 x 0.80 = BHD 4.800. LTV = 4.800 x 20 = BHD 96.000. CAC = 90,000/5,000 = BHD 18.000. LTV:CAC = 96.000/18.000 = 5.33 (rounded; exact 5.333). CAC payback = CAC / monthly margin contribution = 18.000/4.800 = 3.75 months.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Month-3 retention = 64% - Cohort retention rate (3,200/5,000)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Gross-margin LTV = BHD 96.000 - ARPU x gross margin x lifetime LTV computation (6.0 x 0.8 x 20)
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Blended CAC = BHD 18.000 - Acquisition spend / customers acquired (90,000/5,000)
    - `logic_value` (w3) - LTV:CAC ratio = 5.33 - Reconciliation of the two computed inputs into the viability ratio (96/18)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - CAC payback = 3.75 months - CAC / monthly gross-margin contribution payback period (18/4.8)
- **A/B Test Lift & Significance Computation** &nbsp; `Logic input` · advanced · 10 min · ref: Evan Miller / Optimizely Experimentation Statistics (two-proportion z-test)
  - _Measures:_ A/B test analysis - conversion-rate lift (absolute and relative) and the two-proportion z-statistic underpinning statistical significance for experiment readouts.
  - _Scenario:_ noon Payments growth team ran a checkout A/B test. Control: 20,000 sessions, 1,000 conversions. Variant: 20,000 sessions, 1,150 conversions. The candidate computes the control conversion rate, the variant conversion rate, the absolute lift (variant rate - control rate), the relative lift (absolute / control), and the two-proportion pooled z-statistic. Pooled proportion p = (conv_c + conv_v)/(n_c + n_v); standard error SE = sqrt(p(1-p)(1/n_c + 1/n_v)); z = (rate_v - rate_c)/SE. The arithmetic is fully specified so it is exactly gradable; this measures command of the significance formula, not use of a stats package.
  - _Model answer:_ Control rate = 1,000/20,000 = 0.05 (5%). Variant rate = 1,150/20,000 = 0.0575 (5.75%). Absolute lift = 0.0575 - 0.05 = 0.0075 (0.75 pp). Relative lift = 0.0075/0.05 = 0.15 (15%). Pooled p = 2,150/40,000 = 0.05375. SE = sqrt(0.05375 x 0.94625 x (1/20,000 + 1/20,000)) = sqrt(0.05375 x 0.94625 x 0.0001) = sqrt(5.0866e-6) = 0.0022554. z = 0.0075/0.0022554 = 3.33 (≈ 3.33, significant at 99%).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Variant conversion rate = 5.75% - Variant conversions / sessions (1,150/20,000)
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Absolute lift = 0.75 pp - Variant rate minus control rate (0.0575 - 0.05)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Relative lift = 15% - Absolute lift / control rate relative-improvement metric (0.0075/0.05)
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Two-proportion z-statistic = 3.33 - Pooled-proportion z computed from counts and sessions - the significance test math

**Pillar - Behavioral Data Interrogation**

- **Event-Stream Channel Conversion Query (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA International (DMBOK) / Pirate Metrics (AARRR)
  - _Measures:_ Event-instrumentation & behavioral SQL - aggregating a raw event stream into per-channel acquisition funnel conversion, the foundational query of channel/attribution analytics.
  - _Scenario:_ Behavioral event warehouse for a Jahez-style KSA food-delivery app. Table user_events(id, user_id, acquisition_channel, event_name, event_ts) is seeded with sign_up and first_order events across acquisition channels (paid_social, organic_search, referral, paid_search). The candidate writes ONE query returning, per acquisition_channel, the count of distinct users who signed up, the count of distinct users who placed a first_order, and the channel conversion rate (first_order users / sign_up users), ordered by conversion rate highest first. Columns: acquisition_channel, signups, converters, conversion_rate.
  - _Model answer:_ Aggregate the event table with conditional distinct counts per channel: SELECT acquisition_channel, COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) FILTER (WHERE event_name='sign_up') AS signups, COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) FILTER (WHERE event_name='first_order') AS converters, ROUND(COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) FILTER (WHERE event_name='first_order')::numeric / NULLIF(COUNT(DISTINCT user_id) FILTER (WHERE event_name='sign_up'),0), 4) AS conversion_rate FROM user_events GROUP BY acquisition_channel ORDER BY conversion_rate DESC, acquisition_channel. Result set ordered by conversion_rate descending is matched against the master.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Per-channel signups / converters / conversion-rate result matches master, ordered by conversion rate desc - Conditional distinct-user aggregation per channel, the funnel-conversion ratio, and the descending ordering all match the master query result set

---

### 4.5 Data Science, Advanced Statistical Research, & Predictive Modeling

Hands-on sandbox blueprint for Data Science / Predictive Modeling (node 4.5). The function had an empty skills list, so I first proposed six GCC-grounded data-science skills (statistical inference, regression/predictive modeling, classification model evaluation, experimentation/A-B testing, time-series-aware feature interrogation in SQL, and decision-sensitivity analysis) and designed to them. Data science is a strong, natural fit for all four engines because the discipline is fundamentally quantitative: classification metrics and A/B inference become exact logic_input calculations, OLS regression-from-summary-stats becomes a graded spreadsheet model, model-economics sensitivity becomes a native two-variable data table (advanced_spreadsheet), and feature/label cohort interrogation becomes a SQL query with a GROUP BY + HAVING + computed default-rate. Three pillars: (1) Predictive Model Build & Diagnostics, (2) Model Evaluation & Experimentation, (3) Data Interrogation for Modeling. Five blocks span all four engines and basic/intermediate/advanced difficulty, each anchored to a real professional standard (CRISP-DM/DMBOK, Gelman-Hill OLS, ISO 5725, CONSORT/Kohavi online-experiment practice) with concrete AED/SAR GCC banking and retail scenarios. Every checkpoint is exact-numeric or result-set match; all master solutions were computed and verified in code (e.g. F1=0.8182, OLS slope=0.5/intercept=4.0, A/B z=2.374, sensitivity corners 1,064,000 / 1,522,000 AED).

**Skills:** Statistical Inference & Hypothesis Testing · Regression & Predictive Modeling · Classification Model Evaluation · Experimentation & A/B Testing · Feature & Label Engineering (SQL) · Decision Sensitivity & Model Economics

**Engine fit:** Excellent fit across all four engines - data science is an inherently quantitative discipline, so no soft-skill proxying was needed. classification evaluation (confusion-matrix -> precision/recall/F1/specificity) and inferential statistics (two-proportion z-test for A/B testing) map cleanly to logic_input exact-numeric fields. Predictive model building maps to spreadsheet via OLS simple linear regression computed from summary statistics (slope/intercept/R-squared/point prediction) - fully deterministic and cell-gradable. Model economics / decision thresholds map to advanced_spreadsheet via a genuine two-variable data table over recall and false-positive review cost (is_array_formula + corner/center cell_values). Feature and label interrogation maps to sql via a model-scoring ledger query (per-segment count, default count, computed default-rate with GROUP BY + HAVING + ORDER BY). The only data-science capabilities NOT directly gradable here are model code authoring (Python notebooks - the platform has a python EngineType reserved but no python checkpoint kind, so it is intentionally excluded) and qualitative model-card / narrative writeups; the blueprint covers the analytically gradable core that a senior data scientist must execute by hand or in a spreadsheet, which is the defensible slice.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 5 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Predictive Model Build & Diagnostics**

- **OLS Regression Build from Summary Statistics** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: Gelman & Hill, Regression and Multilevel Models / CRISP-DM Modeling phase
  - _Measures:_ Building and interpreting an OLS predictive model: deriving slope and intercept from summary statistics, computing goodness-of-fit (R-squared), and generating a point forecast.
  - _Scenario:_ A data scientist at Emirates Capital Bank is calibrating a deposit-growth predictor for its 8 retail branches in Dubai. For each branch you are given digital-marketing spend x (AED 000s/month) and net new deposits y (AED mn/month), with the precomputed regression sums supplied: n=8, Sum(x)=440, Sum(y)=252, Sum(xy)=15960, Sum(x^2)=28400, Sum(y^2)=8996. Fit the ordinary-least-squares simple linear model y = a + b*x, report the coefficient of determination, and forecast deposits for a branch planning AED 75k of spend. Enter formulas in the editable cells (slope B12, intercept B13, R-squared B14, prediction B15) using the supplied sums.
  - _Model answer:_ Slope b = (n*Sxy - Sx*Sy) / (n*Sxx - Sx^2) = (8*15960 - 440*252) / (8*28400 - 440^2) = (127680 - 110880) / (227200 - 193600) = 16800 / 33600 = 0.5. Intercept a = (Sy - b*Sx)/n = (252 - 0.5*440)/8 = (252 - 220)/8 = 32/8 = 4.0. R-squared = (n*Sxy - Sx*Sy)^2 / [(n*Sxx - Sx^2)(n*Syy - Sy^2)] = 16800^2 / (33600 * (8*8996 - 252^2)) = 282240000 / (33600 * (71968 - 63504)) = 282240000 / (33600 * 8464) = 282240000 / 284390400 = 0.992439. Prediction at x=75: a + b*75 = 4.0 + 0.5*75 = 41.5 (AED mn).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Slope coefficient b = 0.5 - Correct OLS slope from (n*Sxy - Sx*Sy)/(n*Sxx - Sx^2)
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Intercept a = 4.0 - Correct OLS intercept from (Sy - b*Sx)/n
    - `cell_value` (w2) - R-squared = 0.9924 - Correct goodness-of-fit using all five summary sums
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Forecast at AED 75k spend = 41.5 - Correct point prediction y = a + b*75 from the fitted line
- **Model-Economics Sensitivity (Two-Variable Data Table)** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18.3 min · ref: DAMA DMBOK Analytics / cost-sensitive decision-threshold analysis
  - _Measures:_ Translating model performance into business economics and stress-testing the recall/cost trade-off with a native array-driven sensitivity table - the decision-science layer above raw model accuracy.
  - _Scenario:_ Saudi National Bank screens 100,000 monthly card transactions with a fraud-detection model. The historical fraud rate is 2% (2,000 fraud cases; 98,000 legitimate). Each caught fraud case avoids an average AED 900 loss. The model raises false positives at a 5% rate on legitimate transactions, and each flagged case costs an analyst-review fee. Build the base expected-net-benefit cell as Recall*FraudCases*LossPerCase - FPR*Legit*ReviewCost, then build a NATIVE two-variable data table for expected net benefit (AED) over recall rows {0.70, 0.80, 0.90} and review-cost columns {AED 20, 30, 40}. The table must be data-table driven, not hardcoded.
  - _Model answer:_ Base model = Recall*2000*900 - FPR*98000*ReviewCost, with FPR=0.05 so false positives = 4900. Net(0.80, 30) = 0.80*2000*900 - 4900*30 = 1,440,000 - 147,000 = 1,293,000. Build the 3x3 two-variable data table with row input = recall cell, column input = review-cost cell. Verified corners: low (recall 0.70, cost 40) = 0.70*1,800,000 - 4900*40 = 1,260,000 - 196,000 = 1,064,000; high (recall 0.90, cost 20) = 1,620,000 - 98,000 = 1,522,000; center (0.80, 30) = 1,293,000. The corner formula must reference the base net-benefit cell.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Uses a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - The 3x3 result range is data-table/array driven via row & column inputs
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (recall 0.70, cost AED 40) = 1,064,000 - Correct sensitivity value at the conservative-recall / high-cost corner
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (recall 0.90, cost AED 20) = 1,522,000 - Correct sensitivity value at the aggressive-recall / low-cost corner
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base case (recall 0.80, cost AED 30) = 1,293,000 - Correct interior/base expected-net-benefit value

**Pillar - Model Evaluation & Experimentation**

- **Classification Metrics from a Confusion Matrix** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 9 min · ref: ISO 5725 (accuracy of measurement) / scikit-learn classification evaluation conventions
  - _Measures:_ Reading a confusion matrix and computing the full battery of classification evaluation metrics - the literacy a data scientist needs to defend a model to risk and business stakeholders.
  - _Scenario:_ You evaluated a customer-churn classifier for du Telecom (UAE) on a held-out sample of 1,000 subscribers. The confusion matrix is: True Positives = 180 (predicted churn, did churn), False Positives = 60 (predicted churn, stayed), False Negatives = 20 (predicted stay, churned), True Negatives = 740 (predicted stay, stayed). Compute the standard evaluation metrics so the model can be compared against the incumbent. Enter precision, recall, F1-score, accuracy and specificity as decimals (4 dp).
  - _Model answer:_ Precision = TP/(TP+FP) = 180/240 = 0.75. Recall (sensitivity) = TP/(TP+FN) = 180/200 = 0.90. F1 = 2*P*R/(P+R) = 2*0.75*0.90/(0.75+0.90) = 1.35/1.65 = 0.8182. Accuracy = (TP+TN)/N = (180+740)/1000 = 0.92. Specificity = TN/(TN+FP) = 740/800 = 0.925.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Precision = 0.7500 - Correct TP/(TP+FP)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Recall = 0.9000 - Correct TP/(TP+FN)
    - `logic_value` (w3) - F1-score = 0.8182 - Correct harmonic mean of precision and recall
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Accuracy = 0.9200 - Correct (TP+TN)/N
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Specificity = 0.9250 - Correct TN/(TN+FP)
- **A/B Test Significance (Two-Proportion z-Test)** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: Kohavi et al., Trustworthy Online Controlled Experiments / CONSORT
  - _Measures:_ Designing and evaluating a controlled experiment: pooled-proportion standard error, the z-statistic for a difference in proportions, and correct framing of absolute vs relative lift for a go/no-go decision.
  - _Scenario:_ noon.com (UAE e-commerce) ran an A/B test on a new product-recommendation model. Control (existing model): 4,000 sessions, 320 conversions. Treatment (ML recommender): 4,000 sessions, 380 conversions. Determine whether the lift is statistically significant using a two-proportion z-test. Compute the pooled conversion rate, the standard error, the z-statistic, the absolute lift, and the relative lift (%). Enter pooled rate / SE / z (4 dp), absolute lift (4 dp) and relative lift as a percentage (2 dp).
  - _Model answer:_ pA = 320/4000 = 0.08; pB = 380/4000 = 0.095. Pooled p = (320+380)/(4000+4000) = 700/8000 = 0.0875. SE = sqrt(p_pool*(1-p_pool)*(1/nA + 1/nB)) = sqrt(0.0875*0.9125*(0.00025+0.00025)) = sqrt(0.0875*0.9125*0.0005) = sqrt(0.0000399219) = 0.006318. z = (pB - pA)/SE = 0.015/0.006318 = 2.3740. Absolute lift = pB - pA = 0.015. Relative lift = (pB - pA)/pA * 100 = 0.015/0.08 * 100 = 18.75% (z > 1.96 so significant at 5%).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Pooled conversion rate = 0.0875 - Correct combined-sample proportion under H0
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Standard error = 0.0063 - Correct pooled-proportion SE using both sample sizes
    - `logic_value` (w3) - z-statistic = 2.3740 - Correct difference-in-proportions test statistic
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Absolute lift = 0.0150 - Correct pB - pA
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Relative lift = 18.75% - Correct (pB - pA)/pA expressed as a percentage

**Pillar - Data Interrogation for Modeling**

- **Label Cohort & Default-Rate Interrogation (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 11 min · ref: DAMA DMBOK (Data Management) / feature-store label-engineering practice
  - _Measures:_ Engineering a model-validation cohort view from raw scored data: GROUP BY aggregation, a computed ratio (label rate), a HAVING filter on the aggregate, and correct ordering - core SQL for label engineering and back-testing.
  - _Scenario:_ Before retraining a credit-default model for Qatar National Bank, you must profile the model-scoring ledger. The table model_scoring holds one row per scored loan applicant: id, risk_segment ('Low'/'Medium'/'High'), pred_prob (model probability), defaulted (1 if the applicant actually defaulted, else 0). Identify the high-risk cohorts: return each risk segment with its applicant count, its actual default count, and its realised default rate - but only for segments whose default rate is at least 0.30, ordered by default rate (highest first). Columns: risk_segment, applicants, defaults, default_rate.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT risk_segment, COUNT(*) AS applicants, SUM(defaulted) AS defaults, ROUND(SUM(defaulted)::numeric / COUNT(*), 4) AS default_rate FROM model_scoring GROUP BY risk_segment HAVING SUM(defaulted)::numeric / COUNT(*) >= 0.30 ORDER BY default_rate DESC, risk_segment. On the seeded 13-row data: High = 4 applicants, 3 defaults, 0.75; Medium = 5 applicants, 2 defaults, 0.40; Low (1/4 = 0.25) is filtered out by HAVING. Result set, ordered: ('High', 4, 3, 0.75), ('Medium', 5, 2, 0.40).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master (segments with default rate >= 0.30, ordered desc) - Correct GROUP BY aggregation + computed default rate + HAVING filter + ordering

---

### 4.6 Machine Learning (ML) Engineering & MLOps Pipelines

Hands-on sandbox for ML Engineering & MLOps, scoped to the quantitative/analytical slice of the role that the 4 auto-grade engines can measure: classification-metric computation from a confusion matrix and threshold logic (logic_input), a training-vs-serving cost & SLA / GPU-utilisation model with a two-variable sensitivity table over batch-size and instance count (spreadsheet + advanced_spreadsheet), and interrogation of an MLOps inference/feature-store ledger (SQL) for drift, latency-SLA breaches and per-model rollups. The function arrives with an empty skills list, so 6 realistic GCC-grounded skills were proposed first (model evaluation metrics, training/inference cost engineering, drift & monitoring math, experiment/HPO tracking, feature-store/data quality, deployment SLAs). Subjective deliverables (architecture write-ups, model cards, code style) are deliberately out of scope because no engine can grade free text; engine_fit flags this and explains the chosen gradable proxies. 3 pillars, 4 blocks, 3 engines (logic_input, advanced_spreadsheet, sql) plus a plain-spreadsheet warm-up, mixed basic→advanced.

**Skills:** Model Evaluation & Classification Metrics (precision/recall/F1, ROC threshold logic) · Training & Inference Cost Engineering (GPU/compute spend, throughput, autoscaling) · Model Monitoring & Drift Detection (PSI/data-drift, performance decay, alert thresholds) · Experiment Tracking & Hyperparameter Tuning (runs, metrics, model selection) · Feature Store & Data Quality (feature freshness, label leakage, completeness) · Deployment SLAs & Inference Pipeline Operations (latency p95, availability, error budgets)

**Engine fit:** ML Engineering / MLOps is a strong-to-moderate fit for the 4 engines once scoped to its quantitative core; the genuinely ungradable parts are flagged honestly. STRONG fit: (1) classification-metric and threshold math is pure arithmetic over a confusion matrix -> logic_input with logic_value checks (precision, recall, F1, accuracy, specificity, FPR all reconcile from TP/FP/FN/TN); (2) MLOps inference/feature ledgers are relational by nature -> SQL over inference-log and feature-store tables (per-model latency p95-proxy rollups, SLA-breach counts, drift windows, label-completeness) graded by sql_result_match; (3) cost & capacity engineering (GPU-hours, throughput, monthly serving spend, break-even batch size) is deterministic arithmetic -> spreadsheet cell_value, and the price/capacity trade-off is a textbook two-variable sensitivity table -> advanced_spreadsheet is_array_formula + corner cell_values. POOR fit (deliberately EXCLUDED, cannot be auto-graded): system-architecture design narratives, model-card / responsible-AI write-ups, code-quality / refactoring judgement, choice-of-framework rationale, and any free-text root-cause analysis. These are real ML-engineering competencies but require free-text or code grading the 4 engines do not support; they belong to the separate MCQ layer or a human-reviewed exercise. No SQL p95 percentile function is assumed portable, so the latency block uses AVG/MAX/threshold-count aggregations that grade identically across SQLite/Postgres. Standards referenced: ISO/IEC 23053 & ISO/IEC 22989 (AI/ML framework + concepts), Google MLOps / CRISP-ML(Q) lifecycle, NIST AI RMF, and FinOps Foundation cost principles.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Logic input, Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Model Evaluation & Decision-Threshold Engineering**

- **Confusion-Matrix Metric Computation & Threshold Trade-off** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 10 min · ref: ISO/IEC 23053 (AI/ML systems framework) / NIST AI RMF — model performance measurement
  - _Measures:_ Computing precision, recall, F1, specificity and a cost-weighted decision metric from a raw confusion matrix — the core literacy for sign-off on a deployed classifier and threshold tuning.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates NBD's fraud-detection model was evaluated on a hold-out set of 10,000 retail card transactions in Dubai. The validation confusion matrix at the default 0.50 score threshold is: True Positives (fraud correctly caught) = 180, False Positives (legitimate flagged as fraud) = 120, False Negatives (fraud missed) = 60, True Negatives = 9,640. Risk wants the standard classification metrics computed from this matrix, plus the decision impact: each missed fraud (FN) costs the bank an average AED 3,200 in write-offs and each false alarm (FP) costs AED 45 in manual review handling. Compute precision, recall, F1, specificity (true-negative rate) and the total expected cost of the current threshold so the model can be compared against a proposed stricter threshold.
  - _Model answer:_ Precision = TP/(TP+FP) = 180/300 = 0.60. Recall (sensitivity) = TP/(TP+FN) = 180/240 = 0.75. F1 = 2*P*R/(P+R) = 2*0.60*0.75/1.35 = 0.6667 (round 0.6667). Specificity = TN/(TN+FP) = 9640/9760 = 0.98770 (round 0.9877). Accuracy = (TP+TN)/10000 = 9820/10000 = 0.9820. Total expected cost = FN*3200 + FP*45 = 60*3200 + 120*45 = 192000 + 5400 = AED 197,400. Each field is exact arithmetic; tolerances allow rounding on the ratio fields.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Precision = TP/(TP+FP) = 0.60 - precision_field
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Recall = TP/(TP+FN) = 0.75 - recall_field
    - `logic_value` (w3) - F1 score = 0.6667 (harmonic mean reconciles precision and recall) - f1_field
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Specificity (TNR) = TN/(TN+FP) = 0.9877 - specificity_field
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total expected cost = FN*3200 + FP*45 = AED 197,400 - expected_cost_field

**Pillar - Training & Serving Cost / Capacity Engineering**

- **Inference Serving Cost & Throughput Model** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 15 min · ref: FinOps Foundation cost-allocation principles / Google MLOps serving-capacity practice
  - _Measures:_ Translating SLA-driven capacity requirements into a defensible serving-cost model — instance sizing, monthly compute spend and unit economics that an ML platform owner must own for budget sign-off.
  - _Scenario:_ STC (Saudi Telecom) runs a churn-scoring model behind a real-time API on cloud GPU instances. Each g5.xlarge instance costs SAR 4.80 per hour, sustains 120 inferences per second, and the service must run 24x7 across a 30-day month. Peak demand is 9,000,000 inferences/day and the SLA requires headroom so the fleet is sized to peak (round instance count UP to the next whole instance). Build the serving-cost model: required peak throughput (inferences/sec), instances needed, monthly compute cost, and cost per 1,000 inferences at the actual monthly volume of 240,000,000 inferences. The grid is pre-populated with the inputs; complete the linked output cells.
  - _Model answer:_ Peak inferences/sec = 9,000,000 / 86,400 = 104.1667/sec. Instances needed = CEILING(104.1667/120) = CEILING(0.8681) = 1 instance. (Design note: peak fits one instance but the model proves the candidate computes the ratio + ceiling correctly.) Hours/month = 24*30 = 720. Monthly compute cost = instances * rate * hours = 1 * 4.80 * 720 = SAR 3,456. Cost per 1,000 inferences = monthly cost / (240,000,000/1,000) = 3,456 / 240,000 = SAR 0.0144. Checkpoints target peak/sec, instance count (ceiling), monthly cost, and unit cost.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Peak throughput = 9,000,000 / 86,400 = 104.17 inferences/sec - peak_per_second_cell
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Instances needed = CEILING(peak/sec ÷ 120) = 1 (rounds up to whole instances) - instances_cell
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Monthly compute cost = instances × 4.80 × 720 = SAR 3,456 - monthly_cost_cell
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Cost per 1,000 inferences = 3,456 / 240,000 = SAR 0.0144 - cost_per_1k_cell
- **Two-Variable Serving-Cost Sensitivity Table (Batch Size × Fleet Size)** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: AFP/FinOps scenario-modelling practice / Google MLOps capacity planning
  - _Measures:_ Building a real two-variable sensitivity surface (native data table / array formula) over a serving-cost model — the standard MLOps capacity-planning artefact for vendor-commitment and scale-up decisions.
  - _Scenario:_ Continuing the STC churn-serving platform: the team wants to see how monthly GPU compute cost moves as they vary the number of instances (the fleet size) against the per-instance hourly rate negotiated with the cloud vendor under different commitment tiers. Monthly cost = instances × hourly_rate × 720 hours. Build a NATIVE two-variable data table where the row axis is instances (1, 2, 3) and the column axis is the negotiated hourly rate (SAR 3.60, 4.80, 6.00). The corner cell must link to the base monthly-cost formula; the body must be a native data table, not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Base formula in the corner = instances × hourly_rate × 720 (links to the model's instance and rate cells). The data table sweeps instances {1,2,3} down rows and hourly_rate {3.60,4.80,6.00} across columns. Interior values: at 1 inst × 3.60 = 2,592; 2 × 4.80 = 6,912; 3 × 6.00 = 12,960. Corners: low (1 inst, 3.60) = 2,592; high (3 inst, 6.00) = 12,960; centre (2 inst, 4.80) = 6,912. Graded on the presence of a native data-table/array formula AND the three reconciling corner/centre values.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Body uses a native two-variable data table {=TABLE()} / array formula, not hardcoded numbers - data_table_range
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (1 instance × SAR 3.60) = SAR 2,592/month - low_corner_cell
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre (2 instances × SAR 4.80) = SAR 6,912/month - centre_cell
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (3 instances × SAR 6.00) = SAR 12,960/month - high_corner_cell

**Pillar - MLOps Monitoring & Inference-Ledger Interrogation**

- **Inference-Log Drift & SLA-Breach Querying (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: ISO/IEC 22989 (AI concepts/terminology) / Google MLOps monitoring & CRISP-ML(Q) — model monitoring
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating a production inference ledger for per-model operational health — request volume, latency, and SLA-breach counts — the daily SQL an MLOps engineer writes against monitoring stores. Uses portable AVG/COUNT + conditional aggregation (no engine-specific percentile function).
  - _Scenario:_ A Qatar National Bank credit-scoring platform logs every production prediction to an inference_log table (one row per request) with columns: id, model_name, request_ts (date), latency_ms (numeric), score (numeric 0-1), drift_psi (population-stability-index for that day's feature batch, numeric). The platform SLA is latency_ms <= 250. Risk wants a per-model monitoring rollup to spot which models are degrading. Write ONE query returning, per model_name: the number of requests, the average latency (avg_latency), and the count of SLA breaches (requests with latency_ms > 250) as sla_breaches — ordered by sla_breaches highest first, then model_name. Columns: model_name, request_count, avg_latency, sla_breaches.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT model_name, COUNT(*) AS request_count, AVG(latency_ms) AS avg_latency, SUM(CASE WHEN latency_ms > 250 THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS sla_breaches FROM inference_log GROUP BY model_name ORDER BY sla_breaches DESC, model_name. Seed data is crafted so models have distinct breach counts (e.g. credit_score_v3 with several >250 rows ranks above credit_score_v2). Graded by ordered result-set match against the master query so both the aggregation and the ORDER BY are verified.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Per-model rollup matches master: request_count, avg_latency, and SLA-breach count, ordered by breaches desc then model_name - ordered_result_set

---

### 4.7 Deep Learning, Computer Vision, & Natural Language Processing (NLP)

Deep Learning / CV / NLP is fundamentally a model-building discipline whose gradable core is the QUANTITATIVE engineering around the models: forward-pass arithmetic, classification/detection metric computation, threshold and cost-sensitive decisioning, embedding-similarity math, and interrogation of labelled datasets + training telemetry. The function arrives with an empty skills list, so I first proposed six GCC-grounded skills, then designed the analytical slice that the four auto-grading engines can actually mark. Blueprint = 3 pillars, 4 blocks, mixing all four engines: (1) Neural Network & Vision Mechanics - a spreadsheet forward-pass/softmax block (cell_value) plus an advanced_spreadsheet two-variable IoU/confidence sweep for an object-detection model (is_array_formula + corner cell_values); (2) Model Evaluation & Decision Logic - a logic_input confusion-matrix block computing precision/recall/F1 and a cost-weighted decision threshold (logic_value, reconciling); (3) Data & Telemetry Interrogation - a sql block over a labelled-prediction / annotation table for per-class error aggregation (sql_result_match, ordered). Scenarios are concrete GCC contexts (Emirates NBD Arabic chatbot intent classifier, Abu Dhabi Police ANPR plate detector, DHA radiology triage model, a Saudi annotation-vendor QA ledger). Frameworks referenced are real and field-standard (Goodfellow/Bishop DL canon, COCO/Pascal VOC detection protocol, ISO/IEC 4213 classification-performance, scikit-learn metric definitions, DAMA DMBOK for the data layer). NOT a poor engine fit - DL/CV/NLP evaluation is heavily numeric and maps cleanly onto cell/field/SQL grading; the un-gradable parts (architecture design, training loops, free-text labelling judgement) are deliberately excluded.

**Skills:** Neural Network Forward-Pass, Activation & Softmax Mechanics · Computer Vision Model Evaluation (IoU, mAP, detection thresholds) · NLP Pipeline & Embedding / Cosine-Similarity Math · Classification Metrics & Confusion-Matrix Diagnostics (precision/recall/F1) · Inference Threshold Tuning & Cost-Sensitive Decisioning · Labelled-Dataset & Training-Telemetry Interrogation

**Engine fit:** Strong fit overall - despite DL/CV/NLP being a build-heavy discipline, the day-to-day evaluation work a practitioner is accountable for is overwhelmingly numeric and therefore cleanly auto-gradable. What maps well: (a) forward-pass / softmax / cross-entropy arithmetic -> spreadsheet cell_value; (b) detection metric sweeps (IoU x confidence -> precision grid) -> advanced_spreadsheet two-variable data table with is_array_formula + corner cell_values, structurally identical to FP&A's sensitivity block; (c) confusion-matrix metrics (precision/recall/F1/specificity) and cost-weighted threshold selection -> logic_input logic_value fields that must reconcile; (d) per-class error / annotation-agreement aggregation over a labelled-prediction ledger -> sql sql_result_match. Deliberately EXCLUDED as un-gradable (free-text / subjective / code-execution): writing model architectures, training-loop code, prompt drafting, qualitative error analysis, and labelling-guideline authoring. There is NO 'python' engine in the allowed set, so the model-coding dimension is proxied by hand-computed forward-pass and metric math (exactly how these are taught and how interviews probe them). This is an honest, high-signal proxy: a candidate who cannot compute softmax, IoU, F1, or a cost-optimal threshold by formula cannot meaningfully reason about the models that produce them.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 5 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Neural Network & Computer Vision Mechanics**

- **Forward Pass, Softmax & Cross-Entropy on an Arabic Intent Classifier** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 18 min · ref: Goodfellow, Bengio & Courville - Deep Learning (MIT) / Bishop - Pattern Recognition (softmax + categorical cross-entropy)
  - _Measures:_ Can the candidate execute a neural-network output-layer forward pass by hand - matrix-vector logit computation, numerically correct softmax normalisation, and categorical cross-entropy loss - the arithmetic backbone of every classifier they will train.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates NBD is deploying an Arabic-language customer-service chatbot whose final layer classifies an utterance into 3 intents: BALANCE, TRANSFER, COMPLAINT. For one utterance the penultimate (hidden) layer outputs h = [0.5, -1.0, 2.0] and feeds a single dense output neuron per class. The output weights are W (3x3, rows=intent, cols=hidden) and bias b per intent, all given in the grid. The candidate must compute the pre-activation logits z = W.h + b for each intent, apply ReLU is NOT used here (output layer), convert logits to probabilities via softmax, identify the predicted-class probability, and compute the categorical cross-entropy loss against the true label TRANSFER (one-hot [0,1,0]). All raw numbers (h vector, W matrix, b vector, exp() helper column scaffold) are pre-populated; the candidate fills the logit cells, the exp cells, the softmax-denominator cell, the three probability cells, and the loss cell.
  - _Model answer:_ Logits: z_BALANCE = 0.8*0.5 + (-0.5)*(-1.0) + 0.2*2.0 + 0.1 = 0.4+0.5+0.4+0.1 = 1.4 (B12). z_TRANSFER = 0.3*0.5 + 0.6*(-1.0) + 1.0*2.0 + (-0.2) = 0.15-0.6+2.0-0.2 = 1.35 (B13). z_COMPLAINT = -0.4*0.5 + 0.2*(-1.0) + 0.1*2.0 + 0.05 = -0.2-0.2+0.2+0.05 = -0.15 (B14). exp(z): exp(1.4)=4.0552 (C12), exp(1.35)=3.8574 (C13), exp(-0.15)=0.8607 (C14). Denominator = sum = 8.7733 (C16). Softmax probabilities: p_BALANCE = 4.0552/8.7733 = 0.4622 (D12), p_TRANSFER = 3.8574/8.7733 = 0.4397 (D13), p_COMPLAINT = 0.8607/8.7733 = 0.0981 (D14). True class = TRANSFER, so cross-entropy loss = -ln(p_TRANSFER) = -ln(0.4397) = 0.8216 (D18). Note the model would mis-rank here (BALANCE > TRANSFER), which the loss magnitude reflects.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Logit z for TRANSFER intent (W.h + b) - Matrix-vector pre-activation arithmetic for the true class
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Softmax denominator (sum of exp(logits)) - Correct normalisation constant - the most common softmax error
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Softmax probability of predicted top class (BALANCE) - Probabilities are a valid normalised distribution
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Softmax probability of TRANSFER - Per-class probability used by the loss
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Categorical cross-entropy loss vs true label TRANSFER - Loss = -ln(p_true); ties forward pass to the training objective
- **Object-Detection Precision Sweep: IoU x Confidence Threshold Grid** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18 min · ref: Pascal VOC / COCO detection evaluation protocol (IoU-based TP/FP, precision) 
  - _Measures:_ Can the candidate operationalise the detection-evaluation tradeoff (IoU strictness vs confidence cutoff) as a native two-variable sensitivity table - the standard way CV teams pick an operating point - rather than spot-checking one threshold.
  - _Scenario:_ Abu Dhabi Police are evaluating an Automatic Number-Plate Recognition (ANPR) detector at a Sheikh Zayed Road gantry. A small labelled validation batch is summarised by a closed-form proxy already wired in the model area: for a chosen IoU-match threshold and a chosen confidence cutoff, the cell B7 computes Precision = TP / (TP + FP) where TP and FP are given as functions of the two thresholds (the upstream count formulas are pre-built and reference B1 = IoU threshold and B3 = confidence threshold). The candidate must (1) confirm the base-case precision in B7, then (2) build a two-variable DATA TABLE sweeping IoU thresholds {0.50, 0.65, 0.80} down the rows against confidence thresholds {0.30, 0.50, 0.70} across the columns, so engineers can read off how precision hardens as both thresholds tighten. The data table MUST be a native data table referencing the precision cell - not hand-typed numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Base case (B1=0.50 IoU, B3=0.30 conf): with the pre-wired counts TP=180, FP=20, Precision = 180/(180+20) = 0.90 in B7. The corner cell above the table (e.g. B9) links =B7. Row inputs feed B1 (IoU), column inputs feed B3 (confidence). Selecting the range and running Data Table (row input cell B3, column input cell B1) fills C10:E12. Master corner/interior values from the seeded count model: loosest (IoU 0.50, conf 0.30) = 0.90 (C10); base/centre (IoU 0.65, conf 0.50) = 0.9474 (D11); strictest (IoU 0.80, conf 0.70) = 0.9800 (E12). Grader checks the range carries a native {=TABLE()} array AND the three diagonal corners match.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Base-case precision TP/(TP+FP) in the model cell - Precision formula correct before the sweep is built
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sweep range is a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - Candidate used a real sensitivity table referencing the model, not pasted values
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Loosest corner: IoU 0.50 / confidence 0.30 precision - Low-strictness operating point computed by the table
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre cell: IoU 0.65 / confidence 0.50 precision - Interior of the data table is live
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Strictest corner: IoU 0.80 / confidence 0.70 precision - High-strictness operating point computed by the table

**Pillar - Model Evaluation & Decision Logic**

- **Confusion-Matrix Diagnostics for a Radiology Triage Classifier** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: ISO/IEC 4213 (classification-performance assessment) / scikit-learn metric definitions (precision, recall, F1, specificity)
  - _Measures:_ Can the candidate convert a confusion matrix into the full diagnostic panel and understand that in a clinical-safety context recall (missed positives) dominates - the literacy gate for anyone evaluating a high-stakes model.
  - _Scenario:_ Dubai Health Authority (DHA) piloted a deep-learning chest-X-ray triage model at Rashid Hospital to flag scans needing urgent radiologist review. On a held-out test set of 1,000 scans the confusion matrix is: True Positives (correctly flagged urgent) = 180, False Positives (flagged urgent but normal) = 120, False Negatives (missed urgent cases) = 20, True Negatives (correctly cleared) = 680. The candidate must compute, as separate fields, Precision, Recall (Sensitivity), Specificity, the F1 score, and Accuracy - the panel a clinical-AI committee requires before any deployment sign-off. Values are reported as proportions rounded to 4 decimals (e.g. 0.6000), F1 likewise.
  - _Model answer:_ Precision = TP/(TP+FP) = 180/300 = 0.6000. Recall/Sensitivity = TP/(TP+FN) = 180/200 = 0.9000. Specificity = TN/(TN+FP) = 680/800 = 0.8500. F1 = 2*Precision*Recall/(Precision+Recall) = 2*0.6*0.9/(0.6+0.9) = 1.08/1.5 = 0.7200. Accuracy = (TP+TN)/Total = (180+680)/1000 = 0.8600. The reconciliation logic: high recall (0.90) with modest precision (0.60) is the deliberate, clinically-correct operating point for triage (catch urgents, tolerate over-flagging).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Precision = TP/(TP+FP) - Positive predictive value
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Recall / Sensitivity = TP/(TP+FN) - True-positive rate - dominant metric in clinical triage
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Specificity = TN/(TN+FP) - True-negative rate
    - `logic_value` (w3) - F1 score = harmonic mean of precision & recall - Balanced single-figure metric computed from the two prior fields (must reconcile)
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Accuracy = (TP+TN)/Total - Overall correctness; contextualises why accuracy alone is misleading here
- **Cost-Sensitive Threshold Selection for a Fraud-Text NLP Model** &nbsp; `Logic input` · advanced · 10 min · ref: Cost-sensitive learning / expected-cost decision theory (Elkan, 2001) - operating-point selection
  - _Measures:_ Can the candidate move beyond raw metrics to expected-cost reasoning and pick the operating point that minimises business cost - the decision a real ML owner is paid to make, not just report.
  - _Scenario:_ An NLP model at a Saudi fintech (STC Pay) scores incoming Arabic SMS / transaction notes for fraud. At decision threshold A: 90 fraud caught, 10 fraud missed, 200 legitimate wrongly blocked. At threshold B (looser): 96 fraud caught, 4 fraud missed, 600 legitimate wrongly blocked. Each MISSED fraud (false negative) costs SAR 5,000 in losses; each WRONGLY BLOCKED legitimate transaction (false positive) costs SAR 50 in friction/handling. The candidate computes the expected total cost at threshold A, the expected total cost at threshold B, the cost difference (B minus A), and reports the cost-optimal threshold as a coded field (enter 1 for threshold A, 2 for threshold B).
  - _Model answer:_ Cost(A) = FN_cost + FP_cost = (10 * 5000) + (200 * 50) = 50,000 + 10,000 = SAR 60,000. Cost(B) = (4 * 5000) + (600 * 50) = 20,000 + 30,000 = SAR 50,000. Difference (B - A) = 50,000 - 60,000 = -SAR 10,000 (threshold B is SAR 10,000 cheaper). Cost-optimal = threshold B, so the coded decision field = 2. The lesson: the looser threshold wins despite blocking 3x more legitimate traffic, because missed fraud is 100x costlier per event.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Expected total cost at threshold A (SAR) - Weighted FN+FP cost at the strict operating point
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Expected total cost at threshold B (SAR) - Weighted FN+FP cost at the loose operating point
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Cost difference (B minus A, SAR) - Reconciliation of the two cost computations (signed)
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Cost-optimal threshold code (1=A, 2=B) - Correct cost-minimising decision, not just the arithmetic

**Pillar - Labelled-Data & Training-Telemetry Interrogation**

- **Per-Class Error Aggregation over a Model-Prediction Ledger (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 11 min · ref: DAMA DMBOK (data interrogation) / model-evaluation error analysis over a prediction log
  - _Measures:_ Can the candidate interrogate a real prediction log with filtered aggregation and ordering to drive error analysis - the routine SQL an ML engineer runs to decide where the model is weakest and where to spend annotation budget.
  - _Scenario:_ A Saudi data-annotation vendor maintains a predictions table logging every test-set inference from a deployed Arabic document-OCR/NER model used by a Riyadh government records office. Each row has the true label and the model's predicted label per entity class. The QA lead needs to know which entity classes the model gets wrong most often, to prioritise the next labelling sprint. The candidate writes ONE query returning, per true_label class, the count of MISCLASSIFIED rows (where predicted_label <> true_label), ordered most-errors-first.
  - _Model answer:_ Seed a predictions table (id, true_label, predicted_label, confidence, inferred_at) with rows across classes PERSON, ORG, LOCATION, DATE such that the per-class misclassification counts are unambiguous and tie-broken by class name. Master query: SELECT true_label, COUNT(*) AS errors FROM predictions WHERE predicted_label <> true_label GROUP BY true_label ORDER BY errors DESC, true_label. Correct answer requires the WHERE filter (only mismatches), GROUP BY true_label, the alias 'errors', and the descending order with a deterministic name tiebreak. Result set is order-sensitive (ordered=true).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Per-class misclassification counts, most-errors-first, matches master (ordered) - Filtered aggregation (predicted<>true) + GROUP BY true_label + correct descending order with deterministic tiebreak

---

### 4.8 Generative AI (GenAI), Large Language Models, & RAG Architecture

GenAI/LLM/RAG is a build-and-evaluate engineering function whose defensible, auto-gradable core is quantitative: token-and-cost economics of LLM deployment, RAG retrieval quality (precision/recall/F1, chunk/context-window math, cosine similarity), and rigorous output-evaluation analytics (hallucination/accuracy rates, golden-set scoring, inter-rater agreement, A/B uplift) plus SQL interrogation of an inference/evaluation log. Free-text prompt authoring and architecture write-ups are NOT gradable here, so the blueprint targets the numeric slice the four engines can verify: a spreadsheet token-budget/cost model with a 2-variable sensitivity table over context size x request volume; a logic_input RAG retrieval-metrics + chunking computation; a logic_input output-evaluation scorecard (golden-set accuracy, hallucination rate, weighted quality index, Cohen's kappa); and SQL over an LLM inference-log table (cost-by-model, p95 latency, escalation/groundedness rates). 3 pillars, 4 blocks, 3 engines (spreadsheet + advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input x2, sql), mixed basic->advanced, grounded in GCC scenarios (UAE/Saudi banking + government) and real standards (NIST AI RMF, ISO/IEC 42001 & 23053, OWASP LLM Top 10, RAGAS, provider tokenizer/pricing conventions).

**Skills:** Prompt Engineering · LLM Capabilities & Limits · RAG Basics · GenAI Tooling · Output Evaluation · Productivity Workflows

**Engine fit:** Strong fit for the QUANTITATIVE/ANALYTICAL slice of this otherwise build-and-judge function; the un-gradable parts (writing prompts, drafting RAG architecture, qualitative output critique) are deliberately excluded because no engine can grade free text. The gradable proxies map cleanly: (1) spreadsheet/advanced_spreadsheet -> LLM token-and-cost economics + a 2-variable sensitivity data table (monthly cost across context-window size x daily request volume) - exact cell_value + is_array_formula checks; (2) logic_input -> RAG retrieval evaluation (precision/recall/F1 from a retrieval confusion table) and chunking/context math (chunks-per-doc, tokens-per-query, context-budget fit) - exact logic_value checks that reconcile; (3) logic_input -> output-evaluation scorecard (golden-set accuracy %, hallucination rate, weighted quality index, Cohen's kappa inter-rater agreement) - the core 'Output Evaluation' skill rendered numeric; (4) sql -> interrogate a seeded llm_inference_log table (total cost per model, p95-style aggregation, groundedness/escalation rates) - sql_result_match. Prompt Engineering and Productivity Workflows are exercised indirectly through the economics/throughput math rather than free-text authoring. Honest limitation: this measures the candidate's command of the metrics, cost models, and data that govern GenAI delivery decisions - it does NOT measure prompt-writing craft or qualitative architecture judgement, which require human/LLM-judge rubrics outside these four engines.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - LLM Economics & Deployment Sizing**

- **Token Budget & Inference Cost Model with Volume x Context Sensitivity** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18 min · ref: Provider tokenizer & per-1K-token pricing conventions; NIST AI RMF (Measure/Manage); FinOps for AI
  - _Measures:_ LLM cost/token economics, prompt+context token accounting, and scenario sensitivity modelling for GenAI deployment sizing (Productivity Workflows + LLM Capabilities & Limits rendered quantitative).
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Federal Services Authority (Abu Dhabi) is sizing a citizen-services RAG assistant on a hosted LLM billed per 1,000 tokens: input (prompt) at AED 0.012 / 1K tokens and output (completion) at AED 0.036 / 1K tokens. Each request sends a system prompt of 400 tokens + 6 retrieved chunks of 300 tokens each (RAG context) + a 150-token user question, and returns a 250-token answer. Expected steady-state load is 8,000 requests/day, 30 days/month. The Caliber grid is pre-populated with the rate card, per-request token components, and volume assumptions in labelled cells. Complete the cost build: input tokens/request, output tokens/request, blended cost/request (AED), and total monthly cost (AED). Then build a TWO-VARIABLE data table showing total MONTHLY cost as the number of retrieved chunks varies down the rows (4, 6, 8) and daily request volume varies across the columns (6,000 / 8,000 / 10,000), so leadership can see cost sensitivity to retrieval depth and adoption.
  - _Model answer:_ Input tokens/request = 400 system + (6 chunks x 300) + 150 question = 2,350; cost = 2.350 K x AED 0.012 = AED 0.0282. Output tokens/request = 250; cost = 0.250 K x AED 0.036 = AED 0.009. Blended cost/request = 0.0282 + 0.009 = AED 0.0372. Total monthly = 0.0372 x 8,000 x 30 = AED 8,928.00. Sensitivity corner formula links to the monthly-cost cell; the data table re-runs the model varying chunks (row input -> the chunk-count driver cell) and daily volume (column input -> the volume driver cell). Corner values: input cost/request scales with chunks. At 4 chunks (input tokens = 400+1,200+150 = 1,750 -> input cost 0.021; blended 0.030) x 6,000 x 30 = AED 5,400.00. At 8 chunks (input tokens = 400+2,400+150 = 2,950 -> input cost 0.0354; blended 0.0444) x 10,000 x 30 = AED 13,320.00. Base/interior at 6 chunks x 8,000/day = AED 8,928.00.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Input tokens per request = 2,350 (system + 6x300 context + question) - Correct token accounting across system prompt, RAG context, and user question
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Blended cost per request = AED 0.0372 (input @0.012/1K + output @0.036/1K) - Differentiated input/output per-1K-token pricing applied correctly
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Total monthly cost = AED 8,928.00 (cost/req x 8,000 x 30) - Scaling per-request cost to monthly run-rate
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Cost sensitivity grid is a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - Candidate built a real sensitivity table over chunks x volume, not typed numbers
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner = AED 5,400.00 (4 chunks, 6,000 req/day) - Data table low-retrieval / low-adoption corner re-runs the model correctly
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner = AED 13,320.00 (8 chunks, 10,000 req/day) - Data table high-retrieval / high-adoption corner re-runs the model correctly

**Pillar - RAG Retrieval Quality & Context Engineering**

- **Retrieval Metrics & Chunking / Context-Window Fit** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: RAGAS retrieval metrics; ISO/IEC 23053 (AI/ML framework); information-retrieval precision/recall/F1
  - _Measures:_ Quantitative RAG evaluation: retrieval precision/recall/F1, chunking arithmetic, and context-window budgeting (RAG Basics + Output Evaluation).
  - _Scenario:_ Saudi National Bank (Riyadh) is tuning the retriever for a Shariah-compliance Q&A assistant. On a 120-question evaluation set, the retriever is configured to return the top-k = 5 chunks per question. Across the whole set, of the chunks it returned, 360 were relevant (true positives) and 240 were irrelevant (false positives); a further 90 relevant chunks that existed in the corpus were NOT retrieved (false negatives). Separately, the knowledge base holds 4,000 source documents averaging 3,200 tokens each; the team chunks documents at 800 tokens per chunk with a 100-token overlap (stride 700 tokens), and the LLM context window for retrieval is 8,000 tokens with 1,200 tokens reserved for the system prompt and answer. Compute the labelled fields. All retrieval metrics must reconcile (F1 from your own precision and recall).
  - _Model answer:_ Precision = TP/(TP+FP) = 360/(360+240) = 360/600 = 0.6000. Recall = TP/(TP+FN) = 360/(360+90) = 360/450 = 0.8000. F1 = 2PR/(P+R) = 2(0.6)(0.8)/(0.6+0.8) = 0.96/1.4 = 0.6857 (4 dp). Chunks per document with overlap = ceil((3,200 - 800)/700) + 1 = ceil(2,400/700)+1 = ceil(3.4286)+1 = 4+1 = 5 chunks/doc. Max chunks that fit the retrieval budget = floor((8,000 - 1,200)/800) = floor(6,800/800) = floor(8.5) = 8 chunks. Since top-k = 5 <= 8, the top-5 retrieval (5 x 800 = 4,000 tokens) fits within the 6,800-token budget, so context_fits = 1 (true).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Retrieval precision = 0.6000 - Precision = TP/(TP+FP) computed correctly
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Retrieval recall = 0.8000 - Recall = TP/(TP+FN) computed correctly
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Retrieval F1 = 0.6857 - F1 harmonic mean reconciles with candidate's own precision and recall
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Chunks per document (overlap) = 5 - Overlap-aware chunking arithmetic: ceil((len-size)/stride)+1
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Max chunks fitting retrieval token budget = 8 - Context-window budgeting after reserving system+answer tokens
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Top-5 context fits budget flag = 1 (true) - Decision logic comparing top-k token load against available budget

**Pillar - Output Evaluation, Quality & Production Analytics**

- **Golden-Set Evaluation Scorecard & Inter-Rater Agreement** &nbsp; `Logic input` · advanced · 11 min · ref: NIST AI RMF (Measure); OWASP LLM Top 10 (LLM09 overreliance / hallucination); Cohen's kappa for evaluator reliability
  - _Measures:_ Rigorous LLM output evaluation: golden-set accuracy, hallucination-rate risk tracking, weighted quality scoring, and Cohen's kappa inter-rater reliability (Output Evaluation core).
  - _Scenario:_ Mashreq Bank (Dubai) ran a 500-response golden-set evaluation of a customer-service LLM before go-live. Automated + human grading classified each response as: 410 fully correct, 35 partially correct, 30 incorrect-but-harmless, and 25 hallucinated (fabricated facts). The bank scores a Weighted Quality Index awarding 1.0 per fully-correct, 0.5 per partially-correct, and 0.0 otherwise, expressed as a percentage of the maximum possible. Hallucinations are tracked separately as a risk rate. Two independent human reviewers also double-rated a 200-response subsample as pass/fail to validate the eval harness: they AGREED on 170 responses (both pass on 150, both fail on 20); reviewer A passed but B failed 18; reviewer B passed but A failed 12. Compute the labelled fields, including Cohen's kappa for the two reviewers.
  - _Model answer:_ Accuracy (fully correct) = 410/500 = 82.00%. Hallucination rate = 25/500 = 5.00%. Weighted Quality Index = (410 x 1.0 + 35 x 0.5 + 30 x 0 + 25 x 0)/500 = (410 + 17.5)/500 = 427.5/500 = 85.50%. Cohen's kappa on the 200-subsample: observed agreement Po = (150+20)/200 = 170/200 = 0.85. Marginals: A pass = (150+18)/200 = 168/200 = 0.84; B pass = (150+12)/200 = 162/200 = 0.81; A fail = 0.16; B fail = 0.19. Expected agreement Pe = (0.84 x 0.81) + (0.16 x 0.19) = 0.6804 + 0.0304 = 0.7108. Kappa = (Po - Pe)/(1 - Pe) = (0.85 - 0.7108)/(1 - 0.7108) = 0.1392/0.2892 = 0.4813 (4 dp).
  - _Checkpoints:_
