    - `logic_value` (w2) - Golden-set accuracy = 82.00 (%) - Fully-correct rate over the 500-item set
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Hallucination rate = 5.00 (%) - Hallucinated responses tracked as a separate risk metric
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Weighted Quality Index = 85.50 (%) - Partial-credit weighted scoring expressed as % of max
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Observed agreement Po = 0.8500 - Raw inter-rater agreement proportion computed correctly
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Expected (chance) agreement Pe = 0.7108 - Chance agreement from reviewer marginal pass/fail rates
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Cohen's kappa = 0.4813 - Kappa = (Po-Pe)/(1-Pe) reconciles with candidate's own Po and Pe
- **LLM Inference-Log Interrogation (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 11 min · ref: ISO/IEC 42001 (AI management system - monitoring & logging); DAMA DMBOK; LLM observability practice
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating LLM production telemetry to drive cost/quality decisions - aggregation, conditional rate computation, grouping and ranking (GenAI Tooling + observability).
  - _Scenario:_ Qatar National Bank's GenAI platform team logs every production LLM call to an inference_log table for cost and quality monitoring. Each row records the model used, total cost in QAR, end-to-end latency in milliseconds, whether the answer was grounded in retrieved context (a boolean), and whether it was escalated to a human agent. Leadership wants a per-model monitoring summary to decide which models to keep. Write ONE query returning, per model: the number of calls, total cost (QAR), average latency (ms), and the groundedness rate (share of calls where grounded = true, as a fraction 0-1). Return models ordered by total cost, highest first.
  - _Model answer:_ GROUP BY model; COUNT(*) AS calls; SUM(cost_qar) AS total_cost; AVG(latency_ms) AS avg_latency; AVG(CASE WHEN grounded THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS groundedness_rate (equivalently SUM(grounded::int)::numeric/COUNT(*)); ORDER BY total_cost DESC (tie-break by model). The seed has multiple models (e.g. gpt-class, claude-class, a fine-tuned in-house model) across ~12-16 rows so the grouped aggregates, the conditional groundedness fraction, and the cost-descending order are all distinguishable. The result set must match the master query on rows, columns, and order.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Per-model calls, total cost, avg latency, and groundedness rate, ordered by total cost desc - Correct GROUP BY + aggregates + conditional groundedness rate + cost-descending ordering matching the master query

---

### 4.9 AI Governance, Ethics, Bias Mitigation, & Model Risk Management

A hands-on sandbox for the QUANTITATIVE, auto-gradable slice of AI Governance & Model Risk Management. The function as named (ethics, policy, regulatory) is largely qualitative, so this blueprint isolates the numerical control work the role actually owns: (1) Bias & Fairness measurement - computing disparate-impact ratio (4/5ths rule), statistical parity difference and equalized-odds gaps from per-group confusion-matrix counts; (2) Model Risk Management - SR 11-7-style inherent/residual risk tiering and a model-inventory interrogation in SQL; (3) Model Monitoring & Explainability - Population Stability Index (PSI) drift detection and a performance-decay decision built as an array-driven monitoring matrix. Three pillars, four blocks, three engines (logic_input, sql, advanced_spreadsheet) mixed across basic/intermediate/advanced. All scenarios are GCC/MENA-grounded (a UAE retail-credit scoring model under CBUAE/SAMA AI oversight, an enterprise model inventory, an Islamic-bank fraud model drift watch) with concrete figures and reconciling checkpoints. Frameworks: US Fed/OCC SR 11-7, EU AI Act (high-risk obligations), NIST AI RMF 1.0, ISO/IEC 42001, plus fairness-metric conventions (4/5ths rule, equalized odds).

**Skills:** Model Risk Management · Explainability · Bias & Fairness · Regulatory & Ethics · Model Monitoring · AI Policy

**Engine fit:** Strong fit for the analytical core of this function despite its governance/ethics framing. The role's genuinely auto-gradable work is metric computation and threshold decisioning, which maps cleanly onto three of the four engines: logic_input for fairness arithmetic (disparate-impact ratio, statistical-parity difference, equalized-odds gaps) and inherent/residual model-risk scoring; sql for interrogating a model inventory (which models breach validation-overdue / high-tier policy); advanced_spreadsheet for a Population Stability Index (PSI) drift matrix built with a native array/data-table formula plus a monitoring decision. spreadsheet (plain) is intentionally not used - the spreadsheet work here is inherently array/table-shaped (per-bucket PSI), so advanced_spreadsheet is the honest choice. HONEST LIMITATION: the genuinely soft parts of this function - drafting an AI policy, writing an ethics opinion, narrating an explainability finding to a board, judging whether a use case is "acceptable risk" - are NOT gradable by these engines and are deliberately excluded; this sandbox certifies that a candidate can correctly COMPUTE and THRESHOLD the governance metrics, not that they can write the policy prose around them. A complete assessment of this function would pair this sandbox with an MCQ layer (regulatory knowledge) and a human-rated writing sample (policy/ethics judgement).

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Logic input, SQL, Adv. Spreadsheet

**Pillar - Bias & Fairness Measurement**

- **Disparate-Impact & Fairness-Metric Computation** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: EU AI Act (high-risk bias testing) / US EEOC 4/5ths Rule / Equalized-Odds convention
  - _Measures:_ Computing protected-group selection rates and the canonical fairness metrics (disparate impact / 4-fifths, statistical parity difference, equalized-odds TPR gap) from raw confusion-matrix counts, then applying the regulatory pass threshold.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates National Retail Bank (Dubai) deployed an automated retail-credit scoring model now classed high-risk under draft CBUAE AI guidance, so Model Risk owes a fairness test before sign-off. A validation pull of 4,000 decided applications splits into two protected groups by nationality basis. GROUP A (UAE National applicants), n=1,500: model APPROVED 900. Of the 1,000 who actually repaid prior facilities (true positives basis), the model approved 720 (true positives) and wrongly declined 280 (false negatives); of the 500 who later defaulted, it approved 180 (false positives) and declined 320 (true negatives). GROUP B (Expatriate applicants), n=2,500: model APPROVED 1,100. Of the 1,500 good payers, the model approved 960 (true positives) and declined 540 (false negatives); of the 1,000 bad payers, it approved 140 (false positives) and declined 860 (true negatives). Compute the selection (approval) rate for each group, the disparate-impact ratio (less-favoured / more-favoured selection rate), the statistical-parity difference, and the equalized-odds true-positive-rate gap (TPR_A - TPR_B). Flag whether the model passes the 4/5ths rule as a 1 (pass, ratio >= 0.80) or 0 (fail).
  - _Model answer:_ Selection rate = approvals / group n. Group A = 900/1500 = 0.60; Group B = 1100/2500 = 0.44. Disparate-impact ratio = less-favoured(0.44) / more-favoured(0.60) = 0.7333. Statistical-parity difference = 0.60 - 0.44 = 0.16. TPR_A = 720/1000 = 0.72; TPR_B = 960/1500 = 0.64; equalized-odds TPR gap = 0.72 - 0.64 = 0.08. 4/5ths pass flag: ratio 0.7333 < 0.80 -> 0 (fail).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Group A selection (approval) rate = 0.60 - Per-group selection rate from approvals / n
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Group B selection (approval) rate = 0.44 - Per-group selection rate from approvals / n
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Disparate-impact ratio = 0.733 (less-favoured / more-favoured) - Correct identification of reference group and ratio direction
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Statistical-parity difference = 0.16 - Difference-form fairness metric
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Equalized-odds TPR gap = 0.08 - True-positive-rate parity using only the good-payer subgroup, not whole group
    - `logic_value` (w2) - 4/5ths-rule pass flag = 0 (fail, ratio < 0.80) - Applying the regulatory threshold as a binary decision

**Pillar - Model Risk Management & Inventory Control**

- **Inherent / Residual Model-Risk Tiering** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 10 min · ref: US Federal Reserve / OCC SR 11-7 (Model Risk Management) / NIST AI RMF 1.0
  - _Measures:_ Building a weighted inherent-risk score, applying a control-effectiveness haircut to derive residual risk, and mapping the result to a documented policy tier - the core SR 11-7 risk-rating mechanic.
  - _Scenario:_ Saudi Awwal Capital (Riyadh) is rating a new GenAI customer-onboarding model under an SR 11-7 model-risk framework. Inherent risk is scored on three weighted factors, each rated 1-5: Materiality (financial/regulatory exposure) rated 5, weight 0.50; Complexity (opacity / lack of explainability) rated 4, weight 0.30; Use-case Criticality (autonomy / human-in-the-loop absence) rated 3, weight 0.20. The control-effectiveness score from the last validation is 0.40 on a 0-1 scale (0 = no mitigation, 1 = fully mitigated). Residual risk = inherent risk x (1 - control effectiveness). Policy tiers map the residual score: Tier 1 (High) if residual >= 3.0, Tier 2 (Medium) if 1.5 <= residual < 3.0, Tier 3 (Low) if residual < 1.5. Compute the weighted inherent-risk score, the residual-risk score, and output the policy tier as an integer (1, 2 or 3).
  - _Model answer:_ Inherent = 5x0.50 + 4x0.30 + 3x0.20 = 2.50 + 1.20 + 0.60 = 4.30. Residual = 4.30 x (1 - 0.40) = 4.30 x 0.60 = 2.58. Tier: 1.5 <= 2.58 < 3.0 -> Tier 2 (Medium) -> output 2.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Weighted inherent-risk score = 4.30 - Weighted-sum of factor ratings using the given weights
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Residual-risk score = 2.58 - Applying the (1 - control effectiveness) haircut to inherent risk
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Policy tier = 2 (Medium) - Mapping the residual score to the correct documented risk tier
- **Model Inventory Interrogation (Validation-Overdue & Tier Breach)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: SR 11-7 (model inventory) / ISO/IEC 42001 AI management system
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating a model inventory with a date-arithmetic predicate (validation cadence vs committee date), compound filtering on tier + production status, and deterministic ordering - the day-to-day governance reporting query.
  - _Scenario:_ The enterprise AI model register at a Abu Dhabi government holding company (table model_inventory) must be screened for governance breaches before the quarterly risk committee. Each row records id, model_name, business_unit, risk_tier (text: 'high','medium','low'), last_validation_date (date), validation_frequency_months (int = how often the model must be re-validated), and in_production (boolean). A model is OVERDUE when its next-due date (last_validation_date plus validation_frequency_months) is earlier than the committee date 2026-06-30. The committee wants every in-production model that is BOTH risk_tier = 'high' AND overdue, returned worst-lateness first. Seeded rows: (1,'Retail Credit Scorer','Retail','high','2025-01-15',6,true) [due 2025-07-15 - overdue], (2,'AML Transaction Monitor','Compliance','high','2026-03-01',6,true) [due 2026-09-01 - current], (3,'Churn Predictor','Marketing','medium','2024-11-01',12,true) [medium - excluded], (4,'GenAI Onboarding Bot','Retail','high','2024-08-01',12,true) [due 2025-08-01 - overdue], (5,'Branch Footfall Forecaster','Ops','high','2025-12-01',6,false) [not in production - excluded], (6,'Collections Optimizer','Retail','high','2025-02-20',6,true) [due 2025-08-20 - overdue]. Return columns model_name and last_validation_date for breaching models, ordered by last_validation_date ascending (oldest validation first).
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT model_name, last_validation_date FROM model_inventory WHERE in_production = true AND risk_tier = 'high' AND (last_validation_date + (validation_frequency_months \|\| ' months')::interval) < DATE '2026-06-30' ORDER BY last_validation_date ASC. Matches rows 4 (2024-08-01), 6 (2025-02-20), 1 (2025-01-15) re-ordered to: GenAI Onboarding Bot (2024-08-01), Retail Credit Scorer (2025-01-15), Collections Optimizer (2025-02-20). Row 2 current, row 3 medium, row 5 not in production.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result set matches master: high-tier, in-production, overdue models, oldest-validation-first - Date-cadence overdue logic + compound tier/production filter + ascending order all correct

**Pillar - Model Monitoring & Explainability**

- **Population Stability Index (PSI) Drift Matrix & Monitoring Decision** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 20 min · ref: SR 11-7 ongoing monitoring / NIST AI RMF (MEASURE/MANAGE) / model-drift convention
  - _Measures:_ Computing the Population Stability Index drift metric as a filled-down array column (not hardcoded), summing it, and converting the total into the conventional monitoring action band - the core ongoing-monitoring control for deployed models.
  - _Scenario:_ Dubai Islamic-finance fraud model: the validation team monitors score drift between the training population (Expected %) and the live last-quarter population (Actual %) across five score buckets. Bucket Expected% / Actual%: B1 0.10/0.05; B2 0.20/0.15; B3 0.40/0.35; B4 0.20/0.25; B5 0.10/0.20. The per-bucket PSI contribution is (Actual% - Expected%) x LN(Actual% / Expected%). Build a per-bucket PSI column (one formula filled down the five-row bucket range so the column is array/fill-driven, not five hand-typed constants), then total the PSI. Apply the standard monitoring rule into a decision cell: PSI < 0.10 -> output 0 (no significant shift), 0.10 <= PSI < 0.25 -> output 1 (moderate shift, investigate), PSI >= 0.25 -> output 2 (significant shift, revalidate). Provide the total PSI and the decision code.
  - _Model answer:_ Per-bucket PSI = (A-E)*LN(A/E): B1 (0.05-0.10)*LN(0.05/0.10) = -0.05 * -0.6931 = 0.03466; B2 (0.15-0.20)*LN(0.15/0.20) = -0.05 * -0.2877 = 0.01438; B3 (0.35-0.40)*LN(0.35/0.40) = -0.05 * -0.1335 = 0.00668; B4 (0.25-0.20)*LN(0.25/0.20) = 0.05 * 0.2231 = 0.01116; B5 (0.20-0.10)*LN(0.20/0.10) = 0.10 * 0.6931 = 0.06931. Total PSI = 0.13619 (approx 0.1362). Band: 0.10 <= 0.1362 < 0.25 -> decision code 1 (moderate shift, investigate).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Per-bucket PSI column is formula/fill-driven across all five buckets (not hand-typed) - PSI computed with a real filled-down formula referencing Expected/Actual cells
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Bucket B5 PSI contribution = 0.0693 - Largest single-bucket drift contribution computed correctly (sign and LN)
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Total PSI = 0.1362 - Summed drift index across all buckets
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Monitoring decision code = 1 (moderate shift, investigate) - Mapping total PSI to the conventional action band

---

### 4.10 Data Governance, Privacy Compliance, & Master Data Management (MDM)

Function 4.10 has an empty skills list, so I first proposed six GCC-grounded skills (Data Quality Measurement & DQ Dimensions; Master Data Management - Match/Merge & Golden Record; Privacy Compliance - Consent, Retention & Breach Math; Data Governance KPIs & Stewardship; Reference Data & Data Lineage Integrity; Regulatory Mapping - UAE PDPL / Saudi PDPL / GDPR), then designed to them. The function is quantitative-friendly: although "governance" sounds soft, the gradable slice is the data-quality and compliance ANALYTICS that every data steward actually does - DQ scoring across DAMA DMBOK's six dimensions, MDM duplicate detection / survivorship counts via SQL, retention-window and breach-notification deadline math, consent-coverage ratios, and a weighted DPIA / data-risk index. 3 pillars, 4 blocks, 3 engines (logic_input, sql, advanced_spreadsheet). Frameworks: DAMA DMBOK2, ISO 8000, UAE Federal Decree-Law 45/2021, Saudi PDPL, EU GDPR. All checkpoints are numeric cell/field values, an array-formula data table, or a SQL result-set match - nothing free-text.

**Skills:** Data Quality Measurement & DAMA DQ Dimensions · Master Data Management - Match/Merge & Golden Record Survivorship · Privacy Compliance - Consent, Retention & Breach Notification Math · Data Governance KPIs & Stewardship Metrics · Reference Data Control & Data Lineage Integrity · Regulatory Mapping (UAE PDPL / Saudi PDPL / GDPR)

**Engine fit:** Strong fit across 3 of the 4 engines despite "governance" sounding qualitative. The gradable slice is the data-steward's daily analytics, not policy prose. (1) Data Quality scoring is pure arithmetic over record counts - completeness, validity, uniqueness, conformity ratios per DAMA DMBOK2 - ideal for logic_input. (2) MDM match/merge and privacy compliance are relational by nature: counting duplicate clusters, identifying survivorship golden records, finding records past their retention window, and computing consent-coverage all reduce to GROUP BY / HAVING / date-arithmetic queries with deterministic result sets - ideal for sql. (3) A weighted DPIA / data-risk index and a two-variable breach-cost sensitivity table fit logic_input and advanced_spreadsheet. What is NOT gradable here and is deliberately excluded: writing a privacy policy, drafting a data-sharing agreement, judging whether a lawful basis is "appropriate," or authoring a stewardship charter - all free-text/subjective. The blueprint measures the quantitative competence that underpins those judgements (can the candidate correctly compute the retention breach, the DQ score, the duplicate count, the consent ratio, the risk index) rather than the narrative output itself. No genuine engine gap - this function sits comfortably inside the 4 engines.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Logic input, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Data Quality Measurement & Stewardship Metrics**

- **DAMA Data Quality Dimension Scoring** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA DMBOK2 (Data Quality Dimensions) / ISO 8000
  - _Measures:_ Computing the canonical DAMA data-quality dimension percentages from raw profiling counts and aggregating to an overall DQ score - the core arithmetic of any data-quality scorecard.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates National Bank's CRM steward is profiling a 50,000-record retail customer master extract ahead of a UAE PDPL audit. Profiling returns: Completeness - 46,500 of 50,000 records have a non-null Emirates ID; Validity - of those 46,500, 44,175 pass the Emirates ID checksum format (784-YYYY-NNNNNNN-N); Uniqueness - the file contains 2,500 duplicate records (records beyond the first occurrence of a customer); Timeliness - 41,000 records were updated within the last 12 months. The steward must report each DQ dimension as a percentage and a single overall DQ score as the unweighted average of the four dimension percentages (round each dimension and the overall to 2 decimal places). Completeness = non-null / total; Validity = valid-format / non-null (i.e. of populated IDs); Uniqueness = unique records / total, where unique = total - duplicates; Timeliness = fresh / total.
  - _Model answer:_ Completeness = 46500/50000 = 93.00%. Validity = 44175/46500 = 95.00% (denominator is populated IDs, not total - the discriminating step). Uniqueness = (50000-2500)/50000 = 47500/50000 = 95.00%. Timeliness = 41000/50000 = 82.00%. Overall DQ = (93.00+95.00+95.00+82.00)/4 = 365.00/4 = 91.25%.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Completeness % = 93.00 - Completeness = non-null Emirates ID / total records
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Validity % = 95.00 (denominator = populated IDs) - Validity uses the populated-ID denominator, not total - the most common DQ error
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Uniqueness % = 95.00 - Uniqueness = (total - duplicates)/total
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Timeliness % = 82.00 - Timeliness = fresh records / total
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Overall DQ score % = 91.25 - Overall = unweighted mean of the four dimensions and reconciles
- **Cost-of-Poor-Quality Remediation Sensitivity Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: DAMA DMBOK2 (Data Quality ROI) / ISO 8000
  - _Measures:_ Building a defensible COPQ business case with a native two-variable data table - the quantitative backbone of every MDM investment justification.
  - _Scenario:_ ADNOC's data governance office is sizing the annual Cost of Poor Quality (COPQ) for vendor master data so it can justify an MDM investment. The base model: a defect costs AED 35 per record to rework downstream, the vendor master holds 80,000 records, and the current defect rate is profiled at 6%. Annual COPQ = Records x Defect Rate x Cost per Defect. Leadership wants a two-variable sensitivity table showing annual COPQ (in AED) across defect rates of 4%, 6%, 8% (column headers) and cost-per-defect of AED 25, 35, 45 (row headers), holding record count at 80,000. Build the base COPQ formula in the model cell, then build a NATIVE two-variable data table (not hardcoded numbers) feeding the column input from the defect-rate cell and the row input from the cost-per-defect cell.
  - _Model answer:_ Base COPQ = 80000 x 6% x 35 = AED 168,000. Data table = Records(80000) x DefectRate(col) x CostPerDefect(row). Corner low (rate 4%, cost AED 25) = 80000 x 0.04 x 25 = AED 80,000. Centre (rate 6%, cost AED 35) = 80000 x 0.06 x 35 = AED 168,000. Corner high (rate 8%, cost AED 45) = 80000 x 0.08 x 45 = AED 288,000. The data table must be a native {=TABLE()} array, with the column input cell = defect-rate driver and row input cell = cost-per-defect driver.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base COPQ = AED 168,000 - Base model COPQ = Records x DefectRate x CostPerDefect
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sensitivity grid is a native data table (not hardcoded) - The 3x3 grid is formula-driven via a native two-variable data table
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (4%, AED 25) = AED 80,000 - Data table low-corner value is correct
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre (6%, AED 35) = AED 168,000 - Data table base-case interior value is correct
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (8%, AED 45) = AED 288,000 - Data table high-corner value is correct

**Pillar - Master Data Management - Match, Merge & Golden Record**

- **Duplicate Cluster Detection & Survivorship Query** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA DMBOK2 (Master Data Management) / ISO 8000
  - _Measures:_ Identifying MDM duplicate clusters and the survivorship anchor with GROUP BY / HAVING / MAX - the foundational match-merge query behind any golden-record build.
  - _Scenario:_ Saudi Telecom Company (stc) loaded a customer_records staging table from three source systems. Records that share the same national_id are the same real customer (a duplicate cluster). The MDM steward must report, for every national_id that appears more than once (a true duplicate cluster), the national_id, the number of duplicate source rows in the cluster (record_count), and the most recent last_updated date in the cluster (the survivorship anchor date used to pick the golden record). Return only clusters with more than one record. Order by record_count descending, then national_id ascending. Columns required: national_id, record_count, latest_update.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT national_id, COUNT(*) AS record_count, MAX(last_updated) AS latest_update FROM customer_records GROUP BY national_id HAVING COUNT(*) > 1 ORDER BY record_count DESC, national_id ASC. The HAVING COUNT(*) > 1 isolates true clusters (excludes singletons); MAX(last_updated) is the most-recent-survives survivorship rule. Seed data is constructed so several national_ids appear 2-3 times and several appear once, making the HAVING filter and the ordering both discriminating.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result set matches master (clusters, counts, latest date, correct order) - GROUP BY national_id + HAVING COUNT(*)>1 + MAX(last_updated) returns exactly the duplicate clusters in record_count DESC, national_id ASC order

**Pillar - Privacy Compliance & Data Risk Quantification**

- **Retention, Consent & Breach-Notification Compliance Math** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: UAE Federal Decree-Law 45/2021 (PDPL) / Saudi PDPL / EU GDPR
  - _Measures:_ Translating privacy regulation into the exact compliance numbers a DPO must report - retention breach rate, consent coverage, and the statutory 72-hour breach-notification deadline.
  - _Scenario:_ A Dubai fintech's Data Protection Officer is preparing a quarterly privacy compliance dashboard from the data inventory. Facts: (a) Retention - the marketing dataset holds 120,000 contact records; the documented retention policy is 24 months from last activity. A scan finds 18,000 records whose last activity is older than 24 months and must be purged. Report the retention-breach rate as a percentage (breaching / total, 2 dp). (b) Consent - of the 120,000 records, 100,800 carry a valid, time-stamped marketing-consent flag. Report the consent-coverage rate as a percentage (2 dp). (c) Breach notification - a personal-data breach was confirmed (became known) on 10 March 2026 at 09:00. UAE PDPL / GDPR require notifying the regulator without undue delay and within 72 hours of becoming aware. Compute the notification deadline as the number of hours available (the 72-hour window) and the latest permissible notification date and hour expressed as a 24h clock hour on the deadline date - report the deadline DAY of month (e.g. 13) and the deadline HOUR (0-23).
  - _Model answer:_ Retention breach rate = 18000/120000 = 15.00%. Consent coverage = 100800/120000 = 84.00%. Breach window = 72 hours. Deadline = 10 March 09:00 + 72h = 13 March 09:00 -> deadline day = 13, deadline hour = 9. The day/hour split tests correct date arithmetic across day boundaries (72h is exactly 3 days, so the hour stays 09:00 but the day advances by 3).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Retention-breach rate % = 15.00 - Retention breach rate = records past retention / total
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Consent-coverage rate % = 84.00 - Consent coverage = consented records / total
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Breach notification window = 72 hours - Candidate knows the statutory PDPL/GDPR 72-hour window
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Deadline day of month = 13 - 72h date arithmetic advances the day correctly (10 -> 13)
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Deadline hour (24h) = 9 - 72h is an exact 3-day step so the hour is preserved at 09:00

---

## Banking

> **Domain review** - engine coverage OK. All 8 blueprints are structurally sound and internally consistent against the FP&A gold standard. Every blueprint declares exactly 3 pillars and 4 blocks (within the 3-5 rule), and every blueprint uses 3 distinct auto-gradable engines (well above the >=2 minimum), giving a varied sitting. Every block maps to a valid engine from the implemented set (spreadsheet / advanced_spreadsheet / logic_input / sql) and every checkpoint kind cited in engine_fit maps to a valid CheckpointKind in src/lib/technical-sandbox/types.ts (cell_value, is_array_formula, logic_value, sql_result_match). The python engine (present in the EngineType enum but with no checkpoint kind) is correctly avoided everywhere.  Engine-fit quality is strong across the board. The five genuinely "soft" functions (5.3 Wealth, 5.7 AML/Financial Crime, 5.8 Regulatory Affairs, and partially 5.5 Trade Finance, 5.6 Core Banking Ops) all correctly identify and target the QUANTITATIVE / ANALYTICAL gradable slice and explicitly, honestly fence off the non-gradable parts (credit-memo narrative, SAR drafting, UCP 600 document-examination judgement, supervisory liaison, advisory rapport). This matches the task's mandate for non-quantitative roles. The three intrinsically-numeric functions (5.1, 5.2, 5.4) correctly state no soft proxy was needed.  Difficulty mix: every blueprint spans at least two difficulty bands. 5.1, 5.2, 5.3, 5.4, 5.5, 5.7, 5.8 each carry advanced + intermediate (+ basic in 5.1/5.6/5.8), and 5.6 spans basic+intermediate+advanced. No blueprint is mono-difficulty.  ONE SYSTEMIC ISSUE worth surfacing (consistent across all 8, severity low): every SQL block carries exactly 1 checkpoint, which sits below the stated design rule of "3-6 weighted checkpoints per block." This is NOT a defect against the implemented reference - the FP&A gold standard's own SQL block likewise has a single sql_result_match checkpoint (a SQL block grades on one ordered/unordered result-set match by design, so it cannot naturally carry 3-6 independent checks). So the SQL blocks are faithful to the reference but technically under the prose rule's floor. If the reviewer/orchestrator wants the 3-6 rule enforced literally, SQL blocks would need to be split into multiple sub-queries (not recommended - it breaks the "ONE query" SQL-engine contract). Recommendation: treat the SQL 1-checkpoint pattern as the accepted norm (matches FP&A) and relax the prose rule's lower bound for the sql engine specifically.  All non-SQL blocks carry 3-6 checkpoints (range observed: 3 to 6), fully compliant. SQL-block difficulty is sensibly kept basic/intermediate (never advanced), appropriate for a single-query grade.
>
> - _(low)_ 5.1: Engine-fit and structure are excellent (4 blocks, 3 engines, intermediate/advanced/intermediate/basic spread). Only note: the SQL block 'Loan-Book At-Risk Exposure Query' has 1 checkpoint vs the prose 3-6 rule - acceptable because it matches the FP&A reference SQL pattern (single sql_result_match). No change required.
> - _(low)_ 5.2: Strong blueprint: 3 spreadsheet/logic_input/sql engines, all non-SQL blocks at 6 checkpoints, good intermediate->advanced ramp. Minor: two of four blocks use the spreadsheet engine (EMI schedule + ECL build) while the variety still holds at 3 distinct engines - fine, but the sitting leans spreadsheet-heavy. SQL block is single-checkpoint (matches reference). No blocker.
> - _(low)_ 5.3: Best example of finding the gradable slice of a soft (advisory/relationship) function - suitability scoring, allocation math, fee-drag, efficient-frontier-as-data-table, and CRM surveillance SQL. Engine fit and honest-limitation flag are exemplary. Only the standard SQL 1-checkpoint note applies.
> - _(low)_ 5.4: Coherent and rigorous (Basel III LCR/NSFR, IRRBB gap, 2-var liquidity stress data table, treasury blotter SQL). Difficulty mix is intermediate/intermediate/advanced/intermediate - acceptable but slightly flat (no basic block); a hiring bank may want a basic warm-up. Not a defect. Standard SQL 1-checkpoint note applies.
> - _(low)_ 5.5: Solid mapping of trade finance to logic_input/spreadsheet/advanced_spreadsheet/sql with an explicit, correct exclusion of UCP 600 document-examination judgement (genuinely non-gradable). Difficulty is intermediate/advanced/advanced/intermediate - two advanced blocks back-to-back makes this one of the harder sittings; consider whether that matches the target seniority. Not a blocker. Standard SQL 1-checkpoint note applies.
> - _(low)_ 5.6: Good engine fit for an operations/clearing function (net-settlement matrix with zero-sum balance-check mirroring FP&A rigor, intraday liquidity stress table, reserve/shortfall logic_input, returned-item SQL). Best difficulty spread of the set (intermediate/advanced/basic/intermediate). The logic_input block has only 3 checkpoints (at the floor of the 3-6 rule) - compliant but lean; could add a 4th reconciling field. Standard SQL 1-checkpoint note applies.
> - _(low)_ 5.7: Strongest soft-function transformation: AML correctly reframed as risk-scoring, threshold-tuning sensitivity table, fuzzy-match scoring, SAR-aging MIS, and structuring/smurfing detection SQL, with an explicit honest limitation that SAR-narrative quality and escalation judgement are out of scope. Two logic_input blocks (CDD risk rating + sanctions fuzzy-match) means the engine spread is logic_input x2 / advanced_spreadsheet / spreadsheet / sql - still 4 distinct engines, fine. The 'Sanctions / PEP Fuzzy-Match Scoring' block has only 3 checkpoints at advanced difficulty - acceptable but the advanced label with just 3 checks is light; consider a 4th to harden grading. Standard SQL 1-checkpoint note applies.
> - _(low)_ 5.8: Coherent capital-adequacy slice of a policy/liaison function, correctly excluding ICAAP narrative and supervisory submissions. Note a structural quirk: TWO logic_input blocks (MDA cascade + LCR stack) and the engine_fit prose maps Pillar 3 to SQL, implying pillar->block distribution where one pillar may hold 2 blocks - structurally valid (3 pillars, 4 blocks) but verify the two logic_input blocks aren't crammed into one pillar leaving another pillar with a single thin block. Difficulty advanced/intermediate/intermediate/basic is well-spread. Standard SQL 1-checkpoint note applies.
>
> _Recommendations:_ 1. ACCEPT all 8 blueprints - none has a blocking defect. Every block maps to a valid auto-gradable engine, the gradable slice was correctly found for all soft functions, and all structural rules (3 pillars / 4 blocks / 3 engine types / mixed difficulty) are met.  2. SQL-checkpoint rule reconciliation (applies to all 8, do once at the orchestrator level, not per-blueprint): the prose design rule says "3-6 weighted checkpoints per block," but the FP&A reference SQL block - the implemented gold standard - carries exactly 1 sql_result_match checkpoint, and the SQL engine contract is "ONE query graded by result-set match," which cannot naturally yield 3-6 independent checks. Formally relax the lower bound to allow 1 checkpoint for the sql engine, OR optionally bump high-value SQL result-match checkpoints to weight 2-3 so a single check still carries meaningful score share. Do NOT split SQL blocks into multiple queries to hit the count - that breaks the engine.  3. Optional polish (low priority, author discretion): 5.6 and 5.7 each have a block sitting at the 3-checkpoint floor (5.6 reserve/shortfall logic_input; 5.7 sanctions fuzzy-match logic_input at ADVANCED difficulty). Adding one reconciling field/checkpoint each would harden grading granularity, especially for the advanced-labelled 5.7 block.  4. Optional difficulty balancing (author discretion): 5.5 stacks two advanced blocks and 5.4 has no basic warm-up. If these target mid-level analysts rather than senior specialists, consider softening one advanced block in 5.5 to intermediate. Not required.  5. Verify pillar->block assignment for 5.8 (and any blueprint with two same-engine blocks): with 3 pillars and 4 blocks one pillar holds two blocks; confirm the doubled blocks (e.g. 5.8's two logic_input blocks, 5.7's two logic_input blocks, 5.2's two spreadsheet blocks) are distributed so no pillar is left with a single thin block while another holds three. This is not visible in the compact view and should be checked in the full blueprints before sign-off.

### 5.1 Corporate & Commercial Credit Underwriting

Sandbox blueprint for Corporate & Commercial Credit Underwriting (node 5.1, banking). The function's skills_en was empty, so I proposed 6 GCC-grounded underwriting skills (financial-statement spreading & ratio analysis, debt-service & cash-flow analysis, credit risk rating / PD-LGD-EAD, covenant & facility structuring, security & collateral coverage, portfolio risk & regulatory capital). The function is strongly quantitative, so engine fit is excellent. Design: 3 pillars / 4 blocks across 3 engines (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql). Block 1 (spreadsheet, intermediate) spreads a borrower's statements into the core underwriting ratios (leverage, current, interest cover, DSCR, gearing) - cell_value checks. Block 2 (advanced_spreadsheet, advanced) builds a two-variable DSCR sensitivity data table across EBITDA-margin and interest-rate shocks - is_array_formula + corner/centre cell_values. Block 3 (logic_input, intermediate) computes expected loss and Basel risk-weighted capital (PD x LGD x EAD, EL, RWA at 8%, security shortfall) - logic_value checks that reconcile. Block 4 (sql, basic) interrogates a corporate loan-book table to return watchlist/past-due exposure aggregated by sector, highest first - sql_result_match. Frameworks referenced: Basel III/IV (CBUAE/SAMA-aligned), IFRS 9 ECL, IAS 1/7, RMA/Moody's credit-spreading conventions.

**Skills:** Financial Statement Spreading & Ratio Analysis · Debt-Service Capacity & Cash-Flow Analysis · Credit Risk Rating (PD / LGD / EAD) & IFRS 9 ECL · Covenant Design & Facility Structuring · Security, Collateral Coverage & Loss-Given-Default · Portfolio Risk Monitoring & Regulatory Capital (Basel)

**Engine fit:** Excellent fit across all four engines - corporate credit underwriting is intrinsically quantitative (ratio spreading, DSCR/cash-flow, PD/LGD/EAD expected-loss math, Basel RWA, loan-book interrogation), so no soft-skill proxy is needed. Block 1 uses spreadsheet for statement spreading into the standard underwriting ratio set (graded on exact ratio cell values with tolerance). Block 2 uses advanced_spreadsheet for a two-variable DSCR stress table (graded on the native data table being present AND its corner/centre values - the defensible test of whether the candidate can build a real sensitivity grid rather than hardcode it). Block 3 uses logic_input for the expected-loss / regulatory-capital chain (EL = PD x LGD x EAD, RWA, capital charge, collateral shortfall - each a named numeric field that must reconcile). Block 4 uses sql over a seeded corporate loan-book to aggregate at-risk exposure by sector (result-set match, order-sensitive). The only non-gradable parts of real underwriting (the written credit memo / recommendation narrative and qualitative management-quality judgement) are deliberately excluded; the blueprint measures the analytical spine that those judgements must rest on.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Credit Analysis & Financial Spreading**

- **Borrower Financial Spreading & Underwriting Ratios** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 18 min · ref: RMA / Moody's credit-spreading conventions; IAS 1 & IAS 7 presentation
  - _Measures:_ Ability to spread a borrower's audited statements into the core corporate-credit ratios (leverage, current ratio, quick ratio, interest coverage, DSCR proxy, debt-to-equity gearing) accurately and in the conventional underwriting form.
  - _Scenario:_ Gulf Steel Trading LLC (Dubai) has applied for a AED 40m revolving facility. The credit analyst is handed the FY2025 audited statements (AED 000s): Revenue 180,000; EBITDA 27,000; Depreciation & Amortisation 9,000; EBIT 18,000; Interest Expense 6,000; Net Income 9,600; Current Assets 84,000 (of which Inventory 36,000); Current Liabilities 56,000; Total Debt 90,000; Total Equity 60,000; Total Assets 210,000. Spread these into the standard underwriting ratio block so the credit file carries the leverage, liquidity, coverage and gearing metrics the committee requires. The candidate completes the editable ratio cells; raw figures are given.
  - _Model answer:_ Net Debt/EBITDA leverage = Total Debt / EBITDA = 90,000 / 27,000 = 3.33x (B14). Current ratio = Current Assets / Current Liabilities = 84,000 / 56,000 = 1.50 (B15). Quick (acid-test) ratio = (Current Assets - Inventory) / Current Liabilities = (84,000 - 36,000) / 56,000 = 48,000 / 56,000 = 0.857 (B16). Interest coverage (EBIT basis) = EBIT / Interest = 18,000 / 6,000 = 3.00x (B17). EBITDA interest coverage = EBITDA / Interest = 27,000 / 6,000 = 4.50x (B18). Debt-to-Equity gearing = Total Debt / Total Equity = 90,000 / 60,000 = 1.50 (B19). All values rounded to 2 decimals; tolerance absorbs rounding.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Net Debt / EBITDA leverage = 3.33x (B14) - Computes the headline leverage ratio (Total Debt / EBITDA) - the primary covenant metric
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Current ratio = 1.50 (B15) - Computes liquidity as Current Assets / Current Liabilities
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Quick (acid-test) ratio = 0.86 (B16) - Strips inventory from current assets before the liquidity test
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Interest coverage (EBIT) = 3.00x (B17) - Computes EBIT / Interest debt-service headroom
    - `cell_value` (w1) - EBITDA interest coverage = 4.50x (B18) - Computes the cash-basis coverage variant used in covenant setting
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Debt-to-Equity gearing = 1.50 (B19) - Computes capital-structure gearing (Total Debt / Equity)

**Pillar - Debt-Service Capacity & Stress Testing**

- **DSCR Two-Variable Stress Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18 min · ref: AFP / Basel III ICAAP stress-testing principles; CBUAE prudential guidance
  - _Measures:_ Ability to construct a genuine two-variable sensitivity (data) table to stress debt-service coverage against profitability and rate shocks - the core lending stress-test artefact, built natively rather than by manual recomputation.
  - _Scenario:_ For the same Gulf Steel facility the committee wants the debt-service coverage ratio stressed simultaneously across EBITDA margin and the lending interest rate. Base case (AED 000s): Revenue 180,000; EBITDA margin 15.0% (so EBITDA = 27,000); annual principal amortisation 12,000; outstanding debt 90,000; interest rate 6.5%. DSCR = EBITDA / (Interest + Principal) where Interest = Debt x rate. Build the base DSCR cell, then a two-variable data table with EBITDA margin down the rows (13%, 15%, 17%) and interest rate across the columns (6.0%, 6.5%, 7.5%). It MUST be a native data table, not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Base DSCR (B8) = EBITDA / (Debt x rate + Principal) = 27,000 / (90,000 x 0.065 + 12,000) = 27,000 / (5,850 + 12,000) = 27,000 / 17,850 = 1.513. Corner formula (B10) links to B8. Two-variable data table over the 3x3 grid, row input = EBITDA margin cell, column input = interest-rate cell, with EBITDA = Revenue x margin. Low corner C11 (margin 13%, rate 6.0%): EBITDA = 180,000 x 0.13 = 23,400; debt service = 90,000 x 0.06 + 12,000 = 5,400 + 12,000 = 17,400; DSCR = 23,400 / 17,400 = 1.345. Centre D12 (margin 15%, rate 6.5%) = base = 1.513. High-stress corner E13 (margin 17%, rate 7.5%): EBITDA = 180,000 x 0.17 = 30,600; debt service = 90,000 x 0.075 + 12,000 = 6,750 + 12,000 = 18,750; DSCR = 30,600 / 18,750 = 1.632. (Rows = margin, columns = rate; tolerance 0.01.)
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Stress grid C11:E13 uses a native data table (not hardcoded) - The 3x3 DSCR grid is driven by a native {=TABLE()} data table rather than typed-in numbers
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base DSCR = 1.51 (B8) - Computes base-case DSCR = EBITDA / (interest + principal)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Worst-case corner C11 = 1.35 (margin 13%, rate 6.0%) - Lowest-margin / lowest-rate stress cell resolves correctly via the table
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre D12 = 1.51 (margin 15%, rate 6.5%) - Base-case cell reproduced inside the data table
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High-margin corner E13 = 1.63 (margin 17%, rate 7.5%) - Highest-margin / highest-rate stress cell resolves correctly via the table

**Pillar - Risk Quantification & Portfolio Oversight**

- **Expected Loss & Regulatory Capital Computation** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: Basel III/IV IRB approach; IFRS 9 Expected Credit Loss
  - _Measures:_ Ability to apply the expected-loss and regulatory-capital chain (PD x LGD x EAD, collateral shortfall, RWA, 8% capital charge) that converts a single underwriting decision into provisioning and capital numbers.
  - _Scenario:_ The credit committee must size the expected loss and regulatory capital on the Gulf Steel exposure. Inputs: Exposure at Default (EAD) = AED 40,000,000 (fully drawn revolver); through-the-cycle Probability of Default (PD) = 2.5%; the facility is secured by property valued at AED 28,000,000 with an enforceable realisation haircut already applied; Loss Given Default (LGD) = 40%. Use Basel/IFRS 9 conventions. Compute the secured-collateral shortfall, the expected loss, the risk-weighted assets at a 100% corporate risk weight, and the minimum capital charge at the 8% total-capital ratio. Enter each named field.
  - _Model answer:_ Collateral shortfall (unsecured exposure) = EAD - collateral value = 40,000,000 - 28,000,000 = 12,000,000 (field collateral_shortfall). Expected Loss = PD x LGD x EAD = 0.025 x 0.40 x 40,000,000 = 400,000 (field expected_loss). Risk-Weighted Assets at 100% corporate risk weight = EAD x 100% = 40,000,000 (field rwa). Minimum capital charge = RWA x 8% = 40,000,000 x 0.08 = 3,200,000 (field capital_charge). Tolerance 1 currency unit absorbs rounding.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Collateral shortfall = AED 12,000,000 - Computes unsecured exposure = EAD minus realisable collateral
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Expected Loss = AED 400,000 (PD x LGD x EAD) - Applies the IFRS 9 / Basel expected-loss identity correctly
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Risk-Weighted Assets = AED 40,000,000 (100% RW) - Applies the 100% corporate risk weight to EAD
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Minimum capital charge = AED 3,200,000 (8% of RWA) - Applies the Basel 8% minimum total-capital ratio to RWA
- **Loan-Book At-Risk Exposure Query (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · basic · 10 min · ref: IFRS 9 staging; CBUAE / SAMA credit-classification reporting
  - _Measures:_ Ability to interrogate a relational loan book to aggregate and rank non-performing / watchlist exposure by sector - the routine portfolio-monitoring query behind early-warning and IFRS 9 staging reviews.
  - _Scenario:_ The portfolio team maintains a corporate_loans table (one row per facility) with columns: id, borrower, sector, exposure (AED), status ('current','watchlist','past_due'), days_past_due. The Chief Credit Officer wants total at-risk exposure by sector - facilities NOT in 'current' status - ranked by exposure, highest first, to prioritise the watchlist review. Write one query returning sector and total at-risk exposure.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT sector, SUM(exposure) AS at_risk_exposure FROM corporate_loans WHERE status <> 'current' GROUP BY sector ORDER BY at_risk_exposure DESC, sector. The WHERE clause filters out performing facilities so only watchlist + past_due rows aggregate; GROUP BY collapses to sector; ORDER BY ranks largest at-risk exposure first with sector as a deterministic tie-break. Seed data is constructed so sector totals are distinct and the ordering is unambiguous.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w2) - Result matches master (at-risk exposure per sector, highest first) - Filters to non-current facilities, aggregates exposure by sector, and orders descending - the full at-risk monitoring query

---

### 5.2 Retail Lending, Mortgages, & Consumer Credit Risk

Hands-on sandbox for retail/consumer lending and mortgage credit-risk analysts in GCC banks. The function's skills list was empty, so it was anchored to six realistic skills grounded in GCC retail-banking practice: (1) Affordability & Debt-Burden-Ratio Assessment, (2) Loan Pricing & Amortization Mechanics, (3) Mortgage LTV & Eligibility (Central-Bank caps), (4) Application & Behavioural Credit Scoring / PD, (5) IFRS 9 Expected Credit Loss (PD x LGD x EAD, staging), (6) Portfolio Credit-Risk Analytics (vintage, roll-rate, delinquency, NPL). The blueprint splits into three pillars and four blocks across three engines: an EMI/amortization spreadsheet, a DBR + Central-Bank-cap affordability decision via logic_input, an IFRS 9 ECL staging-and-provision model via spreadsheet (12m vs lifetime), and a portfolio delinquency/NPL interrogation via SQL. Every task is quantitative and auto-gradable on exact numeric outputs / result-set match. Frameworks referenced: CBUAE Retail Regulations (50% DBR cap, 80% LTV first-home), SAMA Responsible Lending, IFRS 9, Basel III/IV IRB, GRI not relevant. This is a strong engine fit - consumer credit risk is intrinsically numeric.

**Skills:** Affordability & Debt-Burden-Ratio (DBR) Assessment · Loan Pricing, EMI & Amortization Mechanics · Mortgage LTV, Eligibility & Central-Bank Caps · Application/Behavioural Credit Scoring & Probability of Default · IFRS 9 Expected Credit Loss (PD x LGD x EAD) & Staging · Portfolio Credit-Risk Analytics (Vintage, Roll-Rate, Delinquency, NPL)

**Engine fit:** Excellent fit. Retail lending and consumer credit risk is one of the most quantitative banking functions, so no "soft-function proxy" was needed - every core task is natively numeric and auto-gradable. Engine mapping: (1) EMI/amortization is canonical spreadsheet work (PMT, interest/principal split, closing balance - exact cell_value checks). (2) DBR + Central-Bank affordability caps and the max-eligible-loan decision are discrete computed figures - a perfect logic_input fit (logic_value checks that must reconcile: net income x DBR cap, EMI, headroom, pass/fail flag as 1/0). (3) IFRS 9 ECL is a multi-cell model (12-month vs lifetime ECL, PD x LGD x EAD, stage allocation, total provision) - spreadsheet with cell_value checks including a staged-total cross-check. (4) Portfolio delinquency/NPL/par-30+ analytics over a loans ledger is exactly what SQL is for (sql_result_match on grouped aggregates). The sitting uses three distinct engines (spreadsheet, logic_input, sql) for variety. The only thing NOT measured here is qualitative credit judgement (e.g. narrative justification of an override) - that is intentionally out of scope because it is not auto-gradable; the sandbox measures the analytical/computational backbone that underpins those judgements.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Lending Mechanics & Affordability**

- **Personal-Loan EMI & Amortization Schedule** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: CBUAE Retail Banking Regulations / Basel III Retail Exposures
  - _Measures:_ Loan Pricing, EMI & Amortization Mechanics - reducing-balance EMI via PMT, the interest/principal split per period, the closing-balance roll-forward, and total interest cost.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Gulf Bank (UAE) issues a reducing-balance personal loan of AED 120,000 to a candidate at a flat-quoted nominal annual rate of 6.00%, repayable over 24 monthly instalments. Build the first two rows of the amortization schedule (interest portion, principal portion, closing balance) and compute the equal monthly instalment (EMI) and the total interest paid over the life of the loan on a monthly-reducing basis. Monthly rate = 6.00% / 12 = 0.50%.
  - _Model answer:_ Monthly rate i = 0.06/12 = 0.005. EMI = PMT: P*i*(1+i)^n / ((1+i)^n - 1) with P=120000, n=24 => EMI = 5,320.61 (B5). Month 1: opening 120,000; interest = 120000*0.005 = 600.00 (B8); principal = EMI - 600 = 4,720.61 (C8); closing = 120000 - 4720.61 = 115,279.39 (D8). Month 2: interest = 115279.39*0.005 = 576.40 (B9); principal = 5320.61 - 576.40 = 4,744.21 (C9); closing = 115279.39 - 4744.21 = 110,535.18 (D9). Total interest = EMI*n - P = 5320.61*24 - 120000 = 7,694.64 (B6).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Monthly EMI computed correctly (reducing-balance PMT) - EMI in B5 = 5320.61 (tolerance 1.0)
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Month-1 interest portion - B8 = 600.00 (tolerance 0.5)
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Month-1 closing balance - D8 = 115279.39 (tolerance 1.0)
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Month-2 interest on reduced balance - B9 = 576.40 (tolerance 0.5)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Month-2 closing balance - D9 = 110535.18 (tolerance 1.5)
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Total interest over loan life - B6 = 7694.64 (tolerance 2.0)
- **DBR Affordability & Mortgage LTV Decision** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 9 min · ref: CBUAE Mortgage Regulation (50% DBR cap, 80% LTV first-home) / SAMA Responsible Lending
  - _Measures:_ Affordability & Debt-Burden-Ratio Assessment plus Mortgage LTV / Central-Bank-cap eligibility - reconciling eligible income, the regulatory DBR ceiling, total debt service, headroom, and the max loan the LTV cap permits.
  - _Scenario:_ A UAE-national applicant at National Capital Bank earns net monthly salary AED 32,000 plus a fixed monthly allowance of AED 3,000 (both DBR-eligible income). Existing monthly commitments: a car-loan instalment of AED 2,400 and a credit-card minimum of AED 1,100. She applies for a first home-finance facility on a property valued at AED 2,200,000. The new mortgage's proposed monthly instalment would be AED 11,500. CBUAE rules: total monthly debt service must not exceed a 50% Debt-Burden Ratio of total eligible income, and the maximum LTV for a UAE-national first home under AED 5m is 80%. Compute the affordability figures and decide whether the application passes the DBR test.
  - _Model answer:_ Eligible income = 32000 + 3000 = 35,000. DBR ceiling at 50% = 0.50*35000 = 17,500 (max total monthly debt service). Total debt service with new mortgage = 2400 + 1100 + 11500 = 15,000. DBR headroom = 17500 - 15000 = 2,500 (positive => passes). Actual DBR % = 15000/35000 = 42.857% (~42.86%). Max LTV loan = 0.80*2,200,000 = 1,760,000 (and required minimum down-payment = 2,200,000 - 1,760,000 = 440,000). DBR pass flag = 1 (passes because 15000 <= 17500).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Eligible monthly income - eligible_income field = 35000 (tolerance 0.5)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Regulatory DBR ceiling (50% of eligible income) - dbr_ceiling field = 17500 (tolerance 0.5)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total monthly debt service including new mortgage - total_debt_service field = 15000 (tolerance 0.5)
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Actual DBR percentage - actual_dbr_pct field = 42.86 (tolerance 0.1)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Maximum loan permitted under 80% LTV cap - max_ltv_loan field = 1760000 (tolerance 1)
    - `logic_value` (w3) - DBR pass/fail decision flag (1 = pass) - dbr_pass_flag field = 1 (tolerance 0.01)

**Pillar - Credit Risk Provisioning (IFRS 9)**

- **Expected Credit Loss Staging & Provision Build** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18.3 min · ref: IFRS 9 Financial Instruments (ECL) / Basel III IRB parameters
  - _Measures:_ IFRS 9 Expected Credit Loss & Staging - applying PD x LGD x EAD with the correct 12-month vs lifetime PD by stage, aggregating the provision, and computing the portfolio coverage ratio.
  - _Scenario:_ Gulf Consumer Finance must book the IFRS 9 expected-credit-loss provision on three retail exposures at period end (all AED). Exposure 1 (Stage 1, performing): EAD 500,000, 12-month PD 1.2%, LGD 45%. Exposure 2 (Stage 2, significant increase in credit risk - 35 days past due): EAD 300,000, lifetime PD 9.0%, LGD 50%. Exposure 3 (Stage 3, credit-impaired - 95 days past due): EAD 150,000, lifetime PD 100%, LGD 60%. Stage 1 uses 12-month ECL; Stages 2 and 3 use lifetime ECL. ECL = PD x LGD x EAD per exposure. Compute each exposure's ECL and the total portfolio provision, and confirm the coverage ratio (total ECL / total EAD).
  - _Model answer:_ Exp1 ECL = 0.012*0.45*500000 = 2,700 (B5). Exp2 ECL = 0.09*0.50*300000 = 13,500 (B6). Exp3 ECL = 1.00*0.60*150000 = 90,000 (B7). Total ECL = 2700 + 13500 + 90000 = 106,200 (B8). Total EAD = 500000 + 300000 + 150000 = 950,000 (B9). Coverage ratio = 106200/950000 = 11.179% (~11.18%) (B10).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Stage 1 12-month ECL - B5 = 2700 (tolerance 1)
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Stage 2 lifetime ECL - B6 = 13500 (tolerance 1)
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Stage 3 lifetime ECL (impaired) - B7 = 90000 (tolerance 1)
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Total portfolio ECL provision - B8 = 106200 (tolerance 1)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total exposure at default (EAD) - B9 = 950000 (tolerance 1)
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Portfolio coverage ratio (ECL / EAD) - B10 = 11.18 (tolerance 0.05)

**Pillar - Portfolio Risk Analytics**

- **Delinquency & NPL Interrogation of the Loan Book** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 11 min · ref: Basel III/IV NPL & Past-Due Definitions / IFRS 9 Staging
  - _Measures:_ Portfolio Credit-Risk Analytics - translating the regulatory 90+ DPD NPL definition into a filtered, grouped aggregate query over the loan book and ranking exposure by product.
  - _Scenario:_ The retail credit-risk team at Arabian Retail Bank maintains a loans ledger. Each row is one live consumer/mortgage loan with its outstanding balance, product type, and days-past-due (DPD). Regulatory convention: a loan is non-performing (NPL) when DPD >= 90. The team needs the non-performing exposure and loan count per product type to drive the IFRS 9 Stage 3 review, ranked by non-performing balance (largest first).
  - _Model answer:_ Filter the loans table to dpd >= 90 (non-performing), group by product_type, and aggregate: SELECT product_type, COUNT(*) AS npl_count, SUM(outstanding_balance) AS npl_balance FROM loans WHERE dpd >= 90 GROUP BY product_type ORDER BY npl_balance DESC, product_type. The result set must match the master on the seeded rows (e.g. Mortgage and Personal product types with their summed >=90-DPD balances, ordered by balance descending).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - NPL count and balance per product type, ranked by NPL balance descending (90+ DPD filter applied) - Result set equals master query: per-product npl_count + npl_balance over WHERE dpd>=90, ordered by npl_balance DESC

---

### 5.3 Wealth Management, Private Banking, & Advisory Services

Hands-on sandbox for Wealth Management & Private Banking measuring the quantitative core of the advisory craft: client suitability risk-scoring (logic_input), strategic asset allocation and after-fee portfolio outcome modelling (spreadsheet), an efficient-frontier-style two-variable risk/return sensitivity grid (advanced_spreadsheet), and book-of-clients suitability/concentration surveillance over a private-banking CRM (sql). Soft skills (relationship management, advisory rapport) are not gradable here; the blueprint targets the numerate decision layer that underpins every suitable recommendation - risk tolerance scoring, allocation arithmetic, fee drag, return blending, and regulatory concentration limits - all auto-gradable by exact numeric cell/field values and result-set matching. Grounded in GCC private-banking practice (AED/SAR HNWI mandates, DFSA/SCA suitability, AAOIFI for Sharia-screened sleeves) with concrete figures throughout.

**Skills:** Client Profiling & Suitability · Financial Planning · Product Selection · Portfolio Construction · Relationship Management · Regulatory Suitability

**Engine fit:** Wealth management is mostly client-facing and judgement-heavy, but its defensible core is highly numerate, so the engine fit is strong. The non-gradable slices (relationship-building, advisory narrative, rapport) are deliberately excluded; the gradable analytical slice is targeted instead: (1) Suitability profiling becomes a weighted risk-tolerance index plus a deterministic risk-band cap and a goal-funding gap - pure logic_input. (2) Portfolio construction becomes strategic asset-allocation arithmetic, weighted expected return, and after-fee (TER + advisory fee) net outcome in a spreadsheet. (3) Risk/return trade-off becomes a two-variable data table sweeping equity weight against expected return - a genuine advanced_spreadsheet array/data-table task standing in for efficient-frontier reasoning. (4) Regulatory suitability and book surveillance become SQL over a private-banking CRM: clients holding products above their risk band, single-issuer concentration breaches, and AUM/revenue rollups. The only construct NOT captured is qualitative client communication; everything measured here (suitability math, allocation, fee drag, concentration limits) is exact-numeric and auto-gradable. Honest limitation: this measures the analyst/RM-support competency of an advisor, not their interpersonal advisory skill.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Logic input, Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Client Profiling, Suitability & Financial Planning**

- **HNWI Risk-Tolerance Scoring & Suitability Banding** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DFSA COB Suitability / SCA Suitability Rules; CFA Institute IPS Standards
  - _Measures:_ Translating a client questionnaire into a defensible, weighted risk-tolerance score; applying the capacity-caps-willingness rule to set a final suitability band; and quantifying a retirement goal-funding gap via future-value compounding.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Private Wealth (DIFC) is onboarding a prospective client, Mr. Khalid Al-Marzooqi, and must produce a defensible suitability profile before any recommendation. The client questionnaire yields a weighted risk-tolerance score, the score maps to a conservative/balanced/growth risk band, and a separate goal-funding analysis tests whether his investable assets can meet a stated retirement target. Capacity (ability to bear loss) caps tolerance (willingness): the final suitability band is the LOWER of the willingness band and the capacity band. Questionnaire (each scored 1-5): Time horizon = 4, Loss reaction = 2, Investment knowledge = 3, Income stability = 5, Liquidity need = 2. Item weights: Time horizon 0.30, Loss reaction 0.25, Investment knowledge 0.15, Income stability 0.15, Liquidity need 0.15. Banding on the weighted score (1.00-5.00): <2.50 = Conservative (band code 1), 2.50 to <3.50 = Balanced (band code 2), >=3.50 = Growth (band code 3). Capacity test: investable assets AED 18,000,000; essential annual spending AED 900,000; emergency buffer required = 3 years of essential spending; capacity band = Growth(3) if (assets - buffer) / assets >= 0.80, Balanced(2) if >=0.60, else Conservative(1). Goal-funding: target retirement pot AED 30,000,000 in 12 years; assume a flat 5.5% annual net return, no further contributions; report the projected future value of the AED 18,000,000 and the funding gap (target - projected, positive = shortfall).
  - _Model answer:_ Weighted score = 4(0.30)+2(0.25)+3(0.15)+5(0.15)+2(0.15) = 1.20+0.50+0.45+0.75+0.30 = 3.20 -> Balanced, willingness band code 2. Capacity: buffer = 3 x 900,000 = 2,700,000; (18,000,000 - 2,700,000)/18,000,000 = 15,300,000/18,000,000 = 0.85 >= 0.80 -> capacity band 3 (Growth). Final suitability band = min(willingness 2, capacity 3) = 2 (Balanced). Goal-funding: projected FV = 18,000,000 x 1.055^12 = 18,000,000 x 1.901207 = 34,221,727 (approx); funding gap = 30,000,000 - 34,221,727 = -4,221,727 (negative => surplus, no shortfall). Tolerance bands on fields allow for rounding of the compounding factor.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Weighted risk-tolerance score = 3.20 - Correct weighted-average aggregation of the 5 questionnaire items against their weights
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Willingness band code = 2 (Balanced) - Correct mapping of the weighted score onto the 3-tier band thresholds
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Capacity ratio = 0.85 - Correct emergency-buffer deduction and capacity-ratio computation
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Final suitability band code = 2 - Correct application of the capacity-caps-willingness (min) rule
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Projected future value = 34,221,727 AED (+/- tolerance) - Correct future-value compounding at 5.5% over 12 years
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Funding gap = -4,221,727 AED (surplus) - Correct goal-funding gap sign and magnitude (target minus projected)

**Pillar - Portfolio Construction, Product Selection & Fee Engineering**

- **Strategic Asset Allocation & After-Fee Net Return Model** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: CFA Institute Portfolio Management / Strategic Asset Allocation; AAOIFI (Sharia-screened sleeve)
  - _Measures:_ Converting a strategic asset-allocation policy into AED position sizes, computing a weight-blended expected return, aggregating the weighted total expense ratio plus advisory fee into a total cost in currency, and modelling the after-fee one-year portfolio outcome.
  - _Scenario:_ Mr. Al-Marzooqi is confirmed as a Balanced-mandate client at Emirates Private Wealth. Build the recommended AED 18,000,000 strategic asset allocation across five sleeves and compute the blended gross expected return, the total cost (weighted TER plus a 0.75% advisory fee on AUM), and the projected net portfolio value after one year. Sleeve targets (% of AUM) and assumptions are given per row; you must fill the AED amount per sleeve, the portfolio weighted gross return, total annual fees in AED, and the year-1 net portfolio value. Sleeves: GCC Sukuk (Sharia) target 35%, expected return 4.0%, TER 0.30%; Global Investment-Grade Bonds 15%, 3.5%, 0.20%; GCC & MENA Equities 25%, 8.0%, 0.55%; Global Developed Equities 20%, 7.5%, 0.45%; Cash / Murabaha 5%, 2.0%, 0.05%. Advisory fee = 0.75% of AUM. Net value = AUM x (1 + weighted gross return) - total fees (fees charged on opening AUM).
  - _Model answer:_ Sleeve AED = weight x 18,000,000: Sukuk 6,300,000; IG Bonds 2,700,000; GCC/MENA Eq 4,500,000; Global Eq 3,600,000; Cash 900,000 (sum = 18,000,000). Weighted gross return = 0.35(4.0)+0.15(3.5)+0.25(8.0)+0.20(7.5)+0.05(2.0) = 1.40+0.525+2.00+1.50+0.10 = 5.525%. Weighted TER = 0.35(0.30)+0.15(0.20)+0.25(0.55)+0.20(0.45)+0.05(0.05) = 0.105+0.030+0.1375+0.090+0.0025 = 0.365%. Total fee % = 0.365% + 0.75% = 1.115%; total fees AED = 0.01115 x 18,000,000 = 200,700. Gross growth = 18,000,000 x 0.05525 = 994,500; net value = 18,000,000 + 994,500 - 200,700 = 18,793,800.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - GCC Sukuk sleeve = AED 6,300,000 - Correct weight-to-AED position sizing for the largest sleeve
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Allocation sums to AED 18,000,000 - Allocation fully invested with no residual / over-allocation
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Portfolio weighted gross return = 5.525% - Correct weight-blended expected return across all five sleeves
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Total annual fees = AED 200,700 - Correct weighted-TER plus advisory-fee aggregation in currency
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Year-1 net portfolio value = AED 18,793,800 - Correct after-fee net outcome (gross growth minus total fees on AUM)
- **Equity-Tilt Risk/Return Sensitivity Grid** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: AFP FP&A Body of Knowledge (FPAC); CFA Institute Asset Allocation (risk/return trade-off)
  - _Measures:_ Building a native two-variable sensitivity/data table to stress a portfolio return assumption across equity weight and equity-return inputs - the mechanical core of efficient-frontier and scenario analysis in a private-banking proposal.
  - _Scenario:_ Before locking the Balanced mandate, the advisory desk wants to see how the blended one-year expected portfolio return moves as the equity tilt and the equity expected-return assumption change - a simplified efficient-frontier trade-off view. A two-asset model is set up: Equity sleeve (variable weight) and a Defensive sleeve (Sukuk + bonds + cash) holding the remaining weight at a fixed 3.6% expected return. Portfolio return = EquityWeight x EquityReturn + (1 - EquityWeight) x 3.6%. Build a two-variable data table where the ROW axis is Equity Weight (30%, 45%, 60%) and the COLUMN axis is Equity Expected Return (6%, 8%, 10%), returning the blended portfolio expected return in each cell. It must be driven by a native data table linked to the model formula, not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Model cell: portfolio return = EqW x EqR + (1 - EqW) x 0.036. The data table corner links to the model output. Corner low (EqW 30%, EqR 6%) = 0.30(6.0)+0.70(3.6) = 1.80+2.52 = 4.32%. Base/centre (EqW 45%, EqR 8%) = 0.45(8.0)+0.55(3.6) = 3.60+1.98 = 5.58%. Corner high (EqW 60%, EqR 10%) = 0.60(10.0)+0.40(3.6) = 6.00+1.44 = 7.44%. The grid must be produced by a native {=TABLE()} data-table construct, with row input = equity weight cell and column input = equity expected-return cell.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Grid uses a native data table {=TABLE()} (not hardcoded) - Candidate built a real two-variable data table rather than typing values
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (EqW 30%, EqR 6%) = 4.32% - Correct blended return at the low equity-tilt / low equity-return corner
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre (EqW 45%, EqR 8%) = 5.58% - Correct blended return at the base-case interior cell
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (EqW 60%, EqR 10%) = 7.44% - Correct blended return at the high equity-tilt / high equity-return corner

**Pillar - Regulatory Suitability & Book Surveillance**

- **Private-Bank Book Suitability & Concentration Surveillance (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DFSA / SCA Suitability & Concentration Rules; FATF (book surveillance principles)
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating a private-banking CRM to surface regulatory suitability breaches by joining client risk profiles to holding risk ratings and filtering where the product exceeds the client's authorised band - the auto-gradable core of suitability monitoring.
  - _Scenario:_ Compliance at Emirates Private Wealth runs a quarterly suitability sweep over the private-banking book. Two tables are seeded: clients (id, full_name, risk_band 1-3 where 1=Conservative, 2=Balanced, 3=Growth, rm_name, aum) and holdings (id, client_id, product_name, product_risk 1-3, market_value, issuer). A holding is a SUITABILITY BREACH when its product_risk exceeds the client's risk_band (the client holds something riskier than their suitability profile permits). Write ONE query that returns every breaching holding: the client full_name, product_name, the client's risk_band, the product_risk, and the market_value - ordered by market_value highest first, then full_name. Columns: full_name, product_name, risk_band, product_risk, market_value.
  - _Model answer:_ Join holdings to clients on client_id, filter where holdings.product_risk > clients.risk_band, select the five required columns, and order by market_value DESC then full_name ASC. SELECT c.full_name, h.product_name, c.risk_band, h.product_risk, h.market_value FROM holdings h JOIN clients c ON c.id = h.client_id WHERE h.product_risk > c.risk_band ORDER BY h.market_value DESC, c.full_name. The seed data is crafted so several holdings breach (e.g. a Conservative band-1 client holding a band-3 equity fund, a Balanced band-2 client holding a band-3 structured note) and several are compliant, so the WHERE filter is genuinely load-bearing.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Breaching holdings match master (correct rows, columns, and order) - Correct join, suitability-breach filter (product_risk > risk_band), column projection, and DESC market_value ordering
