### 5.4 Global Markets, Asset Liability Management (ALM), & Liquidity Risk

Hands-on sandbox for Global Markets, ALM & Liquidity Risk. Function had an empty skills list, so I proposed 6 GCC-banking skills (Basel III LCR/NSFR, IRRBB repricing-gap & NII sensitivity, liquidity stress testing & survival horizon, FX/markets position & NOP, funds-transfer-pricing/behavioural maturity, regulatory liquidity reporting). 3 pillars, 4 blocks, 3 engines (logic_input, spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, sql), mixed difficulty. Every block uses concrete AED/SAR figures and real frameworks (Basel III, BCBS IRRBB, SAMA/CBUAE liquidity rules). 18 weighted checkpoints total. All numeric and auto-gradable - excellent engine fit.

**Skills:** Basel III Liquidity Ratios (LCR & NSFR) · Interest-Rate Risk in the Banking Book (IRRBB) - Repricing Gap & NII Sensitivity · Liquidity Stress Testing & Survival Horizon · Global Markets - FX Position, Net Open Position & Money-Market Pricing · Funds Transfer Pricing & Behavioural Maturity Profiling · Regulatory Liquidity Reporting & Cashflow Bucketing

**Engine fit:** Strong fit for all four engines - this is a deeply quantitative treasury/markets function. The proposed skills (Basel III liquidity ratios, IRRBB repricing-gap analysis, FX/markets pricing, liquidity stress testing, NII sensitivity) are all formula- and table-driven, so they grade cleanly on cell_value / is_array_formula / logic_value / sql_result_match. Block 1 (LCR & NSFR) uses logic_input for the multi-step Basel III ratio build (HQLA haircuts, ASF/RSF factors). Block 2 (repricing-gap / NII sensitivity) uses spreadsheet for the time-bucketed gap ladder and earnings-at-risk. Block 3 (2-var liquidity stress matrix) uses advanced_spreadsheet for a native data table flexing run-off and haircut shocks against the survival-horizon / LCR surface. Block 4 (markets/treasury deal blotter) uses sql to aggregate FX and money-market positions, net open position, and concentration. No soft/ungradable content - the whole sitting is numeric. The only honest limitation: real ALM also requires qualitative governance judgement (board risk-appetite calibration, contingency funding plan narrative) which is out of scope here; this sandbox measures the computational core, not the policy narrative.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Logic input, Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Regulatory Liquidity & Funding Ratios**

- **Basel III LCR & NSFR Construction** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: Basel III (BCBS 238 LCR / BCBS 295 NSFR), CBUAE / SAMA Liquidity Rules
  - _Measures:_ Computing Basel III LCR and NSFR with correct HQLA haircuts, Level 2 / Level 2B caps, weighted run-off rates, and ASF/RSF factor application.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Gulf Bank (Abu Dhabi) Treasury must report its Liquidity Coverage Ratio and Net Stable Funding Ratio to the regulator. HQLA holdings (AED m): Level 1 - Cash & central-bank reserves AED 4,000, UAE sovereign sukuk AED 6,000 (0% haircut). Level 2A - GCC sovereign / 20%-RW bonds AED 3,000 (15% haircut). Level 2B - qualifying corporate bonds AED 2,000 (50% haircut). Apply the Basel caps: Level 2 assets after haircut are capped at 40% of total HQLA, and Level 2B (after haircut) is capped at 15% of total HQLA. Stressed 30-day cash outflows: retail stable deposits AED 20,000 at 5% run-off, retail less-stable deposits AED 10,000 at 10%, operational wholesale deposits AED 8,000 at 25%, non-operational wholesale AED 12,000 at 40%. Stressed 30-day cash inflows AED 4,500 (already within the 75%-of-outflows cap). For NSFR: Available Stable Funding (ASF) - Tier 1 capital AED 9,000 at 100%, retail/SME deposits AED 30,000 at 90%, non-financial corporate funding AED 15,000 at 50%. Required Stable Funding (RSF) - Level 1 HQLA AED 10,000 at 5%, performing residential mortgages AED 18,000 at 65%, other loans >1yr AED 12,000 at 85%. Compute every labelled field.
  - _Model answer:_ Adjusted HQLA: L1 = 4000+6000 = 10000. L2A after haircut = 3000*0.85 = 2550. L2B after haircut = 2000*0.50 = 1000. Level 2B cap = 15% of total HQLA; Level 2 cap = 40% of total HQLA. With pre-cap total = 10000+2550+1000 = 13550, the 40% cap on Level 2 = (40/60)*L1 binding test: max Level 2 = 10000*40/60 = 6666.7, actual L2 = 3550 < cap, and L2B 1000 < 15% test (1000 <= (15/85)*L1 => 1764.7), so no cap binds. Total HQLA = 13,550. Total weighted outflows = 20000*0.05 + 10000*0.10 + 8000*0.25 + 12000*0.40 = 1000+1000+2000+4800 = 8,800. Inflow cap 75% of outflows = 6,600; actual inflows 4,500 < cap so net outflows = 8800-4500 = 4,300. LCR = 13550/4300 = 315.1%. ASF = 9000*1.0 + 30000*0.90 + 15000*0.50 = 9000+27000+7500 = 43,500. RSF = 10000*0.05 + 18000*0.65 + 12000*0.85 = 500+11700+10200 = 22,400. NSFR = 43500/22400 = 194.2%.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total adjusted HQLA after haircuts & caps (AED m) = 13,550 - Correct HQLA haircut application and verification that Level 2 / Level 2B caps do not bind
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total weighted 30-day cash outflows (AED m) = 8,800 - Correct run-off rate applied to each deposit category
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Net cash outflows after inflow cap (AED m) = 4,300 - Inflow 75%-cap logic and net-outflow derivation
    - `logic_value` (w3) - LCR (%) = 315.1 - Final LCR ratio computed correctly
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Available Stable Funding total (AED m) = 43,500 - Correct ASF factor weighting across capital and funding sources
    - `logic_value` (w2) - NSFR (%) = 194.2 - Final NSFR ratio (ASF / RSF) computed correctly

**Pillar - Interest-Rate Risk & Liquidity Stress Modeling**

- **Repricing-Gap Ladder & Earnings-at-Risk** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 15 min · ref: BCBS d368 (IRRBB Standards) / SAMA IRRBB Guidelines
  - _Measures:_ Constructing a repricing-gap ladder, computing periodic and cumulative gaps, and translating the gap into a delta-NII earnings-at-risk estimate under a parallel rate shock.
  - _Scenario:_ Build the time-bucketed repricing-gap ladder for Saudi National Markets Bank (Riyadh) banking book (SAR m) and estimate the 12-month Net Interest Income sensitivity to a +200bp parallel rate shock. Rate-sensitive assets repricing within 12 months: floating loans SAR 24,000, money-market placements SAR 6,000, investment securities SAR 4,000. Rate-sensitive liabilities repricing within 12 months: term deposits SAR 18,000, interbank borrowing SAR 9,000, savings deposits (rate-sensitive portion) SAR 5,000. Complete the gap row (RSA - RSL), the cumulative gap, and the NII impact = cumulative 12-month gap x rate shock. Rate shock = +200bp = +0.0200.
  - _Model answer:_ Total RSA(<=12m) = 24000+6000+4000 = 34,000. Total RSL(<=12m) = 18000+9000+5000 = 32,000. Periodic/cumulative 12-month repricing gap = 34000-32000 = +2,000 (asset-sensitive). Delta-NII for +200bp = gap * shock = 2000 * 0.0200 = +40 SAR m. Because the gap is positive (asset-sensitive), rising rates increase NII. RSA total in B-cell, RSL total, gap, and NII impact are each graded.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total rate-sensitive assets <=12m (SAR m) = 34,000 - Correct summation of rate-sensitive assets in the 12-month bucket
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total rate-sensitive liabilities <=12m (SAR m) = 32,000 - Correct summation of rate-sensitive liabilities
    - `cell_value` (w3) - 12-month repricing gap (RSA - RSL) = +2,000 - Gap computed with correct sign (asset-sensitive position)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Cumulative 12-month gap = +2,000 - Cumulative gap roll-up equals periodic gap for a single bucket
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Delta-NII under +200bp shock (SAR m) = +40 - Earnings-at-risk = cumulative gap x rate shock, correct magnitude and sign
- **Two-Variable Liquidity Stress Surface** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18.3 min · ref: Basel III Liquidity Monitoring Tools (BCBS 238) / CBUAE Liquidity Stress Testing
  - _Measures:_ Building a native two-variable data table that flexes a liquidity-stress model across run-off and haircut shock axes, demonstrating array-formula construction and stress-surface interpretation.
  - _Scenario:_ Doha Mercantile Bank (Qatar) Treasury must stress its post-shock liquidity buffer (QAR m). Base inputs: Liquid asset buffer (HQLA) QAR 15,000 before haircut; total stable deposit base QAR 40,000. The stressed net cash outflow = deposit base x deposit run-off rate. The post-stress buffer (numerator) = HQLA x (1 - HQLA haircut). Compute the single-cell stressed LCR proxy = post-stress buffer / stressed net outflow. Then build a two-variable data table for this stressed LCR proxy across a deposit run-off axis (columns: 8%, 10%, 12%) and an HQLA haircut axis (rows: 10%, 15%, 20%). The table must be a native data table driven by the model cell, not hardcoded values.
  - _Model answer:_ Stressed net outflow = 40000 * run-off. Post-stress buffer = 15000 * (1 - haircut). Stressed LCR proxy = buffer / outflow. Base cell (run-off 10%, haircut 15%) = (15000*0.85)/(40000*0.10) = 12750/4000 = 3.1875 (318.75%). Data-table corners: low-stress corner (run-off 8%, haircut 10%) = (15000*0.90)/(40000*0.08) = 13500/3200 = 4.21875. High-stress corner (run-off 12%, haircut 20%) = (15000*0.80)/(40000*0.12) = 12000/4800 = 2.50000. Centre (run-off 10%, haircut 15%) = 3.1875. The data table must be present as a native {=TABLE()} array; corner and centre cells graded on value.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Stress surface uses a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - Candidate built a real data table array, not pasted constants
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Base model cell stressed-LCR proxy = 3.1875 - Driver cell computes buffer/outflow correctly before the table
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low-stress corner (run-off 8%, haircut 10%) = 4.21875 - Best-case stress cell value
    - `cell_value` (w2) - High-stress corner (run-off 12%, haircut 20%) = 2.50000 - Worst-case stress cell value
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre cell (run-off 10%, haircut 15%) = 3.1875 - Interior cell value reconciles with the base model

**Pillar - Global Markets Position & Treasury Data Interrogation**

- **FX & Money-Market Blotter Aggregation (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: Basel III Market Risk (FRTB) Net Open Position / ACI FMA Treasury Standards
  - _Measures:_ Aggregating a markets deal blotter with GROUP BY and ORDER BY to surface currency-pair concentration - the data-interrogation core of position and net-open-position monitoring.
  - _Scenario:_ Kuwait Continental Bank's Global Markets desk maintains a deals blotter in table fx_deals (id int, ccy_pair text, side text, notional_usd numeric, pnl_usd numeric, desk text, trade_date date). The seeded data holds FX spot and money-market trades across the G10 and GCC desks. The risk manager needs the net traded notional exposure per currency-pair, ranked by total notional descending, to identify concentration in the open position. Write ONE query returning each ccy_pair and its total notional (column alias total_notional), highest first.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT ccy_pair, SUM(notional_usd) AS total_notional FROM fx_deals GROUP BY ccy_pair ORDER BY total_notional DESC, ccy_pair. Result set is ordered (highest notional first), grouping rolls every deal in a pair into one row; the master query is the comparison target with order-sensitive matching.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Query returns total notional per currency pair, highest first (ordered) - Correct GROUP BY ccy_pair, SUM(notional_usd), and descending ORDER BY matching the master result set exactly

### 5.5 Corporate Banking Transaction Services & Trade Finance

Sandbox blueprint for Corporate Banking Transaction Services & Trade Finance (node 5.5, banking domain). The source function has an empty skills list and no descriptor, so I first proposed six GCC-grounded skills (Documentary Credits & UCP 600; Trade Finance Pricing & Yield; Cash Management, Liquidity Sweeps & Notional Pooling; Working Capital & Supply Chain Finance; Guarantees, Collections & Documentary Compliance; Transaction Banking MIS) and designed to them. This is a strongly quantitative function, so all four blocks grade cleanly. Three pillars, four blocks, three engines: (1) Trade Finance Structuring & Pricing - a logic_input block computing LC bill-discounting proceeds/yield and a spreadsheet block building a working-capital / cash-conversion-cycle and supply-chain-finance economics model; (2) Liquidity & Cash Management Engineering - an advanced_spreadsheet block building a two-variable interest-benefit sensitivity table over a notional cash-pooling structure (native data table + corner/interior cell checks); (3) Transaction Banking Portfolio Interrogation - a sql block aggregating a trade-finance facilities ledger by product to find tenor-weighted exposure and fee income. Concrete GCC figures throughout (Emirates NBD / SNB / Mashreq-style corporate clients, AED/SAR amounts, real LC/guarantee mechanics). Frameworks: ICC UCP 600, ICC URDG 758, ICC URC 522, Basel III LCR, AFP/CTP treasury practice, DAMA DMBOK. Difficulty mixed basic->advanced.

**Skills:** Documentary Credits (LCs) & UCP 600 Compliance · Trade Finance Pricing, Discounting & Yield · Cash Management, Liquidity Sweeps & Notional Pooling · Working Capital & Supply Chain Finance (CCC / Receivables Financing) · Guarantees, Collections & Documentary Compliance (URDG 758 / URC 522) · Transaction Banking MIS & Portfolio Interrogation

**Engine fit:** Strong fit - this is a quantitative transaction-banking / trade-finance function whose core work (pricing LCs and discounting bills, sizing the cash-conversion cycle and supply-chain-finance economics, modelling liquidity-pooling interest benefit, and interrogating a facilities ledger) is inherently numeric and maps cleanly to three of the four auto-gradable engines. logic_input carries the discrete trade-finance pricing math (discount proceeds, effective yield, commission/tenor arithmetic) where exact named-field answers reconcile; spreadsheet carries the linked working-capital + SCF model (cell_value checks on DSO/DPO/DIO, CCC, and financing-cost outputs); advanced_spreadsheet carries a genuine two-variable sensitivity data table on the notional-pooling interest benefit (is_array_formula plus corner/centre cell_value checks, exactly mirroring the FP&A reference); sql carries the portfolio MIS slice (tenor-weighted exposure and fee income per trade product, ordered). The only non-gradable parts of the real role - UCP 600 document examination judgement, discrepancy waivers, and AML/sanctions narrative on trade transactions - are deliberately out of scope here; they belong to an MCQ layer and human review, and are not faked into the sandbox. No engine limitation flag needed: every block measures demonstrated computation, not prose.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Logic input, Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Trade Finance Structuring & Pricing**

- **LC Bill Discounting - Proceeds & Effective Yield** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: ICC UCP 600 / ISBP 821 (documentary credit usance bill mechanics)
  - _Measures:_ Usance LC discounting arithmetic: flat commission on face value, actual/360 simple-interest discount over tenor, net-proceeds build, and effective annualised cost - the core pricing a transaction-banking trade officer must reconcile before booking.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Steel Industries (Abu Dhabi) presents a complying set of documents under a 120-day usance Letter of Credit for AED 3,000,000 issued by First Abu Dhabi Bank and confirmed by your desk. The exporter requests discounting of the accepted draft today. Your trade desk discounts on a simple-interest basis (actual/360 day count). Confirmation/acceptance commission is 0.85% flat on the face value, deducted up front. The discount rate is 6.50% per annum applied over the 120-day tenor. Compute: (1) the acceptance commission in AED; (2) the discount charge in AED over the 120-day tenor on the full face value (actual/360); (3) the net proceeds paid to the exporter today after deducting BOTH the acceptance commission and the discount charge; (4) the effective annualised cost to the exporter expressed as a percentage = (total charges / net proceeds) x (360 / 120) x 100, rounded to two decimals.
  - _Model answer:_ Face = 3,000,000. (1) Acceptance commission = 3,000,000 x 0.85% = 25,500. (2) Discount charge = 3,000,000 x 6.50% x 120/360 = 3,000,000 x 0.065 x 0.333333 = 65,000. (3) Total charges = 25,500 + 65,000 = 90,500; net proceeds = 3,000,000 - 90,500 = 2,909,500. (4) Effective annualised cost = (90,500 / 2,909,500) x (360/120) x 100 = 0.0311050 x 3 x 100 = 9.33%.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Acceptance commission (AED) = 25,500 - Flat commission computed on LC face value (0.85% x 3,000,000)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Discount charge (AED) = 65,000 - Actual/360 simple-interest discount over the 120-day usance tenor (3,000,000 x 6.5% x 120/360)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Net proceeds to exporter (AED) = 2,909,500 - Net build subtracts BOTH commission and discount from face value
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Effective annualised cost (%) = 9.33 - Total-charges-over-net-proceeds annualised on a 360/120 basis, reconciling all components
- **Working-Capital Cycle & Supply-Chain-Finance Economics** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · advanced · 16.7 min · ref: AFP / CTP Treasury body of knowledge (cash conversion cycle & supplier finance)
  - _Measures:_ Builds a linked working-capital diagnostic (DIO/DSO/DPO and CCC) and prices a supply-chain-finance early-payment - the analytics a transaction-banking SCF structurer runs to size a programme and quote a supplier.
  - _Scenario:_ Almarai Co (Riyadh) is a SCF programme anchor on your bank's payables platform. From the FY figures (SAR 000s): Annual COGS 14,600,000; Annual Credit Sales 19,710,000; Average Inventory 2,000,000; Average Accounts Receivable 2,700,000; Average Accounts Payable 1,200,000. Use a 365-day year. The bank offers a supplier early-payment programme: a supplier with a SAR 5,000,000 approved invoice due in 90 days takes early payment today at a discount margin of 4.20% per annum (actual/360 simple interest) charged for the full 90 remaining days. Complete the model: compute DIO, DSO, DPO, the Cash Conversion Cycle (CCC = DIO + DSO - DPO), the SCF early-payment discount cost in SAR (5,000,000 x 4.20% x 90/360), and the amount the supplier receives today (invoice less discount cost).
  - _Model answer:_ DIO = Avg Inventory / COGS x 365 = 2,000,000/14,600,000 x 365 = 50.00 days. DSO = Avg AR / Credit Sales x 365 = 2,700,000/19,710,000 x 365 = 50.00 days. DPO = Avg AP / COGS x 365 = 1,200,000/14,600,000 x 365 = 30.00 days. CCC = 50 + 50 - 30 = 70.00 days. SCF discount cost = 5,000,000 x 4.20% x 90/360 = 5,000,000 x 0.042 x 0.25 = 52,500. Supplier receives today = 5,000,000 - 52,500 = 4,947,500.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - DIO (days) = 50.00 - Days Inventory Outstanding = Avg Inventory / COGS x 365
    - `cell_value` (w1) - DSO (days) = 50.00 - Days Sales Outstanding = Avg AR / Credit Sales x 365
    - `cell_value` (w1) - DPO (days) = 30.00 - Days Payable Outstanding = Avg AP / COGS x 365
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Cash Conversion Cycle (days) = 70.00 - CCC = DIO + DSO - DPO, linked to the three component cells
    - `cell_value` (w2) - SCF early-payment discount cost (SAR) = 52,500 - Actual/360 discount on the approved invoice over the 90-day remaining tenor
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Amount supplier receives today (SAR) = 4,947,500 - Invoice face less the early-payment discount cost

**Pillar - Liquidity & Cash Management Engineering**

- **Notional Cash-Pool Interest Benefit - Two-Variable Sensitivity** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: Basel III LCR / AFP CTP liquidity-structures practice (notional pooling)
  - _Measures:_ Constructs a genuine two-variable sensitivity (data) table on a liquidity-pooling interest-benefit model using native array mechanics - the stress view a cash-management structurer presents when sizing a notional-pool proposal.
  - _Scenario:_ Majid Al Futtaim Holding (Dubai) runs a multi-entity AED notional cash pool with your bank. Without pooling, debit balances are charged a credit-interest spread and surplus balances earn little. The annual net interest benefit of pooling is modelled as: Benefit = Offset Balance (AED) x Spread (%), where Spread is the saved margin between the debit rate and the surplus rate. Base inputs: Offset Balance AED 80,000,000; Spread 2.50%, giving a base benefit. Build a two-variable data table for the annual interest benefit (AED) across Spread columns of 2.00% / 2.50% / 3.00% and Offset-Balance rows of 60,000,000 / 80,000,000 / 100,000,000. It must use a native data table driving off the Benefit = Offset x Spread formula, not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Base Benefit cell = 80,000,000 x 2.50% = 2,000,000. The data table corner links to the Benefit formula; row input = Offset Balance, column input = Spread. Low corner (Offset 60,000,000, Spread 2.00%) = 60,000,000 x 0.02 = 1,200,000. Centre (Offset 80,000,000, Spread 2.50%) = 80,000,000 x 0.025 = 2,000,000. High corner (Offset 100,000,000, Spread 3.00%) = 100,000,000 x 0.03 = 3,000,000.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sensitivity grid uses a native data table {=TABLE()} (not hardcoded) - The interior grid is driven by a native two-variable data table referencing the Benefit formula
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Base Benefit cell (AED) = 2,000,000 - Benefit = Offset Balance x Spread (80,000,000 x 2.50%)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (Offset 60M, Spread 2.00%) = 1,200,000 - Data-table low corner recomputes Benefit at the minimum offset and spread
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre (Offset 80M, Spread 2.50%) = 2,000,000 - Data-table centre cell equals the base case
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (Offset 100M, Spread 3.00%) = 3,000,000 - Data-table high corner recomputes Benefit at the maximum offset and spread

**Pillar - Transaction Banking Portfolio Interrogation**

- **Trade-Finance Facilities Ledger - Product Exposure & Fee Income** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA International (DMBOK) / ICC URDG 758 & URC 522 product taxonomy
  - _Measures:_ Aggregates a trade-finance facilities ledger into a product-level portfolio MIS slice (exposure and fee income per instrument type, ranked) - the data interrogation a transaction-banking analyst runs to steer the book.
  - _Scenario:_ Your transaction-banking MIS holds a trade_facilities table of outstanding instruments booked for GCC corporates (product types: import_lc, export_lc, guarantee, documentary_collection, scf). Each row carries the instrument's outstanding exposure in AED and the fee income earned on it. The trade head wants a product-level portfolio view to decide where to push next quarter. Write ONE query returning, per product type, the total outstanding exposure and the total fee income, ordered by total exposure from highest to lowest. Columns: product_type, total_exposure, total_fee.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT product_type, SUM(exposure_aed) AS total_exposure, SUM(fee_income_aed) AS total_fee FROM trade_facilities GROUP BY product_type ORDER BY total_exposure DESC, product_type. Seed has clustered rows so import_lc carries the largest aggregate exposure, followed by guarantee, export_lc, scf, documentary_collection; grouping then descending-exposure ordering yields the ranked product view, with product_type as a deterministic tiebreaker.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master: per-product total exposure and fee income, ordered by exposure descending - Correct GROUP BY product_type with SUM aggregates on both exposure and fee, ordered highest-exposure-first (order-sensitive)

### 5.6 Core Banking Systems Operations & Clearinghouse Mechanics

Hands-on sandbox blueprint for the back-office banking-operations function that runs the core banking system and connects the bank to national clearing/settlement infrastructure (CBUAE UAEFTS, SAMA SARIE/RTGS, SWIFT ISO 20022). The function's skills list was empty, so six realistic GCC banking-operations skills were proposed, then designed to. The function is intrinsically quantitative/operational (settlement positions, reserve/liquidity math, batch posting reconciliation, exception SLAs), so it fits all four engines cleanly with no soft-function proxy needed. Blueprint = 3 pillars / 4 blocks across 3 engines: (1) Clearing & Settlement Mechanics [spreadsheet multilateral net settlement matrix; advanced_spreadsheet 2-var intraday liquidity buffer sensitivity table], (2) Reserve & Liquidity Operations [logic_input CBUAE reserve-requirement + intraday liquidity shortfall], (3) Transaction Lifecycle & Exception Interrogation [sql over a core-banking settlement-leg ledger for failed/returned-item exposure].

**Skills:** Payment Clearing & Multilateral Net Settlement (RTGS/ACH) · Nostro/Vostro & GL Settlement Reconciliation · Intraday Liquidity & Central-Bank Reserve Management · Core Banking Batch/EOD Posting & Cut-off Control · Interbank Settlement Position Computation · Exception Handling, Returns & SLA Monitoring

**Engine fit:** Strong, native fit across all four engines - this is a quantitative, rules-driven operations function, so no soft-function proxy was needed. Multilateral net settlement is exactly a matrix/aggregation problem (spreadsheet cell_value on each bank's net position + the system-wide zero-sum balance check, mirroring FP&A's balance-check rigor). Intraday liquidity headroom across two stress drivers (peak outflow x available buffer) is a textbook two-variable sensitivity table (advanced_spreadsheet is_array_formula + corner/centre cell_values). Central-bank reserve requirement and intraday liquidity shortfall are deterministic formula chains over given figures (logic_input logic_value, with a reconciling total). The settlement-leg / returned-item ledger is a relational aggregation (sql_result_match, ordered). The only thing NOT gradable here - and deliberately out of scope - is the qualitative judgement layer (deciding whether to queue, recycle, or reject a gridlocked payment, drafting an incident RCA, regulator liaison); the sandbox measures the computational/reconciliation core that underpins those decisions, which is the defensible, auto-gradable slice.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Clearing & Settlement Mechanics**

- **Multilateral Net Settlement Position Matrix** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 18 min · ref: CBUAE UAEFTS / SWIFT ISO 20022 RTGS net-settlement convention; BIS CPMI Principles for Financial Market Infrastructures (PFMI)
  - _Measures:_ Computing each participant's multilateral net settlement position from a bilateral obligations matrix and proving the system-wide zero-sum settlement integrity check.
  - _Scenario:_ End-of-cycle clearing run on the CBUAE deferred-net-settlement (DNS) session for four UAE banks (Emirates NBD, FAB, ADCB, Mashreq). You are given the bilateral gross obligations matrix (AED 000s) where row bank OWES column bank: ENBD->FAB 4,200; ENBD->ADCB 1,800; ENBD->Mashreq 900; FAB->ENBD 3,100; FAB->ADCB 2,500; FAB->Mashreq 1,400; ADCB->ENBD 2,200; ADCB->FAB 1,900; ADCB->Mashreq 600; Mashreq->ENBD 1,300; Mashreq->FAB 1,100; Mashreq->ADCB 1,500. Complete each bank's total to-pay (sum of its row), total to-receive (sum of its column), and net settlement position (receive minus pay). A negative net = the bank must fund its settlement account; positive = it receives. The system-wide net of all four positions must equal zero (DNS is zero-sum) - this is the settlement balance check the operator must clear before releasing the batch.
  - _Model answer:_ Per bank, to-pay = row sum, to-receive = column sum, net = receive - pay. ENBD: pay 4200+1800+900=6900, receive 3100+2200+1300=6600, net -300. FAB: pay 3100+2500+1400=7000, receive 4200+1900+1100=7200, net +200. ADCB: pay 2200+1900+600=4700, receive 1800+2500+1500=5800, net +1100. Mashreq: pay 1300+1100+1500=3900, receive 900+1400+600=2900, net -1000. System net = -300+200+1100-1000 = 0 (zero-sum proof).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - ENBD net position = -300 (funding short) - Row-pay vs column-receive netting for a debtor-net bank
    - `cell_value` (w1) - FAB net position = +200 (receiver) - Net position for a small creditor-net bank
    - `cell_value` (w2) - ADCB net position = +1,100 (largest receiver) - Largest creditor net position computed correctly
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Mashreq net position = -1,000 (largest funder) - Largest debtor net position computed correctly
    - `cell_value` (w3) - System-wide net of all positions = 0 - Zero-sum DNS settlement integrity / balance check before batch release
- **Intraday Liquidity Buffer Stress Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: BCBS 248 Monitoring tools for intraday liquidity management; Basel III LCR; CBUAE intraday liquidity reporting
  - _Measures:_ Modelling intraday liquidity headroom and stress-testing it across peak-outflow and credit-line scenarios using a native two-variable data table.
  - _Scenario:_ The settlement-operations desk at a UAE bank must size its intraday liquidity headroom on the RTGS account before the morning peak. Inputs: opening RTGS balance AED 6,000 (000s); committed intraday credit line from CBUAE AED 4,000; expected gross outflows during the peak window AED 9,500; expected gross inflows AED 3,200. Build the base intraday net liquidity position = opening balance + credit line + inflows - outflows. Then build a two-variable data table showing ending headroom as PEAK OUTFLOWS vary across columns (9,000 / 9,500 / 10,000) and the COMMITTED CREDIT LINE varies across rows (3,000 / 4,000 / 5,000). The table must be a native data table driven by the base formula, not hardcoded - the operator uses it to decide whether to pre-fund.
  - _Model answer:_ Base headroom = opening 6000 + credit 4000 + inflows 3200 - outflows 9500 = 3700. Data table cell = 6000 + (row credit line) + 3200 - (col outflows). Low corner (credit 3000, outflow 10000) = 6000+3000+3200-10000 = 2200. Centre (credit 4000, outflow 9500) = 3700. High corner (credit 5000, outflow 9000) = 6000+5000+3200-9000 = 5200. Implemented as a {=TABLE()} two-input data table with column input = outflows cell, row input = credit-line cell.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base intraday net liquidity position = 3,700 - Core intraday headroom formula (opening + line + inflows - outflows)
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Stress grid uses a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - Candidate built a real {=TABLE()} array, demonstrating sensitivity-tooling skill
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Stress corner: credit 3,000 / outflow 10,000 = 2,200 - Worst-case headroom (thin line, heavy peak)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Stress centre: credit 4,000 / outflow 9,500 = 3,700 - Base case reproduced inside the data table
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Stress corner: credit 5,000 / outflow 9,000 = 5,200 - Best-case headroom (ample line, light peak)

**Pillar - Reserve & Liquidity Operations**

- **Central-Bank Reserve & Intraday Shortfall Computation** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 9 min · ref: CBUAE Reserve Requirements Regulation; SAMA cash reserve ratio; BCBS 248 intraday liquidity tools
  - _Measures:_ Applying tiered central-bank reserve ratios and tracking the settlement-account balance to detect a reserve shortfall after intraday outflows.
  - _Scenario:_ Treasury-operations close for a UAE bank. The bank holds average eligible demand & savings deposits of AED 50,000 (000s) and average time deposits of AED 30,000. The CBUAE required reserve ratio is 7% on demand/savings deposits and 1% on time deposits, held non-remunerated at the central bank. The bank's current settlement-account balance at the central bank is AED 3,900. During the day a single large outgoing RTGS payment of AED 1,200 settles against that balance. Compute: (a) the total required reserve, (b) the post-payment settlement-account balance, and (c) the reserve shortfall - the amount by which the post-payment balance falls below the required reserve (0 if none, positive shortfall otherwise). The three answers must reconcile (shortfall = required reserve - post-payment balance, floored at 0).
  - _Model answer:_ Required reserve = 50000*0.07 + 30000*0.01 = 3500 + 300 = 3800. Post-payment balance = 3900 - 1200 = 2700. Shortfall = max(0, 3800 - 2700) = 1100. The three values reconcile: shortfall = required - post-payment = 3800 - 2700 = 1100.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total required reserve = 3,800 - Tiered reserve-ratio application (7% demand + 1% time)
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Post-payment settlement balance = 2,700 - Settlement-account balance after intraday RTGS outflow
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Reserve shortfall = 1,100 - Shortfall detection (required minus available, floored at 0) - the reconciling answer

**Pillar - Transaction Lifecycle & Exception Interrogation**

- **Failed & Returned Settlement-Leg Exposure (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: SWIFT ISO 20022 pacs message lifecycle; CBUAE UAEFTS returns/exceptions handling; DAMA DMBOK data-interrogation practice
  - _Measures:_ Writing a filtered relational aggregation over a settlement-leg ledger to rank counterparties by unsettled (returned/failed/queued) exposure.
  - _Scenario:_ You are the operations analyst interrogating the core-banking settlement-leg ledger after the EOD clearing run to quantify exception exposure per counterparty bank. The settlement_legs table holds one row per outbound payment leg with its current lifecycle status. Schema: settlement_legs(id int, counterparty_bank text, channel text, amount numeric, status text, value_date date) where status is one of 'settled','returned','failed','queued'. Write ONE query that returns, for each counterparty bank that has at least one UNSETTLED leg (status in 'returned','failed','queued'), the counterparty_bank and the total unsettled amount, ordered by total unsettled amount highest first (then counterparty_bank A-Z to break ties). Columns: counterparty_bank, unsettled_total.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT counterparty_bank, SUM(amount) AS unsettled_total FROM settlement_legs WHERE status IN ('returned','failed','queued') GROUP BY counterparty_bank ORDER BY unsettled_total DESC, counterparty_bank. Seeded data is constructed so that 'settled' legs are correctly excluded and the ranking is unambiguous; the result set is compared ordered against the master query.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master: unsettled exposure per counterparty, settled legs excluded, ranked desc - Correct status filter, GROUP BY aggregation, and DESC ordering with tie-break

---

### 5.7 Financial Crime, AML, Know-Your-Customer (KYC), & Sanctions Compliance

Sandbox blueprint for the AML / financial-crime function, built around the QUANTITATIVE and ANALYTICAL slice of compliance work that is auto-gradable. The function's skills list in functions.json is empty, so I proposed six GCC-grounded skills (Customer Risk Rating & EDD, Transaction Monitoring & Threshold Tuning, Sanctions & PEP Screening, SAR/STR Case Management, Trade-Based ML Detection, Regulatory Reporting & MIS) and designed to them. Three pillars across four blocks using THREE engines: logic_input (weighted CDD risk-index + sanctions fuzzy-match scoring), advanced_spreadsheet (transaction-monitoring threshold-tuning sensitivity matrix), spreadsheet (SAR aging + alert-disposition KPI MIS), and sql (transaction-ledger structuring/smurfing typology detection). Difficulty mixes basic -> advanced. Concrete GCC figures throughout (AED, real-sounding Emirati/Saudi entities), real standards (FATF 40 Recommendations, UAE Federal Decree-Law 20/2018 + Cabinet Decision 10/2019, CBUAE AML/CFT Guidelines, Wolfsberg, OFAC/UN sanctions, goAML).

**Skills:** Customer Risk Rating & Enhanced Due Diligence (CDD/EDD) · Transaction Monitoring & Scenario Threshold Tuning · Sanctions, PEP & Adverse-Media Screening · Suspicious Activity / Transaction Reporting (SAR/STR) Case Management · Trade-Based Money Laundering & Typology Detection · Regulatory Reporting & Compliance MIS

**Engine fit:** AML/financial-crime compliance is largely a "soft" governance function (judgement, narrative SAR drafting, regulatory interpretation) that the four engines cannot grade directly. I deliberately designed the QUANTITATIVE / ANALYTICAL slice of the role that IS gradable, and excluded everything subjective. What is graded: (1) Customer risk-rating math — a weighted risk index over country/product/channel/PEP factors mapped to a CBUAE risk band, plus a residual-risk after-controls calc (logic_input — exact field values). (2) Transaction-monitoring threshold tuning — a two-variable data table of alert volume across structuring threshold and look-back window, the core "tuning" task analysts actually do, graded on the native data table being present AND corner/interior cell values (advanced_spreadsheet). (3) Sanctions fuzzy-match scoring — a weighted name/DOB/nationality match-score and a true-hit/false-positive disposition count (logic_input). (4) SAR/STR aging + alert-disposition MIS — days-outstanding vs the 35-business-day goAML clock, SLA-breach count, false-positive rate, conversion rate (spreadsheet — exact cell values). (5) Typology detection over a transactions ledger — a single SQL query that surfaces structuring/smurfing (sub-threshold cash deposits clustering just under AED 55,000 across short windows), graded by result-set match. The honest limitation: this measures the analyst/officer's NUMERACY and DATA-INTERROGATION competence (the defensible, examinable core of an AML role) — it does NOT and cannot assess SAR narrative quality, regulatory-judgement nuance, or the reasonableness of an escalation decision, which remain human-reviewed. This is the strongest gradable proxy for the function and is a genuinely good fit because modern AML work is heavily quantitative (risk scoring, threshold tuning, screening math, MIS, data analytics).

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 5 tasks · engines: Logic input, Adv. Spreadsheet, Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Customer Risk & Sanctions Screening Mechanics**

- **Customer Due-Diligence Weighted Risk Rating** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: FATF Recommendation 10 + CBUAE AML/CFT Guidelines (Risk-Based Approach); UAE Cabinet Decision 10/2019
  - _Measures:_ Applies a risk-based-approach weighted scoring model to derive an auditable customer risk rating, maps it to the regulator's risk band, computes residual risk after controls, and applies the EDD-trigger rule.
  - _Scenario:_ Onboarding case at Emirates Gulf Bank (Dubai). A new corporate customer, Al-Mansoori Trading FZE, presents the following inherent-risk factors, each scored 1-5 and carrying a fixed weight in the bank's CDD model: Country/Geography risk = 4 (beneficial owner resident in a FATF grey-list jurisdiction), weight 30%; Product/Service risk = 3 (trade-finance + cross-border wire facility), weight 25%; Delivery-Channel risk = 5 (non-face-to-face digital onboarding), weight 20%; Customer-Type risk = 4 (cash-intensive general-trading FZE with nominee director), weight 15%; PEP/Adverse-Media risk = 2 (no PEP, one resolved historical adverse-media hit), weight 10%. The weighted inherent-risk score (sum of factor x weight) maps to a CBUAE band: 1.00-2.33 = LOW (output the numeric code 1), 2.34-3.66 = MEDIUM (code 2), 3.67-5.00 = HIGH (code 3). Controls applied (EDD: senior-management sign-off + source-of-wealth verification + enhanced ongoing monitoring) reduce inherent risk by a 0.85 control-effectiveness factor to give the residual risk score (residual = inherent x (1 - 0.85)... NOTE for candidate: residual = inherent x (1 - control_effectiveness) where control_effectiveness = 0.40 for this EDD package). EDD is MANDATORY (output code 1 for required, 0 for not required) whenever the inherent band is HIGH.
  - _Model answer:_ Weighted inherent score = 4*0.30 + 3*0.25 + 5*0.20 + 4*0.15 + 2*0.10 = 1.20 + 0.75 + 1.00 + 0.60 + 0.20 = 3.75. Band: 3.75 is in 3.67-5.00 => HIGH => code 3. Residual = inherent * (1 - 0.40) = 3.75 * 0.60 = 2.25. EDD required because inherent band is HIGH => code 1.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Weighted inherent risk score = 3.75 - Correctly multiplies each factor by its weight and sums (the core RBA scoring computation)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Risk band code = 3 (HIGH) - Maps the numeric score to the correct CBUAE risk band boundary
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Residual risk after EDD controls = 2.25 - Applies the control-effectiveness factor to derive residual risk
    - `logic_value` (w1) - EDD required flag = 1 - Applies the mandatory-EDD trigger rule for HIGH-risk customers
- **Sanctions / PEP Fuzzy-Match Scoring & Disposition** &nbsp; `Logic input` · advanced · 10 min · ref: Wolfsberg Group Sanctions Screening Guidance; OFAC SDN / UN Consolidated List; FATF Recommendation 6
  - _Measures:_ Computes a weighted multi-attribute sanctions match-confidence score, applies the bank's auto-block/review/discharge disposition thresholds, and derives the screening false-positive rate used to evidence model performance to the regulator.
  - _Scenario:_ A real-time wire from First Saudi Capital generates a screening alert against the UN Consolidated List. The screening engine scores three attributes and combines them into a weighted match confidence (0-100). Payee on the wire: 'Mohammed A. Al-Harbi', DOB 1979-03-12, nationality Saudi. Closest list entry: 'Muhammad Abdullah Alharbi', DOB 1979-03-12, nationality Saudi. Attribute scores from the matching algorithm: Name similarity = 82 (Jaro-Winkler), weight 50%; DOB match = 100 (exact), weight 30%; Nationality match = 100 (exact), weight 20%. The combined match score = sum(attribute x weight). The bank's policy: combined score >= 85 = AUTO-BLOCK pending L2 review (output disposition code 2); 70-84.99 = MANUAL REVIEW / hold (code 1); < 70 = AUTO-DISCHARGE as false positive (code 0). Separately, the screening batch produced 240 alerts last month, of which 12 were confirmed true matches and 228 were discharged as false positives; compute the false-positive rate as a percentage to one decimal place.
  - _Model answer:_ Combined match score = 82*0.50 + 100*0.30 + 100*0.20 = 41 + 30 + 20 = 91. 91 >= 85 => AUTO-BLOCK => disposition code 2. False-positive rate = 228/240 * 100 = 95.0%.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Combined weighted match score = 91 - Correctly weights name/DOB/nationality attributes into a single match confidence
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Disposition code = 2 (auto-block) - Applies the correct policy threshold to the match score
    - `logic_value` (w2) - False-positive rate = 95.0% - Computes screening-program false-positive rate for model-performance MIS

**Pillar - Transaction Monitoring & Threshold Tuning**

- **Structuring-Scenario Threshold-Tuning Sensitivity Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18.3 min · ref: FATF Recommendation 20; CBUAE Transaction Monitoring expectations; FFIEC BSA/AML Examination Manual (model tuning)
  - _Measures:_ Performs transaction-monitoring scenario threshold tuning - the core analytical task of an FCC tuning analyst - by parameterising a structuring rule and building a native two-variable sensitivity table that quantifies the alert-volume / coverage trade-off across threshold and look-back settings.
  - _Scenario:_ You tune the cash-structuring scenario in the transaction-monitoring system at National Bank of Abu Dhabi's FCC unit. The scenario fires an alert when a customer makes deposits each below a CASH THRESHOLD (T, in AED) whose total over a LOOK-BACK WINDOW (W, in days) exceeds the AED 55,000 mandatory cash-reporting line. The provided sample dataset is summarised by a calibration function already on the sheet: estimated monthly ALERT VOLUME = round( BaseRate * (55000 / T) * (W / 7) ), where BaseRate = 90. You must (1) compute the base-case alert volume in the model cell for T = AED 50,000 and W = 7 days, then (2) build a two-variable data table showing alert volume across cash-threshold columns (AED 40,000 / 50,000 / 55,000) and look-back-window rows (7 / 14 / 30 days), using a NATIVE data table (not hardcoded). Tighter thresholds and longer windows raise alert volume (more analyst workload, fewer missed); the table is the artefact that evidences the tuning decision to the regulator.
  - _Model answer:_ Alert volume = round(90 * (55000/T) * (W/7)). Base case T=50000, W=7: 90 * 1.1 * 1 = 99. Data table corners/interior: (T=40000,W=7) = round(90*1.375*1)=124; (T=55000,W=7)=round(90*1.0*1)=90; (T=40000,W=30)=round(90*1.375*4.2857)=round(530.36)=530; (T=55000,W=30)=round(90*1.0*4.2857)=round(385.71)=386; center (T=50000,W=14)=round(90*1.1*2)=198. The candidate places =alert_volume_formula in the corner cell, sets column input = T cell and row input = W cell, and selects the table range so the engine fills the native {=TABLE()} array.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sensitivity grid uses a native data table (not hardcoded) - Candidate built a real two-variable data table rather than typing values - the gradable proof of the tuning technique
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base-case alert volume (T=50000, W=7) = 99 - Correctly evaluates the structuring scenario calibration formula
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Tightest setting corner (T=40000, W=30) = 530 - Data table propagates the strictest threshold + longest window (max workload corner)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Loosest setting corner (T=55000, W=7) = 90 - Data table propagates the threshold at the reporting line with the shortest window (min workload corner)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Center cell (T=50000, W=14) = 198 - Interior cell confirms the data table varies BOTH inputs simultaneously
- **Alert-Disposition & SAR Aging Compliance MIS** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 15 min · ref: UAE Federal Decree-Law 20/2018 (STR obligation); CBUAE goAML reporting (35-business-day clock); FATF Recommendation 33 (statistics)
  - _Measures:_ Produces the regulator-facing AML compliance MIS - conversion/escalation/false-positive ratios and SAR/STR aging against the statutory filing clock - that evidences the effectiveness and timeliness of the transaction-monitoring program.
  - _Scenario:_ Build the monthly FCC management-information dashboard for the MLRO at Sharjah Islamic Bank. The alert population for the period: total alerts received = 1,250; auto-closed by rules = 500; escalated to L2 analysts = 750; of those L2 cases, 60 were escalated to the MLRO and 30 became filed STRs (suspicious transaction reports). For STR aging, four open cases are tracked against the regulator's 35-business-day filing clock: Case AED-014 opened on business-day count 8 (so 8 days elapsed), AED-022 at 33 days, AED-031 at 36 days, AED-040 at 41 days. Compute: (1) the alert-to-STR conversion rate as a % of total alerts; (2) the L2 escalation rate as a % of total alerts; (3) the false-positive proxy = auto-closed as a % of total alerts; (4) the count of STR cases that have BREACHED the 35-day clock (days elapsed > 35); (5) the average days-elapsed across the four tracked cases.
  - _Model answer:_ Conversion rate = 30/1250 = 2.40%. L2 escalation rate = 750/1250 = 60.00%. Auto-close (FP proxy) = 500/1250 = 40.00%. SLA breaches (>35 days): AED-031 (36) and AED-040 (41) => 2 cases. Average days elapsed = (8 + 33 + 36 + 41)/4 = 118/4 = 29.5.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Alert-to-STR conversion rate = 2.40% - Computes the headline program-effectiveness ratio (STRs over total alerts)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - L2 escalation rate = 60.00% - Computes the analyst-workload escalation ratio
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Auto-close / false-positive proxy = 40.00% - Computes the rules-tuning quality ratio
    - `cell_value` (w3) - STR cases breaching the 35-day clock = 2 - Applies the statutory filing-deadline aging rule (a hard compliance control)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Average case age = 29.5 days - Computes mean aging across the open-case queue

**Pillar - Typology Detection & Data Interrogation**

- **Structuring / Smurfing Detection over the Transaction Ledger (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: FATF Money-Laundering Typologies; Egmont Group; CBUAE cash-reporting threshold (AED 55,000)
  - _Measures:_ Interrogates a transaction ledger with grouped/filtered SQL to surface a named ML typology (structuring/smurfing), correctly applying BOTH the per-transaction sub-threshold filter and the aggregate-over-threshold HAVING condition - the data-analytics core of modern transaction monitoring.
  - _Scenario:_ A seeded `cash_transactions` table at Abu Dhabi Commercial Bank holds individual cash deposits: columns (id int, account_no text, branch text, amount numeric, txn_date date). The FCC unit wants to surface accounts that show STRUCTURING (smurfing): multiple sub-threshold cash deposits that, in aggregate, evade the AED 55,000 mandatory cash-reporting line. Write ONE query that returns each account whose INDIVIDUAL deposits are each strictly below AED 55,000 (so none was reported on its own) BUT whose TOTAL cash deposits sum to AED 55,000 or more - i.e. classic structuring. Return columns: account_no, deposit_count, total_amount. Order by total_amount descending (highest aggregate exposure first), then account_no. Seed data includes Account 8841-A with 4 deposits of 14,000/13,500/15,000/14,800 (all sub-threshold, total 57,300 = structuring); Account 8842-B with one 60,000 deposit (over threshold, reported - NOT structuring, must be excluded); Account 8843-C with 3 deposits of 9,000/8,000/7,500 (sub-threshold but total 24,500 < 55,000 - NOT structuring, must be excluded); Account 8844-D with 5 deposits of 12,000/12,000/12,000/12,000/12,000 (all sub-threshold, total 60,000 = structuring).
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT account_no, COUNT(*) AS deposit_count, SUM(amount) AS total_amount FROM cash_transactions WHERE amount < 55000 GROUP BY account_no HAVING SUM(amount) >= 55000 ORDER BY total_amount DESC, account_no. The WHERE prunes any account-row at/above the reporting line from the per-deposit test; GROUP BY + HAVING enforces the aggregate-evasion condition. Expected result rows: 8844-D (5, 60000) then 8841-A (4, 57300). 8842-B excluded by the WHERE (its 60000 deposit is filtered, leaving 0 rows so it fails HAVING); 8843-C excluded by HAVING (24500 < 55000).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result set matches master structuring query (ordered by total_amount desc) - Correctly combines the sub-threshold WHERE filter, the GROUP BY account, the aggregate-over-threshold HAVING, and the descending order - so only the two true structuring accounts return in the right sequence

---

### 5.8 Banking Regulatory Affairs, Basel IV Compliance, & Capital Adequacy

Hands-on sandbox for the quantitative core of bank regulatory affairs: building the Risk-Weighted Assets (RWA) stack and capital-ratio waterfall with a CET1 stress sensitivity table, computing the Combined Buffer Requirement and the Maximum Distributable Amount (MDA) restriction, computing the Liquidity Coverage Ratio (LCR) from a haircut/run-off stack, and interrogating a regulatory exposure ledger by Basel asset class. The function's skills list was empty, so six skills were first proposed (capital ratios, RWA under the Standardised Approach, capital buffers/MDA, liquidity standards LCR/NSFR, leverage ratio, and Pillar 3 / CBUAE-SAMA reporting) and the gradable arithmetic of each was designed against the four engines. 3 pillars, 4 blocks, three engines (advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql), GCC scenarios in AED with CBUAE D-SIB framing and Basel III/IV standards.

**Skills:** Capital Adequacy & Capital Ratios (CET1 / Tier 1 / Total) · Risk-Weighted Assets under the Standardised Approach (Credit / Market / Operational) · Capital Buffers, Combined Buffer Requirement & MDA Restriction · Liquidity Standards (LCR & NSFR) · Leverage Ratio & Exposure Measure · Regulatory Reporting & Pillar 3 Disclosure (CBUAE / SAMA)

**Engine fit:** Banking regulatory affairs is often perceived as a "soft" policy-and-liaison function, but its defensible core - capital adequacy - is almost entirely arithmetic and therefore a strong fit for these engines. Capital ratios, RWA, buffers, MDA, LCR and leverage are all closed-form computations from regulatory inputs, so no free-text or judgement grading is needed. RWA aggregation, the capital-ratio waterfall and a two-variable CET1 stress table map cleanly to advanced_spreadsheet (cell_value + is_array_formula). The buffer/MDA cascade and the LCR haircut/run-off stack map to logic_input (logic_value) because each is a chain of named intermediate figures that must reconcile. Pillar 3 exposure-class RWA aggregation maps to sql (sql_result_match) over a seeded exposures ledger. The only genuinely non-gradable parts of the real role - drafting regulatory submissions, supervisory-college liaison, and qualitative ICAAP narrative - are deliberately excluded; this sandbox measures the demonstrated quantitative competence that underpins them, which is the part a hiring bank most needs to verify.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Capital Adequacy Engineering & Stress Sensitivity**

- **RWA Stack, Capital-Ratio Waterfall & CET1 Stress Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 20 min · ref: Basel III/IV (BCBS) Standardised Approach for Credit Risk + CBUAE Capital Adequacy Standards
  - _Measures:_ Assembling the Basel Standardised-Approach RWA stack, deriving the CET1/Tier 1/Total capital ratios, and running a native two-variable sensitivity (data table) on the CET1 ratio under combined RWA-growth and credit-loss stress.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Gulf Bank PJSC (a CBUAE-regulated UAE bank, figures in AED millions) is preparing its quarterly capital return. The credit book carries five Standardised-Approach buckets: Sovereign exposure AED 8,000m at a 0% risk weight, Bank exposure AED 4,000m at 20%, Corporate exposure AED 10,000m at 100%, Retail residential mortgages AED 6,000m at 35%, and Past-due (NPL) exposure AED 1,000m at 150%. Market-risk RWA is AED 1,200m and Operational-risk RWA is AED 2,400m (both given). Regulatory capital tiers: CET1 capital AED 2,160m, Additional Tier 1 (AT1) AED 360m, Tier 2 AED 540m. The candidate must (1) compute Credit RWA, then Total RWA; (2) build the capital-ratio waterfall - CET1 ratio, Tier 1 ratio, Total Capital ratio (each as a percentage of Total RWA); and (3) build a two-variable data table for the stressed CET1 ratio with rows = RWA growth (0%, 5%, 10%) and columns = a CET1 credit-loss deduction shock (AED 0m, 200m, 400m), where stressed CET1 ratio = (CET1 - loss) / (Total RWA x (1 + growth)).
  - _Model answer:_ Credit RWA = sum(exposure x risk weight) = 8000x0 + 4000x0.20 + 10000x1.00 + 6000x0.35 + 1000x1.50 = 0 + 800 + 10000 + 2100 + 1500 = AED 14,400m. Total RWA = 14,400 + 1,200 (market) + 2,400 (operational) = AED 18,000m. Tier 1 = CET1 + AT1 = 2,160 + 360 = 2,520; Total capital = 2,520 + 540 (Tier 2) = 3,060. Ratios (x100): CET1 = 2,160/18,000 = 12.00%; Tier 1 = 2,520/18,000 = 14.00%; Total = 3,060/18,000 = 17.00%. Stressed CET1 ratio = (2,160 - loss)/(18,000 x (1+growth)) x 100. Corner low (loss 0, growth 0%) = 12.00%; centre (loss 200, growth 5%) = 1,960/18,900 = 10.37%; corner high (loss 400, growth 10%) = 1,760/19,800 = 8.89%. The 3x3 grid must be produced by a native two-variable data table whose corner cell links to the stressed-CET1 formula, with the loss shock and growth driving the column and row inputs - not hardcoded.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Credit RWA computed correctly (AED 14,400m) - Standardised-Approach credit RWA = sum of exposure x risk weight across all five buckets
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Total RWA = AED 18,000m (credit + market + operational) - Aggregation of credit, market and operational RWA into the denominator
    - `cell_value` (w2) - CET1 ratio = 12.00% - CET1 capital / Total RWA
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total Capital ratio = 17.00% - (CET1 + AT1 + Tier 2) / Total RWA capital-tier roll-up
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Stressed-CET1 grid uses a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - Candidate built a real data-table array driven by row/column inputs rather than typing values
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Stress corner (loss 400, growth 10%) = 8.89% - Stressed CET1 ratio = (CET1 - loss)/(RWA x (1+growth)) at the most severe corner

**Pillar - Buffer, Distribution & Liquidity Constraints**

- **Combined Buffer Requirement & Maximum Distributable Amount (MDA)** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: Basel III Capital Conservation / Countercyclical / D-SIB buffers + MDA framework (BCBS); CBUAE Tier Capital Supply Standard
  - _Measures:_ Computing the Combined Buffer Requirement and applying the Basel capital-conservation MDA quartile cascade to cap permitted distributions when a bank operates inside its buffer.
  - _Scenario:_ National Capital Bank is a CBUAE-designated Domestic Systemically Important Bank (D-SIB). Regulatory minimum CET1 is 4.5% of RWA. Its buffer requirements are: Capital Conservation Buffer (CCB) 2.5%, Countercyclical Buffer (CCyB) 1.0%, and a D-SIB surcharge of 1.5% - all to be met with CET1. The bank's current CET1 ratio is 8.0% (Tier 1 and Total minimums are met by AT1 and Tier 2, so all CET1 above the 4.5% minimum is available to meet buffers). Distributable earnings for the year are AED 800m. The board wants to know the maximum dividend it may pay without breaching the capital-conservation distribution restriction. Compute: the Combined Buffer Requirement, the CET1 available to meet buffers, the buffer shortfall, the applicable MDA payout factor, and the Maximum Distributable Amount.
  - _Model answer:_ Combined Buffer Requirement (CBR) = CCB + CCyB + D-SIB = 2.5 + 1.0 + 1.5 = 5.0%. CET1 available to meet buffers = CET1 ratio - minimum CET1 = 8.0% - 4.5% = 3.5%. Buffer shortfall = CBR - available = 5.0% - 3.5% = 1.5% (bank is inside its buffer, so distributions are restricted). MDA quartile: the proportion of the CBR that is met = 3.5 / 5.0 = 70%, which falls in the third quartile band (>50% to <=75%), giving a maximum payout factor of 40% of eligible earnings. Maximum Distributable Amount = 40% x AED 800m = AED 320m.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Combined Buffer Requirement = 5.0% - Sum of CCB + CCyB + D-SIB surcharge
    - `logic_value` (w2) - CET1 available to meet buffers = 3.5% - CET1 ratio less the 4.5% CET1 minimum
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Buffer shortfall = 1.5% - Combined Buffer Requirement less CET1 available to meet buffers
    - `logic_value` (w3) - MDA payout factor = 40% - Correct quartile of the capital-conservation cascade for 70% buffer coverage
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Maximum Distributable Amount = AED 320m - Payout factor applied to distributable earnings; reconciles the whole cascade
- **Liquidity Coverage Ratio (LCR) - HQLA Stack vs Net Outflows** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: Basel III LCR (BCBS 238) + CBUAE Liquidity Standards
  - _Measures:_ Constructing the post-haircut HQLA stack, applying deposit run-off and inflow rates to derive net cash outflow, and computing the regulatory LCR.
  - _Scenario:_ Gulf Commercial Bank must report its 30-day Liquidity Coverage Ratio (figures in AED millions). High-Quality Liquid Assets: Level 1 (cash and government securities) AED 12,000m at a 0% haircut; Level 2A (qualifying covered bonds) AED 3,000m at a 15% haircut; Level 2B (qualifying corporate bonds) AED 2,000m at a 50% haircut (the Level 2 caps are not binding here). Expected 30-day cash outflows: stable retail deposits AED 40,000m at a 5% run-off; less-stable retail deposits AED 30,000m at 10%; operational wholesale deposits AED 24,000m at 25%; non-operational wholesale deposits AED 10,000m at 40%. Contractual cash inflows are AED 6,000m at a 50% inflow rate (the 75%-of-outflows inflow cap is not binding). Compute total HQLA after haircuts, total expected outflows, net cash outflow, and the LCR.
  - _Model answer:_ Total HQLA = 12,000x(1-0.00) + 3,000x(1-0.15) + 2,000x(1-0.50) = 12,000 + 2,550 + 1,000 = AED 15,550m. Total expected outflows = 40,000x0.05 + 30,000x0.10 + 24,000x0.25 + 10,000x0.40 = 2,000 + 3,000 + 6,000 + 4,000 = AED 15,000m. Inflows = 6,000x0.50 = 3,000 (below the 75% x 15,000 = 11,250 cap). Net cash outflow = 15,000 - 3,000 = AED 12,000m. LCR = 15,550 / 12,000 x 100 = 129.58%.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Total HQLA after haircuts = AED 15,550m - Level 1/2A/2B assets net of regulatory haircuts
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total expected outflows = AED 15,000m - Deposit balances x prescribed run-off rates summed
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Net cash outflow = AED 12,000m - Outflows less capped inflows
    - `logic_value` (w3) - LCR = 129.58% - HQLA / net cash outflow; reconciles the full computation

**Pillar - Regulatory Reporting & Exposure Interrogation**

- **Pillar 3 Exposure-Class RWA Aggregation (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · basic · 10 min · ref: Basel III/IV Pillar 3 Disclosure (template CR4/OV1) + DAMA DMBOK data interrogation
  - _Measures:_ Aggregating a regulatory exposure ledger into the Pillar 3 RWA-by-asset-class disclosure with a grouped, computed, ordered SQL query.
  - _Scenario:_ An exposures ledger holds one row per credit facility with its Standardised-Approach Basel asset class, exposure-at-default (EAD, in AED 000s) and applied risk weight. The regulatory reporting team needs the Pillar 3 RWA breakdown by asset class for the OV1 template. Seeded rows: Sovereign EAD 8,000 @ 0.00; Bank EAD 4,000 @ 0.20; Bank EAD 2,000 @ 0.20; Corporate EAD 10,000 @ 1.00; Corporate EAD 5,000 @ 1.00; Retail Mortgage EAD 6,000 @ 0.35; Retail Mortgage EAD 4,000 @ 0.35; Past Due EAD 1,000 @ 1.50. Write ONE query returning each asset class and its total RWA (EAD x risk weight summed), ordered by RWA descending.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT asset_class, SUM(ead * risk_weight) AS rwa FROM exposures GROUP BY asset_class ORDER BY rwa DESC, asset_class. Per-class RWA: Corporate (10,000+5,000)x1.00 = 15,000; Retail Mortgage (6,000+4,000)x0.35 = 3,500; Past Due 1,000x1.50 = 1,500; Bank (4,000+2,000)x0.20 = 1,200; Sovereign 8,000x0.00 = 0. Result set is the five rows in that descending RWA order.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - RWA-by-asset-class result matches the master (correct totals, descending order) - GROUP BY asset_class with SUM(ead x risk_weight) and ORDER BY rwa DESC produces the exact Pillar 3 breakdown

---

## Project Management (PMO)

> **Domain review** - engine coverage OK. All 4 blueprints map every block to a valid auto-gradable engine (spreadsheet / advanced_spreadsheet / logic_input / sql) with valid checkpoint kinds (cell_value, is_array_formula, logic_value, sql_result_match); no python or free-text grading sneaks in. Every function declares exactly 3 pillars and uses 4 distinct engine types (well above the >=2 minimum), so the sittings are varied. Block counts: 6.1=5 (ok), 6.3=4 (ok), 6.4=4 (ok), 6.2=6 (VIOLATES the 3-5 hard rule). The gradable-slice reasoning is strong on the three non-quantitative-adjacent functions: 6.1 correctly excludes governance-charter/stage-gate narratives and measures EVM + weighted scoring + portfolio roll-ups; 6.2 honestly flags that Scrum facilitation/coaching is not gradable and measures the empirical delivery-metrics half (velocity, Little's Law, WSJF, EVM, flow SQL); 6.4 splits ERM (numeric) from Change Management (soft) and grades the change-economics slice (adoption-benefit sensitivity) instead of narratives. 6.3 is inherently quantitative and maps cleanly. All four anchor to real standards (PMI PMBOK/EVM, AgileCraft/SAFe WSJF + Little's Law, PERT, ERM/EMV) consistent with FP&A's framework_ref rigor. Difficulty mixes: 6.1/6.2/6.4 span basic->intermediate->advanced; 6.3 has NO basic block and skews hard (2 advanced + 2 intermediate). SQL blocks all carry 1 checkpoint (a single sql_result_match), which deviates from the per-block 3-6 checkpoint design rule but exactly matches the canonical FP&A reference's SQL block, so it is an accepted engine-specific pattern rather than a defect.
>
> - _(high)_ 6.2: Block count is 6, which violates the hard design rule of 3-5 blocks total. Drop one block to comply. The cleanest cut is one of the three logic_input blocks: 6.2 currently runs three logic_input blocks (Kanban Flow Metrics, WSJF Backlog Prioritisation, Agile-in-Stage-Gate EVM), so removing one (e.g. fold the EVM index check into the WSJF block or drop the lowest-value one) brings it to 5 blocks AND reduces same-engine monotony in a single edit.
> - _(low)_ 6.2: Engine monotony: half the blocks (3 of 6) use the logic_input engine. Even though 4 distinct engines are present (variety rule satisfied), three identical logic_input sittings make the experience repetitive. Trimming to 5 blocks per the block-count fix should remove one logic_input block to leave a more balanced spread.
> - _(medium)_ 6.3: Difficulty mix skews hard with no basic block: the four blocks are advanced, advanced, intermediate, intermediate. The design rules require mixing difficulty across blocks and the reference sittings include an entry-level on-ramp. Re-grade one block to basic (the PERT/contingency logic_input block is the natural candidate) or add a short basic logic_input block (e.g. simple cost-variance / CV-SV-CPI-SPI computation) so a weaker candidate can demonstrate partial competence.
> - _(low)_ 6.1: Pillar-to-block distribution is unverifiable from the compact view but is at risk: with 3 pillars and 5 blocks, one pillar must hold 1 block. Confirm the EVM/quantitative core (the most defensible PMO skill) is not the single-block pillar, and that the two logic_input blocks (Earned Value Indices and Contingency Reserve) are not both stacked in one pillar leaving another thin. Verify the full blueprint balances blocks ~2/2/1 across the three pillars.
>
> _Recommendations:_ Three of the four are ship-ready after minor edits; engine coverage and gradable-slice identification are sound across the board. Priority fixes: (1) 6.2 MUST drop to 3-5 blocks - remove one logic_input block (it has three), which simultaneously fixes the block-count rule violation and the engine-monotony concern; this is the only hard-rule breach in the set. (2) 6.3 should introduce a basic-difficulty block (re-grade the PERT/contingency block down, or add a short CV/SV/CPI/SPI logic_input on-ramp) so the difficulty curve isn't advanced-heavy. (3) 6.1 - confirm the 5 blocks distribute sensibly across the 3 pillars (target ~2/2/1) with the EVM core not isolated in a single-block pillar. The single-checkpoint SQL blocks across all four are acceptable - they mirror the FP&A reference's SQL pattern exactly - so do not force them to 3-6 checkpoints. No engine-fit gaps: the non-quantitative dimensions (governance narratives, Scrum facilitation, change-leadership) are correctly and honestly excluded with the quantitative proxy designed in their place.

### 6.1 Project Management Office (PMO) Strategy & Governance

Blueprint for the PMO Strategy & Governance sandbox (node 6.1, PMO domain). The function's skills_en list was empty, so I proposed six GCC-grounded PMO skills (Portfolio Prioritization & Selection, Earned Value Management, Capacity & Resource Planning, Stage-Gate Governance & Benefits Realization, Portfolio Risk & Contingency, Portfolio Performance Reporting) and designed the quantitative/analytical slice that the four auto-grading engines can measure. PMO is a strong engine fit: its core technical craft is numeric (EVM cost/schedule indices and forecasts, weighted scoring models, resource-load math, contingency drawdown) plus relational portfolio reporting. The soft parts of PMO (governance narrative, stakeholder alignment, change-management facilitation) are NOT gradable here and are deliberately excluded - see engine_fit. 3 pillars, 4 blocks, 3 engines (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql - actually all four), mixed difficulty. Concrete GCC scenarios in AED/SAR with real PMI PMBOK / Standard for Portfolio Management / AACE references.

**Skills:** Portfolio Prioritization & Selection (weighted scoring) · Earned Value Management (EVM) & Forecasting · Capacity & Resource Planning / Demand Management · Stage-Gate Governance & Benefits Realization · Portfolio Risk, Contingency & Reserve Management · Portfolio Performance Reporting & Dashboarding

**Engine fit:** Strong fit for 3 of 4 engines; PMO's defensible technical core is quantitative. (1) EVM is pure formula work (PV/EV/AC -> CV/SV/CPI/SPI -> EAC/ETC/VAC/TCPI) -> logic_input and spreadsheet. (2) Portfolio prioritization is a weighted scoring matrix with a two-way sensitivity on the selection cut-line -> spreadsheet + advanced_spreadsheet (native data table). (3) Capacity/resource-load and contingency-reserve math -> logic_input. (4) Portfolio status roll-ups (RAG counts, budget burn, variance by sponsor/program) over a project register -> sql. What is NOT gradable and is deliberately excluded: governance charter/operating-model design, stage-gate decision narratives, stakeholder-engagement and change-management facilitation, lessons-learned write-ups, and any subjective 'go/kill/hold' judgement that is not reducible to a scored threshold. Those soft-skill dimensions belong to the behavioural/MCQ layers, not this hands-on sandbox. The blueprint therefore measures DEMONSTRATED command of the PMO's analytical toolkit (the work product a PMO analyst/governance lead actually produces in a spreadsheet or BI tool), which is the honest, auto-gradable slice of the function.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 5 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Portfolio Prioritization & Capital Allocation**

- **Weighted Scoring Model & Portfolio Ranking** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: PMI Standard for Portfolio Management (4th ed.) / weighted scoring model
  - _Measures:_ Building a defensible weighted scoring model (SUMPRODUCT against a normalized weight vector) and applying a capital-constrained, rank-ordered funding rule - the PMO's core project-selection deliverable.
  - _Scenario:_ Emaar Digital Transformation Office must rank six candidate projects for the FY-2026 portfolio against four governance-approved criteria, each with a fixed weight: Strategic Alignment 40%, Net Benefit 25%, Risk-adjusted Feasibility 20%, Regulatory/Compliance Urgency 15%. Each project carries raw 1-5 ratings on every criterion (already entered). You must compute each project's weighted score = SUMPRODUCT of its four ratings against the weight vector, then derive the portfolio's funding decision: the office has an AED 18.0m capital envelope and funds projects in descending weighted-score order until the next project would breach the envelope (greedy fill, no partial funding). Given the per-project capex (AED 000s): P1 'Core Banking API Layer' ratings 5,4,3,5 capex 6,200; P2 'Branch RPA Rollout' ratings 4,5,4,2 capex 4,500; P3 'ESG Reporting Hub' ratings 3,3,3,5 capex 3,000; P4 'Customer Data Platform' ratings 5,5,2,3 capex 7,800; P5 'Treasury Cashflow Tool' ratings 4,3,5,2 capex 2,400; P6 'AI Contact Centre' ratings 3,4,3,3 capex 5,100. Complete the weighted-score column, the cumulative-capex column (in rank order), and the funded-flag total.
  - _Model answer:_ Weights vector w = [0.40, 0.25, 0.20, 0.15]. Weighted score per project = SUMPRODUCT(ratings, w). P1 = 5*.4+4*.25+3*.2+5*.15 = 2.0+1.0+0.6+0.75 = 4.35; P2 = 1.6+1.25+0.8+0.3 = 3.95; P3 = 1.2+0.75+0.6+0.75 = 3.30; P4 = 2.0+1.25+0.4+0.45 = 4.10; P5 = 1.6+0.75+1.0+0.3 = 3.65; P6 = 1.2+1.0+0.6+0.45 = 3.25. Descending rank: P1 (4.35) > P4 (4.10) > P2 (3.95) > P5 (3.65) > P3 (3.30) > P6 (3.25). Greedy fund against AED 18,000k: P1 6,200 (cum 6,200 OK) -> P4 7,800 (cum 14,000 OK) -> P2 4,500 (cum 18,500 BREACH, skip) -> P5 2,400 (cum 16,400 OK) -> P3 3,000 (cum 19,400 BREACH, skip) -> P6 5,100 (breach, skip). Funded set = {P1, P4, P5}; count = 3; total funded capex = 6,200+7,800+2,400 = 16,400k; remaining envelope = 1,600k. Checkpoints target the score cells, the top-rank score, the funded count, and the funded capex total.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - P1 weighted score = 4.35 - SUMPRODUCT of ratings against the 40/25/20/15 weight vector is correct for the top project
    - `cell_value` (w1) - P4 weighted score = 4.10 - Weighted score computed correctly for a high-feasibility-penalty project
    - `cell_value` (w1) - P5 weighted score = 3.65 - Weighted score correct for a mid-rank project that survives the funding cut
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Number of funded projects = 3 - Greedy rank-ordered funding rule applied against the AED 18.0m envelope (skips over-budget projects)
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Total funded capex = AED 16,400k - Sum of the funded set's capex respects the capital constraint
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Remaining envelope = AED 1,600k - Residual capital after the funding rule reconciles (18,000 - 16,400)
- **Two-Way Sensitivity on the Funding Cut-Line** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: AACE International Recommended Practice 31R-03 (sensitivity) / PMI portfolio optimization
  - _Measures:_ Constructing a native two-variable data table to stress-test a portfolio funding decision across capital and quality thresholds - the scenario-planning craft of a senior PMO/portfolio analyst.
  - _Scenario:_ Continuing the Emaar portfolio, the investment committee wants to see how the number of funded projects moves as two governance levers change: the capital envelope (rows: AED 14,000k / 18,000k / 22,000k) and the minimum weighted-score threshold a project must clear to be eligible (columns: 3.50 / 3.80 / 4.00). For each (envelope, threshold) cell the model first drops any project below the score threshold, then greedy-funds the survivors in descending score order until the envelope is exhausted, and returns the COUNT of funded projects. Build this as a native two-variable data table driven by the single 'funded count' engine cell - it must recalculate from the model, not be hardcoded. The same six projects, scores and capex from the prior block apply (P1 4.35/6,200; P4 4.10/7,800; P2 3.95/4,500; P5 3.65/2,400; P3 3.30/3,000; P6 3.25/5,100).
  - _Model answer:_ Engine cell computes funded count given (envelope E, threshold T): eligible = projects with score >= T, then greedy-fund in descending score order within E. Corner/interior values: At T=3.50 the eligible set is {P1,P4,P2,P5} (P3 3.30 and P6 3.25 excluded). E=14,000: P1 6,200 -> P4 14,000 (exactly OK) -> P2 18,500 breach -> P5 16,400 breach => 2. E=18,000: P1,P4 (14,000) -> P2 breach -> P5 16,400 OK => 3. E=22,000: P1,P4,P2 (18,500) -> P5 20,900 OK => 4. At T=3.80 eligible = {P1,P4,P2}. E=14,000: P1,P4 (14,000) -> P2 breach => 2. E=18,000: P1,P4 -> P2 breach => 2. E=22,000: P1,P4,P2 (18,500) => 3. At T=4.00 eligible = {P1,P4}. E=14,000: P1,P4 (14,000) => 2. E=18,000: 2. E=22,000: 2. Data-table grid (rows=envelope, cols=threshold 3.50/3.80/4.00): [14000]->2,2,2; [18000]->3,2,2; [22000]->4,3,2. Checkpoints: array-formula present on the table range; top-left corner (14000,3.50)=2; bottom-left (22000,3.50)=4; centre (18000,3.80)=2.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Funding-count grid is a native two-variable data table - The 3x3 sensitivity range is formula-driven {=TABLE()} off the funded-count engine cell, not hardcoded
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (envelope 14,000k, threshold 3.50) = 2 - Funded count under the tightest envelope at the loosest threshold (P1+P4 fill exactly)
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High-capital corner (envelope 22,000k, threshold 3.50) = 4 - Funded count expands to four when capital is loosened at the loosest threshold
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Centre (envelope 18,000k, threshold 3.80) = 2 - Raising the quality threshold drops the funded count even at the base envelope

**Pillar - Project Performance Control (EVM)**

- **Earned Value Indices & Estimate at Completion** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: PMI PMBOK Guide (7th ed.) Earned Value Management / EIA-748
  - _Measures:_ Demonstrated command of the full earned-value control set - variances, efficiency indices, and the cost-performance-based forecast family - the single most important quantitative competency in PMO project control.
  - _Scenario:_ The Riyadh Metro Line 6 fit-out package is at data date month 8 of an 18-month plan. The PMO control account shows: Budget at Completion (BAC) SAR 24,000,000; Planned Value to date (PV) SAR 11,000,000; Earned Value (EV) SAR 9,600,000; Actual Cost to date (AC) SAR 12,000,000. Compute the cost variance, schedule variance, the two performance indices, the EAC assuming current cost performance continues (EAC = BAC / CPI), the Estimate to Complete (ETC = EAC - AC), the Variance at Completion (VAC = BAC - EAC), and the To-Complete Performance Index to still finish on the original budget (TCPI to BAC = (BAC - EV) / (BAC - AC)). Enter each as a labelled numeric field; index values to 4 decimals, currency to whole SAR.
  - _Model answer:_ CV = EV - AC = 9,600,000 - 12,000,000 = -2,400,000 (over cost). SV = EV - PV = 9,600,000 - 11,000,000 = -1,400,000 (behind schedule). CPI = EV/AC = 9,600,000/12,000,000 = 0.8000. SPI = EV/PV = 9,600,000/11,000,000 = 0.8727 (0.872727...). EAC = BAC/CPI = 24,000,000/0.8 = 30,000,000. ETC = EAC - AC = 30,000,000 - 12,000,000 = 18,000,000. VAC = BAC - EAC = 24,000,000 - 30,000,000 = -6,000,000. TCPI(BAC) = (BAC - EV)/(BAC - AC) = (24,000,000 - 9,600,000)/(24,000,000 - 12,000,000) = 14,400,000/12,000,000 = 1.2000. Tolerances: currency +/-1 SAR effectively (small absolute tol), indices +/-0.001.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Cost Variance (CV) = -2,400,000 - CV = EV - AC computed with correct sign (project is over cost)
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Schedule Variance (SV) = -1,400,000 - SV = EV - PV computed with correct sign (project is behind schedule)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - CPI = 0.8000 - Cost Performance Index = EV/AC
    - `logic_value` (w3) - EAC = 30,000,000 - Estimate at Completion = BAC/CPI (cost performance continues)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - VAC = -6,000,000 - Variance at Completion = BAC - EAC reconciles the forecast overrun
    - `logic_value` (w2) - TCPI to BAC = 1.2000 - To-Complete Performance Index = (BAC - EV)/(BAC - AC) - the efficiency still needed to hit budget

**Pillar - Portfolio Governance Reporting & Reserves**

- **Portfolio Status Roll-Up Query** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: PMI Standard for Portfolio Management - portfolio performance reporting / DAMA DMBOK
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating a portfolio register to produce the governance board's at-risk-spend roll-up - filtering on status and RAG, aggregating per program, and applying a materiality HAVING threshold.
  - _Scenario:_ A seeded 'projects' table holds the live ADNOC enterprise portfolio: id, name, program (e.g. 'Digital', 'Upstream', 'Sustainability'), sponsor, rag_status ('green'/'amber'/'red'), budget_aed, actual_aed, status ('active'/'on_hold'/'closed').
