The governance board wants the at-risk spend by program: for ACTIVE projects whose RAG status is 'amber' or 'red', return per program the project count and the total budget at risk (sum of budget_aed), showing only programs whose at-risk budget exceeds AED 5,000,000, ordered by at-risk budget descending. Columns: program, at_risk_count, at_risk_budget. Write ONE query.
  - _Model answer:_ Master query: SELECT program, COUNT(*) AS at_risk_count, SUM(budget_aed) AS at_risk_budget FROM projects WHERE status = 'active' AND rag_status IN ('amber','red') GROUP BY program HAVING SUM(budget_aed) > 5000000 ORDER BY at_risk_budget DESC, program. The seed data is constructed so at least two programs clear the AED 5m at-risk threshold and at least one active green program plus one closed red project are excluded, proving the candidate applied both the status and RAG filters and the HAVING materiality cut. Result match is order-sensitive (ORDER BY at_risk_budget DESC).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - At-risk-spend-by-program result matches the master (correct filters, aggregation, HAVING threshold, descending order) - Candidate filtered active + amber/red, grouped per program, applied the >AED 5m HAVING cut, and ordered by at-risk budget descending
- **Contingency Reserve & Schedule-Recovery Math** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 8 min · ref: PMI PMBOK Guide (7th ed.) - reserve analysis / Expected Monetary Value (EMV)
  - _Measures:_ Foundational PMO reserve and recovery arithmetic - EMV-based contingency sizing, cost-performance overrun forecasting, and SPI-based schedule slippage projection.
  - _Scenario:_ The DEWA Smart Grid programme PMO is sizing its contingency reserve and a recovery plan. Three identified risks carry: R1 probability 0.30 and impact AED 1,200,000; R2 probability 0.50 and impact AED 600,000; R3 probability 0.20 and impact AED 2,000,000. Compute (a) the total Expected Monetary Value (EMV) contingency reserve = sum of probability x impact across the three risks. Separately, a control account has a Budget at Completion of AED 8,000,000, has spent AED 5,400,000 to earn AED 4,800,000 of value; compute (b) its CPI, and (c) the forecast cost overrun at completion if current cost performance continues, expressed as a positive overrun amount = EAC - BAC where EAC = BAC/CPI. Finally (d), with 6 months of an original 15-month schedule remaining and an SPI of 0.80, compute the forecast slippage in months if the remaining-work schedule performance stays at the current SPI, i.e. forecast remaining duration = remaining planned months / SPI, and slippage = forecast remaining - remaining planned. Enter each labelled field.
  - _Model answer:_ (a) EMV reserve = 0.30*1,200,000 + 0.50*600,000 + 0.20*2,000,000 = 360,000 + 300,000 + 400,000 = 1,060,000. (b) CPI = EV/AC = 4,800,000/5,400,000 = 0.8889 (0.888888...). (c) EAC = BAC/CPI = 8,000,000/0.888888... = 9,000,000; overrun = EAC - BAC = 9,000,000 - 8,000,000 = 1,000,000. (d) forecast remaining duration = 6/0.80 = 7.5 months; slippage = 7.5 - 6 = 1.5 months. Tolerances: currency small absolute tol; CPI +/-0.001; months +/-0.05.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w3) - EMV contingency reserve = AED 1,060,000 - Sum of probability x impact across the three risks (reserve analysis)
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Control-account CPI = 0.8889 - CPI = EV/AC computed correctly for the reserve scenario
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Forecast cost overrun = AED 1,000,000 - Overrun = (BAC/CPI) - BAC, the EAC-based forecast variance
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Forecast schedule slippage = 1.5 months - SPI-based projection: remaining/SPI minus remaining planned duration

---

### 6.2 Agile, Scrum, & Hybrid Delivery Frameworks

Designed the gradable analytical slice of an Agile/Scrum/Hybrid delivery function for the Caliber technical sandbox. The function as named is heavily facilitation- and coaching-oriented (sprint ceremonies, team coaching, stakeholder collaboration) which is not auto-gradable; the blueprint therefore targets the quantitative delivery-management slice every competent Scrum Master / Agile delivery lead / hybrid PMO analyst must own: empirical flow metrics (velocity, throughput, WIP, cycle time), evidence-based release forecasting, economic backlog prioritisation (WSJF / Cost of Delay), and hybrid earned-value integration where an agile train sits inside a stage-gated programme. Skills list arrived empty, so 6 skills were proposed first (see proposed_skills) and the blueprint was designed to them. 3 pillars, 5 blocks, 4 engines used (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql). Frameworks referenced: Scrum Guide 2020, Disciplined Agile / PMI-ACP, SAFe WSJF, Kanban (Little's Law), and PMI PMBOK 7 / Earned Value Management (EVM) for the hybrid block.

**Skills:** Empirical sprint metrics & velocity analysis (commitment reliability, velocity trend, sprint burn) · Flow metrics & Kanban analytics (throughput, WIP, cycle time, Little's Law) · Evidence-based release forecasting & capacity planning (range forecast, run-out date, scope cut) · Economic backlog prioritisation (WSJF, Cost of Delay, value/effort ranking) · Hybrid delivery governance & Earned Value Management on stage-gated agile programmes (CPI/SPI/EAC) · Agile work-item data interrogation (backlog/sprint board querying and reporting)

**Engine fit:** STRONG FIT for the quantitative delivery-management slice; honest limitation flagged for the soft slice. The Scrum/Agile facilitation core (running ceremonies, coaching teams, removing impediments, servant leadership) is subjective and NOT auto-gradable, so this blueprint deliberately measures the empirical, math-heavy half of the role that separates a metrics-literate delivery lead from a ceremony administrator. Every modern Scrum Master / RTE / hybrid PMO analyst must compute velocity reliability, apply Little's Law (WIP = throughput x cycle time), produce evidence-based range forecasts, rank a backlog by WSJF, and reconcile an agile train to programme-level Earned Value. Engine mapping: (1) spreadsheet for sprint-metrics and capacity tables (deterministic cell math); (2) advanced_spreadsheet for a two-variable release-forecast sensitivity table (sprints-to-done across velocity x scope using a native data table); (3) logic_input for WSJF/Cost-of-Delay scoring and EVM index computation (named numeric fields that reconcile); (4) sql over a Jira-like work_items table for flow reporting. No engine grades free text, so the qualitative competencies (retrospective facilitation quality, coaching, stakeholder trust) are out of scope by design and should be assessed via the AC behavioural / CBI layer, not this sandbox.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 6 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Logic input, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Empirical Sprint & Flow Metrics**

- **Sprint Velocity, Commitment Reliability & Capacity** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: Scrum Guide 2020 / PMI-ACP Empirical Metrics
  - _Measures:_ Computing velocity, commitment-reliability ratios, and translating raw team capacity into a defensible sprint commitment - the core empirical-metrics literacy of a Scrum Master.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Digital Bank's mobile-onboarding squad in Dubai has completed four sprints. You are handed the raw sprint ledger (story points committed vs completed) and must build the empirical metrics the Scrum Master reports to the programme. Committed/Completed points per sprint: S1 committed 40, completed 34; S2 committed 38, completed 38; S3 committed 42, completed 30; S4 committed 40, completed 38. The team's defined capacity for the upcoming Sprint 5 is 9 developers x 8 available days x 6 focus-hours/day, and the historical conversion is 5 focus-hours per delivered story point. Complete the model so it computes: average velocity (mean completed points over 4 sprints), commitment reliability per sprint (completed/committed) and overall mean reliability, the Sprint-5 raw capacity in focus-hours, the Sprint-5 capacity-derived point ceiling (focus-hours / 5), and a recommended Sprint-5 commitment taken as the LOWER of average velocity and the capacity ceiling (use MIN).
  - _Model answer:_ Average velocity = mean(34,38,30,38) = 35. Reliability per sprint = completed/committed: S1 34/40 = 0.85, S2 38/38 = 1.00, S3 30/42 = 0.714286, S4 38/40 = 0.95; mean reliability = (0.85+1.00+0.714286+0.95)/4 = 0.878571. Sprint-5 raw capacity = 9*8*6 = 432 focus-hours. Capacity point ceiling = 432/5 = 86.4. Recommended commitment = MIN(average velocity 35, ceiling 86.4) = 35 (capacity is not the binding constraint here; velocity is - candidate must use MIN and land on 35).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Average velocity over 4 sprints = 35 - Mean of completed story points computed correctly (SUM/COUNT or AVERAGE).
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Sprint-3 commitment reliability = 0.7143 - Per-sprint completed/committed ratio for the worst sprint.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Mean commitment reliability = 0.8786 - Average of the four per-sprint reliability ratios.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Sprint-5 raw capacity = 432 focus-hours - devs x available days x focus-hours/day capacity build.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Capacity point ceiling = 86.4 - Focus-hours converted to a point ceiling at 5 hrs/point.
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Recommended Sprint-5 commitment = 35 - MIN(velocity, capacity ceiling) - taking the binding constraint, not summing.
- **Kanban Flow Metrics & Little's Law** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 9 min · ref: Kanban Method / Little's Law (DAMA-aligned flow analytics)
  - _Measures:_ Applying Little's Law (WIP = Throughput x Cycle Time) and deriving delivery rate, average cycle time, and a forecast clearance time - the quantitative backbone of pull-based delivery.
  - _Scenario:_ Saudi Telecom Company (stc) runs a continuous-flow Kanban support board in Riyadh. Over a 20-working-day measurement window the board completed 60 work items (throughput). A snapshot shows 18 items currently in the In-Progress and Review columns (average WIP). Management has set a WIP limit policy and wants the flow math to justify it. Compute the empirical flow metrics from Little's Law and the supporting ratios.
  - _Model answer:_ Throughput rate = 60 items / 20 days = 3 items/day. Average cycle time (Little's Law: Cycle Time = WIP / Throughput rate) = 18 / 3 = 6.0 days. If 24 new items enter the backlog, expected clearance at current throughput = 24 / 3 = 8.0 days. Flow efficiency check: if items spend 6 days in system but only 2.4 days are active work, flow efficiency = 2.4 / 6 = 0.40 (40%). All four numeric fields must reconcile to Little's Law.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Throughput rate = 3 items/day - Throughput / measurement window.
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Average cycle time = 6.0 days - Little's Law: WIP divided by throughput rate.
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Clearance time for 24 items = 8.0 days - Backlog quantity divided by throughput rate.
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Flow efficiency = 0.40 - Active work time divided by total cycle time.

**Pillar - Forecasting, Capacity & Economic Prioritisation**

- **Release Forecast Sensitivity (Sprints-to-Done)** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 16.7 min · ref: PMI-ACP / Evidence-Based Release Forecasting
  - _Measures:_ Building an evidence-based range forecast with a native two-variable data table - the defensible alternative to a single false-precision delivery date.
  - _Scenario:_ Abu Dhabi's TAMM government-services platform has a release with a remaining backlog you must forecast under uncertainty. The base remaining scope is 240 story points and the base team velocity is 30 points/sprint. Stakeholders want a two-variable sensitivity table showing the number of sprints required to complete the release across a range of velocities (down the rows) and remaining-scope figures (across the columns). Build the single forecast cell (sprints = ROUNDUP(scope / velocity)) and then a native two-variable data table: row input = velocity {25, 30, 35}, column input = remaining scope {210, 240, 270}. The table must be a live data table, not typed-in numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Forecast cell = ROUNDUP(remaining_scope / velocity, 0). Base = ROUNDUP(240/30) = 8 sprints. The two-variable data table feeds velocity into the column-input cell and scope into the row-input cell. Corner/interior values (sprints = ceil(scope/velocity)): scope 210 @ vel 25 = ceil(8.4) = 9; scope 270 @ vel 35 = ceil(7.714) = 8; base scope 240 @ vel 30 = 8; worst case scope 270 @ vel 25 = ceil(10.8) = 11. Grading checks the table is a native array/data table plus three reconstructed corner/interior cells.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Forecast grid is a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - The sensitivity range is data-table/array-formula driven, not typed values.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base forecast cell = 8 sprints (ROUNDUP 240/30) - The single forecast formula uses integer round-up of scope/velocity.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Best case (scope 210, velocity 35) = 6 sprints - Low-scope high-velocity interior cell = ceil(210/35) = 6.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Worst case (scope 270, velocity 25) = 11 sprints - High-scope low-velocity corner = ceil(270/25) = 11.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Center base case (scope 240, velocity 30) = 8 sprints - Data table center cell agrees with the standalone forecast.
- **WSJF Backlog Prioritisation (Cost of Delay)** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: SAFe WSJF / Cost of Delay (Reinertsen)
  - _Measures:_ Computing Cost of Delay and WSJF to produce an economically-justified backlog sequence - the prioritisation discipline that separates value-driven delivery from loudest-stakeholder-wins.
  - _Scenario:_ A Qatari fintech, Doha Pay, must sequence three competing epics for its next Program Increment using Weighted Shortest Job First. Each epic is scored on the SAFe relative scale. Epic A: User-Business Value 8, Time Criticality 5, Risk Reduction/Opportunity Enablement 5, Job Size 5. Epic B: Value 13, Time Criticality 3, RR/OE 2, Job Size 3. Epic C: Value 5, Time Criticality 8, RR/OE 8, Job Size 8. WSJF = Cost of Delay / Job Size, where Cost of Delay = User-Business Value + Time Criticality + Risk Reduction/Opportunity Enablement. Compute each epic's WSJF and identify which epic is sequenced first (enter its WSJF as the 'top priority WSJF').
  - _Model answer:_ CoD = Value + Time Criticality + RR/OE. Epic A CoD = 8+5+5 = 18; WSJF = 18/5 = 3.60. Epic B CoD = 13+3+2 = 18; WSJF = 18/3 = 6.00. Epic C CoD = 5+8+8 = 21; WSJF = 21/8 = 2.625. Highest WSJF = Epic B at 6.00, so it is sequenced first; top priority WSJF field = 6.00. Tolerance allows rounding to 2-3 dp.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Epic A WSJF = 3.60 - CoD(18)/JobSize(5).
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Epic B WSJF = 6.00 - CoD(18)/JobSize(3).
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Epic C WSJF = 2.625 - CoD(21)/JobSize(8).
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Top-priority WSJF = 6.00 - Correct selection of the highest WSJF epic for first sequencing.

**Pillar - Hybrid Governance & Delivery Data Interrogation**

- **Agile-in-Stage-Gate Earned Value (CPI/SPI/EAC)** &nbsp; `Logic input` · advanced · 11.7 min · ref: PMI PMBOK 7 / Earned Value Management (EVM)
  - _Measures:_ Integrating agile delivery progress into programme-level Earned Value - the hybrid-governance competency that lets an agile train survive inside a fixed-budget, gated public-sector mandate.
  - _Scenario:_ Kuwait's Ministry of Finance runs a hybrid programme: an agile delivery train operates inside a stage-gated, fixed-budget governance wrapper, so the PMO still reports Earned Value at the gate. The release has a Budget at Completion (BAC) of AED 4,000,000. At the reporting checkpoint: Planned Value (PV) = AED 2,000,000, Earned Value (EV, from accepted story points x planned rate) = AED 1,800,000, and Actual Cost (AC) = AED 2,250,000. Compute the EVM indices and the forecast: Cost Performance Index (CPI = EV/AC), Schedule Performance Index (SPI = EV/PV), Estimate at Completion using the CPI method (EAC = BAC/CPI), and the Variance at Completion (VAC = BAC - EAC).
  - _Model answer:_ CPI = EV/AC = 1,800,000/2,250,000 = 0.80. SPI = EV/PV = 1,800,000/2,000,000 = 0.90. EAC (CPI method) = BAC/CPI = 4,000,000/0.80 = 5,000,000. VAC = BAC - EAC = 4,000,000 - 5,000,000 = -1,000,000 (an over-run; sign matters). All four reconcile from the same EV/AC/PV inputs.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - CPI = 0.80 - EV divided by AC.
    - `logic_value` (w2) - SPI = 0.90 - EV divided by PV.
    - `logic_value` (w3) - EAC = 5,000,000 AED - BAC divided by CPI (CPI-based forecast).
    - `logic_value` (w2) - VAC = -1,000,000 AED - BAC minus EAC, negative sign indicating over-run.
- **Sprint Board Data Interrogation (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA DMBOK / Agile Work-Item Reporting
  - _Measures:_ Querying a work-item tracker to produce completed-throughput reporting - filtering to Done, aggregating points by sprint, and ranking - the data-fluency behind every honest velocity report.
  - _Scenario:_ You have read access to a Jira-style work_items table for the National Bank of Bahrain delivery train. Columns: id (int), epic (text), assignee (text), status (text: 'To Do' \| 'In Progress' \| 'Done'), story_points (numeric), sprint (text). The delivery lead wants completed-throughput per sprint: for items that are Done, return total completed story points grouped by sprint, highest total first. Columns must be sprint, completed_points. Seed rows include items across sprints S1-S3 with a mix of statuses, so the query must filter to status = 'Done' before aggregating, exclude unfinished work, and order descending by the summed points.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT sprint, SUM(story_points) AS completed_points FROM work_items WHERE status = 'Done' GROUP BY sprint ORDER BY completed_points DESC, sprint. The WHERE filter on status='Done' is the discriminating step (To Do / In Progress rows must be excluded); GROUP BY sprint aggregates; ORDER BY the summed points descending (with sprint as a deterministic tiebreaker) gives the ranked completed-throughput. Master result set is order-sensitive.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master (Done-only completed points per sprint, ranked desc) - Correct status filter, sprint aggregation, and descending order against the master query.

---

### 6.3 Project Capital Budgeting, Estimation, & Cost Control

Hands-on sandbox for PMO capital budgeting and project cost control. The function's skills list was empty, so I proposed six GCC-grounded skills (capital investment appraisal/DCF-NPV-IRR, cost estimation & estimate classing, risk-based contingency & PERT, budget baselining / cost loading, earned value management, and project cost-ledger interrogation) and designed the gradable analytical slice to them. Three pillars, four blocks, four engines used (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql) so the sitting is varied and difficulty spans basic to advanced. Block 1 (spreadsheet) builds a 5-year discounted cash-flow appraisal for a Riyadh data-centre capex and resolves NPV / payback / cumulative DCF with a discount-factor build. Block 2 (advanced_spreadsheet) layers a two-variable NPV sensitivity data table across discount rate and capex overrun using a native data table. Block 3 (logic_input) does AACE-style three-point PERT estimation plus risk-weighted contingency and a contingency-loaded budget that reconciles. Block 4 (sql) computes earned value cost-control metrics (CPI/SPI/EAC drivers) from a seeded project cost ledger. Every block carries concrete AED/SAR figures, a real standard (PMI PMBOK/EVMS ANSI-748, AACE RP 17R-97 / 18R-97, CFA capital budgeting, IMA), a master-solution approach, and 3-6 weighted checkpoints mapped to the four allowed checkpoint kinds.

**Skills:** Capital Investment Appraisal (NPV / IRR / Payback / DCF) · Cost Estimation & AACE Estimate Classification · Risk-Based Contingency & Three-Point (PERT) Estimation · Budget Baselining & Cost Loading · Earned Value Management (EVM) & Cost Control · Project Cost-Ledger Interrogation & Reporting

**Engine fit:** Strong fit. Project capital budgeting and cost control are inherently quantitative, so all four auto-gradable engines apply cleanly with no need for soft-skill proxies. Capital investment appraisal maps to a spreadsheet DCF model (NPV, cumulative discounted cash flow, discounted payback) graded by exact cell values, with the discount-factor and net-cash-flow build forcing genuine modelling rather than a single plug. Sensitivity / stress testing maps to an advanced_spreadsheet two-variable data table on NPV (discount rate x capex overrun), graded on the native data-table being present (is_array_formula) plus corner and centre cell values. Estimation, contingency and budget baselining map to logic_input with labelled numeric fields (PERT expected cost, standard deviation, risk-weighted contingency, contingency-loaded budget) that must reconcile. Cost control / EVM maps to sql over a seeded project cost ledger to return per-work-package planned value, earned value and actual cost so CPI/SPI and variances fall out of an aggregation query. The only inherently non-gradable parts of this role (estimate-basis narratives, change-control judgement, governance write-ups) are deliberately excluded; the blueprint measures the demonstrable numeric core that underpins those judgements.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Capital Investment Appraisal & Stress Testing**

- **Discounted Cash-Flow Capital Appraisal (NPV / Discounted Payback)** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18 min · ref: PMI PMBOK 7th Ed. (Cost Management) / CFA Institute Capital Budgeting
  - _Measures:_ Building a fully linked DCF capital-appraisal model: discount factors from the WACC, present value of each year's net cash flow, cumulative discounted position, NPV and the discounted-payback read - demonstrating that the candidate can construct (not just read) an investment case.
  - _Scenario:_ VIFM Data Centre LLC is appraising a SAR 12,000,000 (000s shown as SAR 12,000) modular data-centre build in Riyadh for the King Abdullah Financial District. Year-0 capex outflow is SAR 12,000 (thousands). Net operating cash inflows are forecast at SAR 3,200 / 3,600 / 4,000 / 4,400 / 4,800 (thousands) for Years 1-5, with a SAR 1,500 terminal/residual value received in Year 5. The investment committee mandates a 12% nominal discount rate (WACC). The candidate must build the discount-factor row, the present-value-of-net-cash-flow row, the cumulative discounted cash flow, the project NPV, and the discounted payback indicator, so the appraisal fully links from the given assumptions.
  - _Model answer:_ Discount factor Yr t = 1/(1.12)^t -> 0.8929, 0.7972, 0.7118, 0.6355, 0.5674. Year-5 net cash flow includes the SAR 1,500 terminal value: 4,800+1,500 = 6,300. PV of net cash flows = 3,200*0.8929=2,857.1; 3,600*0.7972=2,869.9; 4,000*0.7118=2,847.1; 4,400*0.6355=2,796.3; 6,300*0.5674=3,574.8. Sum of PVs = 14,945.3 (approx). NPV = sum of PV inflows - 12,000 capex = 2,945.3 (approx, ~SAR 2,945 thousand). Cumulative discounted CF after Yr4 = 2,857.1+2,869.9+2,847.1+2,796.3 - 12,000 = -629.6 (still negative); after Yr5 = +2,945.3, so discounted payback falls in Year 5. Checkpoints target NPV, the Year-5 discounted cash flow (incl. terminal), the cumulative-after-Year-4 figure, and total PV of inflows.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Year-1 discount factor at 12% WACC - Discount factor correctly computed as 1/1.12 = 0.8929 (proves the factor row is rate-driven, not hardcoded).
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Year-5 discounted cash flow includes terminal value - PV of the Year-5 net cash flow of (4,800+1,500)=6,300 discounted at 0.5674 = ~3,574.8, confirming the terminal value was captured.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Total present value of net cash inflows - Sum of the five PV rows ~14,945 (thousands) - the inflow side of the appraisal links correctly.
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Project NPV at 12% - NPV = PV inflows - 12,000 capex = ~2,945 (thousand SAR), the headline investment decision metric.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Cumulative discounted cash flow after Year 4 - Cumulative discounted position after Year 4 is still negative (~ -630), proving discounted payback lands in Year 5.
- **Two-Variable NPV Sensitivity Data Table (Rate x Capex Overrun)** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: AFP FP&A Body of Knowledge (FPAC) / PMI PMBOK Risk & Cost
  - _Measures:_ Constructing a native two-variable sensitivity / stress matrix on a capital-appraisal NPV using a real data table (not hardcoded values), and reading the corner and base-case stress outcomes - the core of capex risk presentation to an investment committee.
  - _Scenario:_ Continuing the Riyadh data-centre case (PV of operating + terminal inflows = SAR 14,945 thousand, base capex SAR 12,000 thousand), the investment committee wants an NPV stress grid. The candidate models NPV = PV_inflows_at_rate - capex*(1+overrun). For the grid, treat the PV of inflows as fixed at SAR 14,945 (a base-case simplification stated in the brief) so NPV varies only with the capex-overrun column input, and build a native two-variable data table whose columns are capex-overrun {0%, 10%, 20%} and whose rows are an informational discount-rate label {10%, 12%, 14%}; the graded driver is the capex-overrun axis applied to base capex. The corner cell links to the live NPV formula. The candidate must use a native data table, not typed numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Base NPV (0% overrun) = 14,945 - 12,000 = 2,945. With capex overrun o applied to base capex 12,000: NPV(o) = 14,945 - 12,000*(1+o). At 0% overrun: 2,945. At 10% overrun: 14,945 - 13,200 = 1,745. At 20% overrun: 14,945 - 14,400 = 545. The two-variable data table (corner = live NPV cell) must populate from the native {=TABLE()} mechanism. Checkpoints: (1) is_array_formula on the table range to confirm a native data table; (2) base-case corner (0% overrun) = 2,945; (3) +10% overrun column = 1,745; (4) +20% overrun column = 545.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Uses a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - The grid range is populated by a native {=TABLE()} data table driven by the corner NPV formula and the column input cell, not typed constants.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Base-case NPV cell (0% capex overrun) - NPV at 0% overrun = 14,945 - 12,000 = 2,945 (thousand SAR), anchoring the grid to the live model.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - NPV at +10% capex overrun - NPV = 14,945 - 13,200 = 1,745, showing the overrun axis flows through correctly.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - NPV at +20% capex overrun (stress corner) - NPV = 14,945 - 14,400 = 545, the worst-case still-positive stress outcome the committee needs.

**Pillar - Cost Estimation & Risk-Based Contingency**

- **Three-Point (PERT) Estimation & Contingency-Loaded Budget** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: AACE International RP 17R-97 / 18R-97 (Estimate Classification) & PMI PMBOK Risk
  - _Measures:_ Applying the standard PERT/beta three-point formula to convert uncertain estimates into an expected cost, pricing a risk register into an EMV contingency, and rolling both into a defensible contingency-loaded budget baseline - the quantitative backbone of risk-based capital estimating.
  - _Scenario:_ A Dubai branch fit-out project (VIFM Facilities Co) has three major work packages estimated under uncertainty. The PMO must produce a PERT expected cost and a risk-weighted contingency for board approval. Work-package three-point estimates (Optimistic O / Most Likely M / Pessimistic P, in AED 000s): MEP works O=900, M=1,100, P=1,700; Civil/finishes O=600, M=800, P=1,000; IT/AV O=300, M=400, P=800. Separately, a risk register identifies two priced risks: a permit-delay risk with AED 250 impact at 40% probability, and a supply-chain risk with AED 600 impact at 25% probability. The candidate computes the PERT expected cost per the standard (O+4M+P)/6, the total PERT base estimate, the expected monetary value (EMV) contingency from the risk register, and the contingency-loaded budget baseline.
  - _Model answer:_ PERT expected = (O+4M+P)/6. MEP = (900+4*1,100+1,700)/6 = (900+4,400+1,700)/6 = 7,000/6 = 1,166.67. Civil = (600+4*800+1,000)/6 = (600+3,200+1,000)/6 = 4,800/6 = 800.00. IT/AV = (300+4*400+800)/6 = (300+1,600+800)/6 = 2,700/6 = 450.00. Total PERT base estimate = 1,166.67+800.00+450.00 = 2,416.67. EMV contingency = 250*0.40 + 600*0.25 = 100 + 150 = 250.00. Contingency-loaded budget baseline = 2,416.67 + 250.00 = 2,666.67 (AED 000s). Fields graded: MEP PERT cost, total PERT base estimate, EMV contingency, contingency-loaded budget (all reconcile).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - MEP work-package PERT expected cost - PERT (O+4M+P)/6 for MEP = 7,000/6 = 1,166.67 (AED 000s), proving correct application of the beta-distribution formula.
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total PERT base estimate (all three work packages) - Sum of the three PERT expected costs = 1,166.67+800+450 = 2,416.67, the pre-contingency project estimate.
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Risk-register EMV contingency - Expected monetary value = 250*0.40 + 600*0.25 = 250.00, the priced contingency reserve.
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Contingency-loaded budget baseline - Base estimate + EMV contingency = 2,416.67 + 250 = 2,666.67, the approved baseline that reconciles base + contingency.

**Pillar - Earned Value Cost Control & Ledger Interrogation**

- **Earned Value Metrics from the Project Cost Ledger (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: EVMS ANSI/EIA-748 / PMI PMBOK (Earned Value Management)
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating a project cost ledger to derive earned-value cost-control reporting - selecting and computing per-work-package cost variance (EV - AC) and ranking the exception list - the day-to-day SQL/reporting core of EVM cost control.
  - _Scenario:_ The PMO maintains a project cost ledger for a Jeddah commercial-tower programme (VIFM Construction Co). Each row records a work package with its planned value (PV / BCWS), earned value (EV / BCWP) and actual cost (AC / ACWP) in SAR. The cost-control lead must report, per work package, the cost variance (EV - AC) and surface where the programme is over budget. The candidate writes one query against the cost_ledger table to return each work package's planned value, earned value, actual cost and cost variance, ordered by cost variance ascending (most over-budget first), so the worst-performing packages appear at the top of the exception report.
  - _Model answer:_ Seed cost_ledger with work packages (wp, pv, ev, ac in SAR): WP-Structure (pv 4,000,000, ev 3,800,000, ac 4,200,000), WP-Facade (pv 2,500,000, ev 2,600,000, ac 2,450,000), WP-MEP (pv 3,000,000, ev 2,700,000, ac 3,100,000), WP-Finishes (pv 1,800,000, ev 1,900,000, ac 1,750,000), WP-Sitework (pv 1,200,000, ev 1,000,000, ac 1,300,000). Master query: SELECT wp, pv, ev, ac, (ev - ac) AS cost_variance FROM cost_ledger ORDER BY cost_variance ASC, wp. This yields cost variances: WP-Sitework -300,000; WP-MEP -400,000; WP-Structure -400,000; WP-Facade +150,000; WP-Finishes +150,000 - reordered ascending puts the over-budget packages (MEP/Structure at -400,000, Sitework -300,000) first. Single sql_result_match checkpoint, ordered=true, verifies the computed column and the exception ordering.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Per-work-package cost variance, ordered most over-budget first - Result set matches the master: wp, pv, ev, ac and computed cost_variance = ev - ac, ordered ascending so the most over-budget work packages surface first (exception report). Order-sensitive.

---

### 6.4 Enterprise Risk Management (ERM) & Change Management Execution

A 4-block hands-on sandbox for Enterprise Risk Management & Change Management Execution (PMO domain), built to FP&A-level rigour. The function's skills list was empty, so six GCC-grounded skills were proposed first. Three pillars: (1) Risk Quantification & the Register - a logic_input block applying inherent/residual scoring and ALE against a stated risk appetite for a UAE bank's core-banking migration; (2) Exposure, Reserves & Change Economics - a spreadsheet block building an Expected-Monetary-Value contingency reserve + risk-adjusted budget for a SAR transformation programme, plus an advanced_spreadsheet 2-variable data table stress-testing change-programme net benefit across adoption rate and benefit-per-user; (3) GRC Data Interrogation - a sql block aggregating open residual exposure by risk category from a seeded risk register. Three distinct engines, mixed difficulty (basic to advanced), all numbers independently verified. Frameworks referenced: COSO ERM 2017, ISO 31000:2018, PMI PMBOK / Practice Standard for Project Risk Management, Prosci/ADKAR + benefit realization, and DAMA DMBOK for the data layer.

**Skills:** Risk Identification, Scoring & the Risk Register (likelihood x impact, inherent vs residual) · Quantitative Risk Exposure (ALE, Expected Monetary Value, contingency & management reserve) · Risk Appetite, Tolerance & Residual-Risk Treatment · Change Adoption & Benefit-Realization Analytics (adoption curve, ROI, sensitivity) · Controls Effectiveness & KRI Monitoring · Risk & Incident Data Interrogation / GRC Reporting

**Engine fit:** Strong fit for the auto-gradable engines once the function is decomposed into its quantitative slice. ERM is inherently numeric (risk scoring, residual-risk arithmetic, annual-loss-expectancy, expected-monetary-value contingency reserves, exposure aggregation, risk-register interrogation) and maps cleanly to logic_input, spreadsheet and sql. The Change Management half is the softer half - the engines cannot grade stakeholder narratives, comms plans or sponsorship strategy, so I designed its measurable analytical slice instead: benefit-realization / NPV sensitivity of an adoption programme (advanced_spreadsheet 2-variable data table) where adoption rate and benefit-per-user drive net benefit. Honest limitation flagged: the assessment measures the QUANTITATIVE risk-and-change-economics competency (scoring, exposure, contingency, benefit modelling, register interrogation) - it does NOT measure qualitative change-leadership, stakeholder judgement, or written risk treatment rationale, which require the separate human-rated / MCQ layers. Engine mix used: logic_input + spreadsheet + advanced_spreadsheet + sql (3 distinct engine types across 4 blocks).

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Logic input, Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Risk Quantification & the Register**

- **Inherent vs Residual Risk Scoring & Appetite Breach** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 10 min · ref: COSO ERM 2017 / ISO 31000:2018 - Risk Assessment & Evaluation
  - _Measures:_ Computing inherent risk (Likelihood x Impact), applying control effectiveness to derive residual risk, evaluating residual scores against a stated risk appetite, and quantifying Annual Loss Expectancy (ALE = SLE x ARO).
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Gulf Bank (Dubai) is migrating to a new core-banking platform. The ERM team has logged three programme risks on the register, each scored on a 1-5 likelihood and 1-5 impact scale. Risk A 'Data migration corruption' (Likelihood 4, Impact 5) has assessed control effectiveness of 40%. Risk B 'Staff readiness gap' (Likelihood 3, Impact 4) has control effectiveness of 75%. Risk C 'Vendor SLA breach' (Likelihood 5, Impact 3) has control effectiveness of 20%. The Board's stated residual-risk appetite threshold is 10 (any residual score strictly above 10 must be escalated). Separately, for the top financial risk the team quantifies Annual Loss Expectancy: a single-loss expectancy of AED 2,000,000 with an annualized rate of occurrence of 0.30.
  - _Model answer:_ Inherent = Likelihood x Impact. Residual = Inherent x (1 - control effectiveness). Risk A: 4x5=20, residual 20x(1-0.40)=12.0. Risk B: 3x4=12, residual 12x(1-0.75)=3.0. Risk C: 5x3=15, residual 15x(1-0.20)=12.0. Appetite breach count = number of residual scores strictly above 10 = Risk A (12) and Risk C (12) = 2. ALE = SLE x ARO = 2,000,000 x 0.30 = 600,000.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Risk A residual score (inherent 20 x (1-0.40)) = 12.0 - Applies control effectiveness to inherent score correctly
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Risk B residual score (12 x (1-0.75)) = 3.0 - Residual calculation reproducible across a well-controlled risk
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Risk C residual score (15 x (1-0.20)) = 12.0 - Residual calculation on a high-likelihood low-control risk
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Count of risks above appetite (residual > 10) = 2 - Evaluates residual exposure against the stated risk appetite threshold
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Annual Loss Expectancy (2,000,000 x 0.30) = 600,000 - Quantifies expected annual loss from SLE and ARO

**Pillar - Exposure, Reserves & Change Economics**

- **Expected Monetary Value Contingency Reserve & Risk-Adjusted Budget** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 15 min · ref: PMI PMBOK / Practice Standard for Project Risk Management - EMV & Reserve Analysis
  - _Measures:_ Building an Expected Monetary Value reserve model: deriving per-risk EMV (probability x impact), aggregating to a contingency reserve, computing a percentage-based management reserve, and assembling a risk-adjusted programme budget.
  - _Scenario:_ Al-Faisaliah Group (Riyadh) is running a SAR 25,000,000 enterprise transformation programme. The risk register lists four quantified risks with a probability and a monetary impact each (all in SAR): Vendor delay (probability 0.40, impact 1,500,000); Scope creep (probability 0.55, impact 900,000); Integration failure (probability 0.25, impact 4,000,000); Regulatory change (probability 0.15, impact 2,000,000). The PMO sizes the contingency reserve as the sum of Expected Monetary Values, and sets a management reserve at 10% of the base programme budget. The candidate completes the EMV column, the contingency reserve total, the management reserve, and the total risk-adjusted budget (base + contingency + management reserve).
  - _Model answer:_ EMV per risk = probability x impact. Vendor delay 0.40x1,500,000=600,000; Scope creep 0.55x900,000=495,000; Integration failure 0.25x4,000,000=1,000,000; Regulatory change 0.15x2,000,000=300,000. Contingency reserve = SUM of EMVs = 2,395,000. Management reserve = 0.10 x 25,000,000 = 2,500,000. Total risk-adjusted budget = 25,000,000 + 2,395,000 + 2,500,000 = 29,895,000.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - EMV Integration failure (0.25 x 4,000,000) = 1,000,000 - Correct per-risk EMV on the largest-impact line
    - `cell_value` (w1) - EMV Scope creep (0.55 x 900,000) = 495,000 - Per-risk EMV with a non-round probability
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Contingency reserve (sum of all EMVs) = 2,395,000 - Aggregates per-risk EMVs into a contingency reserve
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Management reserve (10% x 25,000,000) = 2,500,000 - Computes a percentage-based management reserve distinct from contingency
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Total risk-adjusted budget (25,000,000 + 2,395,000 + 2,500,000) = 29,895,000 - Assembles base, contingency and management reserve into a final risk-adjusted budget
- **Change Adoption Benefit Sensitivity (2-Variable Data Table)** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 16.7 min · ref: Prosci ADKAR / PMI Benefits Realization Management - Adoption & Benefit Modelling
  - _Measures:_ Constructing a native two-variable data table to stress-test change-programme benefit realization, linking the corner cell to a live net-benefit formula and validating the adoption x benefit grid.
  - _Scenario:_ Qatar National Holding is rolling out a new ERP to 2,000 staff. The change team models net annual benefit as: (Users x Adoption rate x Benefit per user) - Annual programme cost, where Users = 2,000 and Annual programme cost = AED 1,800,000. The base case assumes a 70% adoption rate and AED 1,500 benefit per adopting user. The PMO wants a two-variable data table stress-testing net annual benefit across adoption rates (columns: 50%, 70%, 90%) and benefit-per-user (rows: 1,000, 1,500, 2,000). The candidate must build a native data table (not hardcoded values) referencing the base-case formula.
  - _Model answer:_ Net benefit = 2,000 x adoption x benefit_per_user - 1,800,000. Base case (0.70, 1,500) = 2,000 x 0.70 x 1,500 - 1,800,000 = 300,000. The corner cell links to the base-case net-benefit formula; the data table re-runs it with adoption as the column input and benefit-per-user as the row input. Low corner (0.50, 1,000) = 2,000 x 0.50 x 1,000 - 1,800,000 = -800,000. Centre (0.70, 1,500) = 300,000. High corner (0.90, 2,000) = 2,000 x 0.90 x 2,000 - 1,800,000 = 1,800,000.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Grid is a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded numbers) - Uses a real {=TABLE()} data table driven by the adoption and benefit inputs
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner net benefit (adoption 50%, benefit 1,000) = -800,000 - Data table reproduces the downside scenario including a negative result
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre / base case (adoption 70%, benefit 1,500) = 300,000 - Data table interior equals the live base-case formula
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner net benefit (adoption 90%, benefit 2,000) = 1,800,000 - Data table reproduces the upside scenario

**Pillar - GRC Data Interrogation & Reporting**

- **Open Residual-Exposure by Risk Category (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: DAMA International (DMBOK) / GRC Risk Register Reporting
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating a GRC risk register with a single aggregate query: filtering by status, grouping by category, summing residual exposure, counting risks, and applying a deterministic multi-key sort for a board report.
  - _Scenario:_ A GCC sovereign entity's GRC platform stores a risk register in a table risk_register(id int, category text, status text, residual_score numeric). The Chief Risk Officer needs a board pack view: for OPEN risks only, the count of risks and the total residual exposure per category, ordered by total residual exposure highest first (ties broken alphabetically by category). The seeded data contains Operational, Financial, Compliance and Strategic risks with a mix of open and closed statuses.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT category, COUNT(*) AS open_count, SUM(residual_score) AS total_residual FROM risk_register WHERE status = 'open' GROUP BY category ORDER BY total_residual DESC, category. Filtering to open rows and aggregating yields: Compliance (3 risks, 26.0), Financial (2 risks, 26.0), Operational (2 risks, 20.0), Strategic (1 risk, 20.0). The ORDER BY total_residual DESC, category tiebreak makes the result fully deterministic (Compliance before Financial at 26.0; Operational before Strategic at 20.0).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result set matches master: per-category open count + total residual, sorted by total desc then category - Filters to open risks, groups and aggregates by category, and orders deterministically for the board pack

---

## Supply Chain & Procurement

> **Domain review** - engine coverage needs attention. Engine/checkpoint validity: all four blueprints use only the four implemented auto-gradable engines (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql) and every implied checkpoint kind maps correctly to its engine (cell_value/is_array_formula -> spreadsheet/advanced_spreadsheet; logic_value -> logic_input; sql_result_match -> sql). The single weight-1 sql_result_match per SQL block matches the FP&A reference pattern and is acceptable, not a defect. Engine-fit framing is honest across all four - supply chain is genuinely quantitative, the gradable analytical spine (TCO/landed cost, replenishment math, weighted scorecards, spend interrogation) is correctly identified, and the non-gradable slivers (negotiation narrative, relationship judgement, audit-finding drafting) are explicitly excluded. No false claims of gradability.  Structural compliance: 7.1 PASSES cleanly (3 pillars, 4 blocks, all 4 engine types, difficulty intermediate/advanced/intermediate/basic). 7.3 PASSES (3 pillars, 4 blocks, 4 engine types) but has NO basic-difficulty block (intermediate/advanced/advanced/intermediate) - acceptable but the mix skews hard. 7.2 PASSES the hard rules (3 pillars, 4 blocks, 3 engine types >=2) but uses only 3 of 4 engines (no plain spreadsheet), runs two consecutive logic_input blocks, and has no basic block (advanced/intermediate/intermediate/intermediate). 7.4 FAILS the hard 3-5 block rule with 6 blocks, and is engine-imbalanced: 4 of 6 blocks are logic_input (only 3 distinct engine types across 6 blocks), so the sitting is monotonous despite the high block count.  Domain-level coherence (cross-function): the four functions are highly repetitive against each other. The same primitives recur in nearly every blueprint - a price/FX x volume/freight landed-cost two-variable data table (7.1, 7.2, 7.3, 7.4), a weighted vendor/supplier scorecard (7.1, 7.2, 7.4), EOQ/reorder-point/safety-stock math (7.2, 7.3, 7.4), and a maverick/off-contract spend SQL query (7.2, 7.4). A candidate sitting two or more of these functions would face near-duplicate tasks, which weakens differentiation between the four roles and the defensibility of role-specific scores. The functions need more distinct scenarios per role (e.g. 7.3 logistics could lean into network/transport-cost optimization, fill-rate/turns, DC throughput; 7.4 risk/compliance could lean into concentration/HHI indices, SLA-penalty waterfalls, obligation-expiry surveillance) rather than re-skinning the shared sourcing primitives.
>
> - _(high)_ 7.4: Has 6 blocks - violates the hard 3-5 blocks-per-function rule. Must drop at least one block. Recommend cutting one of the redundant logic_input blocks (e.g. fold the SLA Penalty & Liability-Cap Exposure Calculator into the Single-Source Continuity block, or drop the standalone Weighted Supplier Risk Scorecard if risk scoring can be combined) to reach <=5.
> - _(medium)_ 7.4: Engine imbalance: 4 of 6 blocks are logic_input (Weighted Supplier Risk Scorecard, Single-Source Continuity, SLA Penalty, plus the contract-leakage figures), giving only 3 distinct engine types across 6 blocks. The sitting is monotonous - too many small numeric-field tasks in a row. After cutting to 5 blocks, ensure no more than ~2 logic_input blocks remain and the spread/advanced_spreadsheet/sql blocks are retained for variety.
> - _(low)_ 7.2: Uses only 3 of the 4 engines (no plain 'spreadsheet' block) and runs two consecutive logic_input blocks (Weighted Vendor Scorecard then EOQ/Reorder/Safety Stock). Meets the >=2 engine-type minimum but is thinner than 7.1/7.3. Consider converting the EOQ/Reorder/Safety Stock block to a linked-cell 'spreadsheet' replenishment model (as 7.3 does) to add a 4th engine and break up the logic_input run.
> - _(low)_ 7.2: No basic-difficulty block (advanced/intermediate/intermediate/intermediate). Difficulty mix is acceptable but lacks an entry-level on-ramp; consider making the SQL maverick-spend block 'basic' (a straightforward GROUP BY/filter) to broaden the mix.
> - _(low)_ 7.3: No basic-difficulty block (intermediate/advanced/advanced/intermediate) - the sitting skews toward hard. Consider dropping the EOQ/Reorder-Point model or the OTIF SQL block to 'basic' for a more graduated difficulty curve, matching FP&A's basic SQL anchor.
> - _(medium)_ 7.1: Strongest, cleanest blueprint (all 4 engines, valid 3/4 structure, good difficulty curve). Only domain-level concern: its TCO bid-comparison, landed-cost sensitivity table, and weighted vendor scorecard are duplicated almost verbatim in 7.2 and 7.4, so the four functions are not sufficiently differentiated. Diversify scenarios across the domain rather than re-skinning these shared primitives.
>
> _Recommendations:_ Priority fixes: (1) 7.4 MUST be cut from 6 blocks to <=5 to satisfy the hard 3-5 rule - drop or merge one of its four logic_input blocks, which also fixes its engine imbalance in one move. After the cut, target at least 3 distinct engine types with no more than ~2 logic_input blocks. (2) Address domain-level repetition: the landed-cost/FX x volume/freight two-variable data table, the weighted vendor/supplier scorecard, and EOQ/reorder/safety-stock math each appear in 3-4 of the four functions, so a candidate taking multiple sittings sees near-identical tasks. Re-theme the shared primitives per role - 7.3 (logistics) toward transport/network cost optimization, fill-rate, turns, and DC throughput; 7.4 (risk/compliance) toward supplier-concentration/HHI indices, SLA-penalty waterfalls, and obligation-expiry surveillance - so each role's analytical core is genuinely distinct. (3) Optional polish: add a basic-difficulty block to 7.2 and 7.3 (e.g. a straightforward GROUP BY SQL) for a graduated difficulty curve matching the FP&A anchor, and add a plain 'spreadsheet' block to 7.2 so it exercises all four engines. Once 7.4's block count is corrected, all four functions clear the hard structural rules; the remaining items are coherence/quality improvements rather than blockers.

### 7.1 Strategic Sourcing, Category Management, & Vendor Negotiations

Hands-on sandbox for Strategic Sourcing (node 7.1, supply_chain). The function's skills list was empty in functions.json, so six realistic CIPS/PMBOK-grounded skills were proposed (spend analysis, TCO modelling, weighted vendor scorecards, should-cost/price modelling, savings quantification, supplier-spend SQL). Procurement is inherently quantitative, so all four engines fit cleanly with no soft-skill proxying needed. Three pillars, four blocks, three engines (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql) mixing basic/intermediate/advanced: (1) Cost Engineering & Bid Analytics - a multi-element TCO comparison of two GCC bids [spreadsheet] and a two-variable annual-landed-cost sensitivity data table [advanced_spreadsheet]; (2) Vendor Evaluation & Negotiation Math - a weighted three-vendor scorecard plus negotiated-savings percentage [logic_input]; (3) Category Spend Interrogation - spend-per-category aggregation over a seeded purchase-order ledger [sql]. Every checkpoint figure was hand-verified; all amounts in AED with GCC-sounding entities.

**Skills:** Spend Analysis & Category Segmentation · Total Cost of Ownership (TCO) Modelling · Weighted Vendor Scorecard & Bid Evaluation · Should-Cost & Price Modelling · Savings Quantification & Negotiation Levers · Supplier-Spend Data Interrogation

**Engine fit:** Strong fit across all four engines - Strategic Sourcing is a quantitative discipline, so no soft-skill proxying was required. TCO comparison and savings math are exact arithmetic graded by cell_value/logic_value; the price x volume landed-cost surface is a textbook native two-variable data table (advanced_spreadsheet / is_array_formula + corner cell_values); supplier-spend aggregation is the canonical GROUP BY ... ORDER BY total DESC query (sql_result_match). The only genuinely non-gradable parts of the role - the qualitative negotiation tactics, relationship management, and category-strategy narrative - are deliberately excluded; the sandbox measures the analytical spine (cost engineering, weighted bid evaluation, spend interrogation) that underpins defensible sourcing decisions, which is exactly the auto-gradable slice.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Cost Engineering & Bid Analytics**

- **Total Cost of Ownership (TCO) Bid Comparison** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: CIPS Global Standard / PMI PMBOK Procurement Management
  - _Measures:_ Total cost of ownership modelling - moving beyond unit price to the full lifecycle cost stack (acquisition + freight + install + recurring maintenance over the horizon + training - residual), then quantifying the award decision and the per-unit cost.
  - _Scenario:_ Emaar Facilities Co (Dubai) is sourcing 500 industrial HVAC chillers over a 5-year horizon and has two shortlisted bids. Build the full Total Cost of Ownership for each bid so the lowest-TCO award is defensible. Bid A (Gulf Cooling Systems): unit price AED 1,200 x 500 units; one-off freight & logistics AED 45,000; installation AED 30,000; annual maintenance AED 25,000 for each of 5 years; training AED 12,000; end-of-life residual recovery (a credit) AED -20,000. Bid B (Falcon Thermal LLC): unit price AED 1,050 x 500 units; freight AED 80,000; installation AED 55,000; annual maintenance AED 48,000 x 5 years; training AED 18,000; residual recovery AED -10,000. Enter the line subtotals, each bid's TCO, the lowest TCO, the TCO gap between the two bids, and the winning bid's TCO per unit.
  - _Model answer:_ Bid A purchase = 1200 x 500 = 600,000; 5yr maintenance = 25,000 x 5 = 125,000; TCO_A = 600,000 + 45,000 + 30,000 + 125,000 + 12,000 - 20,000 = 792,000. Bid B purchase = 1050 x 500 = 525,000; 5yr maintenance = 48,000 x 5 = 240,000; TCO_B = 525,000 + 80,000 + 55,000 + 240,000 + 18,000 - 10,000 = 908,000. Lowest TCO = Bid A = 792,000. TCO gap = 908,000 - 792,000 = 116,000. Winning (Bid A) TCO per unit = 792,000 / 500 = 1,584.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Bid A 5-year maintenance subtotal (AED 125,000) - Correctly annualises recurring maintenance over the 5-year horizon rather than counting it once.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Bid A total cost of ownership (AED 792,000) - Assembles the full TCO stack for Bid A including the residual credit.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Bid B total cost of ownership (AED 908,000) - Assembles the full TCO stack for Bid B - tests that the higher freight/maintenance is captured.
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Lowest TCO across the two bids (AED 792,000) - Identifies the defensible lowest-lifecycle-cost award, not the lowest unit price (Bid B is cheaper per unit but costs more overall).
    - `cell_value` (w1) - TCO gap between bids (AED 116,000) - Quantifies the magnitude of the award advantage for stakeholder justification.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Winning bid TCO per unit (AED 1,584) - Normalises lifecycle cost to a per-unit basis for benchmarking.
- **Landed-Cost Sensitivity Data Table (Price x Volume)** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: AFP / FPAC FP&A Body of Knowledge; CIPS Cost & Price Analysis
  - _Measures:_ Should-cost / price-sensitivity modelling using a native two-variable data table - stress-testing a frame-agreement commitment across the two negotiation levers (unit price and committed volume) the buyer actually controls.
  - _Scenario:_ ADNOC Distribution's category team is forecasting the annual landed cost of a packaging consumable before locking a frame agreement. Annual landed cost = (unit price + freight per unit) x annual volume, with freight fixed at AED 40 per unit. Base case: unit price AED 1,050, annual volume 12,000 units. Build a two-variable data table for annual landed cost across unit-price columns {1000, 1050, 1100} and annual-volume rows {10000, 12000, 14000}. It must be a native data table driven by the base model cell, not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Base model cell = (unit_price + freight_per_unit) x volume = (1050 + 40) x 12,000 = 1,090 x 12,000 = 13,080,000. The data table re-runs that single formula across the axes. Low corner (price 1000, vol 10000) = (1000+40) x 10000 = 10,400,000. Base/centre (price 1050, vol 12000) = 13,080,000. High corner (price 1100, vol 14000) = (1100+40) x 14000 = 1,140 x 14000 = 15,960,000.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sensitivity grid is a native data table (not hardcoded) - Candidate used a genuine two-variable {=TABLE()} array driven by the model cell, the auditable way to build a sensitivity surface.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base-model annual landed cost (AED 13,080,000) - The driving formula (unit price + freight) x volume is correct before the table fans it out.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner - price 1000, volume 10000 (AED 10,400,000) - Best-case landed cost evaluates correctly at the table's low corner.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre case - price 1050, volume 12000 (AED 13,080,000) - Interior cell reconciles to the base model.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner - price 1100, volume 14000 (AED 15,960,000) - Worst-case landed cost evaluates correctly at the table's high corner.

**Pillar - Vendor Evaluation & Negotiation Math**

- **Weighted Vendor Scorecard & Negotiated Savings** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: CIPS Supplier Selection & Evaluation; PMI PMBOK Source Selection Criteria
  - _Measures:_ Weighted multi-criteria bid evaluation (defensible, auditable source selection) plus negotiation-outcome quantification - the two numeric backbones of a sourcing recommendation.
  - _Scenario:_ STC (Saudi Telecom) is awarding a managed-services contract using a weighted evaluation across four criteria: Price (weight 0.40), Quality (0.25), Delivery / Lead-time (0.20), and Compliance & ESG (0.15) - weights sum to 1.00; each criterion scored 1-10. Vendor X scored Price 8, Quality 7, Delivery 6, Compliance 9. Vendor Y scored Price 6, Quality 9, Delivery 8, Compliance 8. Vendor Z scored Price 9, Quality 6, Delivery 7, Compliance 6. Separately, the chosen vendor's baseline annual price was SAR 2,400,000 and it was negotiated down to SAR 2,148,000. Compute each vendor's weighted total score and the negotiated savings percentage.
  - _Model answer:_ Weighted score = sum(score x weight). Vendor X = 8x0.40 + 7x0.25 + 6x0.20 + 9x0.15 = 3.20 + 1.75 + 1.20 + 1.35 = 7.50. Vendor Y = 6x0.40 + 9x0.25 + 8x0.20 + 8x0.15 = 2.40 + 2.25 + 1.60 + 1.20 = 7.45. Vendor Z = 9x0.40 + 6x0.25 + 7x0.20 + 6x0.15 = 3.60 + 1.50 + 1.40 + 0.90 = 7.40. Winner = Vendor X (7.50). Savings % = (2,400,000 - 2,148,000) / 2,400,000 = 252,000 / 2,400,000 = 0.105 = 10.5%.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Vendor X weighted score (7.50) - Applies the four weights correctly to the winning bid - the highest-stakes computation.
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Vendor Y weighted score (7.45) - Weighted score for the runner-up; tests the score does not collapse to a simple average.
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Vendor Z weighted score (7.40) - Weighted score for the third vendor; confirms ranking is tight and correctly ordered.
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Negotiated savings percentage (10.5%) - Computes savings as a percentage of baseline spend, the standard procurement KPI.

**Pillar - Category Spend Interrogation**

- **Spend-by-Category Aggregation (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · basic · 10 min · ref: DAMA International (DMBOK); CIPS Spend Analysis & Category Management
  - _Measures:_ Spend analysis / category segmentation via relational aggregation - the entry point of any category strategy is knowing where the money goes, ranked.
  - _Scenario:_ Mubadala's procurement analytics team maintains a purchase_orders ledger (id, vendor, category, amount, po_date) of approved spend. To prioritise category-management effort, write one query returning total committed spend per category, highest spend first. Required output columns: category, total.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT category, SUM(amount) AS total FROM purchase_orders GROUP BY category ORDER BY total DESC, category. With the seeded rows (IT Hardware 1,200,000 + 450,000 = 1,650,000; Professional Services 600,000 + 900,000 = 1,500,000; Facilities 320,000 + 180,000 = 500,000; Logistics 250,000 + 150,000 = 400,000) the ordered result is IT Hardware 1,650,000; Professional Services 1,500,000; Facilities 500,000; Logistics 400,000.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Category totals returned highest-spend-first - Query groups by category, sums amount, and orders descending so the high-value categories surface first for prioritisation.

### 7.2 Tactical Procurement, Purchase Requisition, & PO Lifecycle Control

Blueprint for the tactical-procurement function (node 7.2), which had no seeded skills, so six realistic GCC-grounded skills were proposed first: (1) Purchase Requisition & PO Lifecycle Control, (2) 3-Way Match & Invoice/GRN Reconciliation, (3) Total Cost of Ownership & Landed-Cost Costing, (4) Inventory Replenishment (EOQ, Reorder Point, Safety Stock), (5) Vendor Selection & Weighted Scorecards, (6) Spend Analytics & PO Compliance Reporting. The function is strongly quantitative/operational, so all four engines fit cleanly. Design: 3 pillars, 4 blocks, three engines used. Pillar 1 (Sourcing & Award Economics) holds an advanced_spreadsheet two-variable landed-cost sensitivity table (FX rate x freight) and a logic_input weighted vendor scorecard. Pillar 2 (Replenishment & Inventory Control) holds a logic_input EOQ / reorder-point / safety-stock block. Pillar 3 (PO Lifecycle Governance & Spend Compliance) holds a SQL block over a seeded purchase_orders ledger detecting maverick/over-tolerance spend. Frameworks referenced: CIPS, IMA, APICS/ASCM CPIM, ISO 9001 procurement controls, AP 3-way-match control standards. Concrete figures use AED/SAR and real-sounding GCC entities.

**Skills:** Purchase Requisition & PO Lifecycle Control · 3-Way Match & Invoice/GRN Reconciliation · Total Cost of Ownership & Landed-Cost Costing · Inventory Replenishment (EOQ, Reorder Point, Safety Stock) · Vendor Selection & Weighted Scorecards · Spend Analytics & PO Compliance Reporting

**Engine fit:** Tactical procurement is an inherently quantitative, transactional discipline, so it is a strong fit for all four auto-gradable engines with no soft-skill compromise needed. The landed-cost / TCO comparison maps to advanced_spreadsheet as a native two-variable data table (FX rate x freight cost driving total landed unit cost). Weighted vendor scorecards, EOQ, reorder point and safety stock are closed-form formulas that map cleanly to logic_input numeric fields. PO lifecycle governance (maverick spend, over-tolerance invoicing, requisition-to-PO leakage, expiring contracts) is naturally relational and maps to SQL over a seeded purchase_orders / requisitions ledger. The only genuinely non-gradable slivers of this role - negotiation behaviour and supplier-relationship judgement - are deliberately excluded; this sandbox measures the analytical and control mechanics (costing accuracy, replenishment math, three-way-match logic, spend-compliance detection) that are the demonstrable technical core of the requisition-to-PO buyer. No engine limitation flag required.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Adv. Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Sourcing & Award Economics**

- **Landed-Cost Sensitivity Matrix (FX x Freight)** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: CIPS Global Standard / Incoterms 2020 (Landed Cost)
  - _Measures:_ Building a native two-variable sensitivity / stress-test data table for import landed-cost under FX and freight volatility, instead of hardcoding numbers - the core award-economics modelling skill for a GCC import buyer.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Industrial Supplies LLC (Dubai) is importing 5,000 control valves from a German vendor for a refinery contract. The quoted ex-works unit price is EUR 80. The buyer must build a two-variable data table showing the total LANDED UNIT COST in AED across three EUR->AED FX rates (3.90 / 4.00 / 4.10) and three freight-and-duty cost scenarios (AED 12 / 18 / 24 per unit). Base model: landed unit cost = (ex-works EUR price x FX rate) + freight-and-duty per unit. Base case is FX 4.00 and freight AED 18, giving 80 x 4.00 + 18 = AED 338.00. The sitting requires wiring the base formula, the corner link, and a native two-variable data table across the 3x3 grid (rows = freight per unit, columns = FX rate).
  - _Model answer:_ Base landed unit cost in B5 = (B1 ex-works EUR price 80) x (B2 FX rate 4.00) + (B3 freight per unit 18) = 338.00. Corner cell B8 links to B5 (=B5). Column headers C8:E8 are FX rates 3.90 / 4.00 / 4.10; row headers A9:A11 are freight per unit 12 / 18 / 24. The candidate selects C9:E11 and creates a native two-variable data table with row input = FX rate cell (B2) and column input = freight cell (B3). Interior results: at FX 3.90 the EUR component is 80x3.90=312, so freight 12->324 (C9), 18->330, 24->336; at FX 4.00 the EUR component is 320, freight 12->332, 18->338 (D10), 24->344; at FX 4.10 the EUR component is 328, freight 12->340, 18->346, 24->352 (E11). Checks land on the array-formula presence plus the three corner/interior cells C9=324, D10=338, E11=352.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Uses a native two-variable data table {=TABLE()} for the landed-cost grid (not hardcoded) - Candidate built a real data table over C9:E11 rather than typing values - the engineering skill, not just the arithmetic
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base landed unit cost (FX 4.00, freight 18) = AED 338.00 - Base costing formula (ex-works EUR x FX + freight) is wired correctly
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (FX 3.90, freight 12) = AED 324.00 - Lower-bound stress case computed correctly
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre case (FX 4.00, freight 18) = AED 338.00 inside the table - Data-table interior reproduces the base case, proving correct row/column input wiring
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (FX 4.10, freight 24) = AED 352.00 - Upper-bound stress case computed correctly
- **Weighted Vendor Scorecard & Award Decision** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: CIPS Supplier Evaluation / ISO 9001 Supplier Selection
  - _Measures:_ Applying a weighted-criteria evaluation model (sum of weight x raw score) to a multi-vendor award decision - the defensible-sourcing scoring mechanic required to justify a PO award under audit.
  - _Scenario:_ Saudi National Facilities Co. (Riyadh) is awarding an annual MRO supply contract and must score three shortlisted vendors on a weighted scorecard. The criteria weights are: Price 40%, Quality 25%, Delivery/Lead-Time 20%, After-Sales & Compliance 15% (weights sum to 100%). Raw scores are on a 0-100 scale. Vendor Al-Faisal Trading: Price 90, Quality 70, Delivery 80, After-Sales 60. Vendor Gulf Procure Hub: Price 70, Quality 95, Delivery 85, After-Sales 90. Vendor Najd Industrial: Price 80, Quality 80, Delivery 70, After-Sales 75. The candidate computes each vendor's weighted total score and identifies the award by entering the winning weighted score.
  - _Model answer:_ Weighted score = 0.40xPrice + 0.25xQuality + 0.20xDelivery + 0.15xAfterSales. Al-Faisal = 0.40x90 + 0.25x70 + 0.20x80 + 0.15x60 = 36 + 17.5 + 16 + 9 = 78.50. Gulf Procure Hub = 0.40x70 + 0.25x95 + 0.20x85 + 0.15x90 = 28 + 23.75 + 17 + 13.5 = 82.25. Najd Industrial = 0.40x80 + 0.25x80 + 0.20x70 + 0.15x75 = 32 + 20 + 14 + 11.25 = 77.25. Highest weighted score = Gulf Procure Hub at 82.25, which is the awarded vendor's score.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Al-Faisal Trading weighted score = 78.50 - Correct weighted-sum computation for vendor 1
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Gulf Procure Hub weighted score = 82.25 - Correct weighted-sum computation for the winning vendor
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Najd Industrial weighted score = 77.25 - Correct weighted-sum computation for vendor 3
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Winning (awarded) weighted score = 82.25 - Candidate correctly identifies the highest-scoring vendor as the award - the decision output

**Pillar - Replenishment & Inventory Control**

- **EOQ, Reorder Point & Safety Stock** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: APICS / ASCM CPIM (Inventory Management)
  - _Measures:_ Core inventory-replenishment parameterisation - EOQ (Wilson formula), average daily demand, safety stock, and reorder point - the calculations that drive automatic PO triggers in a tactical procurement system.
  - _Scenario:_ Abu Dhabi Maintenance Stores manages a critical spare (hydraulic seal kit). Annual demand is 9,600 units, ordered evenly across the year. The fixed ordering cost per purchase order is AED 75. The annual holding (carrying) cost is AED 6 per unit. Supplier lead time is 10 working days; the store operates 240 working days per year, and average daily demand is therefore 9,600 / 240 = 40 units/day. Management requires a safety stock equal to 5 days of average demand. The candidate computes the Economic Order Quantity, the average daily demand, the safety stock, and the reorder point.
  - _Model answer:_ Average daily demand = annual demand / working days = 9,600 / 240 = 40 units/day. EOQ = sqrt(2 x D x S / H) = sqrt(2 x 9,600 x 75 / 6) = sqrt(1,440,000 / 6) = sqrt(240,000) = 489.90 units (accept 489.9, tolerance covers rounding). Safety stock = 5 days x 40 units/day = 200 units. Reorder point = (average daily demand x lead time) + safety stock = (40 x 10) + 200 = 400 + 200 = 600 units.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Average daily demand = 40 units/day - Correct conversion of annual demand to daily run-rate over working days
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Economic Order Quantity (EOQ) = 489.90 units - Correct application of the Wilson EOQ formula sqrt(2DS/H)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Safety stock = 200 units - Correct days-of-cover safety-stock computation
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Reorder point = 600 units - Correct reorder-point = lead-time demand + safety stock - the PO-trigger output

**Pillar - PO Lifecycle Governance & Spend Compliance**

- **Maverick & Over-Tolerance Spend Detection (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: IMA / 3-Way-Match Control Standard (AP-Procurement Controls)
  - _Measures:_ Relational interrogation of a PO ledger to surface three-way-match / tolerance breaches and aggregate spend-compliance exposure by department - the data skill behind a procurement-controls audit.
  - _Scenario:_ Qatar Energy Services Procurement maintains a purchase_orders ledger. Each row records the PO, the buying department, the contracted vendor, whether the PO was raised against an approved contract (on_contract boolean), the PO value in QAR, and the invoiced value in QAR. Compliance policy: any PO where the invoiced amount exceeds the PO value by more than 5% is an over-tolerance breach. The candidate must write ONE query that returns, per department, the total invoiced QAR of all OVER-TOLERANCE breaches (invoiced > po_value x 1.05), highest exposure first - so the audit team can target the worst-offending departments.
  - _Model answer:_ Filter rows where invoiced_amount > po_value * 1.05 (the over-tolerance breach condition), then GROUP BY department summing invoiced_amount, ORDER BY the summed exposure descending. Master query: SELECT department, SUM(invoiced_amount) AS total_breach FROM purchase_orders WHERE invoiced_amount > po_value * 1.05 GROUP BY department ORDER BY total_breach DESC, department. Result set is matched ordered (exposure descending, department as tiebreaker). Seed data is constructed so two departments have qualifying breaches and at least one department has only within-tolerance POs (excluded), testing both the tolerance filter and the aggregation/ordering.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Query returns per-department over-tolerance breach exposure, highest first (matches master, ordered) - Candidate correctly encoded the >5% tolerance filter, the per-department aggregation, and the descending-exposure ordering in a single query

---

### 7.3 Logistics, Warehousing, & Inventory Distribution Networks

Hands-on sandbox blueprint for the Logistics, Warehousing & Inventory Distribution Networks function (node 7.3, supply_chain). The function had no skills_en or descriptor in functions.json, so I first proposed 6 GCC-grounded skills: Inventory Planning & Replenishment (EOQ / safety stock / reorder point), Warehouse Operations & Slotting Productivity, Transportation & Distribution Network Cost Optimization, Service-Level & Fill-Rate Analytics, Cold-Chain / Perishable & Demand-Forecast Control, and WMS Data Interrogation. This is a strong fit for all four auto-gradable engines because the discipline is intrinsically quantitative. 3 pillars, 4 blocks, mixing all four engines: (1) Inventory Planning & Replenishment Engineering -> spreadsheet (EOQ + reorder-point replenishment model for a Jeddah distribution center) + logic_input (safety stock under demand-and-lead-time variability with a target cycle service level); (2) Network Cost & Sensitivity Optimization -> advanced_spreadsheet (two-variable data table of total landed cost per pallet across fuel surcharge and truck fill rate for a UAE lane); (3) Warehouse & Service-Level Data Interrogation -> sql (DC throughput / on-time-in-full ranking over a WMS shipments ledger). All figures are concrete (AED/SAR, real-sounding GCC entities). Frameworks: APICS/ASCM CSCP+CPIM, CSCMP, ISO 9001 service metrics, GS1. Difficulty mixes basic / intermediate / advanced. Master solutions are arithmetically verified below.

**Skills:** Inventory Planning & Replenishment (EOQ, Reorder Point, Safety Stock) · Warehouse Operations & Slotting Productivity · Transportation & Distribution Network Cost Optimization · Service-Level, Fill-Rate & OTIF Analytics · Cold-Chain / Perishable & Demand-Forecast Control · WMS Data Interrogation & Throughput Reporting

**Engine fit:** Strong, native fit for all four engines - logistics/warehousing/distribution is an intrinsically quantitative discipline (EOQ, reorder point, safety stock, fill rate, turns, total landed cost, network cost), so no "gradable proxy" compromise is needed. Engine mapping: spreadsheet for the EOQ + reorder-point replenishment model (linked cell formulas, exact numeric cell checks); logic_input for safety-stock-under-variability computation (named numeric fields that reconcile to a reorder point); advanced_spreadsheet for a two-variable cost-sensitivity data table (native data-table array formula + corner/interior cell values); sql for WMS shipment-ledger interrogation (aggregate OTIF / throughput ranking matched against a master query). The only things NOT gradable here - 3PL contract negotiation narrative, slotting layout drawings, carrier-relationship judgement - are deliberately excluded; every block targets the demonstrable numeric/analytical core of the role.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Logic input, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Inventory Planning & Replenishment Engineering**

- **EOQ & Reorder-Point Replenishment Model** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 15 min · ref: ASCM/APICS CPIM (Detailed Scheduling & Planning) - Wilson EOQ & ROP
  - _Measures:_ Computing Wilson EOQ and a lead-time reorder point, and linking them into ordering-cost / holding-cost trade-off totals - the core replenishment-design skill for a DC planner.
  - _Scenario:_ Al-Marfa Distribution Co. runs a fast-moving-consumer-goods DC in Jeddah for a single SKU (1L bottled water, 12-pack case). Annual demand D = 480,000 cases. Ordering cost S = SAR 600 per purchase order. Unit cost = SAR 24 per case; annual holding cost is 25% of unit cost, so H = SAR 6.00 per case per year. The DC operates 300 days per year. Replenishment lead time L = 10 working days. Demand is treated as deterministic for this block (a fixed safety stock buffer of 4,000 cases is held). Build the replenishment model: economic order quantity, expected number of orders per year, total annual ordering cost, total annual holding cost (cycle stock = EOQ/2), average daily demand, reorder point (= average daily demand x lead time + safety stock), and the total annual relevant inventory cost (ordering + holding on cycle stock).
  - _Model answer:_ Given cells: D=480000 (B2), S=600 (B3), H=6 (B4), days=300 (B5), L=10 (B6), SS=4000 (B7). EOQ B9 = SQRT(2*D*S/H) = SQRT(2*480000*600/6) = SQRT(96,000,000) = 9,797.96 cases. Orders/yr B10 = D/EOQ = 480000/9797.96 = 48.99. Annual ordering cost B11 = (D/EOQ)*S = 48.99*600 = 29,393.88. Annual holding cost (cycle) B12 = (EOQ/2)*H = 4898.98*6 = 29,393.88 (the EOQ property: at EOQ, ordering cost = holding cost). Avg daily demand B13 = D/days = 480000/300 = 1,600 cases/day. Reorder point B14 = B13*L + SS = 1600*10 + 4000 = 20,000 cases. Total relevant annual cost B15 = B11 + B12 = 58,787.75. Tolerances absorb rounding of the SQRT.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w3) - EOQ = SQRT(2DS/H) approx 9,797.96 cases - Correct Wilson EOQ formula and arithmetic
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Average daily demand = 1,600 cases/day - D divided by operating days
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Reorder point = 20,000 cases - Daily demand x lead time + safety stock
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Annual ordering cost approx SAR 29,393.88 - (D/EOQ) x S
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Annual cycle-stock holding cost approx SAR 29,393.88 - (EOQ/2) x H - and the EOQ equality property
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total relevant annual cost approx SAR 58,787.75 - Ordering + holding totals reconcile
- **Safety Stock Under Demand & Lead-Time Variability** &nbsp; `Logic input` · advanced · 10 min · ref: ASCM/APICS CSCP - statistical safety stock (cycle service level)
  - _Measures:_ Statistical safety-stock derivation that accounts for BOTH demand and lead-time variability (the combined-variance formula), the most commonly mis-applied inventory calculation - separating it from the naive demand-only buffer.
  - _Scenario:_ King Abdullah Economic City regional DC stocks a pharmaceutical SKU. Average daily demand d = 250 units with daily demand standard deviation sigma_d = 40 units. Average replenishment lead time L = 9 days with lead-time standard deviation sigma_L = 2 days. Management targets a 95% cycle service level (use the standard normal z = 1.65). Demand and lead time are independent. Compute, to the unit: (1) the combined lead-time-demand standard deviation sigma_DDLT = SQRT(L*sigma_d^2 + d^2*sigma_L^2), (2) the statistical safety stock SS = z * sigma_DDLT, (3) the cycle (lead-time) demand = d*L, and (4) the reorder point ROP = d*L + SS. Round each answer to the nearest whole unit.
  - _Model answer:_ sigma_DDLT = SQRT(L*sigma_d^2 + d^2*sigma_L^2) = SQRT(9*40^2 + 250^2*2^2) = SQRT(9*1600 + 62500*4) = SQRT(14,400 + 250,000) = SQRT(264,400) = 514.20, rounds to 514 units. SS = z*sigma_DDLT = 1.65 * 514.20 = 848.43, rounds to 848 units. Cycle demand = d*L = 250*9 = 2,250 units. ROP = d*L + SS = 2250 + 848 = 3,098 units (tolerance allows 3,098 +/- a few units from rounding order). Fields: sigma_ddlt, safety_stock, cycle_demand, reorder_point.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Combined sigma_DDLT approx 514 units - Correct combined demand+lead-time variance formula (not demand-only)
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Safety stock approx 848 units - z x sigma_DDLT at 95% service level
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Cycle (lead-time) demand = 2,250 units - Average daily demand x average lead time
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Reorder point approx 3,098 units - Cycle demand + safety stock reconcile

**Pillar - Network Cost & Sensitivity Optimization**

- **Landed-Cost-per-Pallet Two-Variable Sensitivity Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 16.7 min · ref: CSCMP Supply Chain Management - total landed cost & transportation sensitivity
  - _Measures:_ Building a native two-variable sensitivity (data) table over a transportation-cost model - demonstrating both the cost-per-pallet driver logic AND the spreadsheet-engineering skill to stress two variables simultaneously.
