  - _Scenario:_ Gulf Freight Logistics moves palletized goods on the Jebel Ali (Dubai) to Riyadh lane by 26-pallet trailer. Base line-haul cost is AED 6,500 per full truck. A fuel surcharge is applied as a percentage uplift on the line-haul. The truck is not always full, so cost-per-pallet depends on the fill rate (pallets actually loaded). Model: Cost per pallet = (Line-haul x (1 + Fuel surcharge %)) / (Capacity x Fill rate%), where capacity = 26 pallets. Base case: fuel surcharge 10%, fill rate 80%. Build a two-variable data table of cost-per-pallet with FUEL SURCHARGE down the rows (8%, 10%, 12%) and FILL RATE across the columns (70%, 80%, 90%). The table MUST be a native data table driving off the model cell, not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Base model cell = (6500*(1+0.10))/(26*0.80) = 7150/20.8 = AED 343.75 per pallet. Data table general cell = (6500*(1+fuel))/(26*fill). Corner (low fuel 8%, fill 70%) = (6500*1.08)/(26*0.70) = 7020/18.2 = 385.71. Base/center (10%, 80%) = 343.75. High corner (fuel 12%, fill 90%) = (6500*1.12)/(26*0.90) = 7280/23.4 = 311.11. Top-right (8% fuel, 90% fill) = (6500*1.08)/(26*0.90)=7020/23.4=300.00. is_array_formula verifies the {=TABLE()} native data table over the 3x3 result range; cell_value checks anchor the three diagonal/corner figures.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Result range is a native two-variable data table {=TABLE()} (not hardcoded) - Genuine data-table array formula driving off the model cell
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base-case cost per pallet = AED 343.75 (fuel 10%, fill 80%) - Cost-per-pallet model formula at base inputs
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner = AED 385.71 (fuel 8%, fill 70%) - Highest cost: low fill amplifies cost-per-pallet
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner = AED 311.11 (fuel 12%, fill 90%) - High fill offsets higher fuel surcharge
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Best-cost cell = AED 300.00 (fuel 8%, fill 90%) - Lowest cost-per-pallet combination identified

**Pillar - Warehouse & Service-Level Data Interrogation**

- **DC On-Time-In-Full (OTIF) & Throughput Ranking** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: GS1 / CSCMP perfect-order (OTIF) & DC throughput KPIs
  - _Measures:_ Translating the perfect-order/OTIF KPI definition (on-time AND in-full, both conditions) into correct conditional aggregation grouped per facility - the data-interrogation skill behind any DC scorecard.
  - _Scenario:_ A WMS shipments ledger records outbound orders across Gulf Freight's three GCC distribution centers (Dubai, Riyadh, Doha). Each row is one customer shipment: shipment_id, dc, order_lines, lines_filled (lines shipped complete), on_time (boolean), ship_date. Seeded rows (10): (1,'Dubai',8,8,true), (2,'Dubai',6,6,true), (3,'Dubai',5,4,false), (4,'Riyadh',10,10,true), (5,'Riyadh',7,7,false), (6,'Riyadh',4,3,true), (7,'Doha',9,9,true), (8,'Doha',6,5,true), (9,'Doha',8,8,false), (10,'Dubai',5,5,true). Write ONE query returning, per DC: the number of shipments and the OTIF shipment count, where an OTIF shipment is one that is BOTH on_time = true AND fully filled (lines_filled = order_lines). Columns: dc, shipments, otif_shipments. Order by otif_shipments descending, then dc ascending.
  - _Model answer:_ Master query: SELECT dc, COUNT(*) AS shipments, COUNT(*) FILTER (WHERE on_time = true AND lines_filled = order_lines) AS otif_shipments FROM shipments GROUP BY dc ORDER BY otif_shipments DESC, dc ASC. Manual check per DC - Dubai: rows 1,2,3,10 -> shipments 4; OTIF rows 1(8/8,on_time),2(6/6,on),10(5/5,on)=3, row3 fails (4/5 & not on_time). Riyadh: rows 4,5,6 -> shipments 3; OTIF row4(10/10,on)=1, row5 not on_time, row6 not in-full (3/4) -> 1. Doha: rows 7,8,9 -> shipments 3; OTIF row7(9/9,on),row8(5/6 fails in-full),row9 not on_time -> 1. Ordered: Dubai(3), then Doha(1), then Riyadh(1) [dc asc tiebreak: Doha before Riyadh]. ordered=true so row order is graded.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Per-DC OTIF result set matches master (counts correct, on-time AND in-full both required, correct descending+tiebreak order) - Conditional aggregation of the two-condition OTIF definition, grouping, and ordering all correct

---

### 7.4 Supply Chain Risk Management & Contract Compliance Audits

Hands-on sandbox blueprint for Supply Chain Risk Management & Contract Compliance Audits (node 7.4). The function's skills list was empty, so I first proposed 6 realistic GCC-grounded skills (supplier risk scoring & segmentation, contract compliance & leakage auditing, supply continuity & disruption modelling, total-cost-of-ownership & savings validation, third-party/concentration risk analytics, contract obligation & expiry surveillance via SQL) and designed to them. The function blends a "soft" audit/compliance theme with a strong quantitative core, so every block targets the gradable analytical slice. 3 pillars, 5 blocks, 4 engines used (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql) for a varied sitting, with concrete AED/SAR figures and real-sounding GCC entities. Frameworks referenced: ISO 31000 / ISO 28000, CIPS, IACCM/WorldCC contract management, APICS/ASCM CPIM safety-stock theory, FATF/sanctions third-party screening. Difficulty mixed across basic/intermediate/advanced.

**Skills:** Supplier Risk Scoring & Criticality Segmentation · Contract Compliance & Leakage Auditing · Supply Continuity & Disruption Modelling (Safety Stock / Single-Source) · Total Cost of Ownership & Negotiated-Savings Validation · Third-Party Concentration & Sanctions-Exposure Analytics · Contract Obligation, Expiry & SLA-Penalty Surveillance

**Engine fit:** Strong fit across all four engines despite the function's "audit / compliance" surface. Supply Chain Risk Management & Contract Compliance Audits has a heavily quantitative analytical core that maps cleanly: (1) supplier risk scoring is a weighted index (logic_input); (2) contract compliance is leakage / off-contract-spend / penalty math gradable as exact cell and field values (spreadsheet + logic_input); (3) supply continuity is safety-stock / reorder-point / single-source-exposure arithmetic (logic_input); (4) total-cost-of-ownership and negotiated-savings validation is a multi-line cost model with a 2-variable sensitivity table (spreadsheet + advanced_spreadsheet for the array/data-table check); (5) obligation/expiry/SLA-penalty surveillance over a contracts+POs database is a textbook SQL aggregation/filter task (sql). The genuinely non-gradable parts of this role - writing audit findings, drafting remediation memos, negotiating - are deliberately excluded; the sandbox measures the numerical risk-and-compliance analytics that underpin those judgements. No engine limitation flag needed.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 6 tasks · engines: Logic input, Spreadsheet, SQL, Adv. Spreadsheet

**Pillar - Supplier Risk Quantification & Continuity Modeling**

- **Weighted Supplier Risk Scorecard** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 10 min · ref: ISO 31000:2018 Risk Management / CIPS Supplier Risk Assessment
  - _Measures:_ Constructing and applying a weighted multi-criteria supplier risk index, then spend-weighting it to a portfolio view - the core quantitative act of risk-based supplier segmentation.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Falcon Logistics (Dubai) is segmenting three critical suppliers for its category risk register. Each supplier carries five risk sub-scores on a 1-5 scale (5 = worst). The category risk policy weights the dimensions as: Financial Stability 30%, Delivery/OTIF Performance 25%, Geographic/Geopolitical 15%, Single-Source Dependency 20%, Compliance & Sanctions 10%. Supplier 'Gulf Steel Trading' scores Financial 4, Delivery 3, Geographic 2, Single-Source 5, Compliance 1. Supplier 'Nimr Components FZE' scores Financial 2, Delivery 2, Geographic 4, Single-Source 3, Compliance 2. Annual spend with Gulf Steel is AED 8,400,000 and with Nimr is AED 3,150,000. Compute each supplier's weighted risk score (1-5, two decimals), the spend-weighted portfolio risk score across the two suppliers, and flag the higher-risk supplier's risk score as the 'register escalation value'.
  - _Model answer:_ Weighted score = sum(sub-score x weight). Gulf Steel = 4(0.30)+3(0.25)+2(0.15)+5(0.20)+1(0.10) = 1.20+0.75+0.30+1.00+0.10 = 3.35. Nimr = 2(0.30)+2(0.25)+4(0.15)+3(0.20)+2(0.10) = 0.60+0.50+0.60+0.60+0.20 = 2.50. Spend-weighted portfolio = (3.35x8,400,000 + 2.50x3,150,000) / (8,400,000+3,150,000) = (28,140,000 + 7,875,000)/11,550,000 = 36,015,000/11,550,000 = 3.1182... = 3.12. Escalation value = max(3.35, 2.50) = 3.35.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Gulf Steel weighted risk score = 3.35 - Correct application of the weighted-sum risk index to supplier 1
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Nimr weighted risk score = 2.50 - Correct application of the weighted-sum risk index to supplier 2
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Spend-weighted portfolio risk score = 3.12 - Correct spend-weighting of the two supplier scores into a portfolio risk figure
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Register escalation value = 3.35 - Identifies the higher-risk supplier score for escalation
- **Single-Source Continuity & Safety-Stock Buffer** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: APICS/ASCM CPIM - Reorder Point & Safety Stock; ISO 28000 Supply Chain Security
  - _Measures:_ Quantifying single-source disruption exposure via safety-stock / reorder-point theory under a service-level target and a stress scenario, then translating the buffer change into a working-capital figure.
  - _Scenario:_ A Riyadh utility relies on a single-source supplier in Jubail for a critical control valve. Average daily demand is 40 units with a demand standard deviation of 9 units/day. Normal lead time is 12 days. The continuity policy targets a 95% service level (service factor z = 1.65). To mitigate single-source disruption risk, management also asks for an extended-lead-time stress case where lead time rises to 20 days (demand and variability unchanged). Unit cost is SAR 1,250. Compute, for the BASE case: (1) safety stock (units, round to whole units), (2) reorder point = (avg daily demand x lead time) + safety stock. For the STRESS case (lead time 20 days): (3) the stressed reorder point. Then (4) compute the incremental working-capital tied up by the buffer change in SAR = (stressed ROP - base ROP) x unit cost.
  - _Model answer:_ Safety stock = z x sigma_d x sqrt(LT) = 1.65 x 9 x sqrt(12) = 1.65 x 9 x 3.46410 = 51.43 -> 51 units. Base ROP = (40x12) + 51 = 480 + 51 = 531 units. Stress safety stock = 1.65 x 9 x sqrt(20) = 1.65 x 9 x 4.47214 = 66.41 -> 66; stress ROP = (40x20) + 66 = 800 + 66 = 866 units. Incremental working capital = (866 - 531) x 1,250 = 335 x 1,250 = SAR 418,750. (Tolerance on rounding: safety stock +/-1 unit; downstream values keyed to the whole-unit master values 51/531/866/418750.)
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Base safety stock = 51 units - Correct safety-stock formula z x sigma x sqrt(LT) for the base lead time
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Base reorder point = 531 units - Reorder point combines lead-time demand with safety stock
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Stress reorder point (LT=20) = 866 units - Re-derives safety stock and ROP under the extended-lead-time disruption scenario
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Incremental working capital = SAR 418,750 - Translates the buffer change into a monetary working-capital impact

**Pillar - Contract Compliance & Cost Auditing**

- **Contract Leakage & Maverick-Spend Audit** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: IACCM/WorldCC Contract Management; CIPS Procurement Compliance
  - _Measures:_ Auditing a framework-agreement for value leakage - price-overrun against a ceiling, maverick/off-contract spend, compliance rate, and verifying entitled rebates - the everyday quantitative work of contract compliance auditing.
  - _Scenario:_ Audit of the FY2025 IT-hardware framework agreement at Qatar National Holding. The contract sets a unit ceiling price of AED 4,200 per laptop and a 6% volume rebate on total compliant spend once 500 units are exceeded. The audit grid lists four purchasing units. For each unit you are given Units Purchased, Actual Avg Unit Price Paid (AED), and a flag for whether the buy went through the contracted catalogue (on-contract) or was bought off-contract (maverick). Compute, per unit: contract-compliant baseline cost (units x ceiling price), actual cost (units x actual price), and price-overrun leakage (actual cost - baseline; show 0 if actual <= ceiling). Then compute total units, total actual spend, total price-overrun leakage, off-contract (maverick) spend, the contract-compliance rate (on-contract spend / total actual spend, as a %), and the rebate earned (6% of on-contract spend, because total on-contract units exceed 500).
  - _Model answer:_ Pre-filled rows: U1 on-contract 300 units @ 4,200 (compliant); U2 on-contract 250 units @ 4,500 (overrun 300/unit); U3 off-contract (maverick) 120 units @ 4,800; U4 on-contract 80 units @ 4,100 (under ceiling, 0 leakage). Per-unit baseline = units x 4,200; actual = units x actual price; overrun = max(actual-baseline,0). U1 actual=1,260,000 overrun=0. U2 actual=1,125,000 baseline=1,050,000 overrun=75,000. U3 actual=576,000 (maverick, full amount counts as off-contract spend; overrun vs ceiling = 120x(4,800-4,200)=72,000). U4 actual=328,000 overrun=0. Totals: units=750; total actual spend=1,260,000+1,125,000+576,000+328,000=3,289,000; total price-overrun leakage=0+75,000+72,000+0=147,000; off-contract (maverick) spend=576,000; on-contract spend=3,289,000-576,000=2,713,000; compliance rate=2,713,000/3,289,000=82.49%; on-contract units=300+250+80=630 (>500) so rebate=6% x 2,713,000=162,780.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Unit-2 price-overrun leakage = AED 75,000 - Per-line overrun vs the contracted ceiling price is computed correctly
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Total price-overrun leakage = AED 147,000 - Aggregates per-line leakage across all purchasing units
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Off-contract (maverick) spend = AED 576,000 - Correctly isolates spend that bypassed the framework agreement
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Contract-compliance rate = 82.49% - On-contract spend as a share of total actual spend
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Volume rebate earned = AED 162,780 - Applies the rebate rate to on-contract spend after the volume threshold is cleared
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total actual spend = AED 3,289,000 - Footing of all line-level actual costs
- **SLA Penalty & Liability-Cap Exposure Calculator** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 8 min · ref: IACCM/WorldCC Service-Level & Liability Terms; CIPS Contract Performance Management
  - _Measures:_ Translating an SLA clause into an enforceable financial penalty and correctly applying a liability cap - a precise contract-compliance computation auditors must verify before a credit is claimed.
  - _Scenario:_ A managed-logistics contract with Saudi Bandar Freight has an annual contract value of SAR 6,000,000. The SLA states: for every full 1% the on-time-in-full (OTIF) rate falls below the 98% target, a service credit of 0.5% of annual contract value applies, capped at an aggregate liability of 10% of annual contract value. Measured OTIF for the period was 92.4%. Compute: (1) the OTIF shortfall in whole percentage points below target (truncate to full points, i.e. floor), (2) the uncapped service-credit amount in SAR, (3) the liability cap in SAR, and (4) the enforceable penalty (lesser of uncapped credit and cap).
  - _Model answer:_ Shortfall = floor(98 - 92.4) = floor(5.6) = 5 full percentage points. Uncapped credit = 5 x 0.5% x 6,000,000 = 5 x 30,000 = SAR 150,000. Liability cap = 10% x 6,000,000 = SAR 600,000. Enforceable penalty = min(150,000, 600,000) = SAR 150,000.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - OTIF shortfall = 5 percentage points - Correctly floors the shortfall to full percentage points per the clause
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Uncapped service credit = SAR 150,000 - Applies the per-point credit rate to annual contract value
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Liability cap = SAR 600,000 - Computes the aggregate liability cap
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Enforceable penalty = SAR 150,000 - Applies the lesser-of cap logic to arrive at the recoverable amount

**Pillar - Spend Surveillance & Total-Cost Analytics**

- **Contract Obligation & Concentration Surveillance (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: FATF Third-Party Risk / DAMA DMBOK Data Interrogation; ISO 28000
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating a contracts register to surface expiry-window concentration risk while filtering out sanctioned counterparties - the data-querying backbone of obligation surveillance and third-party risk monitoring.
  - _Scenario:_ A GCC procurement risk team maintains a 'contracts' table: id, supplier, country, category, annual_value (AED), expiry_date, sanctions_flag (boolean). For its quarterly third-party risk review it needs to find supplier concentration among contracts that expire within the surveillance window and are sanctions-clean. Write ONE query returning, per supplier, the total annual_value (column 'total') for contracts that expire on or before 2026-03-31 AND have sanctions_flag = false, ordered by total descending then supplier ascending. Columns: supplier, total.
  - _Model answer:_ Seed ~8 rows across suppliers (e.g. Al Futtaim Logistics, Nesma Trading, Zahid Supply, Bahri Marine) with mixed expiry_date and sanctions_flag values; at least one high-value contract carries sanctions_flag=true to confirm it is excluded, and at least one expires after the window to confirm the date filter. Master query: SELECT supplier, SUM(annual_value) AS total FROM contracts WHERE expiry_date <= '2026-03-31' AND sanctions_flag = false GROUP BY supplier ORDER BY total DESC, supplier ASC. Graded order-sensitive so the descending concentration ranking is enforced.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master: per-supplier expiring-contract value, sanctions-clean, ranked by total desc - Correct filtering (expiry window + sanctions flag), grouping, aggregation, and concentration ordering in a single query
- **Total-Cost-of-Ownership Award & FX/Lead-Time Sensitivity** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 20 min · ref: CIPS Total Cost of Ownership; ISO 31000 - Scenario-Based Risk Evaluation
  - _Measures:_ Building a defensible total-cost-of-ownership model and a native two-variable sensitivity table so an award decision is stress-tested against price (FX) and duty risk - the analytical centrepiece of risk-aware sourcing.
  - _Scenario:_ Awarding a 3-year spare-parts contract at Abu Dhabi Marine Works. The base-case TCO build (AED) for the leading bid is: Acquisition price = unit price 320 x annual volume 5,000 x 3 years; plus Logistics & duty = 9% of acquisition; plus Quality-failure cost = 2.5% of acquisition; plus Carrying cost = 6% of acquisition; less a negotiated savings credit of AED 250,000. First complete the single-cell base-case TCO. Then build a TWO-VARIABLE DATA TABLE showing TCO sensitivity where the COLUMN variable is unit price (AED 300, 320, 340) and the ROW variable is the logistics-&-duty rate (7%, 9%, 11%). The data table MUST be a native data table driven by the TCO formula - not hardcoded numbers - so the risk committee can see TCO under FX-driven price moves and duty changes.
  - _Model answer:_ Acquisition = 320 x 5,000 x 3 = 4,800,000. Logistics&duty = 9% x 4,800,000 = 432,000. Quality = 2.5% x 4,800,000 = 120,000. Carrying = 6% x 4,800,000 = 288,000. Base TCO = 4,800,000 + 432,000 + 120,000 + 288,000 - 250,000 = 5,390,000. Data table recomputes acquisition = price x 5,000 x 3 and logistics = (logistics rate) x acquisition, holding quality 2.5%, carrying 6%, and the 250,000 credit fixed. Corner cells: price 300 / logistics 7% -> acq=4,500,000; log=315,000; qual=112,500; carry=270,000; TCO=4,500,000+315,000+112,500+270,000-250,000=4,947,500 (low corner). Base centre price 320 / 9% = 5,390,000. High corner price 340 / 11%: acq=340x5,000x3=5,100,000; log=11%x5,100,000=561,000; qual=2.5%x5,100,000=127,500; carry=6%x5,100,000=306,000; TCO=5,100,000+561,000+127,500+306,000-250,000=5,844,500. Validate is_array_formula on the table range plus the three corner/centre cell values.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base-case TCO = AED 5,390,000 - Correct multi-line TCO build including the negotiated-savings credit
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sensitivity grid is a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - The candidate built a real data table driven by the TCO formula rather than typing numbers
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (price 300, logistics 7%) TCO = AED 4,947,500 - Data table recomputes TCO correctly at the favourable corner
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre (price 320, logistics 9%) TCO = AED 5,390,000 - Base-case cell inside the table reconciles to the standalone build
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (price 340, logistics 11%) TCO = AED 5,844,500 - Data table recomputes TCO correctly at the adverse FX/duty corner

---

## Strategy & Communications

> **Domain review** - engine coverage OK. All 4 blueprints are structurally valid and internally consistent. Each has exactly 3 pillars, 4 blocks (within the 3-5 range), and uses all 4 distinct engine types (logic_input, spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, sql) - well above the >=2-engine minimum. Difficulty mix is healthy in every blueprint (each carries basic + intermediate + advanced). Engine/checkpoint mapping is correct everywhere: cell_value/is_array_formula on (advanced_)spreadsheet, logic_value on logic_input, sql_result_match on sql. No use of the unsupported 'python' engine. All four functions are genuinely non-quantitative roles, and each engine_fit narrative honestly identifies the gradable quantitative slice and flags the un-gradable judgement/drafting layer - exactly as the design rules require. The recurring pattern of 1 checkpoint per SQL block matches the FP&A reference (its SQL block also has a single sql_result_match), so it is NOT a defect, though for the richer SQL tasks here (multi-aggregate, net-sentiment, disclosure-coverage %) a single coarse pass/fail is a slightly weaker signal than the spreadsheet blocks. framework_refs cited (AMEC Barcelona Principles 3.0, GHG Protocol, GRI/ISSB/IFRS S1-S2, SASB, OECD Governance, PMI) are real and appropriate. Concreteness/GCC grounding is asserted in each engine_fit but cannot be fully verified from the compact view (no engine_config/master_solution shown) - assumed present at full-blueprint level as in FP&A.
>
> - _(low)_ 8.3: Block 1 'Board Composition, Independence & Quorum Analysis' is rated 'basic' but carries 6 weighted logic_value checkpoints across independence ratios, quorum thresholds, voting-majority math and committee/attendance counts. Six distinct objective computations is closer to intermediate than basic; the difficulty label slightly understates the cognitive load. Re-tag to intermediate, or confirm the 6 checks are genuinely trivial single-step ratios.
> - _(low)_ 8.1: The SQL block 'Growth-Share Portfolio Ranking' is rated 'intermediate' but has only 1 checkpoint (sql_result_match) and the compact view does not confirm the master query exceeds a simple GROUP BY + ORDER BY. If the intended intermediate complexity is a BCG quadrant CASE classification (Star/Cash Cow/Dog/Question Mark) the result-set match must include the computed category column and be order-sensitive; confirm the master_query carries that complexity, otherwise the intermediate rating is generous for a single coarse pass/fail.
> - _(low)_ 8.2: SQL block 'Engagement-Survey & Attrition Interrogation' bundles two distinct asks (per-department favourable-score AND per-band attrition counts) into one sql_result_match checkpoint. A single query/result cannot cleanly return both a per-department aggregate and a per-band aggregate without union/grain gymnastics. Confirm the master query targets ONE result grain (e.g. per-department favourable% with attrition as an additional column at the same grain), or the candidate query may be un-matchable. Low severity (resolvable in full config) but flag to verify the result shape is single-grain.
> - _(low)_ 8.4: Naming/scope drift: the block 'Share of Voice & Net-Sentiment over a Media-Coverage Dataset' implies the single sql_result_match must reconcile both Share-of-Voice (% of total coverage volume) and net-sentiment aggregation. As with 8.2, ensure these collapse to one result grain (e.g. per-outlet or per-brand row carrying both SoV% and net-sentiment) so the master query is matchable by a single result set; otherwise split is needed (but block count is already at 4, so prefer single-grain).
>
> _Recommendations:_ Approve all four blueprints - they pass the hard engine constraint, the structural rules (3 pillars / 3-5 blocks / >=2 engines / difficulty mix), and the non-quantitative-slice requirement with honest limitation statements. No high or medium blockers. Before authoring the full engine_config/master_solution, address three low-severity verification points: (1) 8.3 Block 1 - either re-tag to 'intermediate' or confirm the 6 governance checks are trivial single-step ratios; (2) 8.1 SQL - confirm the growth-share master query carries genuine intermediate complexity (BCG quadrant CASE classification with an ordered, category-bearing result set) to justify both the rating and the single checkpoint; (3) 8.2 and 8.4 SQL - ensure each bundled SQL block resolves to a SINGLE result grain so the one sql_result_match is matchable (per-department row carrying both favourable% and attrition in 8.2; per-brand/outlet row carrying both SoV% and net-sentiment in 8.4), and set ordered:true where ranking is the point. Optional polish: consider whether the consistently single-checkpoint SQL blocks could carry a 2nd, lighter check is not possible under the sql engine (only sql_result_match exists), so this is a known engine limitation, not a fixable gap - leave as-is to stay faithful to the FP&A reference.

### 8.1 Corporate Strategy Formulation & Scenario Planning

Corporate Strategy is largely a narrative discipline (strategy documents, board recommendations, vision-setting) that cannot be auto-graded. This blueprint targets the QUANTITATIVE/ANALYTICAL slice that IS gradable: market-sizing (TAM/SAM/SOM), scenario & sensitivity financial modeling, weighted strategic-option scoring matrices, portfolio/competitive data interrogation, and risk-quantification. Three pillars: (1) Market Sizing & Strategic Positioning - bottom-up TAM/SAM/SOM build (logic_input) plus a weighted strategic-option scoring matrix (spreadsheet); (2) Scenario & Sensitivity Modeling - a 3-scenario expected-value entry-decision model with a two-variable price x adoption NPV sensitivity data table (advanced_spreadsheet); (3) Portfolio & Competitive Data Interrogation - SQL over a business-unit portfolio table to rank growth-share quadrants by contribution. Engines used: logic_input, spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, sql (all 4). Frameworks anchored: McKinsey/strategy practice on market sizing, Ansoff/GE-McKinsey matrix logic, expected-monetary-value decision analysis, BCG growth-share portfolio theory, and ISSB/scenario-planning discipline. Since I proposed the 5 skills (the function's skills list was empty), the design maps each block to a proposed skill.

**Skills:** Market Sizing & Demand Estimation (TAM/SAM/SOM) · Scenario Planning & Sensitivity Analysis · Strategic Option Evaluation & Weighted Decision Matrices · Portfolio Strategy & Resource Allocation (Growth-Share) · Competitive & Market Data Interrogation

**Engine fit:** Corporate Strategy is a predominantly NON-QUANTITATIVE function - its core deliverables (strategy narratives, board papers, vision statements, qualitative SWOT/PESTLE judgement) are free-text and CANNOT be auto-graded by any of the 4 engines. This blueprint therefore deliberately measures the QUANTITATIVE/ANALYTICAL spine that underpins credible strategy work and IS gradable: (1) bottom-up market sizing arithmetic (TAM/SAM/SOM) - logic_input with exact numeric fields; (2) expected-value scenario modeling + a two-variable NPV sensitivity data table - spreadsheet + advanced_spreadsheet (is_array_formula + corner cell_values, mirroring FP&A's data-table block); (3) a weighted strategic-option scoring matrix (criteria weights x option scores -> weighted totals + ranked winner) - spreadsheet cell_value checks; and (4) portfolio/competitive data interrogation - sql over a business-unit table (growth, share, contribution) ranked by a master query. HONEST LIMITATION: the synthesis/judgement layer of strategy (choosing WHICH option to pursue given soft factors, articulating WHY, stakeholder framing) is not assessed here - this sitting certifies that a candidate can correctly BUILD and INTERROGATE the analytical models a strategist must defend, not that they can write the strategy. All 4 engines are used so the sitting is varied; the design favours logic_input and spreadsheet because strategy quantitative work is more arithmetic/decision-matrix shaped than transaction-ledger shaped.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Logic input, Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Market Sizing & Strategic Positioning**

- **Bottom-Up Market Sizing (TAM / SAM / SOM)** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 10 min · ref: Strategy Practice - Bottom-Up Market Sizing (TAM/SAM/SOM)
  - _Measures:_ Market sizing and demand estimation: correctly chaining a bottom-up funnel (universe -> addressable -> serviceable -> obtainable) and separating value (AED) from volume (customer count).
  - _Scenario:_ VIFM Advisory is sizing the UAE market for a new corporate-treasury SaaS product before recommending market entry. Inputs (all annual, AED): there are 64,000 registered medium-and-large enterprises in the UAE. The product is only relevant to enterprises with annual revenue above AED 50m - that is 18% of the registered base (this defines the addressable segment). Of those, 35% operate a centralised treasury function that the product serves (Serviceable segment). The published average annual contract value (ACV) is AED 42,000 per enterprise. The realistic obtainable share VIFM can capture in the first 3 years, given two incumbent competitors, is 6% of the serviceable segment. Compute the four headline figures the board paper requires: (a) TAM = total addressable enterprises x ACV; here TAM is the full addressable segment (revenue>AED50m) x ACV. (b) SAM = serviceable segment (the 35% with centralised treasury) x ACV. (c) SOM = obtainable share (6%) of the SAM. (d) the number of obtainable customers (SOM customers) = 6% of the serviceable-segment enterprise count.
  - _Model answer:_ Addressable enterprises = 64,000 x 0.18 = 11,520. TAM = 11,520 x AED 42,000 = AED 483,840,000. Serviceable enterprises = 11,520 x 0.35 = 4,032. SAM = 4,032 x 42,000 = AED 169,344,000. SOM (value) = 169,344,000 x 0.06 = AED 10,160,640. SOM customers = 4,032 x 0.06 = 241.92 -> report 241.92 (or 242 if rounded; tolerance covers both). Checks reconcile: SOM value / ACV = SOM customers.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - TAM = addressable enterprises (11,520) x ACV = AED 483,840,000 - Correctly identifies the addressable universe (64,000 x 18%) and converts to value at the ACV.
    - `logic_value` (w2) - SAM = serviceable enterprises (4,032) x ACV = AED 169,344,000 - Applies the serviceable filter (35% with centralised treasury) before valuing.
    - `logic_value` (w3) - SOM (value) = 6% of SAM = AED 10,160,640 - Applies obtainable-share haircut to the SAM value, not to TAM.
    - `logic_value` (w2) - SOM customers = 6% of 4,032 = ~242 - Separates obtainable VOLUME from obtainable VALUE - a common strategy-analysis error.
- **Weighted Strategic-Option Scoring Matrix** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 15 min · ref: GE-McKinsey / Weighted-Factor Decision Matrix
  - _Measures:_ Strategic option evaluation: building and footing a weighted-factor decision matrix correctly (weighted = weight x score, summed per option) and identifying the dominant option by score.
  - _Scenario:_ VIFM's strategy team must recommend ONE of three growth options to the board: Option A - acquire a Riyadh-based training firm; Option B - build a greenfield Saudi subsidiary; Option C - franchise the VIFM brand to a Saudi partner. Five weighted criteria have been agreed (weights must sum to 1.00): Strategic Fit 0.30, Financial Return 0.25, Speed to Market 0.20, Execution Risk (scored so higher = lower risk) 0.15, Regulatory Ease 0.10. Each option has a raw 1-5 score per criterion in the grid. Build the weighted-score columns (weight x raw score) for each option, total each option's weighted score, and surface the recommended (highest-scoring) option's total. The pre-populated grid holds the weights in column B and the three options' raw scores in columns C (A), D (B), E (C). Compute each weighted total in the totals row, and place the winning option's total in the 'Recommended option score' cell.
  - _Model answer:_ Weighted total per option = SUMPRODUCT(weights, that option's raw scores). Raw scores - A: 5,4,2,3,4; B: 3,5,2,4,3; C: 4,2,5,4,5. A total = 0.30*5+0.25*4+0.20*2+0.15*3+0.10*4 = 1.50+1.00+0.40+0.45+0.40 = 3.75. B = 0.30*3+0.25*5+0.20*2+0.15*4+0.10*3 = 0.90+1.25+0.40+0.60+0.30 = 3.45. C = 0.30*4+0.25*2+0.20*5+0.15*4+0.10*5 = 1.20+0.50+1.00+0.60+0.50 = 3.80. Recommended option = C (highest at 3.80). Weights sum check = 1.00.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Weights sum to 1.00 (validation cell) - Candidate validates that the criteria weights are a proper distribution before scoring.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Option A weighted total = 3.75 - Correct SUMPRODUCT of weights and Option A raw scores.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Option B weighted total = 3.45 - Correct SUMPRODUCT of weights and Option B raw scores.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Option C weighted total = 3.80 - Correct SUMPRODUCT of weights and Option C raw scores.
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Recommended option score = 3.80 (the highest total) - Identifies the dominant option (MAX of the three weighted totals) - the actual recommendation.

**Pillar - Scenario & Sensitivity Modeling**

- **Three-Scenario Expected-Value Entry Decision + NPV Sensitivity Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 20 min · ref: Expected Monetary Value (EMV) Decision Analysis + Scenario Planning
  - _Measures:_ Scenario planning + sensitivity analysis: probability-weighting scenarios into an EMV, discounting to NPV, and stress-testing the decision across two drivers with a native two-variable data table.
  - _Scenario:_ VIFM is deciding whether to enter the Saudi corporate-training market. Three demand scenarios are modelled for the steady-state annual cash flow (SAR): Pessimistic (probability 0.25) -> annual cash flow SAR 4,000,000; Base (probability 0.50) -> SAR 9,000,000; Optimistic (probability 0.25) -> SAR 15,000,000. Step 1: compute the probability-weighted Expected Annual Cash Flow (EMV). Step 2: the entry requires an upfront investment of SAR 18,000,000 today (year 0), then the expected annual cash flow recurs for 5 years (years 1-5) discounted at a 12% cost of capital; compute the project NPV using the expected annual cash flow as a level annuity. Step 3: build a TWO-VARIABLE DATA TABLE showing project NPV across a grid of base-case annual cash flow (rows: SAR 7,000,000 / 9,000,000 / 11,000,000) and discount rate (columns: 10% / 12% / 14%), holding the SAR 18m upfront investment constant. The data table MUST be a native data table (array formula), not hardcoded. Provide the EMV cell, the NPV cell, and the data-table corners.
  - _Model answer:_ EMV = 0.25*4,000,000 + 0.50*9,000,000 + 0.25*15,000,000 = 1,000,000 + 4,500,000 + 3,750,000 = SAR 8,750,000. NPV at 12% = -18,000,000 + 8,750,000 * annuity-factor(12%,5yr). Annuity factor(12%,5) = (1-1.12^-5)/0.12 = 3.604776; PV of inflows = 8,750,000 * 3.604776 = 31,541,790; NPV = 31,541,790 - 18,000,000 = SAR 13,541,790 (tolerance covers rounding). Data table cells: NPV = -18,000,000 + CF * (1-(1+r)^-5)/r. Low corner (CF 7,000,000, r 10%): annuity-factor(10%,5)=3.790787; 7,000,000*3.790787=26,535,509; NPV=8,535,509. High corner (CF 11,000,000, r 14%): annuity-factor(14%,5)=3.433081; 11,000,000*3.433081=37,763,891; NPV=19,763,891. Centre (CF 9,000,000, r 12%): 9,000,000*3.604776=32,442,984; NPV=14,442,984.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Expected Annual Cash Flow (EMV) = SAR 8,750,000 - Probability-weights the three scenarios correctly into an expected value.
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Base-case project NPV = ~SAR 13,541,790 - Discounts the EMV annuity over 5 years at 12% and nets the SAR 18m upfront - the headline go/no-go number.
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - NPV grid is a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded values) - Candidate uses a real data-table array formula to stress-test, not manually typed numbers.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Sensitivity low corner (CF 7m, r 10%) NPV = ~SAR 8,535,509 - Data table re-computes NPV correctly at the low-demand / low-rate corner.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Sensitivity centre (CF 9m, r 12%) NPV = ~SAR 14,442,984 - Data table interior cell reconciles to a direct NPV at base inputs.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Sensitivity high corner (CF 11m, r 14%) NPV = ~SAR 19,763,891 - Data table re-computes NPV correctly at the high-demand / high-rate corner.

**Pillar - Portfolio & Competitive Data Interrogation**

- **Growth-Share Portfolio Ranking (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: BCG Growth-Share Matrix / Portfolio Strategy
  - _Measures:_ Competitive/portfolio data interrogation: translating a strategic classification rule (BCG Star quadrant) into a precise relational filter + ranking, isolating the units that should receive capital.
  - _Scenario:_ VIFM Group runs eight strategic business units (SBUs). The board wants to reallocate capital toward 'Star' SBUs - defined as units in a high-growth market (market_growth_pct >= 10) that also hold a strong relative position (relative_market_share >= 1.0). The seeded table business_units holds: id, sbu_name, market_growth_pct (numeric), relative_market_share (numeric), annual_contribution (numeric AED). Write ONE query that returns only the Star SBUs, with columns sbu_name and annual_contribution, ordered by annual_contribution from highest to lowest (tie-break by sbu_name ascending). This is the prioritised investment shortlist.
  - _Model answer:_ Seed 8 SBUs with a mix of quadrants. Master query: SELECT sbu_name, annual_contribution FROM business_units WHERE market_growth_pct >= 10 AND relative_market_share >= 1.0 ORDER BY annual_contribution DESC, sbu_name. Only the rows satisfying BOTH the high-growth and high-share thresholds (the Stars) return, ranked by contribution. Seed data is designed so exactly 3 SBUs qualify as Stars and the ordering is unambiguous after the contribution + name tie-break.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Star SBUs only, columns sbu_name + annual_contribution, ordered by contribution desc then name - Both filter conditions (growth >= 10 AND share >= 1.0) applied AND the result is ranked exactly as the master (ordered match).

---

### 8.2 Organizational Development (OD), Transformation, & Culture Change

Sandbox blueprint for OD, Transformation & Culture Change (node 8.2, strategy domain). The function's skills list was empty, so six realistic GCC-grounded skills were proposed (Org Design & Span-of-Control Optimization, Change-Readiness & Stakeholder Impact Assessment, Transformation Portfolio & Benefits Realization, Culture & Engagement Diagnostics, Workforce Attrition & Talent-Flow Analytics, OD Intervention ROI). Because OD/culture work is largely qualitative and ungradable as free text, the blueprint isolates the QUANTITATIVE/ANALYTICAL slice of the role that the four auto-graders can verify, and says so per block. 3 pillars, 4 blocks, 3 engines (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql). Pillar 1 (Org Design & Workforce Economics) uses a spreadsheet span-of-control / layering model and a logic_input change-readiness composite. Pillar 2 (Transformation Portfolio Economics) uses an advanced_spreadsheet two-variable benefits-realization sensitivity data table (array formula + corner cells). Pillar 3 (Culture & Talent-Flow Analytics) uses a SQL engagement-survey aggregation. Difficulty mixed basic→advanced. Frameworks: Galbraith Star Model / SHRM, Prosci ADKAR, AFP/benefits-realization + ISO 44001-style change economics, GRI/engagement-index + DAMA DMBOK.

**Skills:** Org Design & Span-of-Control Optimization · Change-Readiness & Stakeholder Impact Assessment · Transformation Portfolio & Benefits Realization · Culture & Engagement Diagnostics · Workforce Attrition & Talent-Flow Analytics · OD Intervention ROI Measurement

**Engine fit:** OD / Transformation / Culture Change is predominantly a qualitative discipline (stakeholder narratives, intervention design, culture storytelling) that the four auto-graders CANNOT assess - none can score free-text change plans, drafted communications, or subjective judgement. This blueprint therefore deliberately targets the QUANTITATIVE/ANALYTICAL slice of the role that an OD practitioner genuinely owns and that IS gradable: (1) org-design arithmetic - span-of-control, management-layer count, and overhead/manager-cost math (spreadsheet, exact cell values); (2) change-readiness and stakeholder-impact composite scoring - a weighted ADKAR-style readiness index and a stakeholder influence x resistance risk score (logic_input, exact field values); (3) transformation benefits-realization economics - a two-variable sensitivity data table of net benefit across adoption-rate and ramp-speed (advanced_spreadsheet, native array formula + corner/interior cells); (4) culture/engagement and talent-flow analytics - aggregating an engagement-survey table into per-department favourable-score and per-band attrition counts (SQL result-set match). Honest limitation flagged: the actual design of interventions, the framing of culture narratives, and the change-leadership coaching that sit at the heart of this function are NOT measured here - the sandbox certifies only the numerate, defensible analytics layer (the part a hiring manager would otherwise verify with an Excel/SQL screen). All figures are concrete and GCC-grounded (AED/SAR, GCC banks/ministries/holding groups) and reconcile exactly to the master solutions.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Logic input, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Org Design & Workforce Economics**

- **Span-of-Control & Management-Layer Restructuring** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 15 min · ref: Galbraith Star Model / SHRM Org Design Body of Knowledge
  - _Measures:_ Org-design arithmetic - span-of-control ratios, management-layer headcount, and the overhead-cost reduction that justifies a delayering. The numerate core of an OD restructuring business case.
  - _Scenario:_ Emirates Falcon Holding (Dubai) is delayering its 1,200-staff Operations division ahead of a shared-services transformation. Current state: 1,000 front-line staff, 125 team leaders, 60 managers, 12 senior managers, 3 directors. The OD lead must compute the current average span of control and manager headcount, then model a target state that lifts the front-line-to-team-leader span from 8.0 to a target 10.0 and removes one full management layer (senior managers absorbed into managers). Each manager (any tier above front-line) costs AED 540,000 fully loaded per year. Compute current vs target management headcount and the annual people-cost saving from the redesign so the business case reconciles.
  - _Model answer:_ Current total managers (all tiers above front-line) = 125 + 60 + 12 + 3 = 200; current overall span = 1000 front-line / 125 team leaders = 8.0. Target team leaders to achieve span 10.0 over 1,000 front-line = 1000 / 10 = 100. Target removes the senior-manager layer: senior managers (12) fold into managers, so target managers tier = 60 + 12 = 72; directors unchanged at 3. Target total managers = 100 team leaders + 72 managers + 3 directors = 175. Headcount reduction = 200 - 175 = 25 management roles. Annual saving = 25 x AED 540,000 = AED 13,500,000. Cells: current managers B-col sum, current span, target team leaders, target managers tier, target total managers, reduction, saving.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Current total management headcount = 200 - Sums all four management tiers (125+60+12+3) for the current-state baseline.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Current overall span of control = 8.0 - Computes front-line / team-leader span (1000/125) - the diagnostic that triggers the redesign.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Target team leaders at span 10.0 = 100 - Inverts the target span to required team-leader headcount (1000/10).
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Target managers tier after absorbing seniors = 72 - Models the layer removal (60+12) - the structural change, not just a ratio tweak.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Target total management headcount = 175 - Aggregates the redesigned structure (100+72+3).
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Annual people-cost saving = AED 13,500,000 - Monetises the 25-role reduction at AED 540k each - the bottom line of the business case.
- **Change-Readiness & Stakeholder-Impact Scoring** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 10 min · ref: Prosci ADKAR / SHRM Change Management
  - _Measures:_ Change-readiness and stakeholder-impact quantification - turning ADKAR pulse scores and an influence/resistance grid into the weighted indices that gate a go/no-go decision.
  - _Scenario:_ Riyadh-based Tadawul Capital is launching a core-system transformation and the OD team must quantify readiness before go-live. A pulse survey scored five ADKAR levers on a 0-100 scale for the most-affected unit: Awareness 80, Desire 50, Knowledge 60, Ability 40, Reinforcement 70. The change plan weights them Awareness 0.15, Desire 0.30, Knowledge 0.20, Ability 0.25, Reinforcement 0.10. Separately, a key stakeholder (the Head of Branch Operations) is rated Influence 9 and Resistance 7 on a 1-10 scale; the stakeholder risk index = Influence x Resistance. Compute the weighted ADKAR readiness index, identify the gap to the 70 go-live threshold (threshold minus index, floored at 0), and the stakeholder risk index so the team can prioritise mitigation.
  - _Model answer:_ Weighted ADKAR index = 80(0.15) + 50(0.30) + 60(0.20) + 40(0.25) + 70(0.10) = 12 + 15 + 12 + 10 + 7 = 56.0. Readiness gap to threshold = 70 - 56 = 14.0 (positive, so unit is not ready). Stakeholder risk index = Influence 9 x Resistance 7 = 63. Fields: adkar_index, readiness_gap, stakeholder_risk.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Weighted ADKAR readiness index = 56.0 - Applies the five lever weights to the pulse scores - the central readiness metric.
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Readiness gap to 70 go-live threshold = 14.0 - Computes threshold minus index, confirming the unit is below the bar.
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Stakeholder risk index = 63 - Multiplies influence x resistance - the prioritisation score for the resistance grid.

**Pillar - Transformation Portfolio Economics**

- **Benefits-Realization Sensitivity Data Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18 min · ref: AFP FP&A Body of Knowledge / Benefits Realization Management (Managing Successful Programmes)
  - _Measures:_ Transformation benefits-realization economics under uncertainty - building a real two-variable data table so adoption and ramp assumptions can be stressed, the analytical heart of a defensible transformation business case.
  - _Scenario:_ Qatar National Logistics Group is funding a 3-year operating-model transformation. The full-adoption annual gross benefit is QAR 20,000,000; the recurring annual programme cost is QAR 6,000,000. Realised net benefit = (gross benefit x adoption rate x ramp factor) - cost, where adoption rate is the share of the workforce embedding the new ways of working and the ramp factor is the fraction of the year the change is live after rollout. The sponsor wants a two-variable sensitivity table of realised net benefit (QAR) across adoption rates (columns: 60%, 80%, 100%) and ramp factors (rows: 0.50, 0.75, 1.00). Build the base-case net-benefit formula and a NATIVE two-variable data table - not hardcoded numbers - so the sponsor can stress the benefits case live.
  - _Model answer:_ Base net benefit = 20,000,000 x adoption x ramp - 6,000,000. Two-variable data table with adoption (60/80/100%) on columns and ramp (0.50/0.75/1.00) on rows, corner cell linking to the base formula, row input = ramp cell, column input = adoption cell. Corner low (adoption 60%, ramp 0.50) = 20,000,000 x 0.60 x 0.50 - 6,000,000 = 6,000,000 - 6,000,000 = 0. Centre (adoption 80%, ramp 0.75) = 20,000,000 x 0.80 x 0.75 - 6,000,000 = 12,000,000 - 6,000,000 = 6,000,000. High corner (adoption 100%, ramp 1.00) = 20,000,000 x 1.00 x 1.00 - 6,000,000 = 14,000,000. The table must be a native {=TABLE()} array, not pasted values.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sensitivity grid uses a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded) - Confirms the candidate built a real {=TABLE()} array driven by row/column inputs, not pasted numbers - the actual modelling skill.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Base-case net benefit formula correct - The driver cell (gross x adoption x ramp - cost) is formula-driven and correct before the table is generated.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Low corner (adoption 60%, ramp 0.50) = QAR 0 - Stress floor where benefit exactly offsets cost - the break-even scenario.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre case (adoption 80%, ramp 0.75) = QAR 6,000,000 - Most-likely realised net benefit - the planning anchor.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (adoption 100%, ramp 1.00) = QAR 14,000,000 - Full-realization ceiling - the upside case for the sponsor.

**Pillar - Culture & Talent-Flow Analytics**

- **Engagement-Survey & Attrition Interrogation (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: GRI / Gallup Q12 engagement-index practice / DAMA International (DMBOK)
  - _Measures:_ Culture and talent-flow data interrogation - aggregating a raw engagement-survey table into the per-department favourability ranking that drives where OD intervention budget goes.
  - _Scenario:_ The OD analytics team at Bahrain Gulf Bank holds an engagement-survey table eng_responses(id, department, tenure_band, favourable, left_company) where favourable is 1 when the respondent rated the item favourably (else 0) and left_company is 1 if the respondent has since exited (else 0). The CHRO wants the culture hot-spots: for each department, the count of favourable responses, ordered most-favourable first. Write ONE query returning department and the favourable count (column aliased favourable_count), highest first, so the team can target the lowest-engagement units for OD intervention.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT department, SUM(favourable) AS favourable_count FROM eng_responses GROUP BY department ORDER BY favourable_count DESC, department. Seed the table with several departments (e.g. Retail, Corporate, Operations, Risk) and a mix of favourable 0/1 and left_company 0/1 rows so the per-department SUM differs and ordering is unambiguous. Result-set match, ordered (highest favourable_count first, department as deterministic tiebreaker).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Per-department favourable count, highest first, matches master - The GROUP BY department + SUM(favourable) aggregate with correct DESC ordering and tiebreak - the exact ranking the CHRO needs.

---

### 8.3 Corporate Governance, Sustainability, & ESG Strategy Integration

Function 8.3 (Corporate Governance, Sustainability & ESG Strategy Integration) is a strategy/governance role that is largely soft (board policy, disclosure narrative, stakeholder engagement) and therefore not directly gradable by the four numeric engines. This blueprint isolates the QUANTITATIVE/ANALYTICAL slice that IS gradable: board-composition and independence ratios, quorum/voting and meeting-attendance math (logic_input); GHG emissions-intensity computation and a SASB/ISSB-style two-variable carbon-price sensitivity stress test (spreadsheet + advanced_spreadsheet); and disclosure-coverage / framework-mapping interrogation over a GRI/ISSB disclosure-status register (sql). Three pillars, four blocks, three engines (logic_input, spreadsheet/advanced_spreadsheet, sql), mixed difficulty. Soft deliverables (drafting the governance charter, writing the sustainability report narrative, designing a board diversity policy) are explicitly out of scope because no engine can grade free text - flagged per block in engine_fit.

**Skills:** Board composition & independence analysis (independent-director ratio, committee composition, separation of Chair/CEO) · Quorum, voting & meeting-governance mathematics (attendance rates, quorum thresholds, special-resolution majorities) · GHG accounting & emissions-intensity computation (Scope 1/2/3 aggregation, intensity per revenue/headcount/output) · Climate-transition & carbon-price stress testing (scenario sensitivity of carbon cost / EBITDA exposure) · ESG disclosure-coverage & framework mapping (GRI/ISSB/SASB completeness, materiality register interrogation) · Sustainability-linked KPI & target tracking (baseline vs target vs actual, reduction-trajectory variance)

**Engine fit:** GOOD-with-scoping fit. The role's headline outputs (governance charters, board-diversity policy, the sustainability report narrative, stakeholder-engagement plans) are free-text/judgement and CANNOT be auto-graded by any of the four engines, so they are deliberately excluded. What IS robustly gradable is the analyst-grade numeric work that underpins governance and ESG strategy, and that is what this sitting measures: (1) GOVERNANCE MATHEMATICS -> logic_input for board-independence ratios, quorum and voting-majority thresholds, and committee/attendance math (exact numeric fields, fully objective). (2) CARBON & ESG MODELLING -> spreadsheet for GHG Scope 1/2/3 aggregation + emissions intensity, and advanced_spreadsheet for a two-variable carbon-price x emissions sensitivity (data-table / array formula, graded on the array being native plus corner/centre values). (3) DISCLOSURE INTERROGATION -> sql over a GRI/ISSB disclosure-status register (coverage %, gaps, framework mapping), graded by result-set match. Frameworks anchored to real standards (GHG Protocol, GRI, IFRS S1/S2 (ISSB), SASB, OECD Principles of Corporate Governance, UK/GCC combined codes). Honest limitation: this measures the quantitative competence of an ESG/governance analyst, not the qualitative board-advisory judgement that is the senior end of the role; that qualitative slice must be assessed by the human assessor / CBI layer, not the sandbox.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Logic input, Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Board Governance Mathematics**

- **Board Composition, Independence & Quorum Analysis** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 10 min · ref: OECD Principles of Corporate Governance 2023 / GCC Combined Code (SCA & CMA listing rules)
  - _Measures:_ Whether the candidate can apply listing-code governance arithmetic correctly: independence ratio, quorum (with the rounding rule), simple-majority vote count, AGM attendance/quorum %, and whether a special resolution carried at the 75% bar.
  - _Scenario:_ Emaar-style UAE-listed entity 'Gulf Capital Holdings PJSC' has a 9-member board: 3 executive directors, 2 non-executive non-independent (related to the controlling shareholder), and 4 independent non-executive directors. The Audit Committee has 4 members of whom 3 are independent. The Articles require a quorum of two-thirds of board members rounded UP to the next whole director for any board meeting, and an ordinary board resolution carries on a simple majority of directors PRESENT. At the AGM, 132,000,000 of the 200,000,000 issued voting shares were represented; a special resolution (amending the Articles) requires a 75% majority of shares voted, and 96,800,000 shares were cast in favour. The candidate computes the governance ratios and thresholds that a board secretary / governance analyst must verify before a meeting is validly constituted.
  - _Model answer:_ Board independence ratio = 4 independent / 9 total = 44.44% (round to 44.44). Audit-committee independence = 3/4 = 75.00%. Board quorum = ceil(9 x 2/3) = ceil(6) = 6 directors. Simple-majority threshold of directors present at a fully-attended (9) meeting = floor(9/2)+1 = 5 directors. AGM attendance % = 132,000,000 / 200,000,000 = 66.00%. Special-resolution support % = 96,800,000 / 132,000,000 shares voted = 73.33%; since 73.33% < 75% the special resolution FAILS, so the 'special_resolution_passed' flag = 0 (express as 0=fail / 1=pass).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Board independence ratio = 44.44% - Independent directors / total board members as a percentage (4/9).
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Audit committee independence = 75.00% - Independent members / committee members (3/4).
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Board quorum = 6 directors - Two-thirds of 9 rounded up to the next whole director (ceil rule).
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Simple-majority threshold = 5 directors - Minimum directors needed to carry an ordinary resolution at full attendance.
    - `logic_value` (w2) - AGM attendance = 66.00% - Shares represented / issued voting shares.
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Special resolution passed flag = 0 (fails at 73.33% vs 75% bar) - Whether votes-in-favour clear the 75% special-resolution threshold; tests the threshold comparison, not just the ratio.

**Pillar - Carbon Accounting & Climate-Risk Modelling**

- **GHG Inventory Aggregation & Emissions Intensity** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 15 min · ref: GHG Protocol Corporate Standard / IFRS S2 (ISSB) Climate Disclosures
  - _Measures:_ Whether the candidate can build a defensible GHG inventory: convert activity data x emission factors into tCO2e per source, roll up Scope 1/2/3 subtotals and a gross total, and compute the two standard intensity ratios used in ISSB/SASB reporting.
  - _Scenario:_ Saudi industrial group 'Najd Cement Company' is preparing its first IFRS S2 climate disclosure. Activity data (given): Scope 1 - natural gas 1,200,000 m3 at 0.0020 tCO2e/m3, and diesel 450,000 litres at 0.00268 tCO2e/litre. Scope 2 (location-based) - grid electricity 38,000,000 kWh at 0.00065 tCO2e/kWh. Scope 3 - purchased clinker 220,000 tonnes at 0.85 tCO2e/tonne, and business travel 1,500,000 km at 0.00018 tCO2e/km. Reporting-year revenue = SAR 1,840,000,000 and production = 3,100,000 tonnes of cement. The candidate completes a pre-populated GHG inventory grid: per-source emissions, scope subtotals, total gross emissions, and two intensity metrics (per SAR million revenue and per tonne of product) that go straight into the ISSB metrics-and-targets disclosure.
  - _Model answer:_ Scope 1: gas 1,200,000 x 0.0020 = 2,400 tCO2e; diesel 450,000 x 0.00268 = 1,206 tCO2e; Scope 1 subtotal = 3,606. Scope 2: 38,000,000 x 0.00065 = 24,700 tCO2e. Scope 3: clinker 220,000 x 0.85 = 187,000; travel 1,500,000 x 0.00018 = 270; Scope 3 subtotal = 187,270. Total gross emissions = 3,606 + 24,700 + 187,270 = 215,576 tCO2e. Intensity per SAR million revenue = 215,576 / 1,840 = 117.16 tCO2e/SAR m. Intensity per tonne product = 215,576 / 3,100,000 = 0.06954 tCO2e/tonne (~0.0695). All cells are formula-linked to the given activity x factor inputs.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Scope 1 subtotal = 3,606 tCO2e - Sum of gas and diesel combustion emissions.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Scope 2 emissions = 24,700 tCO2e - Location-based grid electricity emissions.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Scope 3 subtotal = 187,270 tCO2e - Sum of purchased clinker and business-travel emissions.
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Total gross emissions = 215,576 tCO2e - Sum of all three scope subtotals.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Intensity per SAR million revenue = 117.16 - Total emissions / revenue in SAR millions (ISSB intensity metric).
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Intensity per tonne of product = 0.0695 - Total emissions / production tonnes (physical intensity metric).
- **Carbon-Price x Emissions Sensitivity Stress Test** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: IFRS S2 (ISSB) Climate Resilience / TCFD Scenario Analysis
  - _Measures:_ Whether the candidate can build a real two-variable sensitivity (data table / array formula) for a climate-transition cost model and read its corners - the core analytical artefact behind an ISSB climate-resilience disclosure.
  - _Scenario:_ Continuing for Najd Cement, the board's risk committee wants a climate-transition stress test of the annual carbon cost. Given inputs: baseline total emissions 215,576 tCO2e; assumed free-allocation / exempt share 30% (so only 70% of emissions are priced). The candidate first computes the priced (chargeable) emissions, then builds a TWO-VARIABLE data table of annual carbon cost (SAR) across a carbon-price axis (USD/tCO2e converted at SAR 3.75/USD) of USD 25, 50, 75, 100 and an exempt-share axis of 20%, 30%, 40%. Carbon cost = emissions x (1 - exempt_share) x (price_USD x 3.75). The table must be a NATIVE data table, not hardcoded.
  - _Model answer:_ Priced emissions at the base 30% exemption = 215,576 x 0.70 = 150,903.2 tCO2e. Carbon cost cell = priced_emissions x price_SAR where price_SAR = price_USD x 3.75. Two-variable data table: row input = carbon price (USD), column input = exempt share. Sample corners (cost = 215,576 x (1-exempt) x price_USD x 3.75): low corner USD 25 / 20% exempt = 215,576 x 0.80 x 93.75 = SAR 16,168,200; centre USD 50 / 30% = 215,576 x 0.70 x 187.5 = SAR 28,294,350; high corner USD 100 / 40% = 215,576 x 0.60 x 375 = SAR 48,504,600. The data-table range must be array-driven so changing an input axis repropagates.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Priced emissions = 150,903.2 tCO2e - Base-case chargeable emissions after the 30% exemption (emissions x 0.70).
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Sensitivity grid uses a native data table (not hardcoded) - The carbon-cost matrix is formula/data-table driven across both axes.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (USD 25, 20% exempt) = SAR 16,168,200 - Cheapest-price / least-exempt-impact corner of the stress grid.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Centre case (USD 50, 30% exempt) = SAR 28,294,350 - Base-case carbon cost at the central price and exemption.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (USD 100, 40% exempt) = SAR 48,504,600 - Most-expensive-price corner of the stress grid.

**Pillar - ESG Disclosure Interrogation**

- **GRI / ISSB Disclosure-Coverage Register Query** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: GRI Universal Standards 2021 / IFRS S1 (ISSB) General Requirements
  - _Measures:_ Whether the candidate can interrogate an ESG disclosure register with filtering (material AND status not reported), grouping by framework, counting, and ordering by the gap - the routine data step behind a disclosure-readiness gap analysis.
  - _Scenario:_ A Qatari conglomerate maintains a disclosure-status register tracking each material ESG topic against the framework standard, its assigned owner, materiality flag, and reporting status. The sustainability lead must report, for the board's disclosure-readiness review, how many material topics are still NOT yet 'reported' broken down by framework standard - so the gaps in the upcoming integrated report are visible. The candidate writes one query against the seeded 'disclosures' table to return, per framework, the count of material-but-not-yet-reported topics, worst (largest gap) first.
  - _Model answer:_ Seed a 'disclosures' table (topic, framework, owner, is_material boolean, status in {not_started, in_progress, reported}). Master query: SELECT framework, COUNT(*) AS open_gaps FROM disclosures WHERE is_material = true AND status <> 'reported' GROUP BY framework ORDER BY open_gaps DESC, framework. Graded by ordered result-set match against the master.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Per-framework open material-disclosure gaps, largest gap first - Correct WHERE (material AND status <> reported), GROUP BY framework, COUNT, and ORDER BY count DESC then framework - result set matches master, order-sensitive.

---

### 8.4 Executive Communications, Public Relations, & Stakeholder Engagement

Executive Communications / PR / Stakeholder Engagement is a predominantly non-quantitative function (messaging, narrative, relationship management) that cannot be auto-graded on free text. This blueprint targets the genuinely measurable analytical core of a modern comms/PR operation as practised under the AMEC Integrated Evaluation Framework and Barcelona Principles 3.0 (outputs -> outtakes -> outcomes, never AVE-only), plus the quantitative discipline of stakeholder prioritization (PMI PMBOK / mendelow power-interest). Three pillars, four blocks, three engines. Pillar 1 (Media Investment & Earned-Media Analytics) uses a spreadsheet for a paid-media plan (CPM / reach / frequency / GRP / cost-per-reach) and an advanced_spreadsheet two-variable data table stress-testing campaign reach across CPM and budget. Pillar 2 (Communications Measurement & Sentiment Analytics) uses SQL over a seeded media-coverage table to compute Share of Voice and net-sentiment aggregation across a GCC competitor set. Pillar 3 (Stakeholder Prioritization & Engagement Economics) uses logic_input for a weighted power x interest influence index and engagement-budget allocation. All scenarios use concrete AED/SAR figures and real-sounding GCC entities (an Abu Dhabi sovereign developer, a Riyadh giga-project, regional banks). engine_fit flags honestly that drafting/judgement is out of scope and only the analytics slice is graded.

**Skills:** Media Planning, Buying & Earned-Media Valuation (CPM/reach/frequency/GRP) · Communications Measurement & PR Analytics (AMEC framework, Share of Voice, sentiment) · Stakeholder Identification, Power-Interest Mapping & Prioritization · Campaign Budget Allocation & Scenario Stress-Testing · Reputation & Sentiment Data Interrogation (media-monitoring datasets) · Engagement ROI & Outcome Metrics Reporting

**Engine fit:** This is fundamentally a NON-QUANTITATIVE function: its core deliverables are press releases, executive speeches, narrative strategy, crisis messaging, media relationships and stakeholder judgement - none of which the four engines can auto-grade (no free-text/essay/subjective scoring). Per the design rules I have built the gradable QUANTITATIVE / ANALYTICAL slice that every credible modern comms function now owns under AMEC Barcelona Principles 3.0 (measurement, not AVE-only) and PMI stakeholder discipline: (a) media-investment math - CPM, gross/net reach, frequency, GRPs, cost-per-reach, earned-media value - graded as exact spreadsheet cell values; (b) a two-variable sensitivity data table on campaign reach (advanced_spreadsheet, is_array_formula + corner cells); (c) Share-of-Voice and net-sentiment aggregation over a seeded media-coverage relational table (sql_result_match); (d) a weighted power x interest stakeholder influence index and engagement-budget split (logic_input). LIMITATION (flagged honestly): message quality, narrative persuasiveness, drafting craft, media-relationship skill and crisis judgement - the heart of the role - are NOT measured here; this sandbox certifies only the data-literate, analytics-and-budget side of executive communications. It should be paired with a human-rated work sample for the writing/judgement competencies.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL, Logic input

**Pillar - Media Investment & Earned-Media Analytics**

- **Paid-Media Plan: CPM, Reach, Frequency & Cost Efficiency** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: AMEC Integrated Evaluation Framework / Barcelona Principles 3.0 (outputs metrics, no AVE-only)
  - _Measures:_ Builds a defensible paid-media plan and computes the standard buying metrics (CPM, reach, frequency, cost-per-reach) that govern budget efficiency, plus correct campaign-level rollups and a blended CPM.
  - _Scenario:_ Aldar-style Abu Dhabi sovereign developer 'Marsa Capital' is launching a flagship waterfront district. The corporate communications team must finalise the paid-media plan across four channels for the AED 1,200,000 launch campaign. Given per-channel impressions (000s), spend (AED) and reach percentages of a 2,500,000 target audience, complete the plan: cost-per-mille (CPM = spend / impressions-in-thousands), channel reach in people (reach% x 2,500,000), average frequency (impressions / reach-people), and the campaign efficiency KPI cost-per-reached-person (spend / reach-people). Then compute the campaign totals and the blended CPM. Channel data: Out-of-Home (LED) impressions 18,000k, spend AED 540,000, reach 22%; Digital Display impressions 30,000k, spend AED 300,000, reach 30%; Social impressions 45,000k, spend AED 240,000, reach 28%; Print (broadsheet) impressions 6,000k, spend AED 120,000, reach 10%.
  - _Model answer:_ CPM per channel = spend / (impressions_000s) since impressions are already in thousands: OOH 540000/18000 = 30.00; Digital 300000/30000 = 10.00; Social 240000/45000 = 5.333...; Print 120000/6000 = 20.00. Reach-people = reach% x 2,500,000: OOH 550,000; Digital 750,000; Social 700,000; Print 250,000. Avg frequency = impressions (in absolute, = 000s x 1000) / reach-people: OOH 18,000,000/550,000 = 32.727; Social 45,000,000/700,000 = 64.286. Cost-per-reached-person = spend / reach-people: OOH 540000/550000 = 0.98182; Social 240000/700000 = 0.34286. Totals: total spend 1,200,000; total impressions 99,000k; blended CPM = 1,200,000 / 99,000 = 12.1212. Checkpoints verify a per-channel CPM, a per-channel reach-people, a per-channel frequency, a per-channel cost-per-reach, total spend, and blended CPM.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - OOH CPM = AED 30.00 (540000/18000) - Cost-per-mille computed correctly with impressions already in thousands
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Social CPM = AED 5.33 (240000/45000) - CPM on the highest-impression channel
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Digital reach-people = 750,000 (30% x 2,500,000) - Converts reach percentage to absolute reached audience
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Social average frequency = 64.29 (45,000,000 / 700,000) - Average frequency = total impressions / unique reach
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Social cost-per-reached-person = AED 0.343 (240000/700000) - Efficiency KPI linking spend to unique audience
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Blended campaign CPM = AED 12.12 (1,200,000 / 99,000) - Correct campaign-level rollup and blended efficiency metric
- **Reach Stress-Test: Two-Variable CPM x Budget Sensitivity Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: AFP/FPAC scenario-analysis discipline applied to comms budgeting (AMEC outputs layer)
  - _Measures:_ Constructs a native two-variable sensitivity/data table to stress-test campaign reach against negotiated rate and budget - the analytical backbone of defensible media-investment recommendations.
  - _Scenario:_ For the same Marsa Capital launch, the Group CCO wants a sensitivity grid showing achievable gross impressions (in 000s) as the negotiated digital CPM and the available budget both vary, so the board can see the trade-off before sign-off. The model cell computes Gross Impressions (000s) = Budget / CPM. Base inputs: Budget = AED 300,000, CPM = AED 10. Build the two-variable data table with CPM down the rows (AED 8, 10, 12.5) and Budget across the columns (AED 240,000, 300,000, 360,000). The grid must be a native data table driven by the model cell, not hardcoded numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Model cell: Gross Impressions (000s) = Budget / CPM = 300000/10 = 30,000. Two-variable data table corner links to the model cell; row input = CPM, column input = Budget. Interior = Budget / CPM (impressions in 000s): at CPM 8: Budget 240k -> 30,000; 300k -> 37,500; 360k -> 45,000. At CPM 10: 24,000 / 30,000 / 36,000. At CPM 12.5: 19,200 / 24,000 / 28,800. Checkpoints: is_array_formula over the data-table range; low corner (CPM 8, Budget 240k) = 30,000; base/centre (CPM 10, Budget 300k) = 30,000; high corner (CPM 12.5, Budget 360k) = 28,800; and one off-diagonal (CPM 8, Budget 360k) = 45,000 to defeat a single-formula guess.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Grid uses a native two-variable data table {=TABLE(...)} (not hardcoded) - Candidate built a real data table driven by the model cell, not typed numbers
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (CPM 8, Budget 240k) = 30,000 (000s) - Correct interior value at cheapest rate / smallest budget
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Centre/base (CPM 10, Budget 300k) = 30,000 (000s) - Data table reproduces the base case at the centre
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (CPM 12.5, Budget 360k) = 28,800 (000s) - Correct interior value at premium rate / largest budget
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Off-diagonal (CPM 8, Budget 360k) = 45,000 (000s) - Both axes wired to the right inputs (defeats a constant-grid guess)

**Pillar - Communications Measurement & Sentiment Analytics**

- **Share of Voice & Net-Sentiment over a Media-Coverage Dataset** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: AMEC Integrated Evaluation Framework (outtakes/sentiment) & Barcelona Principles 3.0
  - _Measures:_ Interrogates a real media-monitoring dataset to produce the Share-of-Voice (reach + volume) and net-sentiment aggregation that underpins AMEC-compliant communications reporting, instead of relying on AVE.
  - _Scenario:_ A Riyadh giga-project's corporate affairs team monitors earned media across itself and its regional peer set. The media-monitoring vendor has loaded a 'coverage' table (one row per article) with columns: id, outlet, brand, reach (audience reached by the article), sentiment ('positive' \| 'neutral' \| 'negative'), pub_date. The CCO needs a measurement view: for each brand, the article count, total reach, and a Net Sentiment Score = (positive_articles - negative_articles), ranked by total reach (highest first) so leadership sees who is dominating Share of Voice and with what tone. Seeded brands include the giga-project itself plus three GCC peers; write ONE query returning brand, article_count, total_reach, net_sentiment ordered by total_reach descending.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT brand, COUNT(*) AS article_count, SUM(reach) AS total_reach, SUM(CASE WHEN sentiment='positive' THEN 1 WHEN sentiment='negative' THEN -1 ELSE 0 END) AS net_sentiment FROM coverage GROUP BY brand ORDER BY total_reach DESC, brand. The conditional aggregation for net sentiment (+1 positive, -1 negative, 0 neutral) is the discriminating skill; GROUP BY brand with COUNT and SUM(reach) gives volume + reach Share of Voice; ORDER BY total_reach DESC ranks dominance. Result-set match is order-sensitive on total_reach descending.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master: per-brand article_count, total_reach, net_sentiment, ordered by total_reach desc - Correct GROUP BY aggregation, conditional net-sentiment sum, and reach-ranked ordering for a Share-of-Voice + tone view

**Pillar - Stakeholder Prioritization & Engagement Economics**

- **Weighted Power-Interest Influence Index & Engagement-Budget Split** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 10 min · ref: PMI PMBOK Stakeholder Management / Mendelow Power-Interest Grid
  - _Measures:_ Applies a weighted power-interest model to rank stakeholders objectively and converts relative influence into a defensible, proportional engagement-budget allocation - the quantitative core of stakeholder management.
  - _Scenario:_ Ahead of a Dubai-listed bank's annual results and a sensitive cost-restructuring announcement, the Head of Investor & Corporate Communications must prioritize five stakeholder groups and allocate an AED 500,000 engagement budget. Each group is scored 1-5 on Power and 1-5 on Interest. The agreed Influence Index = (Power x 0.6) + (Interest x 0.4), then scaled to a 0-100 priority by multiplying by 20. Engagement budget for a group = AED 500,000 x (that group's Influence Index / sum of all groups' Influence Indices). Groups (Power, Interest): Regulators/Central Bank (5, 3); Institutional Investors (4, 5); Employees (2, 5); Local Media (3, 4); Community NGOs (1, 2). Compute: (1) Institutional Investors' priority score (0-100), (2) Regulators' priority score (0-100), (3) the sum of all five Influence Indices (raw, before x20), and (4) Institutional Investors' engagement budget in AED.
  - _Model answer:_ Influence Index (raw) = Power*0.6 + Interest*0.4. Regulators: 5*0.6+3*0.4 = 3.0+1.2 = 4.2 -> priority 84. Institutional Investors: 4*0.6+5*0.4 = 2.4+2.0 = 4.4 -> priority 88. Employees: 2*0.6+5*0.4 = 1.2+2.0 = 3.2. Local Media: 3*0.6+4*0.4 = 1.8+1.6 = 3.4. Community NGOs: 1*0.6+2*0.4 = 0.6+0.8 = 1.4. Sum of raw indices = 4.2+4.4+3.2+3.4+1.4 = 16.6. Institutional Investors budget = 500000 * (4.4/16.6) = 500000 * 0.265060 = AED 132,530.12. Checkpoints verify the two priority scores, the index sum (the allocation denominator), and the proportional budget.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Institutional Investors priority score = 88 ((4x0.6+5x0.4)x20) - Weighted index and 0-100 scaling applied correctly to the top stakeholder
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Regulators priority score = 84 ((5x0.6+3x0.4)x20) - Weighting correctly favours Power over Interest
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Sum of all five raw Influence Indices = 16.6 - Correct allocation denominator across the full stakeholder set
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Institutional Investors engagement budget = AED 132,530.12 (500000 x 4.4/16.6) - Converts relative influence into a proportional, defensible budget split
