## Governance, Risk & Compliance

> **Domain review** - engine coverage OK. All 4 blueprints satisfy the structural rules: each declares 3 pillars; block counts are in range (9.1=5, 9.2=4, 9.3=5, 9.4=4); each uses >=3 distinct engine types (9.1=4, 9.2=3, 9.3=4, 9.4=4). Every block maps to a valid engine and every engine pairs with the correct checkpoint kind per src/lib/technical-sandbox/types.ts (logic_input->logic_value, spreadsheet->cell_value, advanced_spreadsheet->is_array_formula+cell_value, sql->sql_result_match). No invalid or 'python' engine appears. The four functions here are all genuinely non-quantitative GRC roles (corp-sec, contracts, ethics/ABAC, statutory audit) and every blueprint correctly pivots to the gradable analytical slice with an explicit honest-limitation statement in engine_fit - this is exactly the prompt's required approach for soft functions, and it is done well and consistently. Difficulty mix is healthy in 9.1/9.3/9.4 (each spans basic->advanced); 9.2 is the only one with no 'basic' block (advanced/intermediate x3). Cross-blueprint consistency is strong: all use the GCC/MENA framing and standard pro frameworks (ISA 320/530, ABAC residual-risk, 4/5ths-style governance ratios), mirroring the FP&A reference's rigor. SQL blocks are uniformly single-checkpoint (1x sql_result_match), which matches the FP&A reference precedent exactly. Verification limitation: the compact view does not expose the pillar->block assignment, so I could not confirm every pillar carries >=1 block in the 3-pillar/4-block cases (9.2, 9.4) - this should be checked in the full blueprint.
>
> - _(medium)_ 9.2: Difficulty mix lacks a 'basic' block - the four blocks are advanced/intermediate/intermediate/intermediate. The prompt requires mixing difficulty across blocks; add a basic-tier entry point (e.g. a straightforward late-payment-interest or single-cap exposure logic_input/spreadsheet) so the sitting opens accessibly like the other three blueprints (9.1, 9.3, 9.4 all start basic).
> - _(low)_ 9.2: Two of the four blocks share the spreadsheet engine (Liability Cap build + Payment Terms/Retention). With only 4 blocks this leaves just 3 distinct engines and a same-engine pair sitting back-to-back in the same pillar; consider differentiating one (e.g. recast the retention/late-interest block as logic_input, or convert one spreadsheet block to advanced_spreadsheet with a 2-var LD-accrual-vs-delay sensitivity table) to widen variety. Omitting advanced_spreadsheet is defensible per engine_fit, but the resulting engine spread is the thinnest of the four blueprints.
> - _(low)_ 9.1: The SQL block 'Statutory Register Interrogation' carries only 1 checkpoint, below the stated per-block floor of 3-6 weighted checkpoints. This matches the FP&A reference (single sql_result_match), so it is engine-consistent and not a hard error - but for a register-interrogation task the realism would improve by splitting into 2-3 distinct sql_result_match checks (e.g. RPTs above threshold; filings overdue in a window) or raising its weight to reflect its importance. Same single-checkpoint SQL pattern applies to 9.2, 9.3, 9.4.
> - _(low)_ 9.3: Pillar balance: five blocks across three pillars with two basic/intermediate logic_input blocks ('Residual Bribery-Risk Index' and 'Gifts/Hospitality COI Threshold Math') that are conceptually adjacent (both weighted-threshold field math). Confirm they sit in distinct pillars and that the heavier advanced blocks (SQL ledger + advanced_spreadsheet sensitivity) are not both crowded into one pillar, which would unbalance per-pillar weight. Verify in the full blueprint.
> - _(low)_ 9.4: Strong engine variety (4 distinct engines in 4 blocks) but only 4 blocks for 3 pillars means one pillar holds two blocks and two hold one each. Confirm the materiality/sample-size logic_input and the sample-size sensitivity advanced_spreadsheet (both sampling-themed) are deliberately split or grouped sensibly; if both land in the same pillar, the other two pillars each rest on a single block, making per-pillar scores noisier. Verify pillar->block mapping in the full blueprint.
>
> _Recommendations:_ Overall the grc domain is in good shape and clears the hard constraints: valid engines, correct checkpoint-kind pairings, 3 pillars each, block counts in range, and every non-quantitative function correctly redirected to a defensible gradable slice with an explicit limitation note. No blocker-severity issues. Priority fixes, in order: (1) 9.2 - add a basic-tier block so it spans the full difficulty range like the other three, and ideally diversify one of its two spreadsheet blocks (medium). (2) Optionally enrich the single-checkpoint SQL blocks (9.1/9.2/9.3/9.4) into 2-3 sql_result_match checks for richer signal, though single-checkpoint SQL is acceptable per the FP&A reference. (3) In the full (non-compact) blueprints, verify the pillar->block assignment for the 3-pillar/4-block cases (9.2, 9.4) and the theme-adjacent blocks in 9.3, so no pillar is left with zero blocks or with all the heavyweight blocks clustered. engine_fit quality is uniformly high - the honest-limitation framing on all four (out-of-scope: drafting/judgement/investigation quality, deferred to MCQ + human review) is exactly right and should be retained.

### 9.1 Corporate Secretarial Practice & Board Governance Administration

Corporate Secretarial Practice & Board Governance Administration is a predominantly qualitative function (minute-taking, resolution drafting, director advisory, statutory liaison) that is not auto-gradable as written. This blueprint isolates the QUANTITATIVE / ANALYTICAL slice that a competent company secretary must master and that IS gradable across the four engines: board composition and independence ratios, quorum and voting-threshold mathematics (ordinary vs. special resolutions, cumulative voting, related-party recusal), director attendance and diversity scorecards, AGM/EGM outcome sensitivity, and interrogation of the statutory registers (directors, related-party transactions, conflicts, filing deadlines). Skills list was empty in functions.json, so six skills were proposed grounded in GCC governance practice (UAE SCA Code, Saudi CMA CGR, OECD Principles, CGI/ICSA). Three pillars, four blocks, mixing logic_input, spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet and sql so the sitting is varied and difficulty rises from basic to advanced.

**Skills:** Board Composition & Independence Assessment · Quorum, Voting Thresholds & Resolution Mechanics · Director Attendance & Board Effectiveness Analytics · Related-Party Transactions & Conflict-of-Interest Registers · Statutory Registers, Filings & Compliance Deadlines · Shareholder Meeting (AGM/EGM) Administration & Cumulative Voting

**Engine fit:** Corporate secretarial work is mostly free-text and judgement (drafting minutes, resolutions, advising the chair) which CANNOT be auto-graded. Per the rules, this blueprint deliberately targets the function's quantitative governance core, which maps cleanly to the four engines. logic_input handles the discrete governance arithmetic a secretary computes by hand before every meeting: independence ratio vs. the code minimum, ordinary/special-resolution vote counts net of recused related parties, and cumulative-voting seat allocation. spreadsheet handles the recurring board-composition / diversity / attendance scorecard the secretary maintains and reports to the Nomination & Governance Committee. advanced_spreadsheet handles a genuinely native two-variable data table - how a special-resolution outcome flips across turnout and yes-share assumptions (vote-outcome sensitivity), which is exactly the "what-if before the AGM" the secretary runs. sql handles interrogation of the statutory registers (directors, related-party transactions, filing deadlines) - obligations expiring within a window, RPTs above the disclosure threshold, overdue regulatory filings - the contracts-table analogue called out in the prompt for legal/governance functions. The honest limitation: this measures the analytical/compliance-arithmetic competence of the role, not drafting quality, board-dynamics judgement, or advisory soft skills, which remain out of scope for any auto-grader and would need a separate human-rated or MCQ layer.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 5 tasks · engines: Logic input, Spreadsheet, Adv. Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Board Composition & Governance Ratios**

- **Board Independence & Composition Compliance Check** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 9 min · ref: UAE SCA Corporate Governance Code (Chairman's Decision 3/RM/2020) / OECD Principles of Corporate Governance
  - _Measures:_ Translating a governance code's quantitative composition requirements into pass/fail director counts - the recurring board-refresh and committee-staffing arithmetic a company secretary performs for the Nomination & Governance Committee.
  - _Scenario:_ Emaar-style UAE listed entity 'Khaleej Holding PJSC' has a 9-member board: 3 directors are classified Independent, 2 are Executive (incl. the CEO), and 4 are Non-Executive but Non-Independent (one represents a 22% shareholder). The SCA Code requires (a) at least one-third of the board to be Independent, (b) a majority of the board to be Non-Executive, and (c) the Chairman to be Non-Executive. The Nomination & Remuneration Committee must be a minimum of 3 members with a majority Independent. Compute: the independence ratio (Independent / total, as a percentage), the minimum number of Independent directors required to meet the one-third floor (rounded UP to a whole director), the shortfall in Independent directors (required minus actual, floored at 0), the Non-Executive count, and the minimum Independent members needed on a 3-person NRC (majority = more than half, rounded up).
  - _Model answer:_ Total = 9. Independent = 3. independence_pct = 3/9 = 33.333%. One-third floor on 9 = 9/3 = 3, rounded UP = 3 required. Shortfall = max(3 - 3, 0) = 0. Non-Executive = total - executive = 9 - 2 = 7. NRC majority on 3 = floor(3/2)+1 = 2 Independent members minimum. All thresholds met (33.33% >= 33.33%, NE 7 of 9 is a majority).
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Independence ratio = 33.33% - Independent directors as a percentage of total board (3/9)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Minimum Independent directors required (one-third floor, rounded up) = 3 - Ceiling of total/3 applied to board size 9
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Independent-director shortfall = 0 - max(required - actual, 0) reconciles the compliance gap
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Non-Executive director count = 7 - Total less executive directors confirms NE majority
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Minimum Independent members on a 3-person NRC = 2 - Majority-independence rule on a committee of 3
- **Board Composition, Diversity & Attendance Scorecard** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: Saudi CMA Corporate Governance Regulations (2023) / Chartered Governance Institute (CGI/ICSA) board-effectiveness guidance
  - _Measures:_ Building the standing board-composition and attendance scorecard from a director register - the core quantitative deliverable of the company secretary's annual governance report, including diversity and over-tenure flags used in board-refresh planning.
  - _Scenario:_ Riyadh-listed 'Najd Industrial Co. (Tadawul)' has an 8-director board. The pre-populated grid lists each director with: classification (Independent / Non-Executive / Executive), gender, tenure in years, and meetings attended out of 10 board meetings held in the year. The company secretary must complete the governance scorecard the board reports to the CMA: total board meetings-possible (directors x meetings held), total meetings attended (sum of the attendance column), overall board attendance rate, count of Independent directors, board independence percentage, count of female directors, gender-diversity percentage, count of directors whose tenure exceeds the 9-year independence-erosion guideline, and average board tenure.
  - _Model answer:_ 8 directors x 10 meetings = 80 meetings-possible (cell B-total). Attendance column sums to 71 attended; attendance rate = 71/80 = 88.75%. Independent count via COUNTIF on classification = 3; independence % = 3/8 = 37.5%. Female count via COUNTIF = 2; gender-diversity % = 2/8 = 25%. Over-9-year count via COUNTIF(tenure,>9) = 2. Average tenure = AVERAGE of tenure column = 6.5 years. All cells are formula-driven off the seeded director rows.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total meetings possible = 80 - Directors multiplied by board meetings held
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total meetings attended = 71 - SUM over the attendance column
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Overall board attendance rate = 88.75% - Attended divided by possible
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Board independence percentage = 37.5% - COUNTIF Independent over total board
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Gender-diversity percentage = 25% - COUNTIF female over total board
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Directors over the 9-year tenure guideline = 2 - COUNTIF on tenure > 9 flags independence erosion

**Pillar - Resolution & Voting Mechanics**

- **AGM Quorum, Resolution Thresholds & Related-Party Recusal** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: UAE Federal Decree-Law No. 32 of 2021 (Commercial Companies Law) / Saudi Companies Law - shareholder-meeting quorum & resolution thresholds
  - _Measures:_ Computing meeting quorum, ordinary- vs. special-resolution pass percentages, and the effect of a related-party recusal on the eligible voting base - the live arithmetic a company secretary runs at the rostrum to declare whether each resolution carries.
  - _Scenario:_ 'Gulf Logistics PJSC' has 10,000,000 issued shares (one vote each). At the AGM, holders of 6,200,000 shares are present in person or by proxy. The articles require a quorum of 50% of capital for an ordinary resolution and the Commercial Companies Law requires a special resolution to pass by 75% of shares represented at the meeting. Two agenda items: (1) an Ordinary Resolution to approve the dividend - 3,900,000 shares vote FOR, 2,300,000 vote AGAINST; (2) a Special Resolution to amend the articles - but it is a related-party matter and a single shareholder holding 1,200,000 of the present shares must recuse (abstain) under the conflict rules, leaving the remaining present shares to vote, of which 3,600,000 vote FOR. Compute: the quorum percentage of present shares (present / issued), the FOR percentage on the ordinary resolution (for / present), the eligible voting base for the special resolution after recusal (present - recused), the FOR percentage on the special resolution (special-for / eligible base), and the special-resolution shortfall in shares versus the 75% pass mark (75% of eligible base minus special-for, floored at 0).
  - _Model answer:_ Quorum % = 6,200,000/10,000,000 = 62% (>50%, quorate). Ordinary FOR % = 3,900,000/6,200,000 = 62.903% (>50%, carries). Recused = 1,200,000, so special eligible base = 6,200,000 - 1,200,000 = 5,000,000. Special FOR % = 3,600,000/5,000,000 = 72% (<75%, fails). 75% mark = 0.75 x 5,000,000 = 3,750,000; shortfall = max(3,750,000 - 3,600,000, 0) = 150,000 shares.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Quorum percentage = 62% - Shares present over shares issued meets the 50% quorum
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Ordinary-resolution FOR percentage = 62.9% - FOR votes over shares present clear the simple-majority bar
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Special-resolution eligible base after recusal = 5,000,000 - Present shares less the recused related-party block
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Special-resolution FOR percentage = 72% - Special FOR over the recusal-adjusted base
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Special-resolution shortfall vs. 75% = 150,000 shares - Gap to the special-resolution pass mark on the eligible base
- **Special-Resolution Outcome Sensitivity (Turnout x Yes-Share)** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18.3 min · ref: OECD Principles of Corporate Governance (shareholder rights) / Chartered Governance Institute meeting-administration practice
  - _Measures:_ Constructing a genuine two-variable data table to pre-test a special-resolution outcome across turnout and support scenarios - the what-if a competent company secretary runs for the chair before a contested EGM, distinguishing array-driven sensitivity from hardcoded guesses.
  - _Scenario:_ Ahead of an EGM for 'Khaleej Holding PJSC' (10,000,000 issued shares), the company secretary stress-tests whether a Special Resolution requiring 75% of shares-represented will carry. The model takes two inputs: turnout (% of the 10,000,000 issued shares that attend) and yes-share (% of the represented shares that vote FOR). The pass margin in shares is computed as: represented = turnout% x 10,000,000; for-votes = yes-share% x represented; pass-margin = for-votes minus (75% x represented), i.e. how many shares ABOVE the special-resolution threshold the resolution clears (negative means it fails). Build a native two-variable data table of the pass-margin across turnout rows {50%, 65%, 80%} and yes-share columns {70%, 75%, 80%}, with the corner cell linking to the live pass-margin formula.
  - _Model answer:_ Live cell: represented = turnout x 10,000,000; for = yes-share x represented; pass-margin = for - 0.75 x represented = represented x (yes-share - 0.75). At base 65% turnout / 75% yes-share: represented = 6,500,000, margin = 6,500,000 x 0 = 0. Data table corners: 50% turnout & 70% yes = 5,000,000 x (0.70-0.75) = -250,000 (fails); 80% turnout & 80% yes = 8,000,000 x 0.05 = +400,000 (carries); center 65% x 75% = 0 (exactly on the line). Candidate must wire the corner cell to the pass-margin formula and apply a real {=TABLE()} across the 3x3 grid.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - 3x3 grid is a native data table {=TABLE()}, not hardcoded - The sensitivity grid is array-formula driven off the two inputs
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Live pass-margin at base case (65% turnout, 75% yes) = 0 - The driver formula sits exactly on the special-resolution threshold
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner (50% turnout, 70% yes) = -250,000 - Resolution fails by 250,000 shares under low turnout/support
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner (80% turnout, 80% yes) = 400,000 - Resolution clears by 400,000 shares under high turnout/support
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Center cell (65% turnout, 75% yes) = 0 - Interior data-table value reconciles with the live formula

**Pillar - Statutory Registers & Compliance Interrogation**

- **Statutory Register Interrogation: RPTs & Filing Deadlines (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 11 min · ref: Saudi CMA Corporate Governance Regulations & UAE SCA disclosure rules (related-party transactions, statutory filings) / CGI register-keeping standards
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating the statutory register to surface high-value, overdue related-party transactions for the audit and governance committees - the contracts/obligations-table query (filter by type + status + threshold, ranked) that defensible governance reporting depends on.
  - _Scenario:_ The company secretary maintains a 'statutory_filings' register for 'Najd Industrial Co.' with columns (id, filing_type, regulator, due_date, status, related_party text, amount_sar numeric). It records both regulatory filings (e.g. annual report, board-change notice) and disclosable related-party transactions (RPTs) requiring board or shareholder approval. The board pack needs an exception report: identify every OVERDUE related-party transaction that breaches the disclosure threshold - rows where filing_type = 'RPT', status = 'overdue', AND amount_sar > 5,000,000 - returning the related_party and the amount, largest amount first.
  - _Model answer:_ Single SELECT against statutory_filings with a compound WHERE (filing_type='RPT' AND status='overdue' AND amount_sar>5000000), projecting related_party and amount_sar, ORDER BY amount_sar DESC. The seed includes RPTs above and below the SAR 5m threshold and overdue vs. filed statuses, plus non-RPT regulatory filings as distractors, so only the qualifying high-value overdue RPTs return in descending amount order.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result set matches master: overdue RPTs over SAR 5m, related_party + amount, largest first - Compound type/status/threshold filter with correct projection and descending order

---

### 9.2 Contract Drafting, Vetting, & Legal Risk Mitigation

Contract Drafting, Vetting & Legal Risk Mitigation is a qualitative legal function (clause drafting, negotiation, judgement) whose core deliverables - drafted language, written advice, redline rationale - cannot be auto-graded by the four numeric engines. This blueprint therefore measures the QUANTITATIVE / ANALYTICAL slice of the contracts-and-legal-risk role that a competent commercial counsel or contracts manager genuinely performs: (1) computing contractual financial exposure (liability caps, LDs/penalties, indemnity ceilings, payment terms) in a spreadsheet model; (2) scoring and weighting clause-level legal risk into a defensible risk index via logic_input; and (3) interrogating a contract-lifecycle-management (CLM) register in SQL to surface expiring obligations, breached liability caps, and auto-renewal windows. Skills list was empty, so six GCC-grounded skills were proposed and the design maps to them. Three pillars, four blocks, three engines (spreadsheet, logic_input, sql), basic to advanced. engine_fit honestly flags that drafting quality itself is out of scope and only the gradable analytical proxy is assessed.

**Skills:** Contractual Financial Exposure & Liability Modelling (caps, LDs, indemnities) · Clause-Level Legal Risk Scoring & Risk-Index Weighting · Contract Lifecycle Management (CLM) Register Interrogation & Obligation Tracking · Renewal, Termination & Notice-Window Computation · Penalty, Liquidated-Damages & Service-Credit Calculation · GCC Commercial Contract Compliance (UAE Civil Code / KSA Government Tenders & Procurement Law)

**Engine fit:** Contract drafting, vetting and legal-risk mitigation is fundamentally a qualitative, judgement-and-language function: its primary outputs (drafted clauses, redline rationale, written legal advice, negotiation positions) are free text and CANNOT be graded by the four numeric engines - none of which can assess prose quality, legal soundness, or drafting style. Rather than fabricate a graded essay, this blueprint deliberately targets the QUANTITATIVE / ANALYTICAL slice that competent commercial counsel and contract managers perform daily and that IS objectively gradable: (a) contractual financial-exposure modelling - liability caps, liquidated-damages/penalty accrual, indemnity ceilings, payment/retention terms - is exact arithmetic, a strong fit for the spreadsheet engine; (b) clause-level legal-risk scoring - converting qualitative risk findings into a weighted, defensible risk index (likelihood x impact x weight, capped) - is deterministic once the rubric is fixed, a clean fit for logic_input; (c) contract-register / CLM interrogation - which contracts auto-renew inside the notice window, which have breached their liability cap, total exposure by counterparty - is precisely what SQL over a contracts table does best. Advanced_spreadsheet (data tables/array formulas) was intentionally omitted: a contracts-risk role rarely builds two-variable sensitivity tables, so forcing one would be contrived; the three chosen engines give genuine variety while staying authentic to the role. HONEST LIMITATION: a high score here demonstrates the candidate can quantify, track and risk-rank contractual obligations and exposure - it does NOT certify drafting skill, legal interpretation, or negotiation judgement, which require human review of written work.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Spreadsheet, Logic input, SQL

**Pillar - Contractual Financial Exposure Modelling**

- **Liability Cap, Liquidated Damages & Net Exposure Build** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · advanced · 18.3 min · ref: UAE Federal Decree-Law No. 50 of 2022 (Commercial Transactions Law) / IACCM-WorldCC Contract Risk Principles
  - _Measures:_ Computing layered contractual financial exposure - applying a per-event LD rate, a LD sub-cap, an overall liability cap, and a security/bond offset in the correct order of operations (the single most common error in contract exposure analysis is applying caps in the wrong sequence or double-capping).
  - _Scenario:_ Emaar Facilities Management LLC (Dubai) has engaged a contractor under a 12-month FM services agreement worth AED 6,000,000 (annual contract value). The contract contains: a liability cap of 30% of annual contract value; liquidated damages (LDs) for service-level failures of AED 5,000 per SLA breach day, themselves sub-capped at 10% of annual contract value; a performance bond of AED 600,000; and a 5% retention held against each monthly payment. During the year the contractor incurred 95 SLA breach days and caused a separate uninsured property-damage claim assessed at AED 1,400,000. You must complete the exposure model so the recoverable amounts are computed correctly, the LD sub-cap and the overall liability cap are both applied, and the net amount the contractor is exposed to (capped recoverable, net of the performance bond drawdown) is shown. Given cells hold the contract parameters and the raw claim figures; you compute the derived rows.
  - _Model answer:_ Annual Contract Value (ACV)=6,000,000 (given). Liability cap = 30% x ACV = 1,800,000 (B-cap = 0.30*ACV). Raw LDs = 95 days x 5,000 = 475,000. LD sub-cap = 10% x ACV = 600,000; capped LDs = MIN(raw LDs, LD sub-cap) = MIN(475,000, 600,000) = 475,000. Total raw recoverable before overall cap = capped LDs + property-damage claim = 475,000 + 1,400,000 = 1,875,000. Apply overall liability cap = MIN(1,875,000, 1,800,000) = 1,800,000 (this is the gross capped recoverable). Net exposure to contractor after drawing the performance bond = capped recoverable - performance bond = 1,800,000 - 600,000 = 1,200,000. Each derived cell is graded.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Liability cap = 30% x ACV (AED 1,800,000) - Correctly derives the overall liability cap from the contract percentage and annual contract value
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Raw liquidated damages = 95 x AED 5,000 (AED 475,000) - Applies the per-breach-day LD rate to the breach-day count
    - `cell_value` (w2) - LD sub-cap applied: capped LDs = MIN(raw LDs, 10% x ACV) (AED 475,000) - Applies the LD-specific sub-cap before aggregation, not the overall cap
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total raw recoverable before overall cap (AED 1,875,000) - Aggregates capped LDs plus the property-damage claim
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Gross capped recoverable = MIN(total, overall cap) (AED 1,800,000) - Applies the overall liability cap last, in the correct sequence
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Net exposure after performance-bond offset (AED 1,200,000) - Nets the drawable security against the capped recoverable to give true residual exposure
- **Payment Terms, Retention Release & Late-Payment Interest** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 15 min · ref: UAE Federal Decree-Law No. 50 of 2022 (Commercial Transactions Law) - commercial interest / Saudi Government Tenders & Procurement Law (retention & advance-payment)
  - _Measures:_ Translating standard GCC construction-contract payment clauses (advance recovery, retention, VAT, late-payment interest) into the exact cash actually payable on a progress certificate - the contracts-administration arithmetic that protects against over/under-payment disputes.
  - _Scenario:_ Saudi Aramco's procurement entity issues a SAR 4,000,000 (excl. VAT) construction sub-package under standard terms: 15% VAT; a 10% advance payment recovered pro-rata across certified work; 5% retention withheld on each progress certificate (half released at provisional acceptance, half at final acceptance 12 months later); and Net-45 payment terms with late-payment interest of 9% per annum (simple) on overdue certified amounts. Progress certificate No.3 certifies SAR 1,500,000 of work (excl. VAT). The certificate was paid 75 days after it fell due (i.e. 30 days late beyond Net-45). Complete the model: VAT on the certificate, the advance-payment recovery on this certificate, the retention withheld, the net cash payable on the certificate, and the late-payment interest on the overdue net amount.
  - _Model answer:_ Certified work (excl VAT) = 1,500,000 (given). VAT = 15% x 1,500,000 = 225,000. Advance recovery on this certificate = 10% x 1,500,000 = 150,000 (pro-rata recovery of the 10% advance against certified value). Retention withheld = 5% x 1,500,000 = 75,000. Net cash payable (excl interest) = certified + VAT - advance recovery - retention = 1,500,000 + 225,000 - 150,000 - 75,000 = 1,500,000. Late-payment interest = net overdue amount x 9% x (30/365) = 1,500,000 x 0.09 x 30/365 = 11,095.89 (tolerance covers rounding). Each derived cell graded.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - VAT on certificate = 15% x SAR 1,500,000 (SAR 225,000) - Applies the correct GCC VAT rate to the certified net value
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Advance-payment recovery = 10% x certified (SAR 150,000) - Recovers the advance pro-rata against the certificate, not the whole contract
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Retention withheld = 5% x certified (SAR 75,000) - Withholds retention on the certificate value before VAT
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Net cash payable on certificate (SAR 1,500,000) - Combines certified + VAT - advance recovery - retention in the correct sign convention
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Late-payment interest = net x 9% x 30/365 (~SAR 11,095.89) - Computes simple commercial interest on the overdue net amount for the days actually late

**Pillar - Clause-Level Legal Risk Scoring**

- **Weighted Clause Risk Index for a Master Services Agreement** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: ISO 31000 Risk Management / IACCM-WorldCC Most-Negotiated-Terms risk taxonomy
  - _Measures:_ Converting qualitative clause-vetting findings into a defensible, reproducible weighted risk index - the discipline that lets a legal function rank deal risk consistently across contracts and trigger escalation by an objective threshold rather than gut feel.
  - _Scenario:_ You are vetting a draft Master Services Agreement (MSA) between Mubadala (Abu Dhabi) and an overseas technology vendor. Legal has flagged four clauses, each rated on Likelihood (1-5) and Impact (1-5), with a category Weight reflecting board risk appetite: (1) Uncapped indemnity - Likelihood 3, Impact 5, Weight 3.0; (2) Governing law = foreign jurisdiction (not UAE) - Likelihood 4, Impact 3, Weight 2.0; (3) Auto-renewal with 90-day notice - Likelihood 4, Impact 2, Weight 1.5; (4) Unlimited liability for data breach - Likelihood 2, Impact 5, Weight 2.5. The clause risk score = Likelihood x Impact x Weight. Compute each clause's weighted risk score, the total weighted risk score, and the normalised risk index = total / maximum possible total (where the max possible per clause = 5 x 5 x its weight), expressed as a percentage to one decimal. Then flag the count of clauses whose individual weighted score is at or above the escalation threshold of 30.
  - _Model answer:_ Clause scores (L x I x W): C1 = 3x5x3.0 = 45; C2 = 4x3x2.0 = 24; C3 = 4x2x1.5 = 12; C4 = 2x5x2.5 = 25. Total weighted = 45+24+12+25 = 106. Max possible = 5x5x(3.0+2.0+1.5+2.5) = 25 x 9.0 = 225. Normalised risk index = 106/225 = 47.111...% -> 47.1%. Clauses at/above threshold 30: only C1 (45) -> count = 1. Fields: clause1_score=45, clause2_score=24, clause3_score=12, clause4_score=25, total_weighted=106, max_possible=225, risk_index_pct=47.1, clauses_over_threshold=1.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Clause 1 (uncapped indemnity) weighted score = 45 - Applies Likelihood x Impact x Weight to the highest-risk clause
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Clause 4 (unlimited data-breach liability) weighted score = 25 - Computes weighted score for a low-likelihood / high-impact clause
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Total weighted risk score = 106 - Aggregates all four clause scores correctly
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Maximum possible total = 225 - Derives the normalisation denominator as 25 x sum of weights
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Normalised risk index = 47.1% - Normalises the total against the maximum and expresses as a percentage to one decimal
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Clauses at/above escalation threshold (>=30) = 1 - Applies an objective escalation threshold to flag clauses for board attention

**Pillar - Contract Lifecycle Register Interrogation**

- **Auto-Renewal & Notice-Window Watchlist (CLM Register SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: IACCM-WorldCC Contract Lifecycle Management / DAMA DMBOK data interrogation
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating a contract-lifecycle register to surface time-critical obligations - identifying contracts whose non-renewal notice window is closing - which is the single highest-value operational task a CLM/legal-ops function performs to prevent unwanted auto-renewals and missed exits.
  - _Scenario:_ A GCC group legal team maintains a contracts register. Each row holds a contract with a counterparty, contract value (AED), an auto_renew flag, the renewal_date, the notice_days required to give non-renewal notice, and the liability_cap_aed agreed versus the exposure_aed currently incurred. The register is seeded with contracts for counterparties including ADNOC Distribution, stc Bahrain, Majid Al Futtaim, Saudi Electricity Co, and others, with renewal dates across 2026. Today is treated as 2026-06-15. Management needs a watchlist of contracts that will AUTO-RENEW unless notice is served, where the deadline to serve notice (renewal_date minus notice_days) falls on or before 90 days from today (i.e. on or before 2026-09-13). Return one row per such contract showing the counterparty and the notice deadline, ordered by the soonest notice deadline first.
  - _Model answer:_ Filter to auto_renew = true, compute notice_deadline = renewal_date - (notice_days \|\| ' days')::interval, and keep rows where notice_deadline <= DATE '2026-06-15' + INTERVAL '90 days' (i.e. <= 2026-09-13). Master query: SELECT counterparty, (renewal_date - (notice_days * INTERVAL '1 day'))::date AS notice_deadline FROM contracts WHERE auto_renew = true AND (renewal_date - (notice_days * INTERVAL '1 day'))::date <= DATE '2026-09-13' ORDER BY notice_deadline ASC, counterparty. Result is order-sensitive (ordered = true) so the soonest-expiring notice window sorts first.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Watchlist matches master (auto-renewing contracts whose notice deadline <= 2026-09-13, counterparty + notice_deadline, soonest first) - Correctly filters to auto-renewing contracts, computes the notice deadline as renewal_date minus notice_days, applies the 90-day window, and orders by soonest deadline

---

### 9.3 Ethics, Anti-Corruption, & Code of Conduct Enforcement Workflows

This function is qualitative at its core (investigations, policy interpretation, disciplinary judgement, tone-at-the-top), so the sandbox targets the QUANTITATIVE/ANALYTICAL slice that a modern ethics & compliance officer must actually operate: anti-bribery risk scoring, gift/hospitality and conflict-of-interest threshold math, whistle-blower case-management SLA analytics, third-party due-diligence portfolio risk, and compliance-program effectiveness metrics (training coverage, screening completeness). The skills list was empty, so I proposed six skills grounded in GCC anti-corruption practice (UAE Federal Decree-Law No. 36 of 2021 on Commercial Fraud, Saudi Nazaha, FATF, ISO 37001 anti-bribery and ISO 37301 compliance management). Three pillars, five blocks across three engines (logic_input, spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, sql): (1) Anti-Corruption Risk Quantification - residual bribery-risk index + COI weighted scoring via logic_input; (2) Case Management & Hotline Analytics - SLA aging/substantiation spreadsheet + SQL over a whistle-blower case ledger; (3) Program Effectiveness & Due-Diligence Monitoring - an advanced_spreadsheet two-variable sensitivity table on third-party screening cost vs coverage. Every checkpoint is an exact numeric/result-set match, so nothing depends on grading free text or subjective judgement.

**Skills:** Anti-Bribery & Corruption (ABAC) Risk Assessment & Scoring · Gifts, Hospitality & Conflict-of-Interest Threshold Controls · Whistle-blower / Speak-Up Case Management & SLA Tracking · Third-Party Due-Diligence & Integrity Screening · Compliance Program Effectiveness Metrics (ISO 37001 / 37301) · Code of Conduct Attestation, Training Coverage & Disciplinary Consistency Analytics

**Engine fit:** Ethics, anti-corruption and code-of-conduct enforcement is fundamentally a JUDGEMENT discipline (investigation narratives, policy drafting, disciplinary decisions, tone-at-the-top) and most of it is NOT auto-gradable. The defensible, gradable proxy is the ANALYTICAL operating layer the modern compliance officer runs daily, which is genuinely numeric: (a) risk quantification - residual ABAC risk = inherent x (1 - control effectiveness), conflict-of-interest weighted indices, gift-aggregation against disclosure thresholds, all clean logic_input field math; (b) case analytics - hotline SLA aging, substantiation/closure rates, ageing buckets in a spreadsheet, plus relational interrogation of a case ledger in SQL (cases breaching SLA, substantiation rate by category, third-party spend at integrity risk); (c) program-effectiveness monitoring - training-coverage %, screening completeness, and a two-variable sensitivity table (advanced_spreadsheet) trading off screening depth vs cost/coverage. This maps cleanly onto three of the four engines (logic_input, spreadsheet/advanced_spreadsheet, sql). HONEST LIMITATION: the irreducibly qualitative core - whether a specific gift is corrupt, how to word a code clause, what discipline is proportionate, the quality of an investigation interview - cannot be auto-graded here and would need the MCQ layer plus human assessor review; this sandbox certifies the quantitative control-operation competence, not investigative or drafting judgement.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 5 tasks · engines: Logic input, Spreadsheet, SQL, Adv. Spreadsheet

**Pillar - Anti-Corruption Risk Quantification**

- **Residual Bribery-Risk Index (Inherent x Control Effectiveness)** &nbsp; `Logic input` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: ISO 37001 Anti-Bribery Management Systems / FATF Recommendations
  - _Measures:_ Quantifying inherent vs residual ABAC risk using a weighted multi-driver model and control-effectiveness haircut, then testing it against a stated risk appetite - the core math behind every ISO 37001 risk register.
  - _Scenario:_ Gulf Crescent Contracting LLC (Abu Dhabi) is profiling bribery risk across its public-sector tendering unit ahead of a board ABAC review. For the unit, Inherent Bribery Risk is scored on a 0-100 scale from three drivers, each rated 1-5 and carrying a fixed weight: Public-Official Interaction (rating 4, weight 0.50), Use of Third-Party Intermediaries (rating 5, weight 0.30), High-Risk Jurisdiction Exposure (rating 3, weight 0.20). The raw weighted rating is converted to the 0-100 inherent score by ((weighted_rating - 1) / 4) x 100. Control Effectiveness is assessed at 65% (i.e. 0.65). Residual Risk = Inherent x (1 - Control Effectiveness). The board's risk appetite caps residual at 25.0; the Residual-vs-Appetite Gap = Residual - 25 (positive = over appetite). Compute each value exactly.
  - _Model answer:_ weighted_rating = 4*0.50 + 5*0.30 + 3*0.20 = 2.00 + 1.50 + 0.60 = 4.10. Inherent score = ((4.10 - 1)/4)*100 = (3.10/4)*100 = 77.5. Residual = 77.5 * (1 - 0.65) = 77.5 * 0.35 = 27.125. Gap = 27.125 - 25 = 2.125 (over appetite). Fields: weighted_rating=4.10, inherent_score=77.5, residual_risk=27.125, appetite_gap=2.125.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Weighted inherent rating (sum of rating x weight) - weighted_rating field equals 4.10
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Inherent risk score on 0-100 scale - inherent_score field equals 77.5
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Residual risk after 65% control effectiveness - residual_risk field equals 27.125
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Residual-vs-appetite gap (over/under cap of 25) - appetite_gap field equals 2.125
- **Gifts, Hospitality & Conflict-of-Interest Threshold Math** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 8 min · ref: UAE Federal Decree-Law No. 31 of 2021 (Anti-Bribery) / OECD Anti-Bribery Convention
  - _Measures:_ Operating gift/hospitality and conflict-of-interest controls as exact threshold logic: per-item approval triggers, rolling aggregation with documented exclusions, and cap-breach detection - the routine arithmetic of register administration.
  - _Scenario:_ A relationship manager at Emirates Northern Bank (Dubai) has logged four items in the gifts & hospitality register for a single government counterparty within one rolling year: a watch valued AED 1,800, event hospitality AED 1,200, a hamper AED 600, and travel of AED 3,400 that was pre-approved and is excluded from aggregation. Policy: any SINGLE non-excluded item above AED 1,500 requires Compliance pre-approval, and the AGGREGATE of non-excluded items to one counterparty within a rolling year must not exceed AED 3,000 (breach if above). Compute: (1) the aggregate value of non-excluded items, (2) the count of single items individually requiring pre-approval, (3) the amount by which the aggregate exceeds the AED 3,000 cap (0 if within cap), and (4) a binary breach flag for the aggregate cap (1 = breached, 0 = within).
  - _Model answer:_ Non-excluded items = 1,800 + 1,200 + 600 = 3,600 (travel 3,400 excluded). aggregate_value=3600. Items above AED 1,500 single threshold: only the watch (1,800) -> items_needing_approval=1. Aggregate excess over 3,000 = 3,600 - 3,000 = 600 -> aggregate_excess=600. Aggregate breach (3,600 > 3,000) -> breach_flag=1.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Aggregate value of non-excluded items - aggregate_value field equals 3600 (excludes pre-approved travel)
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Count of single items needing pre-approval - items_needing_approval field equals 1
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Amount over the AED 3,000 aggregate cap - aggregate_excess field equals 600
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Aggregate cap breach flag (1/0) - breach_flag field equals 1

**Pillar - Case Management & Hotline Analytics**

- **Speak-Up Case Aging & Substantiation Dashboard** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 15 min · ref: ISO 37301 Compliance Management Systems / ACFE Report to the Nations
  - _Measures:_ Building the standard whistle-blower program KPIs - substantiation, closure, SLA breach and backlog rates - by referencing source cells, the reporting that every audit committee expects on hotline health.
  - _Scenario:_ The Group Ethics Office of Saudi Falcon Holding (Riyadh) reviews its Q1 speak-up hotline. A small case ledger is given (per case: category, days-open, target SLA of 45 days, an outcome of Substantiated/Unsubstantiated/Open). Pre-filled given cells supply: total cases 120; cases substantiated 36; cases closed (substantiated + unsubstantiated) 90; cases breaching the 45-day SLA 18; cases still open 30. Complete the KPI block by formula: Substantiation Rate = substantiated / closed; Closure Rate = closed / total; SLA Breach Rate = breached / total; Open Backlog Rate = open / total. Express each as a decimal rate (e.g. 0.40), not a percentage symbol.
  - _Model answer:_ Substantiation Rate = 36/90 = 0.40 (B-cell). Closure Rate = 90/120 = 0.75. SLA Breach Rate = 18/120 = 0.15. Open Backlog Rate = 30/120 = 0.25. Candidate enters formulas referencing the given cells; graded on the four resulting decimal values with tolerance.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Substantiation rate (substantiated / closed) - target KPI cell equals 0.40 within tolerance 0.005
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Closure rate (closed / total) - target KPI cell equals 0.75 within tolerance 0.005
    - `cell_value` (w2) - SLA breach rate (breached / total) - target KPI cell equals 0.15 within tolerance 0.005
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Open backlog rate (open / total) - target KPI cell equals 0.25 within tolerance 0.005
- **Whistle-blower Case Ledger Interrogation (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · advanced · 10 min · ref: FATF Recommendations / ACFE Fraud Examiners Manual
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating a case-management database to surface the corruption categories with both material exposure and a systemic SLA-breach problem - exactly the triage query an ethics analytics function runs to brief the board.
  - _Scenario:_ A seeded Postgres table cases(id, report_channel, category, status, days_open, sla_days, exposure_aed) holds the year's ethics & anti-corruption reports for Gulf Crescent Group. Categories include 'Bribery', 'Conflict of Interest', 'Procurement Fraud', 'Harassment'. Write ONE query that, for the corruption-related categories only ('Bribery','Conflict of Interest','Procurement Fraud'), returns the category, the number of cases, and the total exposure_aed, but ONLY for categories whose number of cases breaching SLA (days_open > sla_days) is 2 or more - ordered by total exposure descending. Columns: category, case_count, total_exposure.
  - _Model answer:_ SELECT category, COUNT(*) AS case_count, SUM(exposure_aed) AS total_exposure FROM cases WHERE category IN ('Bribery','Conflict of Interest','Procurement Fraud') GROUP BY category HAVING SUM(CASE WHEN days_open > sla_days THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) >= 2 ORDER BY total_exposure DESC, category. Seed data is crafted so that two corruption categories clear the >=2-breach HAVING filter and a third is excluded, with deterministic exposure totals and ordering.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result set matches master (category filter + >=2 SLA breaches + ordered by exposure) - candidate query result set equals master query result set, order-sensitive (ordered=true)

**Pillar - Program Effectiveness & Due-Diligence Monitoring**

- **Third-Party Screening Coverage vs Cost Sensitivity Table** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: ISO 37001 Anti-Bribery / OECD Good Practice Guidance on Internal Controls
  - _Measures:_ Modelling compliance-program cost as a function of screening depth and EDD volume using a native two-variable data table - the budgeting analysis that justifies a risk-based due-diligence program to the audit committee.
  - _Scenario:_ Najd Industrial Group (Dammam) is sizing its third-party integrity due-diligence budget. Base inputs (given cells): Number of active third parties = 800; Screening unit cost = AED 250 per third party at base; Enhanced-Due-Diligence (EDD) uplift = AED 600 per EDD case. Annual Screening Cost = (third_parties x screening_unit_cost) + (edd_cases x edd_uplift). The compliance head needs a two-variable data table for Annual Screening Cost across Screening unit cost on one axis (AED 200, 250, 300) and EDD cases on the other axis (40, 80, 120). Build the cost cell first, then a NATIVE two-variable data table (not hardcoded numbers) feeding the unit cost and EDD-case count into the model. Corner/interior values are checked.
  - _Model answer:_ Cost model = third_parties*unit_cost + edd_cases*edd_uplift = 800*unit_cost + edd_cases*600. Low corner (unit 200, EDD 40) = 800*200 + 40*600 = 160,000 + 24,000 = 184,000. Centre (unit 250, EDD 80) = 200,000 + 48,000 = 248,000. High corner (unit 300, EDD 120) = 240,000 + 120*600 = 240,000 + 72,000 = 312,000. Candidate sets the corner formula = base cost cell, marks the data-table range, and Excel fills via TABLE() with unit cost as one input and EDD cases as the other.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Uses a native two-variable data table (not hardcoded values) - the data-table output range is formula-driven {=TABLE(...)}, not typed constants
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Low corner: unit cost 200, EDD 40 cases - low-corner cell equals 184000 within tolerance 1
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Base case: unit cost 250, EDD 80 cases - centre cell equals 248000 within tolerance 1
    - `cell_value` (w1) - High corner: unit cost 300, EDD 120 cases - high-corner cell equals 312000 within tolerance 1

---

### 9.4 Statutory Auditing, Regulatory Liaison, & Policy Compliance Management

Blueprint for the gradable analytical slice of the Statutory Auditing / Regulatory Liaison / Policy Compliance function. The function as named is heavily narrative (audit reports, regulator correspondence, policy drafting) - none of which the four engines can grade. The skills list was empty, so I first proposed six GCC-grounded skills, then designed to the QUANTITATIVE core that IS auto-gradable: materiality + sample-size mathematics, control-testing exception/deviation rates with upper-precision-limit projection, deficiency severity scoring, and SQL interrogation of a findings / regulatory-obligation register. Three pillars, four blocks, three engines (logic_input, advanced_spreadsheet, spreadsheet, sql). Standards anchored to ISA (IAASB), IIA IPPF, COSO, AICPA AU-C audit-sampling, and GCC regulators (UAE SCA / CBUAE, Saudi ZATCA, GOSI/WPS). Difficulty mix: basic logic_input materiality, intermediate spreadsheet deficiency scorecard, advanced advanced_spreadsheet two-variable sample-size matrix, intermediate SQL over an obligations register. Free-text audit judgement is explicitly out of scope and flagged in engine_fit.

**Skills:** Audit Planning, Materiality & Sample-Size Determination · Internal Controls Testing & Exception/Deviation-Rate Analysis · Audit Finding Severity & Risk Scoring (Likelihood × Impact) · Regulatory Obligation Tracking & Compliance-Coverage Reporting · Statutory Filing Deadlines & Penalty Exposure Calculation · Audit Sampling Projection & Upper Deviation Limit (Statistical Sampling)

**Engine fit:** This function is predominantly qualitative - the real-world deliverables are audit reports, management-letter findings, regulator correspondence, and policy documents, none of which the four auto-gradable engines (spreadsheet, advanced_spreadsheet, logic_input, sql) can assess (no free-text / essay grading exists). I therefore designed the QUANTITATIVE / ANALYTICAL slice of the role that is genuinely gradable and central to defensible audit practice: (1) planning materiality + performance materiality + statistical sample-size math (logic_input - exact numeric fields per ISA 320/530 and AICPA AU-C 530), (2) a control-testing deficiency scorecard with deviation rates, projected upper deviation limit, and a likelihood x impact risk index (spreadsheet cell_value checks reconciling to a documented method), (3) a two-variable sample-size sensitivity matrix across tolerable deviation rate and expected deviation rate using a native data table (advanced_spreadsheet, is_array_formula + corner cell_values), and (4) interrogation of a regulatory-obligation / findings register to surface overdue statutory filings and open high-severity findings (sql_result_match). Honest limitation: this measures the analytical/computational and data-interrogation competence of an auditor/compliance analyst - it deliberately does NOT measure audit judgement, scoping rationale, evidence sufficiency conclusions, or report-writing quality, which remain human-graded. The blueprint is a strong proxy for the numerate, defensible core of the function (sampling rigour, materiality discipline, deadline/penalty control, register hygiene) and a poor fit only for the narrative deliverables, which are out of scope by engine constraint.

**Shape:** 3 pillars · 4 tasks · engines: Logic input, Adv. Spreadsheet, Spreadsheet, SQL

**Pillar - Audit Planning, Materiality & Statistical Sampling**

- **Materiality, Performance Materiality & Attribute Sample Size** &nbsp; `Logic input` · basic · 10 min · ref: ISA 320 & ISA 530 (IAASB) / AICPA AU-C 320 & 530
  - _Measures:_ Applying ISA 320 materiality benchmarks and ISA 530 attribute sample-size mechanics to set defensible planning thresholds and a test-of-controls sample size.
  - _Scenario:_ You are the engagement senior planning the statutory audit of Al-Faris Manufacturing PJSC (Abu Dhabi), an SCA-listed entity with audited revenue of AED 480,000,000 and profit before tax of AED 36,000,000. Firm policy sets planning materiality at 5% of profit before tax. Performance materiality is set at 75% of planning materiality. Clearly trivial threshold is 5% of planning materiality. For the Accounts Payable population of 4,000 invoices you will run an attribute (test of controls) sample. The firm's sampling table gives a confidence factor of 3.0 (95% confidence, expecting zero deviations). The tolerable deviation rate is 5% of the population and the expected deviation rate is 0%, so sample size = confidence factor / tolerable deviation rate (expressed as a decimal). Compute each planning figure.
  - _Model answer:_ Planning materiality = 5% x AED 36,000,000 PBT = AED 1,800,000. Performance materiality = 75% x 1,800,000 = AED 1,350,000. Clearly trivial threshold = 5% x 1,800,000 = AED 90,000. Attribute sample size = confidence factor / tolerable deviation rate = 3.0 / 0.05 = 60 invoices (round up to whole items). These four fields are the gradable outputs; each is a deterministic arithmetic result from the stated policy percentages and the sampling formula.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Planning materiality = 5% x PBT (AED 1,800,000) - Correct ISA 320 benchmark application (5% of profit before tax).
    - `logic_value` (w2) - Performance materiality = 75% of planning materiality (AED 1,350,000) - Performance-materiality haircut correctly applied to planning materiality.
    - `logic_value` (w1) - Clearly trivial threshold = 5% of planning materiality (AED 90,000) - Clearly-trivial threshold derived from planning materiality, not revenue.
    - `logic_value` (w3) - Attribute sample size = confidence factor / TDR = 60 invoices - ISA 530 attribute sample-size formula (confidence factor over tolerable deviation rate).
- **Two-Variable Sample-Size Sensitivity Matrix** &nbsp; `Adv. Spreadsheet` · advanced · 15 min · ref: AICPA AU-C 530 Audit Sampling / IIA IPPF Standard 2320
  - _Measures:_ Constructing a defensible audit-sampling sensitivity model with native array/data-table mechanics, demonstrating how sample size scales with precision (TDR) and expected error (EPDR).
  - _Scenario:_ For the Procure-to-Pay control test you must show how the statistical sample size moves as the tolerable deviation rate (TDR) and the expected population deviation rate (EPDR) change. The base formula for a 95%-confidence attribute sample is: Sample size = ROUNDUP( ConfidenceFactor / (TDR - EPDR), 0 ), where ConfidenceFactor = 3.0 and TDR and EPDR are decimals. Base inputs in the grid: ConfidenceFactor in B1 = 3.0, TDR in B2 = 0.05, EPDR in B3 = 0.01. The base sample-size formula sits in B5. Build a two-variable data table over the column axis of TDR values {0.04, 0.05, 0.06} in C8:E8 and the row axis of EPDR values {0.00, 0.01, 0.02} in B9:B11, with the corner cell B8 linking to the base sample size. The body C9:E11 must be a native data table, not typed numbers.
  - _Model answer:_ Base case B5 = ROUNDUP(3.0/(0.05-0.01),0) = ROUNDUP(75,0) = 75. The data table feeds each TDR (column input -> B2) and EPDR (row input -> B3) into the formula. Corner low C9 = TDR 0.04, EPDR 0.00 -> ROUNDUP(3/0.04,0) = 75. Centre D10 = TDR 0.05, EPDR 0.01 -> ROUNDUP(3/0.04,0) = 75. Corner high E11 = TDR 0.06, EPDR 0.02 -> ROUNDUP(3/0.04,0) = 75. (Deliberately chosen so the diagonal precision gap (TDR-EPDR) stays 0.04; off-diagonal cells differ, e.g. C11 = TDR 0.04, EPDR 0.02 -> ROUNDUP(3/0.02,0) = 150, and E9 = TDR 0.06, EPDR 0.00 -> ROUNDUP(3/0.06,0) = 50.) Grading checks the data-table is a real array formula plus three interior/corner values.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `is_array_formula` (w3) - Body C9:E11 is a native data table (not hardcoded) - Candidate used a real two-variable data table, not typed-in numbers.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Base sample size B5 = 75 - Base attribute sample-size formula with ROUNDUP is correct.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - Off-diagonal C11 = 150 (TDR 0.04, EPDR 0.02) - Data table correctly recomputes when precision gap halves to 0.02.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Off-diagonal E9 = 50 (TDR 0.06, EPDR 0.00) - Data table correctly recomputes when precision gap widens to 0.06.
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Diagonal D10 = 75 (TDR 0.05, EPDR 0.01) - Centre cell reproduces the base 0.04 precision gap.

**Pillar - Controls Testing & Finding Severity Quantification**

- **Control Deviation Rate, Projected Upper Limit & Finding Risk Index** &nbsp; `Spreadsheet` · intermediate · 16.7 min · ref: COSO Internal Control - Integrated Framework / IIA IPPF Std 2320 / AICPA AU-C 530
  - _Measures:_ Quantifying control-test outcomes into deviation rates, projecting an upper deviation limit for sampling risk, and translating findings into a likelihood x impact risk index for severity triage.
  - _Scenario:_ You have completed test-of-controls fieldwork over four key controls at Gulf Cement Co (Ras Al Khaimah). For each control you sampled items and counted deviations. Compute the sample deviation rate, the projected (upper) deviation limit using the firm's add-on allowance for sampling risk, and a finding risk index = Likelihood (1-5) x Impact (1-5). Given data per control (Sample size, Deviations, Likelihood, Impact, Sampling-risk allowance as a percentage-point add-on): C1 Three-way match - sample 60, deviations 3, likelihood 4, impact 5, allowance 3.0pp; C2 Authorisation limits - sample 40, deviations 1, likelihood 2, impact 4, allowance 4.0pp; C3 Bank reconciliation - sample 25, deviations 0, likelihood 1, impact 5, allowance 6.0pp; C4 Segregation of duties - sample 50, deviations 5, likelihood 5, impact 5, allowance 4.0pp. Deviation rate = Deviations / Sample (as a percentage). Projected upper deviation limit = Deviation rate + Sampling-risk allowance (in percentage points). Risk index = Likelihood x Impact. Then compute the count of controls whose Risk index >= 16 (the firm's 'significant deficiency' escalation gate) and the total deviations across all four controls.
  - _Model answer:_ Per control: deviation rate = deviations/sample x 100. C1 = 3/60 = 5.0%; C2 = 1/40 = 2.5%; C3 = 0/25 = 0.0%; C4 = 5/50 = 10.0%. Projected upper deviation limit = deviation rate + allowance(pp): C1 = 5.0+3.0 = 8.0%; C2 = 2.5+4.0 = 6.5%; C3 = 0.0+6.0 = 6.0%; C4 = 10.0+4.0 = 14.0%. Risk index = L x I: C1 = 4x5 = 20; C2 = 2x4 = 8; C3 = 1x5 = 5; C4 = 5x5 = 25. Controls with risk index >= 16: C1 (20) and C4 (25) -> count = 2. Total deviations = 3+1+0+5 = 9. Graded cells: the four upper deviation limits, the two highest risk indices, the escalation count, and the deviation total.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `cell_value` (w1) - C4 deviation rate = 10.0% - Deviation rate = deviations/sample for the worst control.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - C1 projected upper deviation limit = 8.0% - Upper deviation limit adds the sampling-risk allowance to the observed rate.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - C4 projected upper deviation limit = 14.0% - Upper deviation limit correct for the highest-deviation control.
    - `cell_value` (w2) - C4 risk index = 25 (Likelihood 5 x Impact 5) - Likelihood x impact risk index computed correctly.
    - `cell_value` (w3) - Count of controls with risk index >= 16 = 2 - Significant-deficiency escalation gate applied (COUNTIF logic).
    - `cell_value` (w1) - Total deviations across all controls = 9 - Aggregate deviation count reconciles across the test.

**Pillar - Regulatory Obligation & Filing-Compliance Interrogation**

- **Overdue Statutory Filings & Open High-Severity Findings (SQL)** &nbsp; `SQL` · intermediate · 10 min · ref: GCC statutory filing regimes (UAE SCA / CBUAE, ZATCA, GOSI/WPS) / IIA IPPF Std 2500 Monitoring Progress
  - _Measures:_ Interrogating a regulatory-obligations register with relational logic to surface overdue statutory filings - the core data-hygiene task behind defensible compliance monitoring and regulator liaison.
  - _Scenario:_ Your compliance team maintains an obligations register tracking every statutory filing the group owes across UAE and Saudi regulators, with a due date, a submitted date (NULL if not yet filed), the regulator, and the linked open-finding severity. The compliance reporting date is 2025-04-01. Management wants the list of obligations that are OVERDUE (due on or before the reporting date and not yet submitted), one row per obligation, showing the obligation reference, the regulator, and the days overdue, with the most overdue first. Schema: obligations(id int PK, obligation_ref text, regulator text, due_date date, submitted_date date, severity text). 'Days overdue' = reporting date minus due date.
  - _Model answer:_ Filter to rows where submitted_date IS NULL AND due_date <= DATE '2025-04-01'. Project obligation_ref, regulator, and (DATE '2025-04-01' - due_date) AS days_overdue. Order by days_overdue DESC (then obligation_ref for determinism). Master query: SELECT obligation_ref, regulator, (DATE '2025-04-01' - due_date) AS days_overdue FROM obligations WHERE submitted_date IS NULL AND due_date <= DATE '2025-04-01' ORDER BY days_overdue DESC, obligation_ref. Seed rows include a mix of filed-on-time, filed-late (excluded - already submitted), not-yet-due, and overdue-unfiled obligations so the candidate must correctly combine the NULL submitted_date and due-date conditions; grading is an ordered result-set match.
  - _Checkpoints:_
    - `sql_result_match` (w3) - Result matches master (overdue unfiled obligations, days overdue, most-overdue first) - Correct combination of NULL-submitted filter, due-date cutoff, days-overdue arithmetic, and descending order.

---

## Build / seed plan

1. **Per function, one seed migration** mirroring the FP&A pattern (00077): insert `technical_pillars` rows, then `technical_skill_blocks` rows (engine_type, engine_config, master_solution, checkpoints jsonb, time_limit_seconds, framework_ref), and flip the function `node_status='active'`.
2. **engine_config authoring** is the real work per task: spreadsheet rows + editable cells + master cell values; logic_input fields + scenario; sql `schema_sql` + `seed_sql` + master query. Each checkpoint's numeric `expected` is computed from the master solution.
3. **Bilingual** name_ar / prompt_ar / instructions_ar on every block (Arabic best-effort, human-reviewed per project convention).
4. **Certification pairing:** to make a function's *combined* sitting credential-eligible, also seed SME-approved MCQ items (`tech_assessment_items`) for it and set its cut-score - otherwise the combined sitting is indicative (no credential).
5. **Suggested priority:** Finance core (AP/AR/GL/FA/Payroll/Treasury/Tax) -> Banking (credit, AML, Basel) -> Data/AI -> the rest. Quantitative functions seed fastest; soft functions need the flagged proxy tasks reviewed first.
